when you say she's a programmer , she did do some , but the real thing is to have said the future is going to be much , much more than this .	當你說她是一名程式設計師 , 她做了一些事 , 但真正的一件事就是說未來將會遠遠遠超過這一點 。
now , a hundred years later , this guy comes along , alan turing , and in 1936 , and invents the computer all over again .	一百年後 , 這個傢伙來了 , 艾倫•圖靈在1936年發明了一台電腦 。
now , of course , babbage's machine was entirely mechanical .	當然 , babbage的機器是完全機械化的 。
turing's machine was entirely theoretical .	turing的機器是完全理論的 。
both of these guys were coming from a mathematical perspective , but turing told us something very important .	這些人都來自數學的觀點 , 但 , 圖靈告訴我們一件很重要的事 。
he laid down the mathematical foundations for computer science , and said , " it doesn't matter how you make a computer . "	他為電腦科學奠定了數學基礎 , 說: 「 不管你如何製造電腦 。 」
it doesn't matter if your computer's mechanical , like babbage's was , or electronic , like computers are today , or perhaps in the future , cells , or , again , mechanical again , once we get into nanotechnology .	不管你的電腦機械工程 , 像是babbage , 或電子產品 , 如今的電腦 , 或未來的細胞 , 或者說 , 再一次 , 機械化 , 一旦我們進入奈米技術 。
we could go back to babbage's machine and just make it tiny . all those things are computers .	我們可以回到babbage的機器 , 讓它變小 。 所有這些東西都是電腦 。
there is in a sense a computing essence .	在某種意義上 , 電腦的本質是存在的 。
this is called the church–turing thesis .	這叫做 「 教堂動作論 」 。
and so suddenly , you get this link where you say this thing babbage had built really was a computer .	所以 , 突然間 , 你就有了這個連結 , 你說babbage已經建造了一台電腦 。
in fact , it was capable of doing everything we do today with computers , only really slowly .	事實上 , 它能夠做到今天我們用電腦所做的每一件事 , 只是慢得很慢 。
to give you an idea of how slowly , it had about 1k of memory .	為了讓你們知道它有多慢 , 它有1k的記憶力 。
it used punch cards , which were being fed in , and it ran about 10 , 000 times slower the first zx81 .	它用了打孔卡 , 被放進去 , 它的第一個zx81 , 000倍慢了一萬倍 。
it did have a ram pack .	它的確有一群鐵包 。
you could add on a lot of extra memory if you wanted to .	如果你想的話 , 你可以再加上額外的記憶 。
so , where does that bring us today ?	那麼 , 今天能帶給我們什麼 ?
so there are plans .	所以有一些計畫 。
over in swindon , the science museum archives , there are hundreds of plans and thousands of pages of notes written by charles babbage about this analytical engine .	在瑞典 , 科學博物館的檔案中 , 有數百個計劃和數千頁的筆記本 , 由查爾斯•巴布age所寫 , 關於這個分析引擎 。
one of those is a set of plans that we call plan 28 , and that is also the name of a charity that i started with doron swade , who was the curator of computing at the science museum , and also the person who drove the project to build a difference engine , and our plan is to build it .	其中一組是計劃 , 我們稱之為計劃28 , 這也是我從doronswaade開始的慈善機構 , 他是科學博物館的策展人 , 開著這個計劃去創造一個差異引擎 , 我們的計劃是要建造它 。
here in south kensington , we will build the analytical engine .	在南肯辛頓 , 我們將會建造分析引擎 。
the project has a number of parts to it .	這個專案計畫有幾個部分 。
one was the scanning of babbage's archive .	一個是babbage的檔案掃描 。
that's been done . the second is now the study of all of those plans to determine what to build .	這已經完成了 。 第二個是研究這些計畫的目的 , 來決定要建造什麼 。
the third part is a computer simulation of that machine , and the last part is to physically build it at the science museum .	第三部分是電腦模擬這台機器的模擬 , 最後一部分是在科學博物館的實體建構 。
when it's built , you'll finally be able to understand how a computer works , because rather than having a tiny chip in front of you , you've got to look at this humongous thing and say , " ah , i see the memory operating , i see the cpu operating , i hear it operating . i probably smell it operating . "	當它被建成時 , 你終於能夠了解電腦是如何運作的 , 因為不是在你面前有一小塊小晶片 , 你要看這個巨大的東西 , 然後說: 「 啊 , 我看到記憶運作 , 我看到cpu在運作 , 我聽見它在運作 。 」
but in between that we're going to do a simulation .	但在這兩者之間 , 我們要做一個模擬 。
babbage himself wrote , he said , as soon as the analytical engine exists , it will surely guide the future course of science .	babbage自己寫下 , 他說 , 一旦分析引擎存在 , 它肯定會引導未來科學的軌道 。
of course , he never built it , because he was always fiddling with new plans , but when it did get built , of course , in the 1940s , everything changed .	當然 , 他從來沒有蓋過它 , 因為他一直在充斥新計畫 , 但當它真的被建造出來時 , 當然 , 在1940年代 , 一切都改變了 。
now , i'll just give you a little taste of what it looks like in motion with a video which shows just one part of the cpu mechanism working .	現在 , 我來給你們一些味覺 , 看看這個動作的樣子 , 它只顯示了cpu機制運作的其中一部分 。
so this is just three sets of cogs , and it's going to add . this is the adding mechanism in action , so you imagine this gigantic machine .	這只是三組齒輪 , 加上這就是增加機制的作用所以你想像一下這個巨大的機器
so , give me five years .	所以 , 給我五年 。
before the 2030s happen , we'll have it .	在2030年發生之前 , 我們就有了 。
thank you very much .	非常謝謝大家
in this imagefilled talk , yann arthusbertrand displays his three most recent projects on humanity and our habitat stunning aerial photographs in his series " the earth from above , " personal interviews from around the globe featured in his web project " 6 billion others , " and his soontobereleased movie , " home , " which documents human impact on the environment through breathtaking video .	在這張圖片中 , 雅非•藝術家在最近的三項項項目中展現出他在人性和我們的棲息地上驚人的空拍攝 , 在他的系列《地球之上》中 , 來自全球各地的個人訪問 , 他的網路專案 「 六十億人 」 , 他很快就會在電影《家園》中拍下人類對環境的影響 , 透過呼吸影片來拍攝環境的影響 。
art , climate change , environment , film , future , humanity , media , photography	藝術、氣候變遷、環境、電影、未來、人性、媒體、攝影、攝影 。
yann arthusbertrand captures fragile earth in wideangle	雅恩•阿胡斯伯特蘭在廣角的地球上捕捉到脆弱的地球 , 在廣角上捕捉到脆弱的地球 。
i have a big impact on the planet to travel here by plane .	我對地球有很大的衝擊 , 以飛機來到這裡旅行 。
i emitted , in the atmosphere , nine tons of co2 ; that is the weight of two elephants .	我在大氣中排放了9噸的二氧化碳 ; 那是兩隻大象的重量 。
i came here to speak about ecology , and i emitted as much co2 as a frenchman in one year .	我來到這裡 , 來談談生態學 , 一年我就把二氧化碳當作法國人 。
so what do i have to do ?	所以 , 我該怎麼做 ?
i have to kill a frenchman when i come back at home ?	當我回到家時 , 我得要殺一個法國人 ?
i have to do my carbon offset in another way , like i do every time .	我必須以另一種方式做碳排放 , 就像我每次都會做一樣 。
in fact my work is to show our impact on our planet .	事實上 , 我的工作是要展現我們對地球的影響 。
i'm going to show you some examples of the last pictures i've done in the last year .	我要給你們看一些例子 , 是我去年所拍攝的最後一張照片 。
alberta sand oil , a lot of pollution .	亞伯達石油 , 很多污染 。
you know the problem ; we don't want to believe what we know .	你知道問題 , 我們不想相信我們所知道的 。
in alberta people work nonstop , 24 hours by seven to extract as much oil as they can .	在亞伯達 , 人們工作了24小時 , 七個小時 , 盡可能的抽取石油 。
we know about the end of oil .	我們知道石油的終點 。
oil sand is not a longterm solution .	石油砂不是一個長期的解決方案 。
but we use three times more oil than we find every year .	但我們每年所發現的石油多出三倍 。
we don't want to believe what we know .	我們不想相信我們所知道的 。
coral reef in new caledonia .	珊瑚礁位於紐加里尼亞 。
100 percent of the coral may be wiped out before 2050 because of global warming .	百分之百的珊瑚可能在2050年之前就被滅絕 , 因為全球暖化 。
and you know how coral are very sensitive to temperature , and are very important for the biodiversity of the sea .	你知道珊瑚對溫度非常敏感 , 對海洋的生物多樣性非常重要 。

it was impossible to do this picture 15 years ago .	15年前做這張照片是不可能的 。
now there is a new way open between atlantic and pacific .	大西洋和太平洋之間有一種新的開放方式 。
the thickness of the arctic decreased more than 40 percent since 1960 .	從1960年起 , 北極的厚度降低了40% 。
there is a new face of kilimanjaro without ice .	在沒有冰的情況下 , kilimanjaro就有了新的面孔 。
it lost 80 percent of its ice .	它失去了80%的冰 。
according to scientists , in 100 years all the mountain glacier will be gone .	根據科學家 , 在一百年內 , 所有的山冰川都會消失 。
glaciers are very important for the life on earth .	冰河對地球上的生命是非常重要的 。
like al gore told you , two billion people live on the water from the glacier of himalaya .	如同高爾所說 , 有二十億人住在喜馬拉雅的冰河上 。
return of fish men .	返回魚類的男人 。
one fifth of human kind depend on fish to live .	五分之一的人類是靠魚類生存 。
today now 70 percent of the fish stock are overexploited .	現今有70%的魚類存量過度剝削 。

we don't want to believe what we know .	我們不想相信我們所知道的 。

one human of six have not enough to eat in the world .	六個人中有六個人沒有足夠的食物 。

here in america , 90 percent of the corn cultivated is used to feed animals or to do oil .	在美國 , 百分之九十的玉米培育被用來餵養動物或石油 。
palm tree plantation in borneo .	在婆羅的棕櫚樹種植 。

we all share the same need for the earth's gifts the same wish to rise above ourselves , and become better .	我們都一樣 , 對地球的禮物有著相同的願望 , 能在我們自己上方興起 , 變得更好 。

in less than 50 years we've altered it more thoroughly than in the entire history of mankind .	不到五十年 , 我們已經徹底改變了它 , 比人類歷史上整個歷史都還要更徹底 。
half of the world's forests have vanished .	世界上一半的森林已經消失了 。
water resources are running low .	水資源是很低的 。
intensive farming is depleting soils .	加護農業正在耗盡土壤 。
our energy sources are not sustainable .	我們的能源來源無法永續發展 。
the climate is changing .	氣候正在改變 。
we are endangering ourselves .	我們正在危害我們自己 。
we're only trying to improve our lives .	我們只想改善我們的生活 。
but the wealth gaps are growing wider .	但財富差距正在擴大 。
we haven't yet understood that we're going at a much faster pace than the planet can sustain .	我們尚未明白 , 我們正在邁向比地球還快很多的速度 。

in this accessible talk from tedxboston , richard resnick shows how cheap and fast genome sequencing is about to turn health care upside down .	在tedxboston , richardresnick的這個談話中 , 顯示出 , 要把健康照護轉換成很便宜且快速的基因定序 。
dna , biotech , health care , science , technology	dna、生物科技、健康照護、科學、科技、科技、科技、科技 。
richard resnick: welcome to the genomic revolution	理查•雷斯尼克:歡迎來到基因革命的基因革命 。
ladies and gentlemen , i present to you the human genome .	各位先生女士 , 我向你們展示人類基因組 。
chromosome one , top left .	第一 , 染色體 , 左上方 。
bottom right are the sex chromosomes .	右下角是性染色體 。
women have two copies of that big x chromosome ; men have the x and , of course , that small copy of the y .	女性有兩份大型x染色體 ; 男性有x , 當然 , 男性有y的小版本 。
sorry boys , but it's just a tiny little thing that makes you different .	抱歉男孩們 , 但這只是一個小東西 , 讓你有所不同 。
so if you zoom in on this genome , then what you see , of course , is this double helix structure the code of life spelled out with these four biochemical letters , or we call them bases , right: a , c , g and t .	所以如果你放大這個基因組 , 當然 , 你會看到這個雙螺旋結構--生命的代碼--這四個生物化學字母 , 或者我們稱之為基礎:a、c、g和t 。
how many are there in the human genome ? three billion .	人類基因組有多少 ? 三十億 。
is that a big number ?	這是個很大的數字嗎 ?
well , everybody can throw around big numbers .	嗯 , 所有人都可以投入大量的數字 。
but in fact , if i were to place one base on each pixel of this 1280 by 800 resolution screen , we would need 3 , 000 screens to take a look at the genome .	但事實上 , 如果我把這1280的像素放到1800的解析度螢幕上 , 我們需要3 , 000個螢幕來檢視基因組 。
so it's really quite big .	這真的很大 。
and perhaps because of its size , a group of people all , by the way , with y chromosomes decided they would want to sequence it .	也許是因為它的大小 , 順便一提 , 有一群人 , y染色體決定要定序它 。
and so 15 years , actually , and about four billion dollars later , the genome was sequenced and published .	事實上 , 15年後 , 大約四十億美元後 , 基因組序列和出版了 。
in 2003 , the final version was published , and they keep working on it .	在2003年 , 最後的版本被發表 , 他們繼續研究它 。
that was all done on a machine that looks like this .	這一切都是在這樣的機器上完成的 。
it costs about a dollar for each base a very slow way of doing it .	每一鹼基都要花一塊錢 , 非常緩慢的做法 。
well folks , i'm here to tell you that the world has completely changed and none of you know about it .	各位 , 我來這裡是要告訴各位 , 世界已經完全改變了 , 沒有人知道它 。
so now what we do is we take a genome , we make maybe 50 copies of it , we cut all those copies up into little 50base reads , and then we sequence them , massively parallel .	所以 , 我們現在做的是把基因組做成五十個複製品 , 我們把這些複製品切成五十個頁面 , 然後我們將它們定序 , 大規模平行 。
and then we bring that into software , and we reassemble it and we tell you what the story is .	然後我們把它帶到軟體裡 , 再重組它 , 告訴你這個故事是什麼 。
and so just to give you a picture of what this looks like , the human genome project: 3 gigabases , right .	所以 , 給大家看看這是什麼樣子 , 人類的基因組計畫:三吉布斯 , 沒錯 。
one run on one of these machines: 200 gigabases in a week .	一個在其中一台機器運行:一個星期內有200gb 。
and that 200 is going to change to 600 this summer , and there's no sign of this pace slowing .	今年夏天將改變2000年 , 沒有任何步伐減慢的跡象 。
so the price of a base , to sequence a base , has fallen 100 million times .	所以 , 要定序一個鹼基的價格 , 已經下降了一億倍 。
that's the equivalent of you filling up your car with gas in 1998 , waiting until 2011 , and now you can drive to jupiter and back twice .	等同於你在1998年填滿氣體的車子 , 等到2011年 , 現在你可以開車到木星 , 再回來兩次 。
world population , pc placements , the archive of all the medical literature , moore's law , the old way of sequencing , and here's all the new stuff .	世界人口、pc定位、所有醫學文獻的檔案、摩爾定律、古老的定序方式 , 這裡有所有的新東西 。
guys , this is a log scale ; you don't typically see lines that go up like that .	各位 , 這是一個標誌 , 你通常不會看到像這樣的線條 。
so the worldwide capacity to sequence human genomes is something like 50 , 000 to 100 , 000 human genomes this year .	所以 , 全世界對於人類基因序列的能力大約是今年大約有五萬到十萬個人類基因組 。
and we know this based on the machines that are being placed .	我們知道這個基於被放置的機器 。
this is expected to double , triple or maybe quadruple year over year for the foreseeable future .	這是預期的兩倍 , 三倍或四倍 , 可能是可預期的未來一年 。
in fact , there's one lab in particular that represents 20 percent of all that capacity .	事實上 , 有一個實驗室 , 其中有20%的能力 。
it's called the beijing genomics institute .	它叫做北京基因組學研究所 。
the chinese are absolutely winning this race to the new moon , by the way .	中國人絕對贏得了新月球的比賽 。
what does this mean for medicine ?	這對醫藥有什麼意義 ?
so a woman is age 37 .	一個女人是37歲 。
she presents with stage 2 estrogen receptorpositive breast cancer .	她用 「 階段2 」 來呈現雌激素受體乳癌 。
she is treated with surgery , chemotherapy and radiation .	她接受手術、化療和放射線治療 。
two years later , she comes back with stage three c ovarian cancer .	兩年後 , 她帶著三c型卵巢癌回來 。
unfortunately , treated again with surgery and chemotherapy .	不幸的是 , 再次接受外科手術和化療 。
she comes back three years later at age 42 with more ovarian cancer , more chemotherapy .	三年後她回到42歲 , 患有更多卵巢癌 , 更多化療 。
six months later , she comes back with acute myeloid leukemia .	六個月後 , 她帶著急性骨髓性白血病回來 。
she goes into respiratory failure and dies eight days later .	她進入呼吸衰竭 , 八天後死亡 。
so first , the way in which this woman was treated , in as little as 10 years , will look like bloodletting .	首先 , 這位女士被治療的方式 , 在短短十年內 , 看起來會像血液流動 。
and it's because of people like my colleague , rick wilson , at the genome institute at washington university , who decided to take a look at this woman postmortem .	因為像我同事rickwilson這樣的人 , 在華盛頓大學的基因研究所 , 他決定去看這位女士後遺體 。
and he sequenced , he took skin cells , healthy skin , and cancerous bone marrow , and he sequenced the whole genomes of both of them in a couple of weeks , no big deal .	他定序了皮膚細胞 , 健康的皮膚 , 癌症的骨髓 , 將兩者的整個基因序列定序 , 在幾個星期內 , 沒什麼大不了的 。
and then he compared those two genomes in software , and what he found , among other things , was a deletion , a 2 , 000base deletion across three billion bases in a particular gene called tp53 .	接著 , 他把這兩種基因和軟體比較 , 他發現 , 在其它東西當中 , 是一個刪除 , 一個有兩千多個鹼基的基因 , 一個叫tp53的基因 。
if you have this deleterious mutation in this gene , you're 90 percent likely to get cancer in your life .	如果你在這個基因中有這種良好的突變 , 你就有90%的可能性會罹患癌症 。
so unfortunately , this doesn't help this woman , but it does have severe , profound if you will , implications to her family .	不幸的是 , 這對這位女士並不有幫助 , 但如果你願意的話 , 它的確有嚴重的影響 , 對她的家人有著深刻的影響 。
i mean , if they have the same mutation , and they get this genetic test , and they understand it , then they can go and get regular screens , and they can catch cancer early and potentially live a significantly longer life .	我的意思是 , 如果他們有相同的突變 , 他們得到了這個基因測驗 , 他們了解它 , 那麼他們就可以取得一般的螢幕 , 他們就可以追蹤癌症 , 可能活得更久 。
let me introduce you now to the beery twins , diagnosed with cerebral palsy at the age of two .	讓我向各位介紹beery雙胞胎 , 在兩歲時被診斷出腦性麻痺 。
their mom is a very brave woman who didn't believe that the symptoms weren't matching up , and through some heroic efforts and a lot of internet searching , she was able to convince the medical community that , in fact , they had something else .	他們的母親是一位非常勇敢的女子 , 她不相信症狀並不符合 , 透過一些英勇的努力和網路搜尋 , 她能夠說服醫學界 , 事實上 , 他們還有其他東西 。
what they had was doparesponsive dystonia .	他們所擁有的是 「 雙關節障礙 」 。
and so they were given ldopa , and their symptoms did improve , but they weren't totally asymptomatic .	所以他們得到了dopa , 他們的症狀確實改善了 , 但他們並非完全的症狀 。
turns out the gentleman in this picture is a guy named joe beery , who was lucky enough to be the cio of a company called life technologies .	這張照片中的先生是一位叫joebeery的傢伙他很幸運能成為一家叫做生命科技的公司
they're one of the two companies that makes these massive whole genome sequencing tools .	它們是兩家公司之一 , 製造這些大量的基因組定序工具 。
and so what he did was he got his kids sequenced .	所以他所做的是 , 他拿了他的孩子序列 。
and what they found was a series of mutations in a gene called spr , which is responsible for producing serotonin , among other things .	他們發現一系列的突變 , 在一個叫做 「 春天 」 的基因中 , 負責產生血清素 , 其它東西 。
so on top of ldopa , they gave these kids a serotonin precursor drug , and they're effectively normal now .	所以 , 在dopa的上方 , 他們給了這些孩子一種血清素的先驅藥物 , 他們現在很正常 。
guys , this would never have happened without whole genome sequencing .	各位 , 如果沒有完整的基因定序 , 就不會發生這種事 。
and at the time this was a few years ago it cost $100 , 000 .	幾年前 , 當時是10萬美金 。
today it's $10 , 000 . next year it's $1 , 000 .	今天是一萬元 , 明年是一千元 。
the year after it's $100 , give or take a year .	在百元後的那一年 , 或花一年的時間 。
that's how fast this is moving .	這就是移動的速度 。
so here's little nick likes batman and squirt guns .	這裡有一些小小的尼克 , 像是蝙蝠俠和松鼠槍 。
and it turns out nick shows up at the children's hospital with this distended belly like a famine victim .	結果發現 , 尼克在兒童醫院出現 , 腹部像個饑荒受害者一樣 。
and it's not that he's not eating , it's that when he eats , his intestine basically opens up and feces spill out into his gut .	並不是說他吃不了 , 而是當他吃的時候 , 他的腸道基本上會打開 , 糞便會流出他的腸子 。
so a hundred surgeries later , he looks at his mom and says , " mom , please pray for me . i'm in so much pain . "	一百個手術後 , 他看著他的媽媽說: 「 媽 , 拜託我 , 我很痛苦 。 」
his pediatrician happens to have a background in clinical genetics and he has no idea what's going on , but he says , " let's get this kid's genome sequenced . "	他的小兒科醫師剛好有臨床遺傳學的背景 , 他不知道發生了什麼事 , 但他說: 「 我們來取得這個孩子的基因序列 。 」
and what they find is a singlepoint mutation in a gene responsible for controlling programmed cell death .	而他們發現 , 一個單點突變 , 負責控制程式編寫的細胞死亡的基因 。
so the theory is that he's having some immunological reaction to what's going on to the food essentially , and that's a natural reaction , which causes some programmed cell death .	所以 , 理論是 , 他對食物的反應有一些免疫反應 , 本質上 , 是天然的反應 , 會造成細胞死亡 。
but the gene that regulates that down is broken .	但管制下的基因被破壞了 。
and so this informs , among other things , of course , a treatment for bone marrow transplant , which he undertakes .	當然 , 這也包含了骨髓移植的一種治療方式 , 可以治療骨髓移植 。
and after nine months of grueling recovery , he's now eating steak with a1 sauce .	經過九個月的讚美康復後 , 他現在正在吃牛排一醬 。
the prospect of using the genome as a universal diagnostic is upon us today .	把基因組當作一個普遍診斷的前景 , 現今我們已經有了 。
today , it's here .	今天 , 它在這裡 。
and what it means for all of us is that everybody in this room could live an extra five , 10 , 20 years just because of this one thing .	對我們所有人來說 , 意思是 , 在座的每個人都可以多過5、10、20年 , 因為這一件事 。
which is a fantastic story , unless you think about humanity's footprint on the planet and our ability to keep up food production .	這是個很棒的故事 , 除非你想到地球上人類的足跡 , 以及我們能維持食物生產的能力 。
so it turns out that the very same technology is also being used to grow new lines of corn , wheat , soybean and other crops that are highly tolerant of drought , of flood , of pests and pesticides .	結果發現 , 同樣的技術也被用來種植新的玉米、小麥、大豆和其他農作物 , 這些都是乾旱、洪水、害蟲和殺蟲劑 。
now look , as long as we continue to increase the population , we're going to have to continue to grow and eat genetically modified foods , and that's the only position that i'll take today .	看看 , 只要我們繼續增加人口 , 我們就得繼續種植、吃基因改造食物 , 這是我今天唯一需要的位置 。

this is a typewriter , a staple of every desktop for decades .	這是一台打字機 , 數十年來每個桌面的一大堆 。

consumer applications for genomics , they will flourish .	消費者應用在基因組學上 , 他們會蓬勃發展 。

daniel kraft demos his marrow miner a new device that quickly harvests lifesaving bone marrow with minimal pain to the donor . he emphasizes that the adult stem cells found in bone marrow can be used to treat many terminal conditions , from parkinson's to heart disease .	丹尼爾•克拉夫將他的骨髓採集一個新的裝置 , 快速收集了救命的骨髓 , 和捐贈者的最小痛苦 。 他強調的是 , 骨髓中成人的幹細胞能被用來治療許多終極條件 , 從帕金森氏症到心臟病 。

now , inspired by jill bolte taylor last year , i didn't bring a human brain , but i did bring a liter of bone marrow .	去年jillboltetaylor的靈感 , 我沒有帶一個人腦 , 但我確實帶了一公升的骨髓 。
and bone marrow is actually what we use to save the lives of tens of thousands of patients , most of whom have advanced malignancies like leukemia and lymphoma and some other diseases .	而骨髓其實是我們用來拯救數萬名病人的生命 , 大部分患有先進的惡性腫瘤 , 例如白血病、淋巴瘤和一些其他疾病 。
so , a few years ago , i'm doing my transplant fellowship at stanford .	所以 , 幾年前 , 我在史丹佛做移植研究 。
i'm in the operating room . we have bob here , who is a volunteer donor .	我在手術室 , 我們這裡有鮑勃 , 他是自願捐贈者 。
we're sending his marrow across the country to save the life of a child with leukemia .	我們把他的骨髓送到全國 , 以拯救白血病孩童的生命 。
so actually how do we harvest this bone marrow ?	所以 , 我們要如何收集這些骨髓 ?
well we have a whole o . r . team , general anesthesia , nurses , and another doctor across from me .	嗯 , 我們有一整個o.r.團隊 , 麻醉 , 護士 , 還有另一位醫生在我身邊 。
bob's on the table , and we take this sort of small needle , you know , not too big .	鮑勃站在桌子上 , 我們把這個小針 , 你知道的 , 不太大 。
and the way we do this is we basically place this through the soft tissue , and kind of punch it into the hard bone , into the tuchus that's a technical term and aspirate about 10 mls of bone marrow out , each time , with a syringe .	我們做這件事的方式基本上就是把這個放到軟組織裡 , 把它打進硬骨頭 , 進入塔丘 , 每次用針筒 , 用針筒打開大約十個骨髓 。
and hand it off to the nurse . she squirts it into a tin .	然後把它交給護士 , 她將它放進一個小小的房子裡 。
hands it back to me . and we do that again and again .	把它交給我 。 我們一而再再而三地這樣做 。
about 200 times usually .	通常是兩百次 。
and by the end of this my arm is sore , i've got a callus on my hand , let alone bob , whose rear end looks something more like this , like swiss cheese .	最後 , 我的手臂是如此 , 我手上有一通電話 , 更別說鮑勃 , 他的耳朵看起來像這樣 , 像是瑞士起士 。
so i'm thinking , you know , this procedure hasn't changed in about 40 years .	我在想 , 你知道的 , 這個手術在40年內還沒有改變 。
and there is probably a better way to do this .	可能還有更好的方法來做這件事 。
so i thought of a minimally invasive approach , and a new device that we call the marrow miner .	所以我想到一個最小的入侵方式 , 一個新的裝置我們稱之為 「 骨髓礦工 」 。
and the marrow miner , the way it works is shown here .	而骨髓礦工 , 它的運作方式是在這裡展示的 。
our standard seethrough patient .	我們的標準種子病人 。
instead of entering the bone dozens of times , we enter just once , into the front of the hip or the back of the hip .	與其進入骨頭的數十次 , 我們就只是進入了一遍 , 進入髖骨的前面或髖部的後面 。
and we have a flexible , powered catheter with a special wire loop tip that stays inside the crunchy part of the marrow and follows the contours of the hip , as it moves around .	我們有彈性、發電的導管 , 帶著特殊的電線循環 , 留在骨髓內 , 跟著臀部的旋轉 。
so it enables you to very rapidly aspirate , or suck out , rich bone marrow very quickly through one hole .	所以它能讓你非常快速地吸引人 , 或者說吸了 , 富有的骨髓很快地穿過一個洞 。
we can do multiple passes through that same entry .	我們可以通過相同的入口 。
and , so , very quickly , bob can just get one puncture , local anesthesia , and do this harvest as an outpatient .	所以 , 很快地 , 鮑勃只能得到一個特點 , 當地的麻醉劑 , 把這個做成一個門診 。
so i did a few prototypes . i got a small little grant at stanford .	所以我做了幾個原型 , 我在史丹佛拿到一個小小的格子 。
and played around with this a little bit .	再多玩一點 。
and our team members developed this technology .	我們的團隊成員開發了這項技術 。
and eventually we got two large animals , and pig studies .	最後我們有兩個大型動物和豬研究
and we found , to our surprise , that we not only got bone marrow out , but we got 10 times the stem cell activity in the marrow from the marrow miner , compared to the normal device .	我們發現 , 意外的是 , 我們不只得到骨髓 , 我們還得到了骨髓幹細胞活動的十倍 , 相較於正常的裝置 。
this device was just fda approved in the last year .	這個裝置在去年才被核准 。
here is a live patient . you can see it following the flexible curves around .	這是一名活的病人 。 你可以看到它在周圍的彈性曲線 。
there will be two passes here , in the same patient , from the same hole .	這裡將會有兩個通過 , 同一個病人 , 同一個洞 。
this was done under local anesthesia , as an outpatient .	在麻醉之下 , 這是在當地的麻醉劑 。
and we got , again , about three to six times more stem cells than the standard approach done on the same patient .	同樣的 , 我們得到的幹細胞數量是同一個病人的標準方法的三到六倍 。
so why should you care ? bone marrow is a very rich source of adult stem cells .	你為什麼要關心 ? 骨髓是非常豐富的成人幹細胞來源 。
you all know about embryonic stem cells .	你們都知道胚胎幹細胞 。
they've got great potential but haven't yet entered clinical trials .	他們有很大的潛力 , 但還沒進入臨床試驗 。
adult stem cells are throughout our body , including the bloodforming stem cells in our bone marrow , which we've been using as a form of stemcell therapy for over 40 years .	成體幹細胞在我們的身體裡 , 包括骨髓中血液改造的幹細胞 , 我們用這種幹細胞治療已經超過四十年了 。
in the last decade there's been an explosion of use of bone marrow stem cells to treat the patient's other diseases such as heart disease , vascular disease , orthopedics , tissue engineering , even in neurology to treat parkinson's and diabetes .	過去十年來 , 使用骨髓幹細胞來治療病人其他疾病 , 例如心臟病 , 血管疾病 , 組織工程 , 甚至在神經系統中 , 來治療帕金森氏症和糖尿病 。
we've just come out , we're commercializing , this year , generation 2 . 0 of the marrow miner .	我們剛剛出發 , 我們正在商業化 , 今年 , 兩世世代的骨髓礦工 。
the hope is that this gets more stem cells out , which translates to better outcomes .	希望這能讓更多幹細胞被翻譯成更好的結果 。
it may encourage more people to sign up to be potential livesaving bone marrow donors .	它可能會鼓勵更多人簽名 , 成為可能救命的骨髓捐贈者 。
it may even enable you to bank your own marrow stem cells , when you're younger and healthier , to use in the future should you need it .	甚至可能讓你可以銀行你自己的骨髓幹細胞 , 當你年紀更小、更健康的時候 , 讓你可以在未來使用它 。
and ultimately and here's a picture of our bone marrow transplant survivors , who come together for a reunion each year at stanford .	最終 , 這是我們的骨髓移植倖存者的照片 , 他們每年在史丹佛聚會 。
hopefully this technology will let us have more of these survivors in the future .	希望這項技術能讓我們在未來有更多這些倖存者 。
physicist and surfer garrett lisi presents a controversial new model of the universe that just maybe answers all the big questions . if nothing else , it's the most beautiful 8dimensional model of elementary particles and forces you've ever seen .	物理學家和衝浪者葛雷特•賴西在宇宙中出現了一種爭議性的新模型 , 可能只能回答所有問題 。 如果沒有其他東西 , 它是最美麗的8維的粒子模型 , 強迫你見過 。
physics , science , technology	物理、科學、科技、科技、科技、
garrett lisi on his theory of everything	garretlisi理論上所有東西的理論都是garretlisi 。
whoa , dude . check out those killer equations . sweet .	哇 , 查看那些殺手方程式 。
actually , for the next 18 minutes i'm going to do the best i can to describe the beauty of particle physics without equations .	事實上 , 在接下來的18分鐘裡 , 我要盡我所能地描述在沒有公式的粒子物理的美麗 。
it turns out there's a lot we can learn from coral .	結果發現 , 我們能從珊瑚身上學到很多東西 。
coral is a very beautiful and unusual animal .	珊瑚是非常美麗且不尋常的動物 。
each coral head consists of thousand of individual polyps .	每個珊瑚的頭包含成千上萬個珊瑚蟲 。
these polyps are continually budding and branching into genetically identical neighbors .	這些珊瑚蟲會不斷地在基因上生長和分支 , 成為同一的鄰居 。
if we imagine this to be a hyperintelligent coral , we can single out an individual and ask him a reasonable question .	如果我們想像這是一個超智能的珊瑚 , 我們就能找出一個人 , 並且問他一個合理的問題 。
we can ask how exactly he got to be in this particular location compared to his neighbors if it was just chance , or destiny , or what ?	我們可以問他在這個地點和他的鄰居相比 , 是否只是偶然 , 或命運 , 或什麼 ?
now , after admonishing us for turning the temperature up too high , he would tell us that our question was completely stupid .	把溫度調高得太高之後 , 他會告訴我們 , 我們的問題完全愚蠢 。
these corals can be quite kind of mean , you see , and i have surfing scars to prove that .	你看 , 這些珊瑚是很有意思的 , 你看 , 我有衝浪的疤痕可以證明它 。
but this polyp would continue and tell us that his neighbors were quite clearly identical copies of him .	但這隻珊瑚蟲會繼續告訴我們 , 他的鄰居很明顯是他一模一樣的複製品 。
that he was in all these other locations as well , but experiencing them as separate individuals .	他也處在其它地方 , 但體驗它們和獨立個體是不同的 。
for a coral , branching into different copies is the most natural thing in the world .	對珊瑚而言 , 分枝為不同的複製品是世界上最自然的東西 。
unlike us , a hyperintelligent coral would be uniquely prepared to understand quantum mechanics .	不像我們 , 超級智慧的珊瑚 , 會特別準備好要了解量子力學 。
the mathematics of quantum mechanics very accurately describes how our universe works .	量子力學的數學非常準確地描述我們的宇宙是如何運作的 。
and it tells us our reality is continually branching into different possibilities , just like a coral .	它告訴我們 , 我們的現實是不斷分裂成不同的可能性 , 就像珊瑚一樣 。
it's a weird thing for us humans to wrap our minds around , since we only ever get to experience one possibility .	這對我們人類來說是一件奇怪的事 , 因為我們只能體驗一個可能性 。
this quantum weirdness was first described by erwin schrödinger and his cat .	這種量子奇怪之處在於erwinschrder和他的貓
the cat likes this version better .	貓比較喜歡這個版本 。
in this setup , schrödinger is in a box with a radioactive sample that , by the laws of quantum mechanics , branches into a state in which it is radiated and a state in which it is not .	在這個組合中 , 薛丁格在一個放射性樣本中 , 通過量子力學的定律 , 分支進入一個狀態 , 一個不存在的狀態 。
in the branch in which the sample radiates , it sets off a trigger that releases poison and schrödinger is dead .	在採集樣本的分支中 , 它啟動了釋放毒素和薛丁格死去的部位 。
but in the other branch of reality , he remains alive .	但在現實的另一個層面上 , 他仍然活著 。
these realities are experienced separately by each individual .	這些真相是被不同的個體分開的 。
as far as either can tell , the other one doesn't exist .	據說兩者之間 , 另一人並不存在 。
this seems weird to us , because each of us only experiences an individual existence , and we don't get to see other branches .	這對我們來說是很奇怪的 , 因為我們每一個人都只經歷一個人的存在 , 而我們看不到其他的分支 。
it's as if each of us , like schrödinger here , are a kind of coral branching into different possibilities .	這就好像我們每一個人 , 如薛丁格在這裡 , 有點像珊瑚一樣 , 變成不同的可能性 。
the mathematics of quantum mechanics tells us this is how the world works at tiny scales .	量子力學的數學告訴我們 , 世界的運作方式很小 。
it can be summed up in a single sentence: everything that can happen , does .	它可以用單一句話來做總結:所有可能發生的事情 , 確實 。
but this does not mean everything happens .	但這並不表示一切都會發生 。
the rest of physics is about describing what can happen and what can't .	其他的物理則是描述可能發生什麼事 , 以及什麼是不可能發生的 。
what physics tells us is that everything comes down to geometry and the interactions of elementary particles .	物理學告訴我們 , 一切都歸功於幾何和基本粒子的互動 。
and things can happen only if these interactions are perfectly balanced .	只有這些互動是完全平衡的 。
now i'll go ahead and describe how we know about these particles , what they are and how this balance works .	現在我來說明我們對這些粒子的了解 , 它們是什麼 , 以及平衡如何運作 。
in this machine , a beam of protons and antiprotons are accelerated to near the speed of light and brought together in a collision , producing a burst of pure energy .	在這個機器中 , 一束質子和反質子會加速接近光速的速度 , 並在撞擊中聚集在一起 , 產生出一股純能量 。
this energy is immediately converted into a spray of subatomic particles , with detectors and computers used to figure out their properties .	這種能量立刻被轉換成亞原子粒子的噴射 , 用探測器和電腦來找出它們的特性 。
this enormous machine the large hadron collider at cern in geneva has a circumference of 17 miles and , when it's operating , draws five times as much power as the city of monterey .	這台巨大的機器 , 位於日內瓦的cern大型強子對撞機有十七英里的圍繞 , 當它在運作時 , 比蒙特雷市的城市還要多出五倍 。
we can't predict specifically what particles will be produced in any individual collision .	我們無法準確預測哪些粒子會在任何個別碰撞中產生 。
quantum mechanics tells us all possibilities are realized .	量子力學告訴我們所有可能性都在實現 。
but physics does tell us what particles can be produced .	但物理的確能告訴我們粒子能產生什麼 。
these particles must have just as much mass and energy as is carried in by the proton and antiproton .	這些粒子必須有那麼多質量和能量 , 就像質子和反質子所攜帶的一樣 。
any particles more massive than this energy limit aren't produced , and remain invisible to us .	任何比這個能量有更大的粒子 , 都不會產生出來 , 且對我們來說仍然是看不見的 。
this is why this new particle accelerator is so exciting .	這就是為什麼這個新的粒子加速器如此令人興奮 。
it's going to push this energy limit seven times beyond what's ever been done before , so we're going to get to see some new particles very soon .	它會推動這個能量限制前七倍之多 , 超越之前所做過的事 , 所以我們很快就會看到一些新的粒子 。
but before talking about what we might see , let me describe the particles we already know of .	但在談我們可能看到的之前 , 讓我來描述一下我們已經知道的粒子 。
there's a whole zoo of subatomic particles .	有一大堆亞原子粒子的動物 。
most of us are familiar with electrons .	我們大多數人都熟悉電子 。
a lot of people in this room make a good living pushing them around .	在這間房間裡的許多人 , 讓他們生活良好 。
but the electron also has a neutral partner called the neutrino , with no electric charge and a very tiny mass .	但電子還有一個中立的夥伴 , 叫做中子 , 沒有電荷和非常小的質量 。
in contrast , the upanddown quarks have very large masses , and combine in threes to make the protons and neutrons inside atoms .	相較之下 , 上面的夸克有非常大的質量 , 三分之一的結合 , 來製造原子內的質子和中子 。
all of these matter particles come in left and righthanded varieties , and have antiparticle partners that carry opposite charges .	所有這些粒子都在左邊 , 右邊的多樣性 , 都有反粒子的伴侶帶著相反的載荷 。
these familiar particles also have less familiar second and third generations , which have the same charges as the first but have much higher masses .	這些熟悉的粒子也有較少熟悉的第二代和第三代 , 相同的載荷和第一代相同 , 但質量較高 。
these matter particles all interact with the various force particles .	這些粒子都與各種力粒子互動 。
the electromagnetic force interacts with electrically charged matter via particles called photons .	電磁力會透過光子所引電的粒子相互作用 。
there is also a very weak force called , rather unimaginatively , the weak force , that interacts only with lefthanded matter .	還有一種很弱的力量 , 很不想像力 , 很弱的力量 , 只和左撇子物質產生作用 。
the strong force acts between quarks which carry a different kind of charge , called color charge , and come in three different varieties: red , green and blue .	夸克之間有著不同的載荷 , 叫做色荷 , 三種不同種類的強力作用:紅、綠和藍 。
you can blame murray gellmann for these names they're his fault .	你可以責怪murraygellmann , 他們是他的錯 。
finally , there's the force of gravity , which interacts with matter via its mass and spin .	最後 , 重力會透過質量和旋轉來互動 。
the most important thing to understand here is that there's a different kind of charge associated with each of these forces .	最重要的是 , 每一股力量都有不同的載荷 。
these four different forces interact with matter according to the corresponding charges that each particle has .	這四種不同的力與物質相互作用 , 根據每個粒子都有相互應應變的載荷 。
a particle that hasn't been seen yet , but we're pretty sure exists , is the higgs particle , which gives masses to all these other particles .	一個尚未見過的粒子 , 但我們很確定存在 , 就是希格斯粒子 , 給予所有其他粒子的質量 。
the main purpose of the large hadron collider is to see this higgs particle , and we're almost certain it will .	大型強子對撞機的主要目的是要看到這個希格斯粒子 , 我們幾乎肯定它會發生 。
but the greatest mystery is what else we might see .	但最偉大的謎題是我們還能看到的 。
and i'm going to show you one beautiful possibility towards the end of this talk .	接下來我要向你們展示一個美好的可能性 , 來到這場演講的尾聲 。
now , if we count up all these different particles using their various spins and charges , there are 226 .	如果我們用不同的旋轉和載荷來計算這些不同的粒子 , 就會有226個 。
that's a lot of particles to keep track of .	那是很多粒子用來追蹤的 。
and it seems strange that nature would have so many elementary particles .	大自然有這麼多元素 , 似乎很奇怪 。
but if we plot them out according to their charges , some beautiful patterns emerge .	但如果我們根據他們的載荷來繪製它們 , 有些美麗的圖案會浮現出來 。
the most familiar charge is electric charge .	最熟悉的載荷是電荷 。
electrons have an electric charge , a negative one , and quarks have electric charges in thirds .	電子有電荷 , 負電 , 夸克有三分之一的電荷 。
so when two up quarks and a down quark are combined to make a proton , it has a total electric charge of plus one .	所以 , 當兩個夸克和一個夸克組合成一個質子時 , 它總有一電荷 。
these particles also have antiparticles , which have opposite charges .	這些粒子也有反粒子 , 有相反的載荷 。
now , it turns out the electric charge is actually a combination of two other charges: hypercharge and weak charge .	結果發現電荷是另外兩個載荷的組合:超載荷和弱荷 。
if we spread out the hypercharge and weak charge and plot the charges of particles in this twodimensional charge space , the electric charge is where these particles sit along the vertical direction .	如果我們把超級充電和弱荷散開 , 在這二度載荷空間中繪製出粒子的載荷 , 電荷就是這些粒子在垂直方向的位置 。
the electromagnetic and weak forces interact with matter according to their hypercharge and weak charge , which make this pattern .	電磁力和弱力會根據他們的超充荷和弱荷來互動 , 產生出這種模式 。
this is called the unified electroweak model , and it was put together back in 1967 .	這就是所謂的 「 電子發射模型 」 , 它在1967年被組合起來 。
the reason most of us are only familiar with electric charge and not both of these is because of the higgs particle .	我們大多數人只熟悉電荷 , 而不是兩者都是因為希格斯粒子 。
the higgs , over here on the left , has a large mass and breaks the symmetry of this electroweak pattern .	左邊這邊的希格斯有很大的質量 , 打破這個電路模式的對稱性 。
it makes the weak force very weak by giving the weak particles a large mass .	它讓弱力變弱 , 讓弱粒子的質量變大 。
since this massive higgs sits along the horizontal direction in this diagram , the photons of electromagnetism remain massless and interact with electric charge along the vertical direction in this charge space .	由於這個巨大的希格斯位於水平方向 , 電磁共振造影的光子仍然沒有質量 , 在這個載荷空間中與電荷的垂直方向產生作用 。
so the electromagnetic and weak forces are described by this pattern of particle charges in twodimensional space .	所以電磁力和弱力被這種粒子的模式所描述 , 在二維空間中 , 粒子載荷 。
we can include the strong force by spreading out its two charge directions and plotting the charges of the force particles in quarks along these directions .	我們能將強力推廣它的兩個載荷方向 , 並在這些方向上繪製出石英粒子的載荷 。
the charges of all known particles can be plotted in a fourdimensional charge space , and projected down to two dimensions like this so we can see them .	所有已知的粒子的載荷可以在四度載荷空間中繪製 , 投射到像這樣的二維空間 , 這樣我們就能看見它們 。
whenever particles interact , nature keeps things in a perfect balance along all four of these charge directions .	每當粒子相互作用 , 大自然就會保持完美的平衡 , 和這四個載荷方向的平衡 。
if a particle and an antiparticle collide , it creates a burst of energy and a total charge of zero in all four charge directions .	如果粒子和抗粒子碰撞 , 它會造成能量的爆炸 , 以及四個載荷方向的總載荷 。
at this point , anything can be created as long as it has the same energy and maintains a total charge of zero .	在這一刻 , 任何東西都可以被創造出來 , 只要它有相同的能量 , 維持零的總載荷 。
for example , this weak force particle and its antiparticle can be created in a collision .	例如 , 這種弱力粒子和它的反粒子可以在碰撞中產生 。
in further interactions , the charges must always balance .	在更進一步的互動中 , 指控總是平衡 。
one of the weak particles could decay into an electron and an antineutrino , and these three still add to zero total charge .	其中一個微小的粒子可以腐化成電子和一顆中子 , 這三個粒子依然加上0的總載荷 。
nature always keeps a perfect balance .	大自然總是保持完美的平衡 。
so these patterns of charges are not just pretty .	所以這些載荷的模式並不漂亮 。
they tell us what interactions are allowed to happen .	他們告訴我們 , 哪些互動是可以實現的 。
and we can rotate this charge space in four dimensions to get a better look at the strong interaction , which has this nice hexagonal symmetry .	我們可以把這個載荷空間轉換成四維空間 , 來更好地觀察強烈的相互作用 , 這種對稱性很好 。
in a strong interaction , a strong force particle , such as this one , interacts with a colored quark , such as this green one , to give a quark with a different color charge this red one .	在強烈的互動中 , 強力粒子 , 例如這一個 , 與有色的夸克互動 , 比如這個綠色夸克 , 用不同顏色的夸克給這個紅色 。
and strong interactions are happening millions of times each second in every atom of our bodies , holding the atomic nuclei together .	強烈的互動每秒鐘會發生數百萬次 , 以我們身體的每個原子組成 , 將原子核結合在一起 。
but these four charges corresponding to three forces are not the end of the story .	但這四個載荷對應到三種力量 , 不是故事的結尾 。
we can also include two more charges corresponding to the gravitational force .	我們還可以把兩個載荷和重力相對應 。
when we include these , each matter particle has two different spin charges , spinup and spindown .	當我們把這些粒子納入 , 每個粒子都有兩個不同的旋轉指控、旋轉和旋轉 。
so they all split , and give a nice pattern in sixdimensional charge space .	所以它們都分開 , 用六維載荷空間給一個好的圖案 。
we can rotate this pattern in six dimensions , and see that it's quite pretty .	我們可以在六維空間中旋轉這個模式 , 看到它是很漂亮的 。
right now , this pattern matches our best current knowledge of how nature is built at the tiny scales of these elementary particles .	目前 , 這個模式符合我們目前所知大自然如何在微小的微小粒子的結構 。
this is what we know for certain .	這是我們所知的 。
some of these particles are at the very limit of what we've been able to reach with experiments .	有些粒子是我們能用實驗來達到的極限 。
from this pattern , we already know the particle physics of these tiny scales . the way the universe works with these tiny scales is very beautiful .	從這個模式 , 我們已經知道這些微小的粒子物理學 。 宇宙和這些微小的尺度是非常漂亮的 。
but now i'm going to discuss some new and old ideas about things we don't know yet .	但現在我要來談談一些我們還不知道的新點子 。
we want to expand this pattern using mathematics alone , and see if we can get our hands on the whole enchilada .	我們想單靠數學來拓展這個模式 , 看看我們能否掌握整個enchilada 。
we want to find all the particles and forces that make a complete picture of our universe .	我們想找到所有能創造出完整宇宙的粒子和力量 。
and we want to use this picture to predict new particles that we'll see when experiments reach higher energies .	我們想用這張照片來預測新的粒子 , 我們會看到實驗能達到更高的能量 。
so there's an old idea in particle physics that this known pattern of charges , which is not very symmetric , could emerge from a more perfect pattern that gets broken similar to how the higgs particle breaks the electroweak pattern to give electromagnetism .	粒子物理學有一個古老的想法 , 這種已知的載荷模式 , 不對稱 , 可以從一個更完美的模式中產生出來 , 和希格斯粒子打破電路模式 , 來產生電磁力 。
in order to do this , we need to introduce new forces with new charge directions .	為了做到這一點 , 我們需要引進新的載荷方向 。
when we introduce a new direction , we get to guess what charges the particles have along this direction , and then we can rotate it in with the others .	當我們引進一個新的方向時 , 我們會猜測粒子沿著這個方向負責什麼 , 然後我們可以把它旋轉 。
if we guess wisely , we can construct the standard charges in six charge dimensions as a broken symmetry of this more perfect pattern in seven charge dimensions .	如果我們明智地猜測 , 我們就能在六個載荷空間中建構出標準載荷的對稱性 , 這是七個載荷空間中更完美的圖案 。
this particular choice corresponds to a grand unified theory introduced by pati and salam in 1973 .	在1973年 , 帕蒂和薩拉姆所提出的這個特殊選擇 。
when we look at this new unified pattern , we can see a couple of gaps where particles seem to be missing .	當我們觀察這個新的統一模式時 , 我們可以看到一些缺口 , 粒子似乎是缺少的 。
this is the way theories of unification work .	這是統一理論的運作方式 。
a physicist looks for larger , more symmetric patterns that include the established pattern as a subset .	物理學家尋找更大、更對稱的圖案 , 包含了其特定的圖案 , 以其為單位 。
the larger pattern allows us to predict the existence of particles that have never been seen .	更大的模式讓我們能夠預測那些從未見過的粒子存在 。
this unification model predicts the existence of these two new force particles , which should act a lot like the weak force , only weaker .	這個統一模型預測了這兩個新粒子的存在 , 它應該像弱力一樣 , 只是弱力 。
now we can rotate this set of charges in seven dimensions and consider an odd fact about the matter particles: the second and third generations of matter have exactly the same charges in sixdimensional charge space as the first generation .	我們現在可以在七維空間中旋轉這個載荷 , 思考一個奇怪的事實:第二代和第三代物質在六維載荷空間中有完全相同的載荷 。
these particles are not uniquely identified by their six charges .	這些粒子並非獨一無二的被六個載荷所辨識出來 。
they sit on top of one another in the standard charge space .	他們坐在標準載荷空間的頂端 。
however , if we work in eightdimensional charge space , then we can assign unique new charges to each particle .	然而 , 如果我們在八度載荷空間中工作 , 我們就能將不同的新載荷給每顆粒子 。
then we can spin these in eight dimensions , and see what the whole pattern looks like .	然後我們可以在八度空間中轉動 , 看看整個圖案是什麼樣子 。
here we can see the second and third generations of matter now related to the first generation by a symmetry called " triality . "	在這裡 , 我們可以看到第二和第三代物質的相關性 , 由所謂的 「 審判 」 的對稱性 。
this particular pattern of charges in eight dimensions is actually part of the most beautiful geometric structure in mathematics .	這種八維的載荷模式實際上是數學中最美麗的幾何結構之一 。
it's a pattern of the largest exceptional lie group , e8 .	它是最大例外謊言團體的模式e8 。
this lie group is a smooth , curved shape with 248 dimensions .	這個謊言團體是平滑的 , 曲線形狀有248維度 。
each point in this pattern corresponds to a symmetry of this very complex and beautiful shape .	在這個圖案中的每個點 , 都會對應到這個非常複雜且美麗的形狀 。
one small part of this e8 shape can be used to describe the curved spacetime of einstein's general relativity , explaining gravity .	這個e8形狀的一小部分可以用來描述愛因斯坦廣義相對論的曲線時空 , 解釋重力 。
together with quantum mechanics , the geometry of this shape could describe everything about how the universe works at the tiniest scales .	用量子力學 , 形狀的幾何學可以描述宇宙是如何在最小的尺度中運作的 。
the pattern of this shape living in eightdimensional charge space is exquisitely beautiful , and it summarizes thousands of possible interactions between these elementary particles , each of which is just a facet of this complicated shape .	在八度載荷空間中 , 這種形狀的圖案是非常美麗的 , 它總結了數千種可能的相互作用 , 每一個都只是這複雜的形狀的一面 。
as we spin it , we can see many of the other intricate patterns contained in this one .	隨著我們旋轉 , 我們可以看到許多其它複雜的圖案在這個圖案中存在著 。
and with a particular rotation , we can look down through this pattern in eight dimensions along a symmetry axis and see all the particles at once .	有了特定的旋轉 , 我們就可以在八度空間中觀察這個圖案 , 沿著對稱軸沿著對稱軸沿著一個對稱軸 , 同時看到所有的粒子 。
it's a very beautiful object , and as with any unification , we can see some holes where new particles are required by this pattern .	它是一個非常美麗的物體 , 如同任何統一 , 我們可以看到一些洞 , 在那裡 , 新的粒子被這個模式所需要 。
there are 20 gaps where new particles should be , two of which have been filled by the patisalam particles .	有20個缺口 , 新的粒子應該是 , 其中兩個被帕塔瓦粒子填滿 。
from their location in this pattern , we know that these new particles should be scalar fields like the higgs particle , but have color charge and interact with the strong force .	從這個模式的位置 , 我們知道這些新的粒子應該會像希格斯粒子一樣大 , 但有顏色載荷 , 和強力互動 。
filling in these new particles completes this pattern , giving us the full e8 .	填入這些新的粒子 , 完成了這個模式 , 給我們全e8 。
this e8 pattern has very deep mathematical roots .	這個e8圖案有很深的數學根源 。
it's considered by many to be the most beautiful structure in mathematics .	它被許多人認為是數學中最美麗的結構 。
it's a fantastic prospect that this object of great mathematical beauty could describe the truth of particle interactions at the smallest scales imaginable .	這是個很棒的前景 , 這個偉大的數學美的物體可以描述在最小的尺度中粒子互動的真相 。
and this idea that nature is described by mathematics is not at all new .	這個想法是 , 大自然被數學所描述的 , 完全不是新的 。
in 1623 , galileo wrote this: " nature's grand book , which stands continually open to our gaze , is written in the language of mathematics .	在1623年 , 伽利略寫了這句話: 「 大自然的偉大書籍 , 持續地對我們的觀測敞開眼界 , 用數學的語言寫信 。
its characters are triangles , circles and other geometrical figures , without which it is humanly impossible to understand a single word of it ; without these , one is wandering around in a dark labyrinth . "	它的角色是三角形、圓形和其他幾何圖形 , 沒有任何一個字 , 可以理解它是不可能的 ; 沒有這些 , 一個在黑暗的迷宮中四處遊蕩 。 」
i believe this to be true , and i've tried to follow galileo's guidance in describing the mathematics of particle physics using only triangles , circles and other geometrical figures .	我相信這是真的 , 我試著遵循伽利略的指導 , 描述粒子物理的數學 , 只用三角形、圓形和其他幾何數字 。
of course , when other physicists and i actually work on this stuff , the mathematics can resemble a dark labyrinth .	當然 , 當我和其他物理學家一起研究這些東西時 , 數學可以像黑暗的迷宮一樣 。
but it's reassuring that at the heart of this mathematics is pure , beautiful geometry .	但 , 值得一提的是 , 數學的核心是純粹、美麗的幾何學 。
joined with quantum mechanics , this mathematics describes our universe as a growing e8 coral , with particles interacting at every location in all possible ways according to a beautiful pattern .	與量子力學結合 , 這個數學將我們的宇宙描述為一個不斷成長的e8珊瑚 , 粒子以各種可能的方式來互動 。
and as more of the pattern comes into view using new machines like the large hadron collider , we may be able to see whether nature uses this e8 pattern or a different one .	隨著更多的圖案出現 , 使用像大型強子對撞機的新機器 , 我們可能會看到大自然使用這個e8的圖案或另一個圖案 。
this process of discovery is a wonderful adventure to be involved in .	這個發現的過程是很棒的冒險旅程 。
if the lhc finds particles that fit this e8 pattern , that will be very , very cool .	如果lhc找到符合e8圖案的粒子 , 那就很酷了 。
if the lhc finds new particles , but they don't fit this pattern well , that will be very interesting , but bad for this e8 theory .	如果lhc能找到新的粒子 , 但它們不符合這個模式 , 那會很有趣 , 但對e8理論不好 。
and , of course , bad for me personally .	當然 , 對我來說是不好的 。
now how bad would that be ?	那會有多糟 ?
well , pretty bad .	嗯 , 相當糟糕 。
but predicting how nature works is a very risky game .	但預測大自然是如何運作的 。
this theory and others like it are long shots .	這個理論和其他類似的理論是長時間拍攝 。
one does a lot of hard work knowing that most of these ideas probably won't end up being true about nature .	一個人做了很多辛苦的工作 , 知道大部分這些想法可能不會成為大自然的真相 。
that's what doing theoretical physics is like: there are a lot of wipeouts .	理論物理就是這樣運作的:有很多的擦力 。
in this regard , new physics theories are a lot like startup companies .	在這方面 , 新的物理理論就像新創公司一樣 。
as with any large investment , it can be emotionally difficult to abandon a line of research when it isn't working out .	就像任何大型的投資一樣 , 在沒有成功的情況下 , 要放棄一系列的研究 。
but in science , if something isn't working , you have to toss it out and try something else .	但在科學上 , 如果有東西行不通 , 你就得要把它弄出來 , 嘗試其他東西 。
now , the only way to maintain sanity and achieve happiness in the midst of this uncertainty is to keep balance and perspective in life .	唯一能維持公平和獲得幸福的方法 , 就是保持生活的平衡和觀點 。
i've tried the best i can to live a balanced life .	我嘗試過我能活得平衡的生活 。
i try to balance my life equally between physics , love and surfing my own three charge directions .	我試著平衡我的生活 , 平衡物理、愛、衝浪我自己的三個載荷方向 。
this way , even if the physics i work on comes to nothing , i still know i've lived a good life .	這樣一來 , 就算我所研究的物理都沒有 , 我仍然知道我過著美好的生活 。
and i try to live in beautiful places .	我試著生活在美麗的地方 。
for most of the past ten years i've lived on the island of maui , a very beautiful place .	過去十年來 , 我在馬伊島住的大部分地方 , 一個非常美麗的地方 。
now it's one of the greatest mysteries in the universe to my parents how i managed to survive all that time without engaging in anything resembling fulltime employment .	這是我父母在宇宙中最偉大的謎題之一 , 我是如何在沒有全職員工的情況下存活下來的 。
i'm going to let you in on that secret .	接下來我要告訴你們這個秘密 。
this was a view from my home office on maui .	這是我在maui家的辦公室的景象 。
and you may have noticed that these beautiful views are similar , but in slightly different places .	你可能注意到這些美麗的觀點相似 , 但在不同的地方 。
that's because this used to be my home and office on maui .	那是因為這曾經是我在毛伊島的家和辦公室 。
i've chosen a very unusual life .	我選擇了一件非常不尋常的人生 。
but not worrying about rent allowed me to spend my time doing what i love .	但不用擔心房租 , 讓我花時間做我愛的事 。
living a nomadic existence has been hard at times , but it's allowed me to live in beautiful places and keep a balance in my life that i've been happy with .	生活在一個遊牧的時代是很艱辛的 , 但它讓我生活在美麗的地方 , 保持平衡 , 在我的生活中 , 我一直很高興 。
it allows me to spend a lot of my time hanging out with hyperintelligent coral .	它讓我花很多時間和超級智慧的珊瑚在一起 。
but i also greatly enjoy the company of hyperintelligent people .	但我也很享受超級聰明的人的公司 。
so i'm very happy to have been invited here to ted .	我很高興能被邀請來ted 。
chris anderson: i probably understood two percent of that , but i still absolutely loved it . so i'm going to sound dumb .	克里斯•安德森:我大概明白其中的百分之二 , 但我仍然很愛它 。 所以我要聽起來很蠢 。
your theory of everything garrett lisi: i'm used to coral .	你的理論是garrettlisi:我習慣珊瑚 。
ca: that's right . the reason it's got a few people at least excited is because , if you're right , it brings gravity and quantum theory together .	克里斯:沒錯 , 讓少數人感到興奮的原因是 , 如果你是對的 , 它會把重力和量子理論結合在一起 。
so are you saying that we should think of the universe , at its heart that the smallest things that there are , are somehow an e8 object of possibility ?	所以 , 你是說 , 我們應該想一想宇宙 , 心中有最小的東西 , 像是e8物體的可能性 ?
i mean , is there a scale to it , at the smallest scale , or . . . ?	我的意思是 , 在最小的尺度 , 還是...
gl: well , right now the pattern i showed you that corresponds to what we know about elementary particle physics that already corresponds to a very beautiful shape .	格林:嗯 , 現在我給你們看的圖案和我們所知的基本粒子物理學有關 , 已經對應到一個非常美麗的形狀 。
and that's the one that i said we knew for certain .	那就是我說我們知道的 。
and that shape has remarkable similarities and the way it fits into this e8 pattern could be the rest of the picture .	這種形狀有著驚人的相似性 , 和它融入這個e8圖案的方式 , 可能是圖片的其他部分 。
and these patterns of points that i've shown for you actually represent symmetries of this highdimensional object that would be warping and moving and dancing over the space time that we experience .	我給你們看的這些點 , 其實代表的是這個高維物體的對稱性 , 它會在我們經歷的時空中移動、跳舞和跳舞 。
and that would be what explains all these elementary particles that we see .	這就解釋了我們所看到的所有基本粒子 。
ca: but a string theorist , as i understand it , explains electrons in terms of much smaller strings vibrating i know you don't like string theory vibrating inside it .	克:但弦理論家 , 我了解它 , 用更小的弦震動來解釋電子 , 我知道你不喜歡弦理論在裡面震動 。
how should we think of an electron in relation to e8 ?	我們該如何把電子想成e8 ?
gl: no , it would be one of the symmetries of this e8 shape .	格林:不 , 它是這個e8形狀的一種對稱之一 。
so what's happening is , as the shape is moving over spacetime , it's twisting . and the direction it's twisting as it moves is what particle we see . so it would be ca: the size of the e8 shape , how does that relate to the electron ?	所以 , 當這個形狀在時空中移動時 , 它是扭曲的 。 當它移動時 , 它的方向是扭曲的 。 它會是:e8形狀的大小 , 和電子是如何連結在一起的 ?
i kind of feel like i need that for my picture .	我覺得我需要這張照片 。
is it bigger ? is it smaller ?	更大嗎 ? 更小嗎 ?
gl: well , as far as we know electrons are point particles , so this would be going down to the smallest possible scales .	格林:我們所知的電子是指點粒子 , 所以這將會是最小的可能尺度 。
so the way these things are explained in quantum field theory is , all possibilities are expanding and developing at once .	所以 , 這些東西在量子場理論中解釋的方式是 , 所有可能性都同時擴張和發展 。
and this is why i use the analogy to coral .	這就是為什麼我用比喻珊瑚 。
and in this way , the way that e8 comes in is it will be as a shape that's attached at each point in spacetime .	用這種方式 , e8進來的方式是它的形狀 , 在時空中每一刻都依附在一個形狀 。
and , as i said , the way the shape twists the directional along which way the shape is twisting as it moves over this curved surface is what the elementary particles are , themselves .	如我所說 , 形狀的方向會在曲線的表面上移動時 , 形狀會轉動的方向 , 正是小粒子本身 。
so through quantum field theory , they manifest themselves as points and interact that way .	所以 , 透過量子場理論 , 他們把自己看作點 , 並以這種方式互動 。
i don't know if i'll be able to make this any clearer .	我不知道我能否更明確地做這件事 。
ca: it doesn't really matter .	克里斯:這並不重要 。
it's evoking a kind of sense of wonder , and i certainly want to understand more of this .	它喚起了一種奇妙的感覺 , 我當然也想了解更多 。
but thank you so much for coming . that was absolutely fascinating .	但 , 非常謝謝你來 。 這絕對是非常吸引人的 。
the legendary chimpanzee researcher jane goodall talks about tacare and her other community projects , which help people in booming african towns live sidebyside with threatened animals .	傳奇的黑猩猩研究員傑內.古爾談到坦尚及其它社區計畫 , 協助波普非洲市居住的居民 , 威脅到動物 。
africa , animals , biodiversity , environment , global issues , pollution , primates , science	非洲、動物、生物多樣性、環境、全球議題、污染、靈長類、科學、科學、科學、科學等問題 。
jane goodall helps humans and animals live together	珍古德能協助人類和動物一起生活 。
good afternoon , good evening , whatever .	午安 , 晚安 , 等等 。
we can go , jambo , guten abend , bonsoir , but we can also ooh , ooh , ooh , ooh , ooh , ooh , ooh , ooh , ooh .	我們能去 , 喔 , 喔 , 喔 , ~ ~ ~ ~ ~ ~ 噢 , 噢 , 噢 , 噢 , 噢 , 噢 , 噢 , 噢 , 噢 , 噢 , 噢 。
that is the call that chimpanzees make before they go to sleep in the evening .	這就是黑猩猩在晚上睡覺前的叫聲 。
you hear it going from one side of the valley to the other , from one group of nests to the next .	你聽到它從山谷的一邊移動到另一邊 , 從一群巢穴到下一邊 。
and i want to pick up with my talk this evening from where zeray left off yesterday .	今天晚上我要跟大家談談 , 是昨天的zeray留下來的地方 。
he was talking about this amazing , threeyearold australopithecine child , selam .	他談到這個驚人、三歲的幼兒 , 塞拉姆 。
and we've also been hearing about the history , the family tree , of mankind through dna genetic profiling .	我們也聽過關於歷史、家庭樹、人類基因改造的歷史 。
and it was a paleontologist , the late louis leakey , who actually set me on the path for studying chimpanzees .	這是古生物學家 , 最近的路易斯•路易斯•路克 , 他讓我走上了研究黑猩猩的路上 。
and it was pretty extraordinary , way back then .	當時是非常了不起的 。
it's kind of commonplace now , but his argument was because he'd been searching for the fossilized remains of early humans in africa .	現在有點常見 , 但他的論點是 , 因為他一直在尋找非洲早期人類的化石 。
and you can tell an awful lot about what those beings looked like from the fossils , from the shape of the muscle attachments , something about the way they lived from the various artifacts found with them .	你可以看到這些生物的樣子 , 從化石的形狀 , 從肌肉的形狀 , 和它們的生存方式有關 。
but what about how they behaved ? that's what he wanted to know .	但他們如何表現呢 ? 這是他想知道的 。
and of course , behavior doesn't fossilize .	當然 , 行為不會化石 。
he argued and it's now a fairly common theory that if we found behavior patterns similar or the same in our closest living relatives , the great apes , and humans today , then maybe those behaviors were present in the apelike , humanlike ancestor some seven million years ago .	他主張 , 現在是個相當常見的理論 , 如果我們在最接近的物種身上找到類似的行為模式 , 大猩猩 , 和人類身上的行為 , 大約七百萬年前 , 人類的祖先 。
and therefore , perhaps we had brought those characteristics with us from that ancient , ancient past .	因此 , 也許我們已經把這些特性帶到古代 , 古老的過去 。
well , if you look in textbooks today that deal with human evolution , you very often find people speculating about how early humans may have behaved , based on the behavior of chimpanzees .	嗯 , 假如你去看今天正在處理人類演化的教科書 , 你經常會看到人們在推測早期人類的行為 , 根據黑猩猩的行為 。
they are more like us than any other living creature , and we've heard about that during this ted conference .	它們比我們任何其他生物都更像我們 , 在ted會議中 , 我們已經聽說過了 。
so it remains for me to comment on the ways in which chimpanzees are so like us , in certain aspects of their behavior .	所以 , 對我來說 , 對於黑猩猩和我們來說 , 黑猩猩在某些方面是如此相似的 。
every chimpanzee has his or her own personality .	每個黑猩猩都有自己的性格 。
of course , i gave them names . they can live to be 60 years or more , although we think most of them probably don't make it to 60 in the wild .	當然 , 我會給他們名字 。 他們可以活到60年或更久 , 不過我們認為大部分的人可能不會在野外60歲 。
mr . wurzel . the female has her first baby when she's 11 or 12 .	沃茲爾先生 。 女性生了她十一或十二歲時的第一個嬰兒 。
thereafter , she has one baby only every five or six years , a long period of childhood dependency when the child is nursing , sleeping with the mother at night , and riding on her back .	在那裡 , 她每五、六年就有一個嬰兒 , 一個長期的童年依賴期 , 當孩子在護理時 , 晚上和母親一起睡覺 , 背上騎著 。
and we believe that this long period of childhood is important for chimpanzees , just as it is for us , in relation to learning .	我們相信這段長期的童年對黑猩猩來說是很重要的 , 就如同對我們來說 , 與學習有關 。
as the brain becomes ever more complex during evolution in different forms of animals , so we find that learning plays an ever more important role in an individual's life history .	隨著大腦在不同的動物演化過程中變得更複雜 , 所以我們發現學習在個人生命歷史中扮演著更重要的角色 。
and young chimpanzees spend a lot of time watching what their elders do .	年輕的黑猩猩花了很多時間觀察他們的長者的做法 。
we know now that they're capable of imitating behaviors that they see .	我們現在知道他們能夠模仿他們所看到的行為 。
and we believe that it's in this way that the different toolusing behaviors that have now been seen in all the different chimpanzee populations studied in africa how these are passed from one generation to the next , through observation , imitation and practice , so that we can describe these toolusing behaviors as primitive culture .	我們相信它是以這種方式 , 目前在非洲各個不同黑猩猩族群中所看到的不同的隔閡行為是如何從一個世代傳到下一個世代 , 透過觀察、模仿和練習 , 來形容這些獨立的行為為原始文化 。
chimpanzees don't have a spoken language . we've talked about that .	黑猩猩沒有口語 。 我們已經談到這個了 。
they do have a very rich repertoire of postures and gestures , many of which are similar , or even identical , to ours and formed in the same context . greeting chimpanzees embracing .	它們的確有非常豐富的姿勢和姿勢 , 許多都很相似 , 甚至相同的 , 在同一個背景下形成 , 希臘的黑猩猩擁抱著 。
they also kiss , hold hands , pat one another on the back .	他們也會親吻、握手、拍手 , 背後的另一隻 。
and they swagger and they throw rocks .	牠們會變大 , 會扔石頭 。
in chimpanzee society , we find many , many examples of compassion , precursors to love and true altruism .	在黑猩猩社會中 , 我們發現許多許多關於同情心的例子 , 愛和真正的利他主義 。
unfortunately , they , like us , have a dark side to their nature .	不幸的是 , 他們和我們一樣 , 對他們的天性很黑暗 。
they're capable of extreme brutality , even a kind of primitive war .	他們有能力極度殘酷 , 甚至是一種原始的戰爭 。
and these really aggressive behaviors , for the most part , are directed against individuals of the neighboring social group .	這些非常積極的行為 , 大部分的情況下 , 都被指導要對抗鄰近社會群體的個體 。
they are very territorially aggressive .	它們是非常具侵略性的 。
chimpanzees , i believe , more than any other living creature , have helped us to understand that , after all , there is no sharp line between humans and the rest of the animal kingdom .	我相信 , 比任何其他生物都更能幫助我們了解 , 畢竟 , 人類和其他動物界之間沒有明顯的界線 。
it's a very blurry line , and it's getting more blurry all the time as we make even more observations .	這是一條非常模糊的線 , 每當我們看到更多的觀察時 , 都會越來越模糊 。
the study that i began in 1960 is still continuing to this day .	我從1960年開始的研究至今仍然持續著 。
and these chimpanzees , living their complex social lives in the wild , have helped more than anything else to make us realize we are part of , and not separated from , the amazing animals with whom we share the planet .	而這些黑猩猩 , 活在野外複雜的社交生活 , 幫助我們了解到我們是其中的一部分 , 而不是和我們共有的偉大的動物 。
so it's pretty sad to find that chimpanzees , like so many other creatures around the world , are losing their habitats .	所以 , 要找到黑猩猩 , 和世界上許多其他生物一樣 , 會失去牠們的棲息地 。
this is just one photograph from the air , and it shows you the forested highlands of gombe .	這只是一張空氣拍攝的照片 , 這張照片顯示了戈米貝的森林高地 。
and it was when i flew over the whole area , about 16 years ago , and realized that outside the park , this forest , which in 1960 had stretched almost unbroken along the eastern shore of lake tanganyika , which is where the tiny , 30squaremile gombe national park lies , that a question came to my mind .	大約16年前 , 我飛越整個區域 , 發現在公園之外 , 這片森林在1960年 , 在坦尼卡的東岸 , 幾乎沒有破裂 , 在那裡 , 三十平方的戈米貝國家公園就在我腦海中浮現一個問題 。
" how can we even try to save these famous chimpanzees , when the people living around the national park are struggling to survive ? "	「 我們要如何拯救這些有名的黑猩猩 ? 當住在全國公園的人們掙扎生存 ? 」
more people are living there than the land could possibly support .	更多人住在那裏 , 比土地還多 。
the numbers increased by refugees pouring in from burundi and over the lake from congo .	難民湧入緬甸的數量增加了 , 從剛果的湖中湧入的數量 。
and very poor people they couldn't afford to buy food from elsewhere .	非常貧窮的人 , 他們負擔不起從其他地方買食物 。
this led to a program , which we call tacare .	這就導致了一項計畫 , 我們稱之為 「 坦尚尼亞 」 。
it's a very holistic way of improving the lives of the people living in the villages around the park .	這是一種非常全面的改善居住在公園裡的人們的生活方式 。
it started small with 12 villages . it's now in 24 .	從12個村落開始 , 現在是24個村落 。
there isn't time to go into it , but it's including things like tree nurseries , methods of farming most suitable to this now very degraded , almost desertlike land up in these mountains .	沒有時間考慮它 , 包括樹木護士、農業方法 , 最適合目前在這些山脈下降 , 幾乎沙漠地面積在這些山脈上 。
ways of controlling , preventing soil erosion .	控制、預防土壤侵蝕的方式 。
ways of reclaiming overused farmland , so that within two years they can again be productive .	重建過度使用的農田 , 這樣一來 , 兩年內 , 他們再次有生產力 。
working to help the villagers obtain fresh water from wells .	致力於協助村民取得新鮮的水源 。
perhaps build some schoolrooms .	也許建造一些學校室 。
most important of all , i believe , is working with small groups of women , providing them with opportunities for microcredit loans .	最重要的是 , 我相信 , 和一小群婦女合作 , 提供他們機會給微型貸款給他們 。
and we've got , as is the case around the world , about 95 percent of all loans returned .	而我們有的 , 正如世界各地 , 大約有95%的貸款回來 。
empowering women , working with education , providing scholarships for girls so they can finish secondary school , in the clear understanding that , all around the world , as women's education improves , family size drops .	賦予女性權力 , 和教育合作 , 提供獎學金給女孩 , 讓他們能完成中學 , 明確地了解全世界 , 身為女性教育改善家庭大小 。
we provide information about family planning and about hiv/aids .	我們提供家庭規劃和愛滋病的資訊 。
and as a result of this program , something's happening for conservation .	由於這個計劃的結果 , 保育的發展 。
what's happening for conservation is that the farmers living in these 24 villages , instead of looking on us as a bunch of white people coming to study a whole bunch of monkeys and by the way , many of the staff are now tanzanian but when we began the tacare program , it was a tanzanian team going into the villages .	保育的原因是 , 居住在這24個村落的農民 , 而不是把我們當成一群白人來研究一群猴子 , 順帶一提 , 很多是坦尚尼亞人 , 但當我們開始計程時 , 一個坦尚尼亞的團隊進入村落 。
it was a tanzanian team talking to the villagers , asking what they were interested in .	那是坦尚尼亞的團隊 , 和村民談話 , 問他們對什麼有興趣 。
were they interested in conservation ? absolutely not .	他們對保育感興趣嗎 ? 絕對不是 。
they were interested in health ; they were interested in education .	他們對健康有興趣 , 他們對教育有興趣 。
and as time went on , and as their situation began to improve , they began to understand ever more about the need for conservation .	隨著時間過去 , 當他們的情況開始改善 , 他們開始了解保育的必要性 。
they began to understand that as the upper levels of the hills were denuded of trees , so you've got this terrible soil erosion and mudslides .	他們開始了解 , 隨著山丘的上層被砍伐 , 所以你就有了這種可怕的土壤侵蝕和泥土 。
today , we are developing what we call the greater gombe ecosystem .	今天 , 我們正在開發我們所謂的更大的戈米貝生態系統 。
this is an area way outside the national park , stretching out into all these very degraded lands .	這是國家公園之外的一個區域 , 延伸到各個非常退化的土地上 。
and as these villages have a better standard of life , they are actually agreeing to put between 10 percent and 20 percent of their land in the highlands aside , so that once again , as the trees grow back , the chimpanzees will have leafy corridors through which they can travel to interact as they must for genetic viability with other remnant groups outside the national park .	當這些村落有更好的生活水準時 , 他們實際上同意把土地的10%到20% , 在高地旁邊 , 再一次 , 當樹木長回來 , 黑猩猩會穿過這些樹葉走廊 , 牠們可以在國家公園以外的遺傳性與其它的遺傳性交流 。
so tacare is a success .	所以 , 坦誠是成功的 。
we're replicating it in other parts of africa , around other wilderness areas which are faced with extreme population pressure .	我們在非洲其他地方複製它 , 在其他地方 , 面對極端人口壓力 。
the problems in africa , however , as we've been discussing for the whole of these first couple of days of ted , are major problems .	然而 , 非洲的問題 , 正如我們過去幾天來在ted討論的一樣 , 都是重大的問題 。
there is a great deal of poverty .	有很大的貧窮 。
and when you get large numbers of people living in land that is not that fertile , particularly when you cut down trees , and you leave the soil open to the wind for erosion , as desperate populations cut down more and more trees , so that they can try and grow food for themselves and their families , what's going to happen ? something's got to give .	而當你有大量的居住地 , 不那麼肥沃 , 尤其是當你砍樹的時候 , 你就把土壤打開 , 讓土壤被摧毀 , 因為絕望的人口減少了更多的樹木 , 所以他們可以為自己和家人種食物 , 有什麼事會發生 ?
and the other problems in not only africa , but the rest of the developing world and , indeed , everywhere what are we doing to our planet ?	而其他的問題不只在非洲 , 還在開發中國家 , 的確 , 無所不在 , 我們對地球做了什麼 ?
you know , the famous scientist , e . o . wilson said that if every person on this planet attains the standard of living of the average european or american , we need three new planets .	你知道 , 著名的科學家艾.威爾森說如果地球上的每一個人都能維持一般歐洲人或美國人的平均生活水準 , 我們需要三個新的星球 。
today , they are saying four . but we don't have them . we've got one .	今天 , 他們說四個 , 但我們沒有 。 我們有一個 。
and what's happened ? i mean , the question here is , here we are , arguably the most intelligent being that's ever walked planet earth , with this extraordinary brain , capable of the kind of technology that is so well illustrated by these ted conferences , and yet we're destroying the only home we have .	到底發生了什麼事 ? 我的意思是 , 問題是 , 在這裡 , 我們是最有智慧的 , 地球行走的地球 , 擁有這種非凡的大腦 , 能夠被這些ted會議所描繪出來的科技 , 然而我們卻在摧毀我們唯一的家園 。
the indigenous people around the world , before they made a major decision , used to sit around and ask themselves , " how does this decision affect our people seven generations ahead ? "	世界各地的原住民 , 在他們做了重大決策之前 , 習慣自己坐下來問自己: 「 這個決策會如何影響我們七個世代的人 ? 」
today , major decisions and i'm not particularly talking about africa here , but the developed world major decisions involving millions of dollars , and millions of people , are often based on , " how will this affect the next shareholders' meeting ? "	今天 , 主要的決策 , 我不是特別談非洲 , 而是已開發國家的重大決策 , 來自數百萬人 , 通常都是基於 「 下一個股東會議如何影響下一個股東會議 ? 」
and these decisions affect africa .	這些決策會影響非洲 。
as i began traveling around africa talking about the problems faced by chimpanzees and their vanishing forests , i realized more and more how so many of africa's problems could be laid at the door of previous colonial exploitation .	當我開始在非洲四處旅行 , 談到黑猩猩和森林面臨的問題時 , 我了解到更多 , 更多非洲的問題可以被限制在過去殖民地開發的大門 。
so i began traveling outside africa , talking in europe , talking in the united states , going to asia .	所以我開始在非洲外面旅行 , 在歐洲聊天 , 在美國聊天 , 去亞洲 。
and everywhere there were these terrible problems .	到處都有這些可怕的問題 。
and you know the kind i'm talking about . i'm talking about pollution .	你知道我所說的那種 , 我在談污染 。
the air that we breathe that often poisons us .	我們常呼吸的空氣會毒害我們 。
the earth is poisoning our foods .	地球正在毒害我們的食物 。
the water water is perhaps one of the most crucial issues that we're going to face in this century and everywhere water is being polluted by agricultural , industrial and household chemicals that still are being sprayed around the world , seemingly with the inability to profit from past experience .	水源也許是我們這個世紀所要面對的最關鍵問題之一 , 到處都是水污染 , 被農業、工業和家庭的化學物質所污染 , 這些化學物質仍然在世界各地噴灑 , 似乎無法從過去的經驗中獲利 。
the mangroves are being cut down ; the effects of things like the tsunami get worse .	紅樹林被砍伐 , 海嘯的影響會更糟 。
we've talked about the soil erosion .	我們已經談過土壤的侵蝕 。
we have the reckless burning of fossil fuels along with other greenhouse gasses , so called , leading to climate change .	我們有不可思議的燃燒化石燃料 , 和其他溫室氣體一起燃燒 , 稱為氣候變遷 。
finally , all around the world , people have begun to believe that there is something going on very wrong with our climate .	最後 , 全世界的人們開始相信氣候變遷發生了一些問題 。
all around the world climates are mixed up .	全世界的氣候都混合在一起 。
and it's the poor people who are affected worse .	那些被影響更糟的窮人
it's africa that already is affected .	非洲已經受到影響了 。
in many parts of subsaharan africa , the droughts are so much worse .	在撒哈拉以南非洲的許多地區 , 乾旱更糟 。
and when the rain does come , it so often leads to flooding and added distress , and the cycle of poverty and hunger and disease .	當雨來臨時 , 常常會造成洪水 , 加上煩惱 , 以及貧窮、飢餓和疾病的循環 。
and the numbers of people living in an area that the land cannot support , who are too poor to buy food , who can't move away because the whole land is degraded .	住在這個地區的人們無法支援 , 他們太貧窮 , 無法購買食物 , 因為整片土地已經退化了 。
and so you get desertification creeping , creeping , creeping as the last of the trees are cut down .	所以你會得到沙漠化的珊瑚礁 , 如樹的最後一棵樹被砍了下來 。
and this kind of thing is not just in africa . it's all over the world .	這種東西並不只是在非洲 , 全世界都是如此 。
so it wasn't surprising to me that as i was traveling around the world i met so many young people who seemed to have lost hope .	所以 , 我並不意外 , 當我在世界各地旅行時 , 我遇到許多年輕人似乎失去了希望 。
we seem to have lost wisdom , the wisdom of the indigenous people .	我們似乎失去了智慧 , 原住民的智慧 。
i asked a question . " why ? "	我問了一個問題: 「 為什麼 ? 」
well , do you think there could be some kind of disconnect between this extraordinarily clever brain , the kind of brain that the ted technologies exemplify , and the human heart ? talking about it in the nonscientific term , in terms of love and compassion . is there some disconnect ?	嗯 , 你認為這種非凡聰明的大腦之間可能有某種區別嗎 ? 這種大腦是ted科技的絕種 , 而人類的心呢 ? 以非科學的角度來說 , 在愛和同情的角度來說 , 有沒有其他的連結 ?
and these young people , when i talk to them , basically they were either depressed or apathetic , or bitter and angry . and they said more or less the same thing , " we feel this way because we feel you've compromised our future and there's nothing we can do about it . "	而這些年輕人 , 當我和他們談話時 , 基本上他們是憂鬱或厭惡感 , 或厭惡感和憤怒 。 他們說了更多的話: 「 我們會這樣感覺 , 因為我們覺得你已經妥協了我們的未來 , 我們什麼都沒做 。 」
we have compromised their future .	我們有妥協他們的未來 。
i've got three little grandchildren , and every time i look at them and i think how we've harmed this beautiful planet since i was their age , i feel this desperation .	我有三位孫子 , 每次我看著他們 , 我就會想我們如何傷害這個美麗的星球 , 從我年紀開始 , 我就感到絕望 。
and that led to this program we call roots and shoots , which began right here in tanzania and has now spread to 97 countries around the world .	結果我們稱之為 「 根與芽 」 , 起源於坦尚尼亞 , 現在已經擴散到全世界97個國家 。
it's symbolic . roots make a firm foundation .	它是象徵性的 。 樹根會創造一個堅定的基礎 。
shoots seem tiny ; to reach the sun they can break through a brick wall .	槍枝看起來很小 ; 要抵達太陽 , 就能穿過一堵磚牆 。
see the brick wall as all these problems we've inflicted on the planet , environmental and social . it's a message of hope .	把磚牆看成我們在地球上所遇到的問題 , 環境和社會問題 。 這是一種希望的訊息 。
hundreds and thousands of young people around the world can break through and can make this a better world for all living things .	世界各地有成千上萬的年輕人可以打破這個世界 , 讓所有生物都能成為更好的世界 。
the most important message of roots and shoots: every single one of us makes a difference , every single day .	根與芽的最重要的訊息:我們每一個人每天都會有所改變 。
we have a choice . every one of us in this room , we have a choice as to what kind of difference we want to make .	我們有選擇 。 在座的每一個人 , 我們都有選擇去做出我們想要的差異 。
the very poor have no choice . it's up to us to change things so that the poor have choice as well .	非常貧窮的人沒有選擇 , 決定要改變事情 , 讓窮人也有選擇 。
the roots and shoots groups all choose three projects .	根部和槍枝團體都選擇三個計畫 。
it depends on how old they are , and which country , whether they're in a city or rural , as to what kinds of projects .	它取決於它們有多老 , 哪個國家 , 不論是城市或鄉村 , 都要仰賴什麼樣的計畫 。
but basically , we have programs now from preschool right through university , with more and more adults starting their own roots and shoots groups .	但基本上 , 我們現在有了從幼稚園到大學的程式 , 越來越多成年人開始自己的根源和芽團體 。
and every group chooses , between them , three different kinds of project to make this a better world , recognizing that all these different problems are interconnected and impinge on each other .	每個團體的選擇 , 兩者之間有三種不同的專案 , 讓這個世界變得更美好 , 認知所有這些不同的問題都互相連結 , 互相衝突 。
so one of their projects will be to help their own human community .	其中一項計畫是幫助他們自己的人類社群 。
and then , if they're able , they may raise money to help communities in other parts of the world .	接著 , 如果他們能夠的話 , 他們可能會募到錢來協助世界上其他地方的社區 。
one of their projects will be to help animals not just wildlife , domestic animals as well .	其中一個計畫是幫助動物 , 不僅僅是野生動物 , 還有家畜 。
and one of their projects will be to help the environment that we all share .	其中一個計畫是幫助我們共享的環境 。
and woven throughout all of this is a message of learning to live in peace and harmony within ourselves , in our families , in our communities , between nations , between cultures , between religions and between us and the natural world .	在這一切中 , 都包含了學習的訊息 , 是關於我們內在的和平和和諧 , 在我們的家庭、在我們的社區、國家、文化之間、宗教之間、和自然界之間 。
we need the natural world . we cannot go on destroying it at the rate we are .	我們需要自然界 。 我們不能以速率破壞它 。
we not do have more than this one planet .	我們沒有超過這顆行星 。
just picking one or two of the projects right here in africa that the roots and shoots groups are doing , one or two projects only in tanzania , in uganda , kenya , south africa , congobrazzaville , sierra leone , cameroon and other groups . and as i say , it's in 97 countries around the world .	在非洲這裡挑選其中一兩項項目 , 由根和槍枝組成 , 其中一兩項目 , 只有一兩項目 , 在坦尚尼亞、肯亞、南非、剛果、獅子山共和國、喀麥隆和其它團體 。 如我所說的 , 世界上有97個國家 。
of course , they're planting trees . they're growing organic vegetables .	當然 , 他們種植樹 , 種植有機蔬菜 。
they're working in the refugee camps , with chickens and selling the eggs for a little amount of money , or just using them to feed their families , and feeling a sense of pride and empowerment , because they're no longer helpless and depending on others with their vegetables and their chickens .	他們在難民營工作 , 用雞和雞來賣蛋 , 或用它們來餵他們的家人 , 感受到自豪和賦權 , 因為它們不再是無助的 , 依靠蔬菜和雞肉來取代別人 。
it's being used in uganda to give some psychological help to exchild soldiers .	它被用在烏干達 , 給予精神上的幫助 , 給予智能士兵 。
doing projects like this is bringing them out of themselves .	做像這樣的項目 , 會讓他們自己脫離 。
once again , they're useful members of society .	再一次 , 他們是有用的社會成員 。
we have this program in prisons as well .	我們在監獄也有這個計畫 。
so , there's no time for more roots and shoots now .	所以 , 現在沒有時間可以多一點根和芽 。
but oh , they're also working on hiv/aids .	但 , 喔 , 他們也在研究愛滋病 。
that's a very important component of roots and shoots , with older kids talking to younger ones .	那是根與芽的非常重要的部分 , 年長的孩子會和較年輕的孩子交談 。
and unwanted pregnancies and things like that , which young people listen to better from other youth , rather than adults .	像這樣的事 , 年輕人會傾聽其他年輕人的傾聽 , 而不是成年人 。
hope . that's the question i get asked as i'm going around the world: " jane , you've seen so many terrible things , you've seen your chimpanzees decrease in number from about one million , at the turn of the century , to no more than 150 , 000 now , and the same with so many other animals .	希望 , 我在世界各地被問到這個問題: 「 珍 , 你看過這麼多可怕的東西 , 你見過黑猩猩數量從一百萬年開始 , 到現在都不到十五萬 , 和許多其他動物都一樣 。
forests disappearing , deserts where once there was forest .	森林消失 , 曾經有過森林的沙漠 。
do you really have hope ? " well , yes .	你真的有希望嗎 ? " 是的 。
you can't come to a conference like ted and not have hope , can you ?	你不能來參加像ted這樣的會議 , 沒有希望 , 你能嗎 ?
and of course , there's hope . one is this amazing human brain .	當然 , 這裡有希望 。 一個是令人驚嘆的大腦 。
and i mean , think of the technologies .	我的意思是 , 想想科技 。
and i've just been so thrilled , finally , to come to people talking about compost latrines .	最後 , 我真的很興奮 , 終於 , 大家來談談作曲公司 。
it's one of my hobbyhorses .	這是我的嗜好之一 。
we just flush all this water down the lavatory , it's terrible .	我們把所有的水都沖下了 , 很糟糕 。
and then talking about renewable energy desperately important .	接著 , 談到可再生能源 , 迫切重要 。
do we care about the planet for our children ?	我們是否在乎我們的孩子的星球 ?
how many of us have children or grandchildren , nieces , nephews ?	有多少人有孩子或孫子、姪女、姪女 ?
do we care about their future ?	我們是否在乎他們的未來 ?
and if we care about their future , we , as the elite around the world , we can do something about it . we can make choices as to how we live each day .	如果我們在乎他們的未來 , 我們 , 身為世界各地的精英 , 我們能做點什麼 。 我們可以做一些選擇 , 來做我們每天生活的方式 。
what we buy . what we wear .	我們買什麼 , 穿什麼衣服 。
and choose to make these choices with the question , how will this affect the environment around me ?	選擇用問題來做這些選擇 , 這會如何影響我周遭的環境 ?
how will it affect the life of my child when he or she grows up ?	在成長過程中 , 它會如何影響我孩子的生命 ?
or my grandchild , or whatever it is .	或是我的孫子 , 不管是什麼 。
so the human brain , coupled with the human heart , and we join hands around the world .	所以 , 人類的大腦 , 和人類的心結合 , 我們加入世界各地的手 。
and that's what ted is helping so well with , and google who help us , and esri are helping us with mapping in gombe national park .	這也是ted幫助我們做的 , google幫助我們 , esri幫助我們在國立公園繪製戈米貝爾國家公園 。
all of these technologies we can use .	所有這些我們能使用的科技 。
now let's link them , and it's beginning to happen , isn't it ?	現在讓我們把它們連結起來 , 開始發生 , 不是嗎 ?
you've heard about it this afternoon . it's beginning to happen .	你們今年下午聽說過它 , 正開始發生 。
this change , this change . to see change that we must have if we care about the future .	這種改變 , 這種改變 。 若我們在乎未來 , 我們就必須要看到改變 。
and the next reason for hope nature is amazingly resilient .	而希望大自然的下一個理由 , 是驚人的韌性 。
you can take an area that's absolutely destroyed , with time and perhaps some help it can regenerate .	你可以把一個絕對被摧毀的區域 , 花點時間 , 也許有些協助它再生 。
and an example is the tacare program .	一個例子是 「 坦尚尼 」 。
i told you , where a seemingly dead tree stump if you stop hacking them for firewood , which you don't need to because you have wood lots , then in five years you can have a 30foot tree .	我跟你說 , 一棵似乎已經死掉的樹木 , 如果你阻止它們生火 , 你不需要因為有木頭 , 那麼五年內你就可以有一棵三十英尺長的樹 。
and animals , almost on the brink of extinction , can be given a second chance . that's my next book .	動物 , 幾乎是滅絕的邊緣 , 可以給予第二次機會 。 這是我的下一本書 。
it's inspiring . and it brings me to my last category of hope , and we've heard about this so much in the last two days: this indomitable human spirit . this determination of people , the resilience of the human spirit , so that people who you would think would be battered by poverty , or disease , or whatever , can pull themselves up out of it , sometimes with a helping hand , and take their part in society , and take their part in changing the world .	它激勵了我 。 它帶給我最後一類的希望 , 在過去的兩天中 , 我們已經聽說過這一點:這可行的人類精神 。 人類精神的決心 , 人類精神的韌性 , 所以你認為會被貧窮、疾病打擊 , 或什麼 , 都可以把他們自己從中拔出來 , 有時是有幫助的手 , 帶著他們參與社會的一部分 , 改變世界的一部分 。
and just to think of one or two people out of africa who are just really inspiring .	光是想一下 , 非洲只有一兩個人真的很鼓舞人心 。
we could make a very long list , but obviously nelson mandela , emerging from 17 years of hard physical labor , 23 years of imprisonment , with this amazing ability to forgive , so that he could lead his nation out the evil regime of apartheid without a bloodbath .	我們可以列出非常長的清單 , 但很明顯的 , 曼德拉 , 從十七年的辛苦實體勞動 , 23年的監禁 , 帶著寬恕的能力 , 讓他能夠帶領國出種族隔離的邪惡政權 , 卻沒有血腥戰爭 。
ken sarowiwa , in nigeria , who took on the giant oil companies , and although people around the world tried their best , was executed .	在奈及利亞 , 肯薩洛伊瓦 , 他採用了巨大的石油公司 , 雖然世界各地的人盡了最好 , 卻被處決了 。
people like this are so inspirational .	像這樣的人是非常鼓舞人心的 。
people like this are the role models we need for young africans .	像這樣的人 , 是非洲年輕人所需要的典範 。
and we need some environmental role models as well , and i've been hearing some of them today .	我們也需要一些環保的榜樣 , 今天我聽到了其中一些 。
