so i'm really grateful for this opportunity to share this message again , with everyone at ted .	所以我很感激這個機會 , 能再次和ted的所有人分享這個訊息 。
and i hope that some of us can get together and talk about some of these things , especially the roots and shoots program .	我希望有些人能聚在一起討論這些事 , 尤其是根與芽計畫 。
and just a last word on that the young woman who's running this entire conference center , i met her today .	最後一個字是那個跑完整個會議中心的年輕女子 , 我今天見到她 。
she came up so excited , with her certificate . she was [in] roots and shoots .	她很興奮 , 用她的認證 , 她是根和芽 。
she was in the leadership in dar es salaam .	她在達拉姆的領導階層 。
she said it's helped her to do what she's doing .	她說 , 協助她做她正在做的事 。
and it was very , very exciting for me to meet her and see just one example of how young people , when they are empowered , given the opportunity to take action , to make the world a better place , truly are our hope for tomorrow .	對我來說 , 很興奮 , 能見到她 , 看到一個例子 , 說明年輕人是如何被賦予權力 , 因為有機會採取行動 , 讓世界更美好 , 真正是我們明天的希望 。
artist dianna cohen shares some tough truths about plastic pollution in the ocean and in our lives and some thoughts on how to free ourselves from the plastic gyre .	藝術家dannacohen分享了一些關於海洋的塑膠污染以及我們的生活以及一些想法 , 來解放我們自己 , 避免塑膠垃圾 。
consumerism , global issues , green , mission blue , oceans , plastic	消費主義、全球議題、綠色、使命藍色、海洋、塑膠、塑膠等問題、
dianna cohen: tough truths about plastic pollution	戴安娜柯恩:關於塑膠污染的艱難事實 。
i'm a visual artist , and i'm also one of the cofounders of the plastic pollution coalition .	我是一位視覺藝術家 , 我也是塑膠污染聯盟的共同創辦人之一 。
i've been working with plastic bags , which i cut up and sew back together as my primary material for my artwork for the last 20 years .	我和塑膠袋合作 , 在過去二十年間 , 我把這些塑膠袋剪起來 , 用我的藝術作品做為我的主要材料 。
i turn them into two and threedimensional pieces and sculptures and installations .	我把它們變成兩個三維的碎片、雕塑和裝置 。
upon working with the plastic , after about the first eight years , some of my work started to fissure and break down into smaller little bits of plastic .	在與塑膠合作後 , 大約八年後 , 我的一些作品開始裂縫 , 分裂成小小的塑膠 。
and i thought , " great .	我心想: 「 太棒了 。
it's ephemeral just like us . "	它就像我們一樣 。 」
upon educating myself a little further about plastics , i actually realized this was a bad thing .	在教導我更進一步關於塑膠的知識之後 , 我發現這是一件壞事 。
it's a bad thing that plastic breaks down into smaller little bits , because it's always still plastic .	塑膠破裂成較小的部分 , 因為它一直都是塑膠 。
and what we're finding is that a lot of it is in the marine environment .	我們發現 , 在海洋環境中有很多東西 。
i then , in the last few years , learned about the pacific garbage patch and the gyre .	接下來的幾年 , 我學到了太平洋垃圾堆和垃圾堆 。
and my initial reaction and i think this is a lot of people's first reaction to learning about it is , " oh my god !	我最初的反應是 , 很多人的第一反應是: 「 天啊 !
we've got to go out there and clean this thing up . "	我們得把這個東西清理乾淨 。 」
so i actually developed a proposal to go out with a cargo ship and two decommissioned fishing trawlers , a crane , a chipping machine and a coldmolding machine .	所以 , 我真的開發了一個提案 , 用一艘貨船和兩艘退貨拖網商、一台拖車、一台磨碎機和一台冷貨機 。
and my intention was to go out to the gyre , raise awareness about this issue and begin to pick up the plastic , chip it into little bits and cold mold it into bricks that could potentially be used as building materials in underdeveloped communities .	我的意圖是去到gyre , 提高對於這個議題的意識 , 然後開始把塑膠 , 晶片變成一點點 , 把它冷藏成磚塊 , 可以被用來建造在被開發的社區內的建築材料 。
i began talking with people who actually had been out to the gyre and were studying the plastic problem in the marine environment and upon doing so , i realized actually that cleaning it up would be a very small drop in the bucket relative to how much is being generated every day around the world , and that actually i needed to back up and look at the bigger picture .	我開始和那些曾經去過海灣的人們談話 , 研究海洋環境中的塑膠問題 , 在做這件事時 , 我了解到 , 清理它將會是非常小的一滴 , 相對於全世界每天產生多少東西 , 我需要回頭看更大的照片 。
and the bigger picture is: we need to find a way to turn off the faucet .	更大的看法是:我們需要找到一種方法來關掉錯誤 。
we need to cut the spigot of singleuse and disposable plastics , which are entering the marine environment every day on a global scale .	我們需要切割單一和可丟棄的塑膠的位置 , 每天都在全球的海洋環境中進入海洋環境 。
so in looking at that , i also realized that i was really angry .	所以 , 看看這一點 , 我也發現我真的很生氣 。
i wasn't just concerned about plastic that you're trying to imagine out in the middle of the pacific ocean of which i have learned there are now 11 gyres , potentially , of plastic in five major oceans in the world .	我不只關心塑膠 , 而是你試著想像在太平洋中間 , 我所學到的 , 現在有11gyres , 潛在五大洋的塑膠 。
it's not just that gyre of plastic that i'm concerned about it's the gyre of plastic in the supermarket .	不只是我所關心的塑膠垃圾 , 是超市的塑膠垃圾 。
i'd go to the supermarket and all of my food is packaged in plastic .	我會去超市 , 我所有的食物都是用塑膠包裝的 。
all of my beverages are packaged in plastic , even at the health food market .	我所有的平均值都包含在塑膠上 , 甚至在健康食品市場上 。
i'm also concerned about the plastic in the refrigerator , and i'm concerned about the plastic and the toxins that leach from plastic into us and into our bodies .	我也關心冰箱裡的塑膠 , 我關心的是塑膠和塑膠的毒素 , 將塑膠帶進我們的身體 。
so i came together with a group of other people who were all looking at this issue , and we created the plastic pollution coalition .	所以我和一群人一起研究這個問題 , 我們創造了塑膠污染聯盟 。
we have many initiatives that we're working on , but some of them are very basic .	我們有許多計畫正在進行 , 但其中有一些是非常基本的 。
one is: if 80 to 90 percent of what we're finding in the ocean of the marine debris that we're finding in the ocean is plastic , then why don't we call it what it is .	第一:如果我們在海洋中發現的海洋中 , 80%到90%到90%都是塑膠 , 那麼我們為什麼不把它稱為它 。
recycling everybody kind of ends their books about being sustainable and greening with the idea of recycling .	回收每個人的書籍 , 內容是要以回收方式來維持永續和綠化 。
you put something in a bin and you don't have to think about it again .	你把東西放進一個桶子裡 , 你不需要再想一想 。
what is the reality of that ?	什麼是它的現實呢 ?
in the united states , less than seven percent of our plastics are recycled .	在美國 , 少於7%的塑膠回收 。
and if you really look into it , particularly when it comes to plastic bottles , most of it is only downcycled , or incinerated , or shipped to china .	如果你真的仔細看 , 尤其是關於塑膠瓶 , 大部分的瓶子只會下降 , 或被送到中國 。
it is downcycled and turned into lesser things , while a glass bottle can be a glass bottle again or can be used again a plastic bottle can never be a plastic bottle again .	它被拆解 , 變成更少的東西 , 而玻璃瓶可以再次成為玻璃瓶 , 或者再次使用塑膠瓶 , 永遠不會再次成為塑膠瓶 。
so this is a big issue for us .	這對我們來說是個大問題 。
another thing that we're looking at and asking people to think about is we've added a fourth r onto the front of the " reduce , reuse , recycle , " three r's , and that is refuse .	另一件我們正在看的東西 , 請大家思考 , 我們已經在 「 減少、再利用、回收 」 前面加上了第四個環 , 那就是拒絕 。
whenever possible , refuse singleuse and disposable plastics .	無論何時 , 都會拒絕單一的塑膠 。
alternatives exist ; some of them are very oldschool .	替代方案存在 ; 有些是非常古老的學者 。
i myself am now collecting these cool pyrex containers and using those instead of glad and tupperware containers to store food in .	我現在正在收集這些很酷的pyx容器 , 而不是用那些玻璃和tuperware的容器來儲存食物 。
and i know that i am doing a service to myself and my family .	我知道我在為自己和家人服務 。
it's very easy to pick up a stainlesssteel bottle or a glass bottle , if you're traveling and you've forgotten to bring your stainlesssteel bottle and fill that up with water or filtered water , versus purchasing plastic bottled water .	如果你在旅行時 , 很容易就拿起一瓶不粘的酒瓶或玻璃瓶 , 你已經忘了帶著一瓶不變的汽水填滿水或過濾的塑膠瓶 , 和購買塑膠瓶的水 。
i guess what i want to say to everybody here and i know that you guys know a lot about this issue is that this is a huge problem in the oceans , but this is a problem that we've created as consumers and we can solve .	我猜我想在這裡對大家說些什麼 , 我知道你們對這個議題了解很多 , 就是這在海洋中是很大的問題 , 但我們身為消費者 , 能解決的問題 。
we can solve this by raising awareness of the issue and teaching people to choose alternatives .	我們可以藉由提高意識到問題和教導人們選擇替代性 。
so whenever possible , to choose alternatives to singleuse plastics .	所以 , 無論何時 , 選擇選擇單一使用塑膠的替代方案 。
we can cut the stem tide the stem of this into our oceans and in doing so , save our oceans , save our planet , save ourselves .	我們可以把幹線切成海洋 , 這樣做 , 拯救我們的海洋 , 拯救我們的星球 , 拯救我們自己 。
this demo from pattie maes' lab at mit , spearheaded by pranav mistry was the buzz of ted . it's a wearable device with a projector that paves the way for profound interaction with our environment . imagine " minority report " and then some .	這位ptiemaes在麻省理工學院的實驗室的展示 , 帕拉夫•米萊特是ted的推動裝置 。 這是一台可穿戴式裝置 , 以與我們的環境互動為例 。 想像一下 「 少數族群報告 」 , 然後有些 。
demo , design , interface design , technology	展示、設計、介面設計、科技、科技、科技等 。
pattie maes and pranav mistry demo sixthsense	pattiemaes和pranavdemose第六感測器 。
i've been intrigued by this question of whether we could evolve or develop a sixth sense a sense that would give us seamless access and easy access to metainformation or information that may exist somewhere that may be relevant to help us make the right decision about whatever it is that we're coming across .	我對這個問題很感興趣 , 究竟我們能否進化或發展出第六感 , 一種感覺 , 一種感覺 , 一種讓我們無縫可取代、容易取得的資訊 , 或可能存在於某處 , 來協助我們做出正確的決定 , 來決定我們要面對的是什麼 。
and some of you may argue , well , don't today's cell phones do that already ?	在座有些人可能會認為 , 嗯 , 今天的手機已經做到了嗎 ?
but i would say no .	但我會說 , 不行 。
when you meet someone here at ted and this is the top networking place , of course , of the year you don't shake somebody's hand and then say , " can you hold on for a moment while i take out my phone and google you ? "	當你在ted見到某人時 , 當然是最頂尖的網絡地點 , 你不會握某人的手 , 然後說: 「 你能拿出手機和谷歌嗎 ? 」
or when you go to the supermarket and you're standing there in that huge aisle of different types of toilet papers , you don't take out your cell phone , and open a browser , and go to a website to try to decide which of these different toilet papers is the most ecologically responsible purchase to make .	或者 , 當你去超市 , 你站在那裡 , 那裡有大量不同的廁所論文 , 你不會拿手機 , 打開瀏覽器 , 然後去一個網站 , 試著決定哪些不同的廁所論文是最環保的購買方式 。
so we don't really have easy access to all this relevant information that can just help us make optimal decisions about what to do next and what actions to take .	所以 , 我們沒有很容易取得這些相關的資訊 , 來協助我們做出最佳決定 , 來決定接下來要做什麼 , 以及要採取什麼行動 。
and so my research group at the media lab has been developing a series of inventions to give us access to this information in a sort of easy way , without requiring that the user changes any of their behavior .	所以我在媒體實驗室的研究團隊已經開發了一系列的發明 , 讓我們能以簡單的方式取得這些資訊 , 不需要使用者改變他們的行為 。
and i'm here to unveil our latest effort , and most successful effort so far , which is still very much a work in process .	我來這裡是為了揭開我們最新的努力 , 目前為止 , 大部分成功的努力 , 這仍然是過程中非常重要的工作 。
i'm actually wearing the device right now and we've sort of cobbled it together with components that are off the shelf and that , by the way , only cost 350 dollars at this point in time .	我現在穿著這個裝置 , 我們把它和櫃子上架的零件組合在一起 , 順帶一提 , 那時只有350美金 。
i'm wearing a camera , just a simple webcam , a portable , batterypowered projection system with a little mirror .	我戴著一台攝影機 , 只是一個簡單的網路攝影機 , 一個可攜式的電池驅動投影系統 , 上面有一面鏡子 。
these components communicate to my cell phone in my pocket which acts as the communication and computation device .	這些元件在我的口袋裡傳達給我的手機 , 可以當作溝通和計算設備 。
and in the video here we see my student pranav mistry , who's really the genius who's been implementing and designing this whole system .	在這段影片中 , 我們看到我的學生帕拉夫•米特里 , 他是當時正在實施和設計這個系統的天才 。
and we see how this system lets him walk up to any surface and start using his hands to interact with the information that is projected in front of him .	我們看到這個系統如何讓他走到任何表面上 , 開始用他的雙手和投射在他面前的資訊互動 。
the system tracks the four significant fingers .	系統追蹤四個重要的手指 。
in this case , he's wearing simple marker caps that you may recognize .	在這個例子中 , 他戴著簡單的標記帽子 , 你可能認得出來 。
but if you want a more stylish version you could also paint your nails in different colors .	但如果你想要一個更風格的版本 , 你也可以用不同的顏色來畫你的指甲 。
and the camera basically tracks these four fingers and recognizes any gestures that he's making so he can just go to , for example , a map of long beach , zoom in and out , etc .	攝影機基本上可以追蹤這四根手指 , 辨識出他正在做的任何手勢 , 例如 , 長灘的地圖放大 , 等等 。
the system also recognizes iconic gestures such as the " take a picture " gesture , and then takes a picture of whatever is in front of you .	這個系統也能辨識出有代表性的姿勢 , 比如 「 拍照 」 的姿勢 , 然後拍下你面前的任何東西 。
and when he then walks back to the media lab , he can just go up to any wall and project all the pictures that he's taken , sort through them and organize them , and resize them , etc . , again using all natural gestures .	當他走回媒體實驗室時 , 他可以走到任何牆上 , 投影他所拍攝的所有照片 , 透過這些照片 , 整理它們 , 將它們放大 , 再次使用各種自然手勢 。
so , some of you most likely were here two years ago and saw the demo by jeff han or some of you may think , " well , doesn't this look like the microsoft surface table ? "	所以 , 在座有些人可能兩年前來到這裡 , 傑夫•漢或者有些人可能會想: 「 這不是微軟的表面桌子嗎 ? 」
and yes , you also interact using natural gestures , both hands , etc .	沒錯 , 你也會用自然手勢、雙手等等互動 。
but the difference here is that you can use any surface , you can walk to up to any surface , including your hand if nothing else is available and interact with this projected data .	但這裡的差別是 , 你可以用任何表面 , 你可以走到任何表面上 , 包括你的手 , 如果沒有其他東西可以使用 , 並與這個投影資料互動 。
the device is completely portable , and can be . . .	這個裝置是完全可攜帶的 , 也可以是......
so one important difference is that it's totally mobile .	其中一個重要的差別是它完全是行動裝置 。
another even more important difference is that in mass production this would not cost more tomorrow than today's cell phones and would actually not sort of be a bigger packaging could look a lot more stylish than this version that i'm wearing around my neck .	另外一個更重要的差別在於 , 大量生產--這並不會比今日的手機還多 , 實際上不會像一個更大的包裝 , 看起來會比我穿著脖子的這個版本還多 。
but other than letting some of you live out your fantasy of looking as cool as tom cruise in " minority report , " the reason why we're really excited about this device is that it really can act as one of these sixthsense devices that gives you relevant information about whatever is in front of you .	但 , 除了讓你們之外 , 在《少數報告》中 , 湯姆•克魯斯的幻想中 , 除此之外 , 我們對這個裝置感到興奮的原因之一 , 是它真的可以作為第六感設備 , 讓你知道你面前的任何東西 。
so we see pranav here going into the supermarket and he's shopping for some paper towels .	我們看到帕拉走進超市 , 他在購物一些紙巾 。
and , as he picks up a product the system can recognize the product that he's picking up , using either image recognition or marker technology , and give him the green light or an orange light .	當他拿起產品時 , 系統就能辨識出他所撿到的產品 , 使用影像辨識或標記技術 , 給他綠燈或橘色燈 。
he can ask for additional information .	他可以尋求額外的資訊 。
so this particular choice here is a particularly good choice , given his personal criteria .	所以這個特殊的選擇 , 是一個特別好的選擇 , 因為他個人的標準 。
some of you may want the toilet paper with the most bleach in it rather than the most ecologicallyresponsible choice .	你們之中有些人可能想要有最多麻煩的馬桶紙而不是最環保的選擇
if he picks up a book in the bookstore , he can get an amazon rating it gets projected right on the cover of the book .	如果他在書店裡拿起一本書 , 他就可以拿到亞馬遜評分 , 書的封面就會被投射出來 。
this is juan's book , our previous speaker , which gets a great rating , by the way , at amazon .	這是juan的書 , 我們先前的講者 , 順便一提 , 在亞馬遜有很棒的評分 。
and so , pranav turns the page of the book and can then see additional information about the book reader comments , maybe sort of information by his favorite critic , etc .	所以 , 帕拉夫轉換了這本書的頁面 , 然後再看出額外的資訊 , 關於書讀者的評論 , 也許是他最喜歡的資訊 。
if he turns to a particular page he finds an annotation by maybe an expert of a friend of ours that gives him a little bit of additional information about whatever is on that particular page .	如果他轉向某個特定的頁面 , 他可能是一位朋友的專家 , 給他一些額外的資訊 , 關於那個頁面上的任何東西 。
reading the newspaper it never has to be outdated .	閱讀報紙 , 它永遠不會過時 。
you can get video annotations of the event that you're reading about you can get the latest sports scores etc .	你可以得到你正在閱讀的事件的視覺表達 , 你可以得到最新的運動分數 。
this is a more controversial one .	這是一個更具爭議性的 。
as you interact with someone at ted , maybe you can see a word cloud of the tags , the words that are associated with that person in their blog and personal web pages .	當你和ted的某個人互動時 , 也許你能看到一個標籤的雲朵 , 和那個人的部落格和個人網頁有關的字詞 。
in this case , the student is interested in cameras , etc .	在這個案例中 , 學生對攝影機感興趣等等 。
on your way to the airport , if you pick up your boarding pass , it can tell you that your flight is delayed , that the gate has changed , etc .	在你到機場的路上 , 如果你拿起你的登機 , 它可以告訴你你的飛行器延遲 , 門已經改變了 , 等等 。
and , if you need to know what the current time is it's as simple as drawing a watch on your arm .	如果你需要知道目前的時光 , 就好像在手臂上畫著手錶一樣簡單 。
so that's where we're at so far in developing this sixth sense that would give us seamless access to all this relevant information about the things that we may come across .	這就是我們目前正在開發第六感 , 使我們能夠無縫地取得所有相關資訊 , 來了解我們可能遇到的事物 。
my student pranav , who's really , like i said , the genius behind this .	我的學生帕拉 , 真的 , 像我剛才說的 , 是背後的天才 。
he does deserve a lot of applause because i don't think he's slept much in the last three months , actually .	他的確需要很多掌聲 , 因為我不認為他在過去三個月內睡得多 。
and his girlfriend is probably not very happy about him either .	他的女朋友可能也不高興他 。
but it's not perfect yet , it's very much a work in progress .	但它還不完美 , 它在進步中非常重要 。
and who knows , maybe in another 10 years we'll be here with the ultimate sixth sense brain implant .	誰知道 , 也許在接下來的十年 , 我們將會來到終極的第六感植入 。
phyllis rodriguez and aicha elwafi have a powerful friendship born of unthinkable loss . rodriguez' son was killed in the world trade center attacks on september 11 , 2001 ; elwafi's son zacarias moussaoui was convicted of a role in those attacks and is serving a life sentence . in hoping to find peace , these two moms have come to understand and respect one another .	菲利斯•羅德里奇和阿西瓦菲有著強烈的友誼 , 出生於不可思議的損失 。 羅德里格斯的兒子在2001年9月11日被殺 ; 艾爾瓦夫的兒子祖撒拉索瑞亞•莫薩波撒瓦伊被定罪於攻擊中的角色 , 希望能找到和平 , 這兩位母親已經開始了解並尊重彼此 。
culture , global issues , politics	文化、全球議題、政治、政治、
9/11 healing: the mothers who found forgiveness , friendship	9/11療癒:找到寬恕、友誼的母親 。
phyllis rodriguez: we are here today because of the fact that we have what most people consider an unusual friendship .	菲利斯•羅德里格茲:我們今天來到這裡 , 是因為我們有許多人認為非凡的友誼 。
and yet , it feels natural to us now .	但 , 現在對我們來說 , 感覺很自然 。
i first learned that my son had been in the world trade center on the morning of september 11th , 2001 .	我第一次了解到 , 我兒子在2001年9月11日早上 , 在世貿中心 。
we didn't know if he had perished yet until 36 hours later .	我們不知道他是否在36小時後死了 。
at the time , we knew that it was political .	當時 , 我們知道這是政治的 。
we were afraid of what our country was going to do in the name of our son my husband , orlando , and i and our family .	我們害怕我們的國家會以我們兒子的名義來做些什麼 , 奧蘭多 , 我和我們的家人 。
and when i saw it and yet , through the shock , the terrible shock , and the terrible explosion in our lives , literally , we were not vengeful .	然而當我看到它 , 透過震驚、可怕的震驚 , 以及我們人生中可怕的爆炸 , 實際上 , 我們並非有毒的 。
and a couple of weeks later when zacarias moussaoui was indicted on six counts of conspiracy to commit terrorism , and the u . s . government called for a death penalty for him , if convicted , my husband and i spoke out in opposition to that , publicly .	幾個星期後 , 祖撒拉索伊號指出了六個陰謀 , 要犯下恐怖主義 , 美國政府稱他為死刑 , 如果被定罪 , 我的丈夫和我在公開的對立中發言 。
through that and through human rights groups , we were brought together with several other victims' families .	透過這些人權團體 , 我們和其他受害者的家人聚在一起 。
when i saw aicha in the media , coming over when her son was indicted , and i thought , " what a brave woman .	當我在媒體上看到aicha , 她兒子被指控時 , 我心想: 「 什麼是一位勇敢的女人 。
someday i want to meet that woman when i'm stronger . "	有一天 , 我想要在我強壯的時候認識那個女人 。 」
i was still in deep grief ; i knew i didn't have the strength .	我還在深深的悲傷中 , 我知道我沒有力量 。
i knew i would find her someday , or we would find each other .	我知道我有一天會找到她 , 或者我們會找到彼此 。
because , when people heard that my son was a victim , i got immediate sympathy .	因為 , 當人們聽到我兒子是受害者時 , 我馬上就有同理心了 。
but when people learned what her son was accused of , she didn't get that sympathy .	但當人們學會兒子被指控時 , 她沒有得到同情心 。
but her suffering is equal to mine .	但她的苦難和我一樣 。
so we met in november 2002 , and aicha will now tell you how that came about .	所以 , 我們在2002年11月見面 , aicha將告訴你們這如何發生 。
aicha elwafi: good afternoon , ladies and gentlemen .	aichaelwafi:午安 , 各位先生女士 。
i am the mother of zacarias moussaoui .	我是zariassaoui的母親 。
and i asked the organization of human rights to put me in touch with the parents of the victims .	我問了人權組織 , 讓我聯絡受害者的父母 。
so they introduced me to five families .	所以他們把我介紹給五個家庭 。
and i saw phyllis , and i watched her .	我看到了phyllis , 我看著她 。
she was the only mother in the group .	她是群體中唯一的母親 。
the others were brothers , sisters .	其他人則是兄弟姊妹 。
and i saw in her eyes that she was a mother , just like me .	我在她的眼中看到她是母親 , 就像我一樣 。
i suffered a lot as a mother .	我身為母親 , 遭遇了許多苦難 。
i was married when i was 14 .	我14歲時結婚了 。
i lost a child when i was 15 , a second child when i was 16 .	我十五歲時失去了一個孩子 , 我十六歲時第二個孩子 。
so the story with zacarias was too much really .	所以 , zacaria的故事實在太多了 。
and i still suffer , because my son is like he's buried alive .	我仍然受苦 , 因為我的兒子就好像他活著一樣 。
i know she really cried for her son .	我知道她真的為她的兒子哭了 。
but she knows where he is .	但她知道他在哪裡 。
my son , i don't know where he is .	我的兒子 , 我不知道他在哪裡 。
i don't know if he's alive . i don't know if he's tortured .	我不知道他是否還活著 , 我不知道他是否受到折磨 。
i don't know what happened to him .	我不知道他發生了什麼事 。
so that's why i decided to tell my story , so that my suffering is something positive for other women .	這就是為什麼我決定說我的故事 , 所以我的痛苦對其他女性來說是正面的 。
for all the women , all the mothers that give life , you can give back , you can change .	對所有女性來說 , 所有給予生命的母親 , 你可以回饋 , 你可以改變 。
it's up to us women , because we are women , because we love our children .	由於我們女性 , 因為我們是女性 , 因為我們愛我們的孩子 。
we must be handinhand and do something together .	我們必須是手持人 , 一起做點什麼 。
it's not against women , it's for us , for us women , for our children .	不是對女人 , 而是對我們、對我們女人、對我們的孩子 。
i talk against violence , against terrorism .	我反對暴力 , 反對恐怖主義 。
i go to schools to talk to young , muslim girls so they don't accept to be married against their will very young .	我去學校跟年輕的穆斯林女孩說話 , 這樣她們就不接受嫁給她們的意願還很年輕 。
so if i can save one of the young girls , and avoid that they get married and suffer as much as i did , well this is something good .	所以 , 如果我能拯救其中一位年輕女孩 , 避免他們結婚和受苦 , 這樣就好了 。
this is why i'm here in front of you .	這就是為什麼我站在你們面前 。
pr: i would like to say that i have learned so much from aicha , starting with that day we had our very first meeting with other family members which was a very private meeting with security , because it was november 2002 , and , frankly , we were afraid of the superpatriotism of that time in the country those of us family members .	帕特.羅斯:我想說我從阿里卡學到很多 , 從那天開始 , 我們第一次見到其他家庭成員 , 那是個非常私人的會議 , 因為那是2002年11月 , 坦白說 , 我們害怕當時在這個國家的超級病菌 。

then we sat in a circle with support , with help , from people experienced in this kind of reconciliation .	然後我們就坐在一個有幫助的圈子裡 , 從人們的這種和解的圈子裡 。
and aicha started , and she said , " i don't know if my son is guilty or innocent , but i want to tell you how sorry i am for what happened to your families .	aicha開始 , 她說: 「 我不知道我的兒子有沒有罪惡感或無辜 , 但我想告訴各位 , 我對你的家人有多抱歉 。

and what happened then is we all told our stories , and we all connected as human beings .	接下來發生的是 , 我們都說了我們的故事 , 我們都以人類的身分連結起來 。
by the end of the afternoon it was about three hours after lunch we'd felt as if we'd known each other forever .	下午結束時 , 午餐後大約有三小時 , 我們會感覺到我們永遠都知道彼此 。
now what i learned from her , is a woman , not only who could be so generous under these present circumstances and what it was then , and what was being done to her son , but the life she's had .	我從她身上學到的是 , 一個女人 , 不僅可以在這些當下的情況下如此慷慨 , 還有她兒子做了什麼 , 她的人生也一樣 。
i never had met someone with such a hard life , from such a totally different culture and environment from my own .	我從來沒有遇過過這種艱難生活的人 , 來自完全不同的文化和環境 。
and i feel that we have a special connection , which i value very much .	我覺得我們有一種特殊的連結 , 我非常重視它 。
and i think it's all about being afraid of the other , but making that step and then realizing , " hey , this wasn't so hard .	我認為這一切都是為了害怕他人 , 但要踏出那一步 , 然後意識到: 「 嘿 , 這不是那麼難 。
who else can i meet that i don't know , or that i'm so different from ? "	我還有誰可以碰到我不知道 , 還是和我這麼不同 ? 」
so , aicha , do you have a couple of words for conclusion ?	所以 , 亞克哈 , 你有幾個字要結論嗎 ?
because our time is up .	因為我們的時間到了 。
aw: i wanted to say that we have to try to know other people , the other .	aw:我想說 , 我們得要試著認識其他人 。

then statistics would actually say that half of you would now be suffering with diarrhea .	然後統計數字會說 , 你們當中有一半的人會受腹瀉所苦 。
i talked a lot in the past about statistics , and the provision of safe drinking water for all .	過去我談了很多關於統計 , 以及為所有人提供安全飲用水的代價 。
but they just don't seem to get through .	但他們似乎沒有經歷過 。
and i think i've worked out why .	我想我已經搞清楚為什麼了 。
it's because , using current thinking , the scale of the problem just seems too huge to contemplate solving .	因為 , 用當前的思考 , 問題的規模似乎太大了 , 無法去思考解決問題 。
so we just switch off: us , governments and aid agencies .	所以我們就關掉了:我們、政府和援助機構 。
well , today , i'd like to show you that through thinking differently , the problem has been solved .	今天 , 我想用不同的思維來展示 , 問題已經解決了 。
by the way , since i've been speaking , another 13 , 000 people around the world are suffering now with diarrhea .	順道一提 , 從我開始講話 , 世界各地有一萬三千人現在都患有腹瀉 。
and four children have just died .	四個孩子剛死了 。
i invented lifesaver bottle because i got angry .	我發明了救生員瓶 , 因為我生氣了 。
i , like most of you , was sitting down , the day after christmas in 2004 , when i was watching the devastating news of the asian tsunami as it rolled in , playing out on tv .	我和大多數人一樣 , 在2004年聖誕節後的那天 , 當我在看亞洲海嘯摧殘的消息時 , 在電視上演 。
the days and weeks that followed , people fleeing to the hills , being forced to drink contaminated water or face death .	接下來的幾天、幾週 , 人們逃到山丘 , 被迫喝污染的水或面臨死亡 。
that really stuck with me .	這真的困擾著我 。
then , a few months later , hurricane katrina slammed into the side of america .	接著 , 幾個月後 , 卡崔娜颶風卡崔娜陷入美國的一側 。
" okay , " i thought , " here's a first world country , let's see what they can do . "	「 好吧 ! 」 我心想: 「 這是第一個世界國家 , 我們來看看他們能做什麼 。 」
do you know it took five days to get water to the superdome ?	你知道要花五天才能把水送到超級大眾嗎 ?
people were shooting each other on the streets for tv sets and water .	人們在街上互相槍擊 , 拍攝電視機和水 。
that's when i decided i had to do something .	那是我決定要做點什麼的時候 。
now i spent a lot of time in my garage , over the next weeks and months , and also in my kitchen much to the dismay of my wife .	現在我花了很多時間在我的車庫 , 接下來的幾個月 , 在我的廚房裡 , 和我太太的不滿 。
however , after a few failed prototypes , i finally came up with this , the lifesaver bottle .	然而 , 經過幾次失敗的原型之後 , 我終於想出了這個 , 救生員瓶 。
okay , now for the science bit .	好吧 , 現在是科學的一部分 。
before lifesaver , the best hand filters were only capable of filtering down to about 200 nanometers .	在救生人員之前 , 最好的手只能過濾到大約200奈米 。
the smallest bacteria is about 200 nanometers .	最小的細菌大約是200奈米 。
so a 200nanometer bacteria is going to get through a 200nanometer hole .	所以 , 一個200奈米的細菌將會穿過一個200奈米的洞 。
the smallest virus , on the other hand , is about 25 nanometers .	另一方面 , 最小的病毒大約是25奈米 。
so that's definitely going to get through those 200 nanometer holes .	所以這肯定會通過那200奈米的洞 。
lifesaver pores are 15 nanometers .	救生員有15奈米 。
so nothing is getting through .	所以 , 什麼都沒有穿過 。
okay , i'm going to give you a bit of a demonstration .	好 , 我要給你們一些示範 。

but i got to thinking , you know , if we were in the middle of a flood zone in bangladesh , the water wouldn't look like this .	但我想 , 如果我們在孟加拉的洪水區中央 , 水就不會像這樣 。
so i've gone and got some stuff to add into it .	所以 , 我已經把一些東西加進去了 。
and this is from my pond .	這是我的池塘 。

that's not dirty enough . let's just stir that up a little bit .	這還不夠髒 , 讓我們稍微攪拌一下 。

okay . there we go .	好了 , 開始了 。
give it a few pumps . okay ?	給你幾個幫浦 。 好嗎 ?
that's all that's necessary .	這些都是必要的 。
now as soon as i pop the teat , sterile drinking water is going to come out .	一旦我放棄了茶葉 , 無菌飲用水就會出現 。

okay . lifesaver bottle is used by thousands of people around the world .	好 , 世界上數以千計的人都用過生命安全的瓶子 。
it'll last for 6 , 000 liters .	它會維持6 , 000公升 。
and when it's expired , using failsafe technology , the system will shut off , protecting the user .	當它爆發時 , 使用失敗的技術 , 系統就會關閉 , 保護使用者 。
pop the cartridge out . pop a new one in .	把車子拿出來 , 打開一個新的 。
it's good for another 6 , 000 liters .	這對六千公升有益 。
so let's look at the applications .	讓我們來看看這個應用程式 。
traditionally , in a crisis , what do we do ?	傳統上 , 在危機中 , 我們該怎麼做 ?
then , after a few weeks , we set up camps .	幾週後 , 我們設立營地 。
and people are forced to come into the camps to get their safe drinking water .	人們被迫進入難民營 , 得到安全的飲用水 。
what happens when 20 , 000 people congregate in a camp ?	當兩萬人聚集在難民營時 , 會發生什麼事 ?
diseases spread . more resources are required .	疾病傳播 , 需要更多的資源 。
the problem just becomes selfperpetuating .	問題就在於自我複製 。
but by thinking differently , and shipping these , people can stay put .	但用不同的方式思考 , 運送這些東西 , 人們可以留下來 。
they can make their own sterile drinking water , and start to get on with rebuilding their homes and their lives .	他們可以製造自己的無菌飲用水 , 開始重建他們的家園和生活 。
now , it doesn't require a natural disaster for this to work .	這樣做並不需要天然的災難 。
using the old thinking , of national infrastructure and pipe work , is too expensive .	使用舊的想法 , 國家基礎建設和管道工作 , 太貴了 。
when you run the numbers on a calculator , you run out of noughts .	當你在計算機上計算時 , 你就沒辦法搞定了 。
so here is the " thinking different " bit .	這是 「 思考 」 的部分 。
instead of shipping water , and using manmade processes to do it , let's use mother nature . she's got a fantastic system .	不用運送水 , 用人造的過程來做 , 讓我們用大自然 。 她有一個很棒的系統 。
she picks the water up from there , desalinates it , for free , transports it over there , and dumps it onto the mountains , rivers , and streams .	她從那裡撿起水 , 免費 , 運送到那裡 , 然後把它丟到山上、河流和溪流上 。
and where do people live ? near water .	人們住在哪裡 ? 靠近水 。
all we've go to do is make it sterile . how do we do that ?	我們要做的就是讓它無菌 。 我們要怎麼做呢 ?
well , we could use the lifesaver bottle .	嗯 , 我們可以用救生員的瓶子 。
or we could use one of these .	或者 , 我們可以使用其中一個 。
the same technology , in a jerry can .	同樣的技術 , 可以用在機械裝置上 。
this will process 25 , 000 liters of water ; that's good enough for a family of four , for three years .	這會處理2萬5千公升的水 , 這足以容納四個家庭 , 三年來 。
and how much does it cost ?	要花多少錢 ?
about half a cent a day to run .	每天大約有半分錢來跑 。
so , by thinking differently , and processing water at the point of use , mothers and children no longer have to walk four hours a day to collect their water .	所以 , 用不同的方式思考 , 用水處理 , 母親和孩子們不再需要每天四個小時來收集他們的水 。
they can get it from a source nearby .	他們可以從附近的來源取得它 。
so with just eight billion dollars , we can hit the millennium goal's target of halving the number of people without access to safe drinking water .	所以只要花了八十億美金 , 我們就能達到千禧目標的目標 , 來減少減少沒有安全飲用水的人數 。
to put that into context , the u . k . government spends about 12 billion pounds a year on foreign aid .	若要將它放入情境中 , 英國政府每年花費大約一百二十億英鎊在外國援助上 。
but why stop there ?	但為什麼就這樣停下來 ?
with 20 billion dollars , everyone can have access to safe drinking water .	有了兩百億美金 , 每個人都可以取得安全飲用水 。
so the threeandahalf billion people that suffer every year as a result , and the two million kids that die every year , will live .	所以 , 每年有三十五億人因為結果而遭受痛苦 , 而每年死亡的兩百萬個孩子 , 將會活下來 。
paddy ashdown claims that we are living in a moment in history where power is changing in ways it never has before . in a spellbinding talk at tedxbrussels he outlines the three major global shifts that he sees coming .	帕迪•阿希德宣稱我們生活在歷史上的一個時刻 , 權力正在改變它以前從未有過的方式 。 在tedxbrusel的一個拼字演說中 , 他排出了他所看到的三大全球轉變 。
foreign policy , global issues , politics , world cultures	外交政策、全球議題、政治、世界文化、文化 。
paddy ashdown: the global power shift	帕迪•阿什德市:全球的權力轉移 。
there's a poem written by a very famous english poet at the end of the 19th century .	在十九世紀末 , 一首非常有名的英國詩人寫了一首詩 。
it was said to echo in churchill's brain in the 1930s .	在1930年代 , 古希爾的大腦中 , 有人說是回應 。
and the poem goes: " on the idle hill of summer , lazy with the flow of streams , hark i hear a distant drummer , drumming like a sound in dreams , far and near and low and louder on the roads of earth go by , dear to friend and food to powder , soldiers marching , soon to die . "	詩歌說: 「 在夏天的山丘上 , 帶著溪流的流動 , 哈馬克 , 我聽見一個遙遠的鼓聲 , 像在夢裡的聲音 , 距離很近 , 很近 , 很近 , 很低 , 很親愛的朋友和食物傳給粉末 , 士兵很快就死了 。 」
those who are interested in poetry , the poem is " a shropshire lad " written by a . e . housman .	那些對詩意感興趣的人 , 詩是《鯊魚鯊》由艾倫斯曼寫的 。
but what housman understood , and you hear it in the symphonies of nielsen too , was that the long , hot , silvan summers of stability of the 19th century were coming to a close , and that we were about to move into one of those terrifying periods of history when power changes .	但霍斯曼也明白了 , 在尼爾森的交響曲中也聽到了它 , 就是在十九世紀的穩定性夏季即將接近近 , 而我們即將進入歷史中最恐怖的時期之一 , 當權力改變時 。
and these are always periods , ladies and gentlemen , accompanied by turbulence , and all too often by blood .	女士們先生們 , 這些經常是亂流的時期 , 經常是血液 。
and my message for you is that i believe we are condemned , if you like , to live at just one of those moments in history when the gimbals upon which the established order of power is beginning to change and the new look of the world , the new powers that exist in the world , are beginning to take form .	我給你們的訊息是 , 我相信我們是被譴責的 , 假如你喜歡 , 生活在歷史上的那些瞬間 , 當建立權力的秩序開始改變和新的看待世界 , 存在著新的權力 , 開始形成形式 。
and these are and we see it very clearly today nearly always highly turbulent times , highly difficult times , and all too often very bloody times .	今天我們很清楚地看到它 , 幾乎永遠都是亂亂的時代 , 極度困難的時代 , 經常是非常血腥的時代 。
by the way , it happens about once every century .	順道一提 , 它每世紀都會發生一次 。
you might argue that the last time it happened and that's what housman felt coming and what churchill felt too was that when power passed from the old nations , the old powers of europe , across the atlantic to the new emerging power of the united states of america the beginning of the american century .	你可能認為 , 最後一次發生 , 那就是霍斯曼的感受 , 和教堂的感受 , 就是當權力從舊的國家、歐洲的舊勢力 , 跨過大西洋到美國的新興權力 , 美國是美國一世紀初期 。
and of course , into the vacuum where the tooold european powers used to be were played the two bloody catastrophes of the last century the one in the first part and the one in the second part: the two great world wars .	當然 , 在真空之中 , 歐洲人曾經有過太多權力在上個世紀的兩場血腥災難中 , 第一部分也是第二部分:兩場大戰 。
mao zedong used to refer to them as the european civil wars , and it's probably a more accurate way of describing them .	毛澤東曾經稱他們為歐洲內戰 , 它可能是更精確的描述方式 。
well , ladies and gentlemen , we live at one of those times .	各位先生女士 , 我們住在其中一個時代 。
but for us , i want to talk about three factors today .	但對我們來說 , 我今天想談三個因素 。
and the first of these , the first two of these , is about a shift in power .	首先 , 這裡的前兩個是權力的轉變 。
and the second is about some new dimension which i want to refer to , which has never quite happened in the way it's happening now .	第二個是關於新的維度 , 我想要指的是 , 它從來沒有發生過 。
but let's talk about the shifts of power that are occurring to the world .	但 , 讓我們來談談權力的轉變 , 會發生在世界上 。
and what is happening today is , in one sense , frightening because it's never happened before .	今天發生的事是 , 在某種意義上 , 恐怖 , 因為它從來沒有發生過 。
we have seen lateral shifts of power the power of greece passed to rome and the power shifts that occurred during the european civilizations but we are seeing something slightly different .	我們已經看到了權力轉變了希臘傳往羅馬的力量以及在歐洲文明中發生的權力轉變 , 但我們看到了有點不同的東西 。
for power is not just moving laterally from nation to nation .	權力不僅僅是從國家移到國家 。
it's also moving vertically .	它也垂直移動 。
what's happening today is that the power that was encased , held to accountability , held to the rule of law , within the institution of the nation state has now migrated in very large measure onto the global stage .	今天正在發生的是 , 被監禁的權力 , 被責任的權力 , 被限制在法律的制度中 , 在這個國家的制度已經被移民到全球舞台上 。
the globalization of power we talk about the globalization of markets , but actually it's the globalization of real power .	我們談到全球化市場的全球化 , 但它其實是全球化的權力 。
and where , at the nation state level that power is held to accountability subject to the rule of law , on the international stage it is not .	在國家層面上 , 權力是指責法規的 , 在國際舞台上 , 權力是指責的 。
the international stage and the global stage where power now resides: the power of the internet , the power of the satellite broadcasters , the power of the money changers this vast moneygoround that circulates now 32 times the amount of money necessary for the trade it's supposed to be there to finance the money changers , if you like , the financial speculators that have brought us all to our knees quite recently , the power of the multinational corporations now developing budgets often bigger than mediumsized countries .	國際舞台和全球的權力現在還在國際舞台上:網際網路的力量、衛星廣播的力量、金錢的力量改變了這個巨大的金錢包圍著交易所需的金錢 , 應該是財務改變者 , 如你所說的 , 金錢的權力、金融顧問帶給我們所有人 , 最近 , 跨國企業企業的權力 , 經費者 , 經費大於發展中國家的金融 。
these live in a global space which is largely unregulated , not subject to the rule of law , and in which people may act free of constraint .	這些人生活在一個極為不規則的全球空間裡 , 而不是對法律規則的主題 , 人們可能會不受限制 。
now that suits the powerful up to a moment .	此時此刻 , 此時此刻 , 強而有力 。
it's always suitable for those who have the most power to operate in spaces without constraint , but the lesson of history is that , sooner or later , unregulated space space not subject to the rule of law becomes populated , not just by the things you wanted international trade , the internet , etc . but also by the things you don't want international criminality , international terrorism .	對於那些擁有最大權力的人來說 , 總是適合在空間中運作的人 , 沒有限制 , 但歷史的教訓是 , 更早或更晚 , 沒有規則的空間 , 不單單單是那些你想要的國際貿易、網路等等 。 還有你不想要的事物 , 國際犯罪、國際恐怖主義 。
the revelation of 9/11 is that even if you are the most powerful nation on earth , nevertheless , those who inhabit that space can attack you even in your most iconic of cities one bright september morning .	9/11的揭示是 , 即使你是地球上最強大的國家 , 儘管如此 , 居住的居民 , 那些空間可以攻擊你 , 甚至在你最明亮的城市之一早上 。
it's said that something like 60 percent of the four million dollars that was taken to fund 9/11 actually passed through the institutions of the twin towers which 9/11 destroyed .	據說 , 大約有百分之六十四百萬美金被帶到資助911事件中 , 實際上通過雙胞胎塔 , 911事件摧毀了 。
you see , our enemies also use this space the space of mass travel , the internet , satellite broadcasters to be able to get around their poison , which is about destroying our systems and our ways .	我們的敵人也用這個空間 , 大眾旅行、網際網路、衛星廣播機 , 來圍繞它們的毒物 , 這關乎摧毀我們的系統和方法 。
sooner or later , sooner or later , the rule of history is that where power goes governance must follow .	更早或更早 , 歷史的規則是 , 權力的統治必須遵守 。
and if it is therefore the case , as i believe it is , that one of the phenomenon of our time is the globalization of power , then it follows that one of the challenges of our time is to bring governance to the global space .	如果我相信 , 這種情況正是我們這個時代的一個現象就是全球化的力量 , 那麼我們這個時代的其中一個挑戰就是把治理帶到全球空間 。
and i believe that the decades ahead of us now will be to a greater or lesser extent turbulent the more or less we are able to achieve that aim: to bring governance to the global space .	我相信 , 數十年來 , 我們現在將會成為更大或更少的混亂 , 我們能達成這個目標:將治理帶給全球空間 。
now notice , i'm not talking about government .	請注意 , 我不是在談政府 。
i'm not talking about setting up some global democratic institution .	我不是在說要建立一些全球民主制度 。
my own view , by the way , ladies and gentlemen , is that this is unlikely to be done by spawning more u . n . institutions .	順道一提 , 女士們先生們 , 我自己看來 , 不太可能是藉由產出更多聯合國機構來完成的 。
if we didn't have the u . n . , we'd have to invent it .	如果我們沒有聯合國 , 我們就得發明它 。
the world needs an international forum .	世界需要一個國際論壇 。
it needs a means by which you can legitimize international action .	它需要一個可以合法化國際行動的手段 。
but when it comes to governance of the global space , my guess is this won't happen through the creation of more u . n . institutions .	但當談到全球治理時 , 我猜這不會發生在聯合國創立更多聯合國機構裡 。
it will actually happen by the powerful coming together and making treatybased systems , treatybased agreements , to govern that global space .	它會發生 , 由強而有力的結合 , 創造出以治療為基礎的系統 , 協議 , 來管理這個全球空間 。
and if you look , you can see them happening , already beginning to emerge .	如果你看 , 你可以看到它們正在發生 , 已經開始出現了 。
the world trade organization: treatybased organization , entirely treatybased , and yet , powerful enough to hold even the most powerful , the united states , to account if necessary .	世界貿易組織: 「 條約組織 」 、 「 條約 」 、 「 條約性的組織 , 但 , 強大到足以支撐最強大的美國 , 如果必要的話 。
kyoto: the beginnings of struggling to create a treatybased organization .	kyoto:掙扎的開端 , 創造出以約定為基礎的組織 。
the g20: we know now that we have to put together an institution which is capable of bringing governance to that financial space for financial speculation .	g20:我們現在知道 , 我們得要建立一個機構 , 能夠把治理帶到金融空間中 , 來推動金融推測 。
and that's what the g20 is , a treatybased institution .	而g20就是g20所謂的 「 條約 」 機構 。
now there's a problem there , and we'll come back to it in a minute , which is that if you bring the most powerful together to make the rules in treatybased institutions , to fill that governance space , then what happens to the weak who are left out ?	現在有一個問題 , 我們等一下再回來談一下 , 如果你把最強大的組織集合起來 , 來制定以 「 條約為基礎的機構 」 規則 , 來填補治理空間 , 那會發生什麼事 ?
and that's a big problem , and we'll return to it in just a second .	那是個大問題 , 我們等一下再回來 。
so there's my first message , that if you are to pass through these turbulent times more or less turbulently , then our success in doing that will in large measure depend on our capacity to bring sensible governance to the global space .	所以 , 我的第一個訊息是如果你多花點時間通過這些亂流 , 那麼我們的成功會取決於我們的大量的治理能力 , 取決於我們能把合理的治理能力帶到全球 。
and watch that beginning to happen .	看著這一切開始發生 。
my second point is , and i know i don't have to talk to an audience like this about such a thing , but power is not just shifting vertically , it's also shifting horizontally .	我的第二個重點是 , 我知道我不需要跟這樣的觀眾談談這種事 , 但權力不僅僅是垂直的轉變 , 也是橫向的轉變 。
you might argue that the story , the history of civilizations , has been civilizations gathered around seas with the first ones around the mediterranean , the more recent ones in the ascendents of western power around the atlantic .	你可能會認為 , 關於文明歷史 , 文明歷史 , 一直在海洋中聚集的文明 , 和地中海最早的文明 , 西方的權力越近期 。
well it seems to me that we're now seeing a fundamental shift of power , broadly speaking , away from nations gathered around the atlantic [seaboard] to the nations gathered around the pacific rim .	在我看來 , 我們現在看到的是權力的基本轉變 , 廣泛地說 , 遠離大西洋的國家 , 到太平洋的國家聚集在一起 。
now that begins with economic power , but that's the way it always begins .	這就從經濟力量開始了 , 但這也是它始終的開始 。
you already begin to see the development of foreign policies , the augmentation of military budgets occurring in the other growing powers in the world .	你已經開始看到外交政策的發展 , 軍事預算的擴增 , 發生在世界上其他種植的權力中 。
i think actually this is not so much a shift from the west to the east ; something different is happening .	我認為這不是從西方移轉到東方 , 有些不同的事情正在發生 。
my guess is , for what it's worth , is that the united states will remain the most powerful nation on earth for the next 10 years , 15 , but the context in which she holds her power has now radically altered ; it has radically changed .	我的猜測是 , 為了值得的 , 美國在未來的十年 , 將會保有最強大的國家 , 但她擁有的權力現在已經徹底改變了 ; 它已經徹底地改變了 。
we are coming out of 50 years , most unusual years , of history in which we have had a totally monopolar world , in which every compass needle for or against has to be referenced by its position to washington a world bestrode by a single colossus .	我們在五十年後 , 最不尋常的歷史中 , 我們有一個完全不道德的世界 , 在這個世界中 , 每一根羅盤都必須被華盛頓所羅德的稱呼所指出 , 一個單一的大腸評估 。
but that's not a usual case in history .	但這不是歷史上常見的情況 。
in fact , what's now emerging is the much more normal case of history .	事實上 , 現在出現的是更正常的歷史 。
you're beginning to see the emergence of a multipolar world .	你開始看到多極端世界的出現 。
up until now , the united states has been the dominant feature of our world .	到目前為止 , 美國是我們的世界主流特徵 。
they will remain the most powerful nation , but they will be the most powerful nation in an increasingly multipolar world .	他們會維持最強大的國家 , 但他們將會是世界上越來越多極端國家最強大的國家 。
and you begin to see the alternative centers of power building up in china , of course , though my own guess is that china's ascent to greatness is not smooth .	你開始看到中國的另一種權力中心 , 當然 , 我的猜測是 , 中國的優秀性不是平滑的 。
it's going to be quite grumpy as china begins to democratize her society after liberalizing her economy .	當中國開始將她的社會民主化 , 在解放她的經濟之後 , 將會很糟糕 。
but that's a subject of a different discussion .	但這是一個不同的討論題目 。
you see india , you see brazil .	你看到印度 , 你看到巴西 。
you see increasingly that the world now looks actually , for us europeans , much more like europe in the 19th century .	你可以看到 , 越來越多的世界看起來 , 對我們歐洲人來說 , 比較像19世紀的歐洲人 。
europe in the 19th century: a great british foreign secretary , lord canning , used to describe it as the " european concert of powers . "	歐洲在十九世紀:一個偉大的英國外交部秘書 , 名稱是 「 歐洲的權力協議 」 。
there was a balance , a fivesided balance .	有一個平衡 , 一個五邊平衡 。
britain always played to the balance .	英國一直都在平衡中 。
if paris got together with berlin , britain got together with vienna and rome to provide a counterbalance .	如果巴黎和柏林合作 , 英國與維也納和羅馬結合 , 提供一個反對的平衡 。
now notice , in a period which is dominated by a monopolar world , you have fixed alliances nato , the warsaw pact .	請注意 , 在一個由獨立世界主導的時期 , 你有固定的盟國領袖 , 華沙特 。
a fixed polarity of power means fixed alliances .	固定的權力是固定的聯盟 。
but a multiple polarity of power means shifting and changing alliances .	但多個權力意味著移轉和改變聯盟 。
and that's the world we're coming into , in which we will increasingly see that our alliances are not fixed .	那就是我們要進入的世界 , 我們會逐漸看到我們的聯盟並不固定 。
canning , the great british foreign secretary once said , " britain has a common interest , but no common allies . "	偉大的英國外交秘書曾說過: 「 英國有共同的利益 , 但沒有共通的盟友 。 」
and we will see increasingly that even we in the west will reach out , have to reach out , beyond the cozy circle of the atlantic powers to make alliances with others if we want to get things done in the world .	我們會看到 , 即使我們西方也能向外伸出援手 , 超越大西洋電力的舒適圈 , 來和他人結盟 , 如果我們想把世界做好 。
note , that when we went into libya , it was not good enough for the west to do it alone ; we had to bring others in .	請注意 , 當我們走進利比亞時 , 西方國家不夠好 ; 我們得把他人帶進去 。
we had to bring , in this case , the arab league in .	在這個案例中 , 我們必須引進阿拉伯聯盟 。
my guess is iraq and afghanistan are the last times when the west has tried to do it themselves , and we haven't succeeded .	我的猜測是伊拉克和阿富汗最後一次 , 西方試圖自己做這件事 , 我們還沒成功 。
my guess is that we're reaching the beginning of the end of 400 years i say 400 years because it's the end of the ottoman empire of the hegemony of western power , western institutions and western values .	我的猜測是400年後 , 我說是400年之初 , 因為它是西方權力的終點 , 西方制度和西方價值觀的末端 。
you know , up until now , if the west got its act together , it could propose and dispose in every corner of the world .	你知道 , 直到現在 , 如果西方國家能一起行動 , 它可以在世界各個角落提出建議和用途 。
but that's no longer true .	但這已經不是真的了 。
take the last financial crisis after the second world war .	以第二次世界大戰後的金融危機為例 。
the west got together the bretton woods institution , world bank , international monetary fund the problem solved .	西方國家的布雷頓森林機構 , 世界銀行、國際貨幣基金--問題解決了 。
now we have to call in others .	現在我們要打電話給他人 。
now we have to create the g20 .	現在我們必須創造g20 。
now we have to reach beyond the cozy circle of our western friends .	我們必須超越我們西方的舒適圈 。
let me make a prediction for you , which is probably even more startling .	讓我預測一下 , 這可能更令人驚訝 。
i suspect we are now reaching the end of 400 years when western power was enough .	我猜我們現在已經到了400年後 , 西方的權力已經足夠了 。
people say to me , " the chinese , of course , they'll never get themselves involved in peacemaking , multilateral peacemaking around the world . "	人們對我說: 「 中國 , 當然 , 他們永遠不會參與到世界各地的和平、多邊的和平 。 」
oh yes ? why not ?	噢 ? 爲什麽不呢 ?
how many chinese troops are serving under the blue beret , serving under the blue flag , serving under the u . n . command in the world today ?	有多少中國軍隊在藍色貝雷特下服務 , 在藍色旗幟下服務 , 在聯合國指揮下服務 ?
how many americans ? 11 .	有多少美國人 ? 11 。
what is the largest naval contingent tackling the issue of somali pirates ?	索馬利亞海盜最大的海軍如何解決索馬利亞海盜問題 ?
the chinese naval contingent .	中國的海軍陸戰隊 。
of course they are , they are a mercantilist nation .	當然 , 他們是一位超級富豪的國家 。
they want to keep the sea lanes open .	他們想讓海道保持開放 。
increasingly , we are going to have to do business with people with whom we do not share values , but with whom , for the moment , we share common interests .	漸漸地 , 我們要和那些我們不共享價值的人做生意 , 但 , 在此時此刻 , 我們有共同的利益 。
it's a whole new different way of looking at the world that is now emerging .	這是一種全新的看待世界的方式 , 現在正在興起 。
and here's the third factor , which is totally different .	第三個因素 , 完全不同 。
today in our modern world , because of the internet , because of the kinds of things people have been talking about here , everything is connected to everything .	現今在我們的現代世界裡 , 因為網際網路 , 人們一直在談論這些東西 , 所有東西都和所有東西有關 。
we are now interdependent .	我們現在是相互依賴的 。
we are now interlocked , as nations , as individuals , in a way which has never been the case before , never been the case before .	我們現在彼此連結 , 作為國家 , 作為個體 , 在以前從來沒有發生過這種情況下 , 從來沒有發生過 。
the interrelationship of nations , well it's always existed .	國家之間的關聯性 , 總是存在著 。
diplomacy is about managing the interrelationship of nations .	外交的重點是要管理國家之間的關係 。
but now we are intimately locked together .	但現在我們被緊密連結在一起 。
you get swine flu in mexico , it's a problem for charles de gaulle airport 24 hours later .	在墨西哥 , 豬流感是24小時後查爾斯國際安全局在24小時後出現的問題 。
lehman brothers goes down , the whole lot collapses .	雷曼兄弟下降了 , 整個崩潰了 。
there are fires in the steppes of russia , food riots in africa .	在俄羅斯、非洲的糧食暴動中 , 有火災 。
we are all now deeply , deeply , deeply interconnected .	我們現在都深深地相互連結了 。
and what that means is the idea of a nation state acting alone , not connected with others , not working with others , is no longer a viable proposition .	意思是說 , 一個國家獨自執行 , 而非和他人連結 , 不再與他人合作 , 不再是可行的提議 。
because the actions of a nation state are neither confined to itself , nor is it sufficient for the nation state itself to control its own territory , because the effects outside the nation state are now beginning to affect what happens inside them .	因為一個國家的行動 , 不是因為它本身 , 也不足以控制它自己的國度 , 因為在國外的影響已經開始影響它們的內部 。
i was a young soldier in the last of the small empire wars of britain .	我是英國最後一名年輕的軍人 。
at that time , the defense of my country was about one thing and one thing only: how strong was our army , how strong was our air force , how strong was our navy and how strong were our allies .	那時 , 我的國家辯護的重點是一件事 , 只有一件事:我們的軍隊有多強 , 我們的空軍有多強 , 我們的海軍有多強 , 我們的盟友有多強 。
that was when the enemy was outside the walls .	那是在牆外的敵人 。
now the enemy is inside the walls .	敵人在牆壁內 。
now if i want to talk about the defense of my country , i have to speak to the minister of health because pandemic disease is a threat to my security , i have to speak to the minister of agriculture because food security is a threat to my security , i have to speak to the minister of industry because the fragility of our hitech infrastructure is now a point of attack for our enemies as we see from cyber warfare i have to speak to the minister of home affairs because who has entered my country , who lives in that terraced house in that inner city has a direct effect on what happens in my country as we in london saw in the 7/7 bombings .	現在 , 如果我想要談我的國家防禦 , 我得要和健康部談談 , 因為流行病對我的安全有威脅 , 我得要和農業部談談 , 因為糧食安全對我安全的威脅 , 我得要和產業部談談 , 因為我們的希臘基礎設施的脆弱 , 是我們的敵人 , 來對我們的敵人 , 來談談到我們在網路戰爭中所造成的衝擊 , 我得要和國內部的人談談 , 因爲我們國內的主流感 , 因爲我們已經失去了7個居家 。
it's no longer the case that the security of a country is simply a matter for its soldiers and its ministry of defense .	國家的安全性不再是對軍人和國防方面的重要性 。
it's its capacity to lock together its institutions .	它能夠把制度鎖在一起 。
and this tells you something very important .	這告訴各位一件非常重要的事 。
it tells you that , in fact , our governments , vertically constructed , constructed on the economic model of the industrial revolution vertical hierarchy , specialization of tasks , command structures have got the wrong structures completely .	它告訴你 , 事實上 , 我們的政府 , 垂直建構 , 建立在工業革命的經濟模式上 , 垂直階級制度 , 任務、指令結構完全錯誤的結構 。
you in business know that the paradigm structure of our time , ladies and gentlemen , is the network .	在商業界你知道我們這個時代的典範結構 , 女士們先生們 , 就是網路 。
it's your capacity to network that matters , both within your governments and externally .	這是你對網絡很重要的能力 , 無論在你的政府或外部都很重要 。
so here is ashdown's third law .	這是ashdown的第三個法則 。
by the way , don't ask me about ashdown's first law and second law because i haven't invented those yet ; it always sounds better if there's a third law , doesn't it ?	順便一提 , 不要問阿什德市第一定律和第二定律 , 因為我還沒發明過 ; 若有第三條法則 , 聽起來會比較好嗎 ?
ashdown's third law is that in the modern age , where everything is connected to everything , the most important thing about what you can do is what you can do with others .	ashdown的第三個法則是 , 在現代 , 一切都與一切相關 , 最重要的是你能做的事 , 就是你能和他人做的事 。
the most important bit about your structure whether you're a government , whether you're an army regiment , whether you're a business is your docking points , your interconnectors , your capacity to network with others .	不論你是政府 , 不論你是軍隊註冊 , 不論你是生意是你的點 , 你的國際指標 , 你和他人建立連結的能力 。
you understand that in industry ; governments don't .	你明白這一點 , 在工業界 , 政府不懂 。
but now one final thing .	但最後一件事 。
if it is the case , ladies and gentlemen and it is that we are now locked together in a way that has never been quite the same before , then it's also the case that we share a destiny with each other .	如果是這樣的 , 各位先生女士們 , 是我們現在被鎖在一個從未相同的方式上 , 那也是我們彼此共同命運的案例 。
suddenly and for the very first time , collective defense , the thing that has dominated us as the concept of securing our nations , is no longer enough .	突然間 , 第一次 , 集體的防禦 , 把我們當作安全的概念 , 不再足夠 。
it used to be the case that if my tribe was more powerful than their tribe , i was safe ; if my country was more powerful than their country , i was safe ; my alliance , like nato , was more powerful than their alliance , i was safe .	以前 , 如果我的部落比他們的部落更強大 , 我是安全的 ; 如果我的國家比他們的國家強大 , 我是安全的 ; 我的盟國 , 像娜塔 , 比他們的盟友更強大 , 我是安全的 。
it is no longer the case .	不再是這樣 。
the advent of the interconnectedness and of the weapons of mass destruction means that , increasingly , i share a destiny with my enemy .	大規模毀滅性武器的發生 , 意味著 , 越來越多 , 我和敵人有著共同的命運 。
when i was a diplomat negotiating the disarmament treaties with the soviet union in geneva in the 1970s , we succeeded because we understood we shared a destiny with them .	當我是外交官 , 在1970年代和蘇聯在日內瓦的蘇聯協會談判時 , 我們成功了 , 因為我們了解我們和他們分享命運 。
collective security is not enough .	集體安全不夠 。
peace has come to northern ireland because both sides realized that the zerosum game couldn't work .	和平來到北愛爾蘭 , 因為雙方都了解到 , 零和賽局是行不通的 。
they shared a destiny with their enemies .	他們與敵人分享命運 。
one of the great barriers to peace in the middle east is that both sides , both israel and , i think , the palestinians , do not understand that they share a collective destiny .	中東和平的大阻礙之一 , 是兩方 , 以色列 , 我認為 , 巴勒斯坦人 , 並不知道他們有共同的命運 。
and so suddenly , ladies and gentlemen , what has been the proposition of visionaries and poets down the ages becomes something we have to take seriously as a matter of public policy .	所以 , 各位先生女士們 , 遠見和詩人的主張 , 在這個時代 , 我們必須認真看待公共政策的問題 。
i started with a poem , i'll end with one .	我從一首詩開始 , 以一首詩作結尾 。
the great poem of john donne's .	約翰•唐尼的偉大詩 。
" send not for whom the bell tolls . "	「 請不要送鈴聲給誰 。 」
the poem is called " no man is an island . "	這首詩叫做 「 沒有人是島嶼 」 。
and it goes: " every man's death affected me , for i am involved in mankind , send not to ask for whom the bell tolls , it tolls for thee . "	上面寫著: 「 每個人的死亡都影響著我 , 因為我參與人類 , 不要求鐘聲叫叫誰 , 它會為elle 。 」
for john donne , a recommendation of morality .	對於約翰•唐尼 , 道德建議 。
for us , i think , part of the equation for our survival .	對我們來說 , 我想 , 是我們生存的一部分 。
to find the path to long life and health , dan buettner and team study the world's " blue zones , " communities whose elders live with vim and vigor to recordsetting age . at tedxtc , he shares the 9 common diet and lifestyle habits that keep them spry past age 100 .	為了找到長壽和健康的路徑 , 丹•布特納和團隊研究世界的 「 藍寶區 」 , 那些長者和vim及訪客一起生活的社區 , 在tedxtc上 , 他分享了9種常見的飲食和生活方式習慣 , 讓他們在過去一百歲以上流行 。
biology , culture , exploration , food , health , life , science	生物、文化、探索、食物、健康、科學、科學、科學、科學、生物 。
dan buettner: how to live to be 100+	danbuetner:如何活著成為一百個+百個 。
something called the danish twin study established that only about 10 percent of how long the average person lives , within certain biological limits , is dictated by our genes .	所謂的丹麥雙胞胎研究機構 , 在某些生物限制中 , 只有百分之十的平均壽命 , 由我們的基因決定 。
the other 90 percent is dictated by our lifestyle .	另外90%是由我們的生活方式來決定 。
so the premise of blue zones: if we can find the optimal lifestyle of longevity we can come up with a de facto formula for longevity .	所以藍色區域的前提是:如果我們能找到長壽的最佳生活方式 , 我們就能找到一個長壽的真相公式 。
but if you ask the average american what the optimal formula of longevity is , they probably couldn't tell you .	但如果你問一般美國人 , 長壽的最佳公式是什麼 , 他們可能無法告訴你 。
they've probably heard of the south beach diet , or the atkins diet .	他們可能聽說過南海灘飲食 , 或墨水飲食 。
you have the usda food pyramid .	你有美國食品金字塔 。
there is what oprah tells us .	歐普拉告訴我們什麼 。
there is what doctor oz tells us .	奧茲醫生告訴我們什麼 。
the fact of the matter is there is a lot of confusion around what really helps us live longer better .	事實是 , 對於真正幫助我們活得更久的困惑 , 有很多的困惑 。
should you be running marathons or doing yoga ?	你該跑馬拉松還是做瑜伽嗎 ?
should you eat organic meats or should you be eating tofu ?	你應該要吃有機肉 , 還是要吃豆腐 ?
when it comes to supplements , should you be taking them ?	談到供應 , 你應該帶他們去嗎 ?
how about these hormones or resveratrol ?	荷爾蒙或逆轉荷爾蒙呢 ?
and does purpose play into it ?	目的是要玩嗎 ?
spirituality ? and how about how we socialize ?	靈性 ? 那我們如何社交呢 ?
well , our approach to finding longevity was to team up with national geographic , and the national institute on aging , to find the four demographically confirmed areas that are geographically defined .	我們找到長壽的方法是和國家地理頻道合作 , 國家老化研究所 , 找出四個人口分佈地理定義的區域 。
and then bring a team of experts in there to methodically go through exactly what these people do , to distill down the crosscultural distillation .	接著 , 帶一組專家去處理這些人在做的事 , 去除跨文化的分散 。
and at the end of this i'm going to tell you what that distillation is .	最後 , 我要告訴你們這個幻視是什麼 。
but first i'd like to debunk some common myths when it comes to longevity .	但 , 首先 , 我想在談到長壽時展現一些常見的迷思 。
and the first myth is if you try really hard you can live to be 100 .	第一個迷思是如果你真的努力去活一百歲
the problem is , only about one out of 5 , 000 people in america live to be 100 .	問題是 , 五千人當中只有一人活到一百歲 。
your chances are very low .	你的機率非常低 。
even though it's the fastest growing demographic in america , it's hard to reach 100 .	儘管它是美國成長最快的人口 , 很難達到一百人 。
the problem is that we're not programmed for longevity .	問題是 , 我們不是為了長壽而設計 。
we are programmed for something called procreative success .	我們為 「 繁榮成功 」 程式設計 。
i love that word .	我愛那個詞 。
it reminds me of my college days .	它提醒了我大學的日子 。
biologists term procreative success to mean the age where you have children and then another generation , the age when your children have children .	生物學家稱之為 「 成功 」 , 意思是你有孩子的年齡 , 接著是另一代 , 你的孩子有孩子的年齡 。
after that the effect of evolution completely dissipates .	之後演化的效應完全消失了 。
if you're a mammal , if you're a rat or an elephant , or a human , in between , it's the same story .	如果你是哺乳類 , 如果你是一隻老鼠或一隻大象 , 或在兩者之間 , 相同的故事 。
so to make it to age 100 , you not only have to have had a very good lifestyle , you also have to have won the genetic lottery .	所以要讓它變成一百歲 , 你不只擁有良好的生活方式 , 你還得贏得基因彩票 。
the second myth is , there are treatments that can help slow , reverse , or even stop aging .	第二個迷思是 , 有治療方法可以緩慢、反轉 , 甚至停止老化 。
when you think of it , there is 99 things that can age us .	想想看 , 有99件事情可以讓我們老化 。
deprive your brain of oxygen for just a few minutes , those brain cells die , they never come back .	只要幾分鐘 , 腦細胞就會死亡 , 它們永遠不會回來 。
play tennis too hard , on your knees , ruin your cartilage , the cartilage never comes back .	玩網球太硬 , 在你的膝蓋上 , 你的軟骨 , 軟骨永遠不會回來 。
our arteries can clog . our brains can gunk up with plaque , and we can get alzheimer's .	我們的動脈可以網索 , 我們的大腦可以用斑塊來連接 , 我們就能得到阿茲海默症 。
there is just too many things to go wrong .	有太多事情會出錯 。
our bodies have 35 trillion cells , trillion with a " t . " we're talking national debt numbers here .	我們的身體有35兆個細胞 , 裡面有 「 t 」 。 我們在這裡談的是國家債務數字 。
those cells turn themselves over once every eight years .	這些細胞每八年就會轉動一次 。
and every time they turn themselves over there is some damage . and that damage builds up .	每當他們把自己轉過來 , 就會有一些損害 , 而損害就會增加 。
and it builds up exponentially .	它是以指數型態來建造的 。
it's a little bit like the days when we all had beatles albums or eagles albums and we'd make a copy of that on a cassette tape , and let our friends copy that cassette tape , and pretty soon , with successive generations that tape sounds like garbage .	有點像我們都有披頭四的專輯或老鷹的日子 , 我們會用膠帶做複本 , 讓我們的朋友複製膠帶 , 很快地 , 帶有成功的世代 , 像垃圾一樣的膠帶 。
well , the same things happen to our cells .	同樣的事情也發生在我們的細胞上 。
that's why a 65yearold person is aging at a rate of about 125 times faster than a 12yearold person .	這就是為什麼一個65歲的孩子在老化的速度 , 比一個12歲的人快125倍 。
so , if there is nothing you can do to slow your aging or stop your aging , what am i doing here ?	所以 , 如果沒有東西可以減緩你的老化或阻止你的老化 , 我在這裡做什麼 ?
well , the fact of the matter is the best science tells us that the capacity of the human body , my body , your body , is about 90 years , a little bit more for women .	事實上 , 最好的科學告訴我們 , 人體的能力 , 我的身體 , 你的身體 , 大約九十年 , 對女人來說 , 有一點點 。
but life expectancy in this country is only 78 .	但在這個國家的平均壽命只有78歲 。
so somewhere along the line , we're leaving about 12 good years on the table .	所以 , 在線上某個地方 , 我們在桌子上留下了大約12年的美好年 。
these are years that we could get .	這些年是我們可以得到的 。
and research shows that they would be years largely free of chronic disease , heart disease , cancer and diabetes .	研究顯示 , 牠們大多會不會因為慢性疾病 , 心臟病 , 癌症和糖尿病 。
we think the best way to get these missing years is to look at the cultures around the world that are actually experiencing them , areas where people are living to age 100 at rates up to 10 times greater than we are , areas where the life expectancy is an extra dozen years , the rate of middle age mortality is a fraction of what it is in this country .	我們認為這些消失的最佳方法就是看看全世界的文化 , 真正體驗他們 , 居住的地方 , 人口比我們高出十倍 , 人口預期壽命延長十倍 , 中年死亡率是這個國家中年死亡率的一部分 。
we found our first blue zone about 125 miles off the coast of italy , on the island of sardinia .	我們在義大利海岸找到了第一區大約125英里的藍色區域 , 位在薩丁尼亞島 。
and not the entire island , the island is about 1 . 4 million people , but only up in the highlands , an area called the nuoro province .	而不是整個島 , 島嶼大約有一百四百萬人 , 但在高地 , 一個叫做努羅省的地方 。
and here we have this area where men live the longest , about 10 times more centenarians than we have here in america .	在這裡 , 男性壽命最長的區域 , 比美國這裡的百歲人多十倍 。
and this is a place where people not only reach age 100 , they do so with extraordinary vigor .	這個地方 , 人們不只達到一百歲 , 他們還用非凡的維生人來做這件事 。
places where 102 year olds still ride their bike to work , chop wood , and can beat a guy 60 years younger than them .	在那裡 , 102歲的老年人仍然騎自行車去工作 , 木頭可以擊敗一個比他們年輕六十歲的人 。
their history actually goes back to about the time of christ .	他們的歷史其實是回到基督時代 。
it's actually a bronze age culture that's been isolated .	它實際上是一個被隔離的青銅文化 。
because the land is so infertile , they largely are shepherds , which occasions regular , lowintensity physical activity .	因為土地是如此的不公平 , 它們大多是牧羊 , 常常有的、較低的身體活動 。
their diet is mostly plantbased , accentuated with foods that they can carry into the fields .	牠們的飲食主要是以植物為基礎的 , 牠們能帶到田野中 。
they came up with an unleavened whole wheat bread called carta musica made out of durum wheat , a type of cheese made from grassfed animals so the cheese is high in omega3 fatty acids instead of omega6 fatty acids from cornfed animals , and a type of wine that has three times the level of polyphenols than any known wine in the world .	他們想出了無數的麵包 , 叫做carta音樂 , 由土壤餵養的動物所組成 , 一種乳酪是高於omega-3脂肪酸而不是omega-6脂肪酸來自玉米受損的動物 , 還有一種葡萄酒含有三倍於全世界所知的葡萄酒量 。
but the real secret i think lies more in the way that they organize their society .	但我認為真正的秘密是他們如何組織他們的社會 。
and one of the most salient elements of the sardinian society is how they treat older people .	而薩丁尼亞社會最瘋狂的元素之一就是他們如何對待老年人 。
you ever notice here in america , social equity seems to peak at about age 24 ?	你有沒有注意到在美國 , 社會平等似乎在24歲時達到高峰 ?
just look at the advertisements .	看看廣告 。
here in sardinia , the older you get the more equity you have , the more wisdom you're celebrated for .	在薩丁尼亞 , 越老越平等 , 你就越有智慧 。
you go into the bars in sardinia , instead of seeing the sports illustrated swimsuit calendar , you see the centenarian of the month calendar .	你走進薩丁尼亞的酒吧 , 不是看運動的標示游泳日曆 , 而是月曆的百歲人 。
this , as it turns out , is not only good for your aging parents to keep them close to the family it imparts about four to six years of extra life expectancy research shows it's also good for the children of those families , who have lower rates of mortality and lower rates of disease .	結果發現 , 這不僅對你老年的父母來說是好的 , 可以讓他們靠近家人 , 提高大約四到六年的預期壽命研究顯示 , 對那些家庭的孩子而言 , 死亡率較低 , 疾病的死亡率也較低 。
that's called the grandmother effect .	這叫做 「 祖母效應 」 。
we found our second blue zone on the other side of the planet , about 800 miles south of tokyo , on the archipelago of okinawa .	我們在地球的另一端發現了第二個藍色區域 , 東京南部大約有八百英哩 , 在奧林加拉哥的阿基拉哥 。
okinawa is actually 161 small islands .	okinawa其實是161個小島 。
and in the northern part of the main island , this is ground zero for world longevity .	在主島北部 , 這是世界長壽的根本零 。
this is a place where the oldest living female population is found .	這是最古老的女性族群所在的地方 。
it's a place where people have the longest disabilityfree life expectancy in the world .	這個地方 , 人們有世界上最長壽的缺陷人數 。
they have what we want .	他們有我們想要的 。
they live a long time , and tend to die in their sleep , very quickly , and often , i can tell you , after sex .	牠們活了很長一段時間 , 往往在牠們的睡眠很快 , 通常 , 我可以告訴你 , 在性愛之後 。
they live about seven good years longer than the average american .	他們的壽命比美國人平均要長七年 。
five times as many centenarians as we have in america .	美國的百歲人數有五倍 。
one fifth the rate of colon and breast cancer , big killers here in america .	第五個蜂群和乳癌的比率 , 美國這裡的大型殺手 。
and one sixth the rate of cardiovascular disease .	六分之一的心血管疾病 。
and the fact that this culture has yielded these numbers suggests strongly they have something to teach us .	事實上 , 這個文化給了這些數字 , 表示他們有一定的教訓能力 。
what do they do ?	他們會怎麼做 ?
once again , a plantbased diet , full of vegetables with lots of color in them .	再一次 , 一個以植物為基礎的飲食 , 裡面有許多顏色的蔬菜 。
and they eat about eight times as much tofu as americans do .	他們吃大約八倍的豆腐比美國人多 。
more significant than what they eat is how they eat it .	比他們吃的東西更重要 。
they have all kinds of little strategies to keep from overeating , which , as you know , is a big problem here in america .	他們有各式各樣的小策略來避免過量 , 如你所知 , 在美國 , 是個大問題 。
a few of the strategies we observed: they eat off of smaller plates , so they tend to eat fewer calories at every sitting .	我們觀察到的幾個策略是:它們會吃比較小的盤子 , 所以它們通常會吃比較少的卡路里 。
instead of serving family style , where you can sort of mindlessly eat as you're talking , they serve at the counter , put the food away , and then bring it to the table .	與其提供家庭風格 , 你可以在談話時不經心地吃東西 , 他們會在櫃台上服務 , 把食物帶走 , 然後把它帶到桌子上 。
they also have a 3 , 000yearold adage , which i think is the greatest sort of diet suggestion ever invented .	他們還有一個三千歲的小孩 , 我覺得這是史上最棒的飲食建議 。
it was invented by confucius .	它是由混亂創造出來的 。
and that diet is known as the hara , hatchi , bu diet .	這種飲食就是所謂的 「 哈特拉、哈蒂、布爾飲食 」 。
it's simply a little saying these people say before their meal to remind them to stop eating when their stomach is [80] percent full .	只是說這些人在吃飯前提醒他們要停止吃80%的食物
it takes about a half hour for that full feeling to travel from your belly to your brain .	要花半小時的時間才能從腹部到腦部旅行 。
and by remembering to stop at 80 percent it helps keep you from doing that very thing .	記住要停止百分之八十 , 它能協助你避免做這件事 。
but , like sardinia , okinawa has a few social constructs that we can associate with longevity .	但 , 就像薩丁尼亞一樣 , okinawa有幾個社會建構 , 我們能與長壽相關 。
we know that isolation kills .	我們知道隔離會致命 。
fifteen years ago , the average american had three good friends .	15年前 , 美國平均有三個好朋友 。
we're down to one and half right now .	我們現在已經降到一半了 。
if you were lucky enough to be born in okinawa , you were born into a system where you automatically have a half a dozen friends with whom you travel through life .	如果你夠幸運地出生在okinawa , 你就生在一個系統中 , 你自動擁有一半的朋友 , 和你一輩子旅行 。
they call it a moai . and if you're in a moai you're expected to share the bounty if you encounter luck , and if things go bad , child gets sick , parent dies , you always have somebody who has your back .	他們稱它為 「 摩艾 」 。 如果你在摩艾 , 你被期待要分享這個反彈 , 如果你碰到運氣 , 如果壞事發生 , 孩子生病 , 父母就會死亡 , 你總是有你背後的人 。
this particular moai , these five ladies have been together for 97 years .	這張特別的moai , 這五位女士已經在一起了九十七年 。
their average age is 102 .	他們的平均年齡是102歲 。
typically in america we've divided our adult life up into two sections .	通常在美國 , 我們把成年人的生命分為兩部分 。
there is our work life , where we're productive .	我們的工作是有生產力的 。
and then one day , boom , we retire .	然後有一天 , 砰 , 我們退休了 。
and typically that has meant retiring to the easy chair , or going down to arizona to play golf .	通常這意味著退休 , 退休到亞利桑那州去玩高爾夫球 。
in the okinawan language there is not even a word for retirement .	在okinawan語言中 , 甚至沒有退休的詞語 。
instead there is one word that imbues your entire life , and that word is " ikigai . "	相反地 , 有一個詞會影響你一生 , 這個詞就是 「 ikigai 」 。
and , roughly translated , it means " the reason for which you wake up in the morning . "	大概是翻譯 , 意思是 「 早上起床的理由 。 」
for this 102yearold karate master , his ikigai was carrying forth this martial art .	對於這位102歲的卡爾特•卡爾特 , 他的ikigai正為此帶著這場火星藝術 。
for this hundredyearold fisherman it was continuing to catch fish for his family three times a week .	對這位百歲的漁夫來說 , 每週要捕魚三次 。
and this is a question . the national institute on aging actually gave us a questionnaire to give these centenarians .	這是一個問題 , 國家老化的研究所 , 給了我們一個問卷 , 給這些百歲人 。
and one of the questions , they were very culturally astute , the people who put the questionnaire .	其中一個問題是 , 他們是非常文化的 , 那些提出問卷的人 。
one of the questions was , " what is your ikigai ? "	其中一個問題是: 「 你的ikigai是什麼 ? 」
they instantly knew why they woke up in the morning .	他們馬上就知道為什麼早上起床 。
for this 102 year old woman , her ikigai was simply her greatgreatgreatgranddaughter .	這位102歲的女子 , 她的ikigai只是她的曾曾曾曾曾孫女 。
two girls separated in age by 101 and a half years .	兩個女孩在101歲時分離 。
and i asked her what it felt like to hold a greatgreatgreatgranddaughter .	我問她 , 拿著一個曾曾曾曾孫女的感覺是什麼樣子 。
and she put her head back and she said , " it feels like leaping into heaven . "	她把頭放回來 , 說: 「 感覺就像跳進天堂 。 」
i thought that was a wonderful thought .	我覺得這是個很棒的思維 。
my editor at geographic wanted me to find america's blue zone .	我在地理雜誌的編輯希望我能找到美國的藍色區域 。
and for a while we looked on the prairies of minnesota , where actually there is a very high proportion of centenarians .	有一陣子 , 我們在明尼蘇達的草原上 , 那裡有非常高的百歲人 。
but that's because all the young people left .	但那是因為所有的年輕人都離開了 。
so , we turned to the data again .	所以 , 我們又轉向數據 。
and we found america's longestlived population among the seventhday adventists concentrated in and around loma linda , california .	我們發現了美國最長壽的人口 , 七天的冒險家集中在加州的洛馬林達市附近 。
adventists are conservative methodists .	進步主義者是保守主義者 。
they celebrate their sabbath from sunset on friday till sunset on saturday .	星期五 , 他們在星期五的日落慶祝自己的休息日 。
a " 24hour sanctuary in time , " they call it .	他們稱之為 「 24小時的聖所 」 。
and they follow five little habits that conveys to them extraordinary longevity , comparatively speaking .	他們遵循了五個小習慣 , 傳遞給他們非凡的長壽 , 相較之下 , 他們會說話 。
in america here , life expectancy for the average woman is 80 .	在美國 , 平均女性平均壽命是80歲 。
but for an adventist woman , their life expectancy is 89 .	但對一位臨時主義的女性而言 , 他們的壽命是89 。
and the difference is even more pronounced among men , who are expected to live about 11 years longer than their american counterparts .	與男性之間的差異更為明顯 , 他們預期能活得比他們美國的對手多11年 。
now , this is a study that followed about 70 , 000 people for 30 years .	這個研究追蹤了大約七萬人三十年 。
sterling study . and i think it supremely illustrates the premise of this blue zone project .	很驚人的研究 。 我想它馬上就說明了這個藍色區域專案的前提 。
this is a heterogeneous community .	這是一個異性戀的社群 。
it's white , black , hispanic , asian .	它是白色、黑色、西班牙裔、亞洲人 。
the only thing that they have in common are a set of very small lifestyle habits that they follow ritualistically for most of their lives .	唯一的共通點 , 是一組非常小的生活習慣 , 讓他們遵循傳統生活習慣 。
they take their diet directly from the bible .	他們從聖經直接取飲食 。
genesis: chapter one , verse [29] , where god talks about legumes and seeds , and on one more stanza about green plants , ostensibly missing is meat .	基因:第一章 , 和第二章 , 上帝談到樂高和種子 , 再來談談綠色植物 , 很可能缺少的是肉 。
they take this sanctuary in time very serious .	他們認真看待這個保護區 。
for 24 hours every week , no matter how busy they are , how stressed out they are at work , where the kids need to be driven , they stop everything and they focus on their god , their social network , and then , hardwired right in the religion , are nature walks .	每週24小時 , 不論他們多忙 , 工作壓力多大 , 孩子們需要被開車 , 停車 , 專注於上帝、社交網路 , 然後 , 在宗教中 , 天生就行走了 。
and the power of this is not that it's done occasionally , the power is it's done every week for a lifetime .	這種力量的力量並不是偶爾 , 它的力量是 , 每週一次都要完成的 。
none of it's hard . none of it costs money .	沒有一個是難的 , 沒有一個花錢 。
adventists also tend to hang out with other adventists .	進步主義者也傾向和其他進步主義者相處 。
so , if you go to an adventist's party you don't see people swilling jim beam or rolling a joint .	所以 , 如果你去參加一個冒險家的派對 , 你不會看到人們在游泳時游泳 , 或是在關節上跑 。
instead they're talking about their next nature walk , exchanging recipes , and yes , they pray .	相反地 , 他們談的是下一個大自然走路 , 交換食譜 , 是的 , 他們祈禱 。
but they influence each other in profound and measurable ways .	但它們會以深遠且可測量的方式影響彼此 。
this is a culture that has yielded ellsworth whareham .	這個文化產出了埃爾斯•威倫漢姆 。
ellsworth whareham is 97 years old .	埃爾斯•華麗姆是97歲 。
he's a multimillionaire , yet when a contractor wanted 6 , 000 dollars to build a privacy fence , he said , " for that kind of money i'll do it myself . "	他是個百萬百萬富翁 , 但當一個承包商想要蓋一個隱私籬時 , 他說: 「 為了這類錢 , 我會自己做 。 」
so for the next three days he was out shoveling cement , and hauling poles around .	所以 , 接下來的三天他出去發發發射水泥 , 四處挖洞 。
and predictably , perhaps , on the fourth day he ended up in the operating room .	可想而知 , 或許 , 在第四天 , 他最後到了手術室 。
but not as the guy on the table ; the guy doing openheart surgery .	但不是桌子上的那個人 , 而是在做開心手術的人 。
at 97 he still does 20 openheart surgeries every month .	九十七歲時 , 他每個月仍然進行二十次開放式手術 。
ed rawlings , 103 years old now , an active cowboy , starts his morning with a swim .	愛德華•古林斯 , 103歲 , 一位活躍的牛仔 , 早上開始了游泳 。
and on weekends he likes to put on the boards , throw up rooster tails .	在週末 , 他喜歡把板子放上去 , 扔上長尾 。
her grandson actually lives in the twin cities here .	她的孫子其實住在雙胞胎城市裡 。
she starts her day with lifting weights .	她從每天開始舉起重量開始 。
she rides her bicycle .	她騎著腳踏車 。
and then she gets in her rootbeer colored 1994 cadillac seville , and tears down the san bernardino freeway , where she still volunteers for seven different organizations .	接著 , 她進入了她的根部1994年的凱迪拉克•席維爾 , 在聖貝納多高速公路上 , 她仍然自願參與七個不同的組織 。
i've been on 19 hardcore expeditions .	我曾經參加過19個硬體探險 。
i'm probably the only person you'll ever meet who rode his bicycle across the sahara desert without sunscreen .	我可能是唯一一個你見過的人 , 穿越撒哈拉沙漠 , 穿越撒哈拉沙漠 。
but i'll tell you , there is no adventure more harrowing than riding shotgun with marge deton .	但我要告訴各位 , 沒有冒險比和馬吉•德頓騎車更加傷心 。
" a stranger is a friend i haven't met yet ! " she'd say to me .	「 陌生人是我還沒見過的朋友 ! 」 她會對我說 。
so , what are the common denominators in these three cultures ?	那麼 , 這三種文化中有什麼共同點呢 ?
what are the things that they all do ?	他們都在做些什麼 ?
and we managed to boil it down to nine .	我們成功地將它歸為九個 。
in fact we've done two more blue zone expeditions since this and these common denominators hold true .	事實上 , 我們已經完成了兩次藍色區域的探險 , 和這些共同的決策者是真的 。
and the first one , and i'm about to utter a heresy here , none of them exercise , at least the way we think of exercise .	首先 , 我即將要在這裡說一下 , 沒有一個運動 , 至少我們對運動的看法 。
instead , they set up their lives so that they are constantly nudged into physical activity .	相反地 , 他們建立了自己的生命 , 使他們不斷地被推向實體活動 。
these 100yearold okinawan women are getting up and down off the ground , they sit on the floor , 30 or 40 times a day .	這些百歲的okinawan婦女在地面上起伏 , 她們每天坐在地板上 , 每天30或40次 。
sardinians live in vertical houses , up and down the stairs .	薩丁尼亞人住在垂直的房子裡 , 上下樓梯 。
every trip to the store , or to church or to a friend's house occasions a walk .	每次去商店 , 教堂 , 或去朋友的家 , 都會有一個散步 。
they don't have any conveniences .	他們沒有任何便利 。
there is not a button to push to do yard work or house work .	沒有一個按鈕 , 來做園藝或家庭工作 。
if they want to mix up a cake , they're doing it by hand .	如果他們想把蛋糕混合在一起 , 他們會用手做蛋糕 。
that burns calories just as much as going on the treadmill does .	那燃燒的卡路里就跟跑步機一樣 。
when they do do intentional physical activity , it's the things they enjoy . they tend to walk , the only proven way to stave off cognitive decline , and they all tend to have a garden .	當他們做刻意的身體活動時 , 他們很享受的事物 , 他們傾向走路 , 唯一能證明脫離認知衰退的方法 , 他們都傾向有花園 。
they know how to set up their life in the right way so they have the right outlook .	他們知道如何以正確的方式來設定自己的生命 , 以便他們有正確的外觀 。
each of these cultures take time to downshift .	每一種文化都需要時間改變 。
the sardinians pray . the seventhday adventists pray .	薩丁尼亞人祈禱 , 第七天的冒險家祈禱 。
the okinawans have this ancestor veneration .	okinawans有這種祖先的植入 。
but when you're in a hurry or stressed out , that triggers something called the inflammatory response , which is associated with everything from alzheimer's disease to cardiovascular disease .	但當你在急促或緊張時 , 會觸發一種叫 「 發炎反應 」 的反應 , 它會和阿茲海默症及心血管疾病有關 。
when you slow down for 15 minutes a day you turn that inflammatory state into a more antiinflammatory state .	當你每天放慢15分鐘 , 把那發炎狀態轉變成更抗炎的狀態 。
they have vocabulary for sense of purpose , ikigai , like the okinawans .	他們有目的、ikigai的詞彙 , 像是okinawans 。
you know the two most dangerous years in your life are the year you're born , because of infant mortality , and the year you retire .	你知道你生命中最危險的兩年是你出生的那一年 , 因為嬰兒死亡率 , 而你退休的那一年 。
these people know their sense of purpose , and they activate in their life , that's worth about seven years of extra life expectancy .	這些人知道他們的目的 , 他們活在他們的生活中 , 價值約七年的預期壽命 。
there's no longevity diet .	沒有長壽的飲食 。
instead , these people drink a little bit every day , not a hard sell to the american population .	相反地 , 這些人每天都喝一點點酒 , 而不是對美國人口販售的辛苦 。
they tend to eat a plantbased diet .	牠們通常會吃植物的飲食 。
doesn't mean they don't eat meat , but lots of beans and nuts .	不是說牠們不吃肉 , 而是很多豆類和堅果 。
and they have strategies to keep from overeating , little things that nudge them away from the table at the right time .	他們有策略可以避免過度 , 一些小東西在適當的時間點把它們推離桌子 。
and then the foundation of all this is how they connect .	接著 , 所有這些的基礎就是它們如何連結 。
they put their families first , take care of their children and their aging parents .	他們把家人放在第一 , 照顧他們的孩子和他們的老父母 。
they all tend to belong to a faithbased community , which is worth between four and 14 extra years of life expectancy if you do it four times a month .	他們都屬於一個以信仰為基礎的社區 , 值四到十四年的預期壽命是值得的 。
and the biggest thing here is they also belong to the right tribe .	最重要的是 , 他們也屬於對的部落 。
they were either born into or they proactively surrounded themselves with the right people .	他們天生就要不就好 , 不然就把自己和對的人包圍在一起 。
we know from the framingham studies , that if your three best friends are obese there is a 50 percent better chance that you'll be overweight .	我們從弗明罕研究中得知 , 如果你三個最好的朋友肥胖 , 你的體重過重的機率是50% 。
so , if you hang out with unhealthy people , that's going to have a measurable impact over time .	所以 , 如果你和不健康的人在一起 , 會隨著時間影響到一個可衡量的影響 。
instead , if your friend's idea of recreation is physical activity , bowling , or playing hockey , biking or gardening , if your friends drink a little , but not too much , and they eat right , and they're engaged , and they're trusting and trustworthy , that is going to have the biggest impact over time .	相反地 , 假如你的朋友對於重建的概念是實體的活動、弓、踢泥巴、騎腳踏車或園藝 , 如果你的朋友喝了一點點酒 , 但他們吃得不太對 , 他們有信任和值得信賴 , 那將會隨著時間影響最大 。
diets don't work . no diet in the history of the world has ever worked for more than two percent of the population .	飲食是行不通的 , 全世界的歷史上沒有飲食 , 超過百分之二的人口 。
exercise programs usually start in january ; they're usually done by october .	運動計畫通常從一月開始 , 他們通常是十月完成的 。
when it comes to longevity there is no short term fix in a pill or anything else .	當談到長壽問題時 , 沒有任何短期的修復方式 , 不管是藥丸或其他東西 。
but when you think about it , your friends are longterm adventures , and therefore , perhaps the most significant thing you can do to add more years to your life , and life to your years . thank you very much .	但當你想想看 , 你的朋友是長期的冒險 , 因此 , 也許你能做最重要的事情 , 讓你能在人生中多年 , 生命多年 。 謝謝你 。
