ink that conducts electricity ; a window that turns from clear to opaque at the flip of a switch ; a jelly that makes music . all this stuff exists , and catarina mota says: it's time to play with it . mota leads us on a tour of surprising and cool new materials , and suggests that the way we'll figure out what they're good for is to experiment , tinker and have fun .	墨水會引導電力 ; 一扇窗 , 從清晰轉變到一個開關的不透明 ; 一個製造音樂的珠寶 。 所有這些東西都存在 , 卡特琳娜•莫塔說: 「 該是玩的時候了 。 」 莫塔斯帶領我們到一個驚喜又酷的新材料 , 暗示我們如何找出它們對實驗、粉碎、有趣 。
creativity , design , technology	創造力、設計、科技、科技、
catarina mota: play with smart materials	克里娜•莫塔:玩聰明的材料 。
i have a friend in portugal whose grandfather built a vehicle out of a bicycle and a washing machine so he could transport his family .	我有個朋友在葡萄牙 , 他的祖父在腳踏車和洗衣機上建造了一台車 , 讓他可以運送他的家人 。
he did it because he couldn't afford a car , but also because he knew how to build one .	他做到了 , 因為他買不起車 , 但也是因為他知道如何建造一台車 。
there was a time when we understood how things worked and how they were made , so we could build and repair them , or at the very least make informed decisions about what to buy .	曾經有段時間 , 我們了解事情是如何運作的 , 和如何做出來的 , 我們就能建立並修復它們 , 或者 , 最不知情的決定 , 來決定該如何購買 。
many of these doityourself practices were lost in the second half of the 20th century .	在二十世紀後半葉 , 許多這種做法迷失了 。
but now , the maker community and the opensource model are bringing this kind of knowledge about how things work and what they're made of back into our lives , and i believe we need to take them to the next level , to the components things are made of .	但現在 , 創作者和開放原始碼的模型 , 正是關於事物如何運作的知識 , 以及它們是如何構成我們的生活的知識 , 我相信我們需要把它們帶到下一個層級 , 到組成的元素 。
for the most part , we still know what traditional materials like paper and textiles are made of and how they are produced .	大部分的時候 , 我們仍然知道紙張和紡織品的傳統材料是由什麼組成的 , 以及它們是如何產生的 。
but now we have these amazing , futuristic composites plastics that change shape , paints that conduct electricity , pigments that change color , fabrics that light up .	但現在我們有了這些驚人、自閉症複合的塑膠 , 改變形狀的顏料 , 影響電力的顏料 , 會改變顏色 , 會亮起來的布料 。
let me show you some examples .	讓我給你們看一些例子 。
so conductive ink allows us to paint circuits instead of using the traditional printed circuit boards or wires .	所以導電的墨水能讓我們繪製電路 , 而不是使用傳統的印刷電路板或電線 。
in the case of this little example i'm holding , we used it to create a touch sensor that reacts to my skin by turning on this little light .	以我手上的這個小例子為例 , 我們用它來創造一個觸控感測器 , 來對我的皮膚產生反應 , 藉由啟動這個小小的光 。
conductive ink has been used by artists , but recent developments indicate that we will soon be able to use it in laser printers and pens .	導電墨被藝術家用過 , 但最近的發展顯示 , 我們很快就能用在雷射印表機和筆上 。
and this is a sheet of acrylic infused with colorless lightdiffusing particles .	這張是加密片 , 上面有無色的光驅光粒子 。
what this means is that , while regular acrylic only diffuses light around the edges , this one illuminates across the entire surface when i turn on the lights around it .	這意味著 , 雖然一般的加密器只會在邊緣散射光 , 但在我打開周圍的光線時 , 整個表面都會發光 。
two of the known applications for this material include interior design and multitouch systems .	這材料有兩個已知的應用 , 包括內部設計和多個觸控系統 。
and thermochromic pigments change color at a given temperature .	而溫度上的色素會在特定溫度上改變顏色 。
so i'm going to place this on a hot plate that is set to a temperature only slightly higher than ambient and you can see what happens .	所以我要把這個放在一個熱板上 , 設定在一個溫度上 , 溫度只比環境高一點 , 你可以看到會發生什麼事 。
so one of the principle applications for this material is , amongst other things , in baby bottles , so it indicates when the contents are cool enough to drink .	這種材料的其中一個原則是 , 在嬰兒瓶中 , 其它的原理是 , 在嬰兒奶瓶中 , 它會顯示 , 當內容夠酷的時候 , 可以喝酒 。
so these are just a few of what are commonly known as smart materials .	這些只是我們一般所知的智慧材料一般稱為 「 智慧型材料 」 。
in a few years , they will be in many of the objects and technologies we use on a daily basis .	幾年後 , 它們會出現在我們每天所使用的許多物品和技術中 。
we may not yet have the flying cars science fiction promised us , but we can have walls that change color depending on temperature , keyboards that roll up , and windows that become opaque at the flick of a switch .	我們還可能還沒有飛行車科幻小說給我們帶來的保證 , 但我們可以用牆來改變顏色 , 依據溫度、鍵盤來滾動 , 窗戶就會在開關上轉動 。
so i'm a social scientist by training , so why am i here today talking about smart materials ?	所以 , 我是社會科學家 , 我為什麼今天在這裡談論智慧型材料 ?
well first of all , because i am a maker .	首先 , 因為我是製造家 。
i'm curious about how things work and how they are made , but also because i believe we should have a deeper understanding of the components that make up our world , and right now , we don't know enough about these hightech composites our future will be made of .	我很好奇事情是如何運作的 , 也是因為我相信我們應該更深入了解構成我們的世界的元素 , 而現在 , 我們對這些高科技複合材料的了解不夠多 。
smart materials are hard to obtain in small quantities .	智能材料很難在很小的質量中取得 。
there's barely any information available on how to use them , and very little is said about how they are produced .	幾乎沒有任何資訊可以用來使用它們 , 且很少有關於它們是如何產生的 。
so for now , they exist mostly in this realm of trade secrets and patents only universities and corporations have access to .	所以 , 目前 , 它們主要存在於貿易秘密和專利只能上大學和企業才能取得 。
so a little over three years ago , kirsty boyle and i started a project we called open materials .	三年前 , 凱西男孩和我開始了一個計畫 , 我們稱之為 「 開放材料 」 。
it's a website where we , and anyone else who wants to join us , share experiments , publish information , encourage others to contribute whenever they can , and aggregate resources such as research papers and tutorials by other makers like ourselves .	這是個網站 , 我們和其他想加入的人 , 分享實驗、出版資訊 , 鼓勵其他人隨時可以做出貢獻 , 並聚集資源 , 例如其他製造者的研究論文和教學 。
we would like it to become a large , collectively generated database of doityourself information on smart materials .	我們希望它能成為一個龐大、集體的資料庫 , 由智慧型材料所產生的資訊庫 。
but why should we care how smart materials work and what they are made of ?	但為什麼我們要關心智慧材料如何運作 , 以及它們是由什麼組成的 ?
first of all , because we can't shape what we don't understand , and what we don't understand and use ends up shaping us .	首先 , 因為我們無法形塑我們不了解的事物 , 以及我們不了解和使用的東西 , 最終會塑造我們 。
the objects we use , the clothes we wear , the houses we live in , all have a profound impact on our behavior , health and quality of life .	我們所使用的物品、衣服、我們所居住的房子 , 都對我們的行為、健康和生活品質有著深遠的影響 。
so if we are to live in a world made of smart materials , we should know and understand them .	所以如果我們活在一個由智慧材料構成的世界裡 , 我們應該要知道並了解它們 。
secondly , and just as important , innovation has always been fueled by tinkerers .	第二 , 同樣重要的是 , 創新一直以來都是由小工人來推動 。
so many times , amateurs , not experts , have been the inventors and improvers of things ranging from mountain bikes to semiconductors , personal computers , airplanes .	很多時候 , 業餘人士 , 不是專家 , 是發明家 , 改進了從山腳踏車到半導體、個人電腦、飛機 。
the biggest challenge is that material science is complex and requires expensive equipment .	最大的挑戰是 , 材料科學是複雜的 , 需要昂貴的設備 。
but that's not always the case .	但事實並非如此 。
two scientists at university of illinois understood this when they published a paper on a simpler method for making conductive ink .	伊利諾州大學的兩位科學家了解這一點 , 他們發表了一篇論文 , 用一個簡單的方法製造導電墨水 。
jordan bunker , who had had no experience with chemistry until then , read this paper and reproduced the experiment at his maker space using only offtheshelf substances and tools .	jordanbunker , 他在當時沒有化學經驗 , 讀了這篇論文 , 並在他的製造者空間裡重複這個實驗 , 只用現成的物質和工具 。
he used a toaster oven , and he even made his own vortex mixer , based on a tutorial by another scientist/maker .	他用烤麵包機 , 甚至用他自己的旋渦混合器 , 根據另一位科學家/maker的教學 。
jordan then published his results online , including all the things he had tried and didn't work , so others could study and reproduce it .	約旦在網路上發表了他的結果 , 包括所有他曾經嘗試過的東西 , 沒有成功 , 其他人可以研究並繁殖它 。
so jordan's main form of innovation was to take an experiment created in a wellequipped lab at the university and recreate it in a garage in chicago using only cheap materials and tools he made himself .	所以jordan的主要創新形式是要在大學裡進行一個完整的實驗 , 並在芝加哥的車庫裡重建這個實驗 , 只使用便宜的材料和工具 。
and now that he published this work , others can pick up where he left and devise even simpler processes and improvements .	現在他發表了這個作品 , 其他人可以拿出他所剩的位置 , 設計出更簡單的過程和改善 。
another example i'd like to mention her project's goal is to highlight the expressive qualities of materials while focusing on the creativity and skills of the builder .	另外一個例子 , 我想提一下她的專案計畫的目標 , 是要強調材料的表達品質 , 同時要專注於製造者的創意和技能 。
electronics kits are very powerful in that they teach us how things work , but the constraints inherent in their design influence the way we learn .	電子設備是非常強大的 , 它們教導我們事物如何運作 , 但它們的設計限制會影響我們學習的方式 。
so hannah's approach , on the other hand , is to formulate a series of techniques for creating unusual objects that free us from predesigned constraints by teaching us about the materials themselves .	另一方面 , 漢娜的做法是設立一系列的技術 , 來創造出不尋常的物體 , 使我們免於設定限制 , 教導我們這些材料本身 。
so amongst hannah's many impressive experiments , this is one of my favorites .	在漢娜的許多令人印象深刻的實驗中 , 這是我最喜歡的一個實驗之一 。
[ " paper speakers " ] what we're seeing here is just a piece of paper with some copper tape on it connected to an mp3 player and a magnet .	我們現在看到的只是一張紙 , 上面有一些銅膠帶 , 連接到mp3播放器和磁鐵 。
so based on the research by marcelo coelho from mit , hannah created a series of paper speakers out of a wide range of materials from simple copper tape to conductive fabric and ink .	根據麻省理工學院的marcelocoelho的研究漢娜創造了一系列的紙張講者從簡單的銅膠帶到導電的布料
just like jordan and so many other makers , hannah published her recipes and allows anyone to copy and reproduce them .	就像jordan和很多的製造者漢娜發表了她的食譜讓任何人都能複製並繁殖這些食譜
but paper electronics is one of the most promising branches of material science in that it allows us to create cheaper and flexible electronics .	但紙電子是最有希望的材料科學分支之一 , 它讓我們能創造出更便宜、更靈活的電子 。
so hannah's artisanal work , and the fact that she shared her findings , opens the doors to a series of new possibilities that are both aesthetically appealing and innovative .	漢娜的手工藝作品 , 她分享了她的發現 , 為一系列新的可能性打開門 , 讓她能吸引人心和創新 。
so the interesting thing about makers is that we create out of passion and curiosity , and we are not afraid to fail .	所以 , 關於製造者有趣的是 , 我們從熱情和好奇心中創造出來 , 我們不怕失敗 。
we often tackle problems from unconventional angles , and , in the process , end up discovering alternatives or even better ways to do things .	我們經常處理無條件的角度的問題 , 在過程中 , 發現了其他的替代方案 , 甚至更好的方式來做事 。
so the more people experiment with materials , the more researchers are willing to share their research , and manufacturers their knowledge , the better chances we have to create technologies that truly serve us all .	所以 , 越多人實驗 , 越多研究人員願意分享他們的研究 , 製造商他們的知識 , 我們就越有機會創造出真正服務我們所有人的科技 。
so i feel a bit as ted nelson must have when , in the early 1970s , he wrote , " you must understand computers now . "	我覺得有點像tednelson在1970年代初期 , 他寫道: 「 你現在必須要了解電腦 。 」
back then , computers were these large mainframes only scientists cared about , and no one dreamed of even having one at home .	當時 , 電腦是這些大型的主機 , 只有科學家在乎 , 沒有人夢想在家中有一個 。
so it's a little strange that i'm standing here and saying , " you must understand smart materials now . "	所以這有點奇怪 , 我站在這裡說: 「 你現在必須要了解智慧型材料 。 」
just keep in mind that acquiring preemptive knowledge about emerging technologies is the best way to ensure that we have a say in the making of our future .	請記住 , 關於新興科技的先例知識是確保我們能在未來實現這個說法的最佳方法 。
when we drive , we get into a glass bubble , lock the doors and press the accelerator , relying on our eyes to guide us even though we can only see the few cars ahead of and behind us . but what if cars could share data with each other about their position and velocity , and use predictive models to calculate the safest routes for everyone on the road ? jennifer healey imagines a world without accidents .	當我們開車時 , 我們會進入一個玻璃泡 , 鎖上門 , 按下加速器 , 依賴我們的眼睛來引導我們 , 儘管我們只能看到前方幾輛車子 , 但如果汽車能與彼此分享他們的位置和速度 , 用預測模型來計算路上所有人最安全的路徑 , 珍妮佛雷諾•亨利會在不意外的世界中想像一個沒有意外的世界 。
jennifer healey: if cars could talk , accidents might be avoidable	珍妮佛亨利:如果車子可以說話 , 意外可能是可避免的可能是可避免的 。
let's face it: driving is dangerous .	讓我們面對現實:開車是危險的 。
it's one of the things that we don't like to think about , but the fact that religious icons and good luck charms show up on dashboards around the world betrays the fact that we know this to be true .	這是我們不喜歡思考的其中一件事 , 但事實上 , 宗教象徵和好運的迷惑出現在世界各地的儀表板上 , 背叛了我們所知道的事實 。
car accidents are the leading cause of death in people ages 16 to 19 in the united states leading cause of death and 75 percent of these accidents have nothing to do with drugs or alcohol .	汽車意外是美國16到19歲的人死亡的主要原因 , 其中75%與毒品或酒精無關 。
no one can say for sure , but i remember my first accident .	沒有人能肯定地說 , 但我記得我的第一個意外 。
i was a young driver out on the highway , and the car in front of me , i saw the brake lights go on .	我在高速公路上是個年輕的司機 , 在我面前的車子 , 我看到了煞車的燈亮亮著 。
i'm like , " okay , all right , this guy is slowing down , i'll slow down too . "	我說: 「 好吧 , 好吧 , 這個傢伙慢下來 , 我也會慢下來 。 」
i step on the brake .	我踏上煞車 。
but no , this guy isn't slowing down .	但 , 不 , 這個傢伙並沒有慢下來 。
this guy is stopping , dead stop , dead stop on the highway .	這傢伙停了 , 停了下來 , 停在高速公路上 。
it was just going 65 to zero ?	剛剛六十五歲到零 ?
i slammed on the brakes .	我撞上了煞車 。
i felt the abs kick in , and the car is still going , and it's not going to stop , and i know it's not going to stop , and the air bag deploys , the car is totaled , and fortunately , no one was hurt .	我覺得abs跑進去 , 車子還在走 , 它不會停下來 , 我知道它不會停下來 , 空氣袋部署 , 車子完全安定了 , 幸運的是 , 沒有人會受傷 。
but i had no idea that car was stopping , and i think we can do a lot better than that .	但我完全不知道車停了 , 我想我們能做得更好 。
i think we can transform the driving experience by letting our cars talk to each other .	我認為我們可以透過讓車子彼此交談 , 來改變駕駛體驗 。
i just want you to think a little bit about what the experience of driving is like now .	請各位思考一下開車的經驗現在是什麼樣子 。
get into your car . close the door . you're in a glass bubble .	走進你的車子 , 關上門 。 你在玻璃泡泡裡 。
you can't really directly sense the world around you .	你無法直接感知你周遭的世界 。
you're in this extended body .	你在這個擴張的身體裡 。
you're tasked with navigating it down partiallyseen roadways , in and amongst other metal giants , at superhuman speeds .	你任務是要將它導向某個部分的路面 , 進到另一個巨人的高速公路上 。
okay ? and all you have to guide you are your two eyes .	好嗎 ? 你只需要引導你兩個眼睛 。
okay , so that's all you have , eyes that weren't really designed for this task , but then people ask you to do things like , you want to make a lane change , what's the first thing they ask you do ?	好 , 這就是你所擁有的目光 , 不是為了這個任務而設計 , 但後來人們要求你做這樣的事 , 你想做一個改變 , 他們要做的第一件事是什麼 ?
take your eyes off the road . that's right .	把你的眼睛從路上脫下來 , 沒錯 。
stop looking where you're going , turn , check your blind spot , and drive down the road without looking where you're going .	停下來看看你要去哪裡 , 轉身 , 檢查你的盲點 , 開車到路上 , 看你要去哪裡 。
you and everyone else . this is the safe way to drive .	你和其他人 。 這是安全的開車方式 。
why do we do this ? because we have to , we have to make a choice , do i look here or do i look here ?	為什麼我們要這樣做 ? 因為我們必須做出選擇 , 我看這裡還是看這裡 ?
and usually we do a fantastic job picking and choosing what we attend to on the road .	通常我們會做一個很棒的工作 , 挑選我們在路上的目的是什麼 。
but occasionally we miss something .	但偶爾我們忽略了某件事 。
occasionally we sense something wrong or too late .	偶爾 , 我們會感覺出錯或太遲 。
in countless accidents , the driver says , " i didn't see it coming . "	在無數的意外中 , 司機說: 「 我看不到它會來 。 」
and i believe that . i believe that .	我相信 , 我相信這一點 。
we can only watch so much .	我們只能看得太多 。
but the technology exists now that can help us improve that .	但現在科技的存在 , 可以幫助我們改善這一點 。
in the future , with cars exchanging data with each other , we will be able to see not just three cars ahead and three cars behind , to the right and left , all at the same time , bird's eye view , we will actually be able to see into those cars .	在未來 , 車子彼此交換資料 , 我們不僅能看見前面三輛車 , 後面三輛車 , 右邊和左邊 , 同時 , 鳥的視野 , 我們就能看見這些車子 。
we will be able to see the velocity of the car in front of us , to see how fast that guy's going or stopping .	我們將會看到前方車輛的速度 , 看看那傢伙要走多快或停車 。
if that guy's going down to zero , i'll know .	如果那個傢伙要去零 , 我會知道 。
and with computation and algorithms and predictive models , we will be able to see the future .	有了計算、演算法和預測模型 , 我們就能看見未來 。
you may think that's impossible .	你可能覺得不可能 。
how can you predict the future ? that's really hard .	你要如何預測未來 ? 這真的很難 。
actually , no . with cars , it's not impossible .	事實上 , 不 , 車子 , 不可能 。
cars are threedimensional objects that have a fixed position and velocity .	車子是三維的物體 , 有固定的位置和速度 。
they travel down roads .	他們在道路上旅行 。
often they travel on prepublished routes .	通常他們會在預備的路線上旅行 。
it's really not that hard to make reasonable predictions about where a car's going to be in the near future .	對於不久將來車子的未來 , 並不難做出合理的預測 。
even if , when you're in your car and some motorcyclist comes bshoom ! 85 miles an hour down , lanesplitting i know you've had this experience that guy didn't " just come out of nowhere . "	就算你在車上和一些摩托車上時速85英里 , 一小時85英里 , 我知道你有這種經驗 , 沒有 「 出出門 」 。
that guy's been on the road probably for the last half hour .	那傢伙已經在路上待了半個小時 。
right ? i mean , somebody's seen him .	對吧 ? 我的意思是 , 有人看過他 。
ten , 20 , 30 miles back , someone's seen that guy , and as soon as one car sees that guy and puts him on the map , he's on the map position , velocity , good estimate he'll continue going 85 miles an hour .	十、二十、三十英哩 , 有人看過那傢伙 , 一旦車子看到那傢伙 , 把他放在地圖上 , 他就位在地圖、速度 , 估計他每小時85英里 。
you'll know , because your car will know , because that other car will have whispered something in his ear , like , " by the way , five minutes , motorcyclist , watch out . "	你們會知道 , 因為你的車子會知道 , 其他車子會在他的耳中發出一些東西 , 比如: 「 順道一提 , 五分鐘 , 摩托車騎士 , 仔細看 。 」
you can make reasonable predictions about how cars behave .	你可以對汽車的行為做出合理的預測 。
i mean , they're newtonian objects .	我的意思是 , 他們是牛頓人物 。
that's very nice about them .	這對他們來說很棒 。
so how do we get there ?	所以 , 我們要如何做到呢 ?
we can start with something as simple as sharing our position data between cars , just sharing gps .	我們可以從簡單的開始 , 來分享汽車的位置 , 分享gps的位置 。
if i have a gps and a camera in my car , i have a pretty precise idea of where i am and how fast i'm going .	如果我有gps和攝影機在我的車上 , 我有一個非常精確的點子 , 知道我在哪裡 , 以及我要走多快 。
with computer vision , i can estimate where the cars around me are , sort of , and where they're going .	有了電腦視覺 , 我可以估計我身邊的車子在哪裡 , 有點像是在哪裡 。
and same with the other cars .	其他車也一樣 。
they can have a precise idea of where they are , and sort of a vague idea of where the other cars are .	它們可以精確地知道它們在哪裡 , 對於其他車子的位置 , 可以有精確的概念 。
what happens if two cars share that data , if they talk to each other ?	如果兩個汽車共享這些數據 , 如果他們彼此交談 , 會發生什麼事 ?
i can tell you exactly what happens .	我可以告訴你們發生了什麼事 。
professor bob wang and his team have done computer simulations of what happens when fuzzy estimates combine , even in light traffic , when cars just share gps data , and we've moved this research out of the computer simulation and into robot test beds that have the actual sensors that are in cars now on these robots: stereo cameras , gps , and the twodimensional laser range finders that are common in backup systems .	鮑勃教授和他的團隊做了電腦模擬 , 當fuszy估計加起來時 , 甚至在光速交通中 , 汽車只是分享gps的資料 , 我們把這個研究從電腦模擬中移到機器人測試的實際感應器上 , 在這些機器人身上:sereo、gps , 以及2d的雷射 , 在後備系統中常見 。
we also attach a discrete shortrange communication radio , and the robots talk to each other .	我們也將一個距離簡短的通訊無線電 , 機器人彼此交談 。
when these robots come at each other , they track each other's position precisely , and they can avoid each other .	當這些飛行器互相撞擊時 , 它們會精確地追蹤對方的位置 , 它們可以互相避開 。
we're now adding more and more robots into the mix , and we encountered some problems .	我們現在在混合中加入了更多的機器人 , 我們遇到了一些問題 。
one of the problems , when you get too much chatter , it's hard to process all the packets , so you have to prioritize , and that's where the predictive model helps you .	其中一個問題 , 當你得到太多章節時 , 要處理所有的包裝是很難的 , 所以你得要先排序 , 這就是預測模式協助你的地方 。
if your robot cars are all tracking the predicted trajectories , you don't pay as much attention to those packets .	如果你的機器人車都在追蹤預期的軌跡 , 你就不太會注意那些包裝 。
you prioritize the one guy who seems to be going a little off course .	你把一個看起來有點偏離軌道的人列為優先順序 。
that guy could be a problem .	那傢伙可能是個問題 。
and you can predict the new trajectory .	你可以預測新的軌道 。
so you don't only know that he's going off course , you know how .	所以你不只知道他要怎麼做 , 你知道的 。
and you know which drivers you need to alert to get out of the way .	而且你知道哪一位司機需要警告才能脫離路線 。
and we wanted to do how can we best alert everyone ?	我們想做個最好的警告方式嗎 ?
how can these cars whisper , " you need to get out of the way ? "	這些車子怎麼會說: 「 你得走路 ? 」
well , it depends on two things: one , the ability of the car , and second the ability of the driver .	嗯 , 它取決於兩件事:一 , 車子的能力 , 第二 , 駕駛的能力 。
if one guy has a really great car , but they're on their phone or , you know , doing something , they're not probably in the best position to react in an emergency .	如果一個人有一台很棒的車 , 但他們在手機上或做一些事 , 他們可能不是在緊急情況下反應最好的位置 。
so we started a separate line of research doing driver state modeling .	所以 , 我們開始了一系列的研究 , 做司機的模型 。
and now , using a series of three cameras , we can detect if a driver is looking forward , looking away , looking down , on the phone , or having a cup of coffee .	現在 , 用了一系列三台攝影機 , 我們能偵測到駕駛是否向前看 , 向下看 , 向下看 , 手機或喝杯咖啡 。
we can predict the accident and we can predict who , which cars , are in the best position to move out of the way to calculate the safest route for everyone .	我們可以預測意外發生 , 我們可以預測誰、哪些車子 , 最好的位置 , 去計算每個人最安全的路線 。
fundamentally , these technologies exist today .	基本上 , 這些技術今天存在 。
i think the biggest problem that we face is our own willingness to share our data .	我認為我們面臨的最大問題是我們自己的意願來分享我們的資料 。
i think it's a very disconcerting notion , this idea that our cars will be watching us , talking about us to other cars , that we'll be going down the road in a sea of gossip .	我認為這是一個非常讓人不安的概念 , 我們的車子會看著我們 , 和其他車子聊聊 , 我們會在路上走下去 。
but i believe it can be done in a way that protects our privacy , just like right now , when i look at your car from the outside , i don't really know about you .	但我相信它可以用一種方式來保護我們的隱私 , 就像現在 , 當我從外面看你的車 , 我並不知道你 。
if i look at your license plate number , i don't really know who you are .	如果我看你的車牌牌號碼 , 我並不知道你是誰 。
i believe our cars can talk about us behind our backs .	我相信我們的車子可以在我們的背後談論我們 。
and i think it's going to be a great thing .	我認為這將會是一件很棒的事 。
i want you to consider for a moment if you really don't want the distracted teenager behind you to know that you're braking , that you're coming to a dead stop .	我想請各位思考一下 , 如果你真的不想要身後的那個分心的青少年 , 知道你在煞車 , 你要來到一個死路 。
by sharing our data willingly , we can do what's best for everyone .	藉由願意分享我們的資料 , 我們就能為每個人做最好的事 。
so let your car gossip about you .	所以 , 讓你的車子走向你 。
it's going to make the roads a lot safer .	它會讓道路更安全 。
x prize founder peter diamandis talks about how he helped stephen hawking fulfill his dream of going to space by flying together into the upper atmosphere and experiencing weightlessness at zero g .	xprize創辦人彼得•戴曼迪斯談到他如何協助史蒂芬•霍金實現了他的夢想 , 透過飛行到大氣中 , 體驗到零g的無重力 。
business , flight , science , short talk , space , technology , universe	商業、飛行、科學、短談話、太空、科技、宇宙、宇宙、宇宙 。
peter diamandis on stephen hawking in zero g	彼得•戴曼迪斯在史蒂芬•霍金的零號中 , 在史蒂芬•霍金的零號中 。
those of you who know me know how passionate i am about opening the space frontier .	認識我的人 , 知道我有多熱情 , 我在開太空邊境 。
so when i had the chance to give the world's expert in gravity the experience of zero gravity , it was incredible .	所以當我有機會給世界重力的專家-零重力的體驗時 , 真是不可思議 。
and i want to tell you that story .	我想告訴你們這個故事 。
i first met him through the archon x prize for genomics .	我首次見到他 , 穿越了archonx獎 , 來做基因組學 。
it's a competition we're holding , the second x prize , for the first team to sequence 100 human genomes in 10 days .	這是我們所擁有的競爭 , 第二個xprize , 第一組在10天內完成一百個人類基因組 。
we have something called the genome 100 100 individuals we're sequencing as part of that .	我們有一種叫 「 基因組一百個人 」 的序列 。 我們被稱為 「 基因組 」 。
craig venter chairs that event .	克萊格•凡特斯那天事件 。
and i met professor hawking , and he said his dream was to travel into space .	我遇見了霍金教授 , 他說他的夢想是進入太空旅行 。
and i said , " i can't take you there , but i can take you into weightlessness into zerog .	我說: 「 我不能帶你到那裏 , 但我可以帶你進入零 。
and he said , on the spot , " absolutely , yes . "	他說 , 在這個點上 , 「 絕對是的 。 」
well , the only way to experience zerog on earth is actually with parabolic flight , weightless flight .	要在地球上體驗零的唯一方法 , 其實是帶著偏執的飛行 , 無重力的飛行 。
you take an airplane , you fly over the top , you're weightless for 25 seconds .	你拿起飛機 , 飛過頂端 , 你是無重力的25秒 。
come back down , you weigh twice as much .	再回來 , 你的重量是兩倍 。
you do it again and again .	你一而再再而三地做 。
you can get eight , 10 minutes of weightlessness how nasa's trained their astronauts for so long .	你可以得到8、10分鐘的無重力 , 美國太空總署如何訓練他們的太空人 , 長久以來 。
we set out to do this .	我們開始這樣做 。
it took us 11 years to become operational .	我們花了11年才開始營運 。
and we announced that we were going to fly stephen hawking .	我們宣布我們要飛行史蒂芬霍金 。
we had one government agency and one company aircraft operator say , you're crazy , don't do that , you're going kill the guy .	我們有一個政府機構和一家公司的飛機操作員說 , 你瘋了 , 不要這樣做 , 你要殺了那個傢伙 。
and he wanted to go .	他想要去 。
we worked hard to get all the permissions .	我們努力取得所有許可 。
and six months later , we sat down at kennedy space center .	六個月後 , 我們坐在甘迺迪太空中心 。
we had a press conference , we announced our intent to do one zerog parabola , give him 25 seconds of zerog .	我們有一場記者會議 , 我們宣佈我們的目的要做一場零拋物傘 , 給他25秒的零 。
and if it went really well , we might do three parabolas .	如果真的很順利 , 我們可能會做三場拋物機 。
well , we asked him why he wanted to go up and do this .	嗯 , 我們問他為什麼要去做這件事 。
and what he said , for me , was very moving .	對我來說 , 他所說的 , 是非常感人的 。
he said , " life on earth is at an everincreasing risk of being wiped out by disaster . . .	他說: 「 地球上的生命正在不斷地冒著被災難摧毀的風險......
i think the human race doesn't have a future if it doesn't go into space .	我想 , 如果人類進入不存在的話 , 人類就不會有未來了 。
i therefore want to encourage public interest in space . "	我想要鼓勵公眾對太空的興趣 。 」
we took him out to the kennedy space center , up inside the nasa vehicle , into the back of the zerog airplane .	我們帶他到甘迺迪太空中心 , 到nasa車內 , 到零飛機的後面 。
we had about 20 people who made donations we raised $150 , 000 in donations for children's charities who flew with us .	我們有大約20個人捐款 , 捐贈了15萬美金給兒童慈善機構的捐款 。
a few tedsters here .	這裡有幾個ted人 。
we set up a whole er .	我們設立了整個急診室 。
we had four emergency room doctors and two nurses on board the airplane .	我們有四個急診室醫生和兩位護士在飛機上 。
we were monitoring his po2 of his blood , his heart rate , his blood pressure .	我們在監視他的血液中 , 他的心率 , 他的血壓 。
we had everything all set in case of an emergency ; god knows , you don't want to hurt this worldrenowned expert .	我們有所有事情都發生在緊急情況下 , 上帝知道 , 你不想傷害這個世界知名的專家 。
we took off from the shuttle landing facility , where the shuttle takes off and lands .	我們從太空梭降落場起飛 , 在那裡 , 太空梭起落和降落 。
and my partner byron lichtenberg and i carefully suspended him into zerog .	我的另一半是雷恩•里希伯格和我仔細地把他暫停為零 。
once he was there , [we] let him go to experience what weightlessness was truly like .	一旦他到那裡 , 我們就讓他去體驗真正無重力的感覺 。
and after that first parabola , you know , the doc said everything is great . he was smiling , and we said go .	在那第一個拋物面鏡之後 , 你知道的 , 醫生說一切都很棒 , 他微笑 , 我們說 , 開始吧 。
so we did a second parabola .	所以我們做了第二個拋物面鏡 。
we actually floated an apple in homage to sir isaac newton because professor hawking holds the same chair at cambridge that isaac newton did .	我們真的把一個蘋果漂浮到艾薩克•牛頓 , 因為在劍橋的劍橋教授 , 和牛頓同一座椅子一樣 。
and we did a fourth , and a fifth and a sixth .	我們做了第四個 , 第五個和第六個 。
and a seventh and an eighth .	第七和第八 。
and this man does not look like a 65yearold wheelchairbound man .	這個人看起來不像一位65歲的輪椅男子 。
he was so happy .	他很高興 。
we are living on a precious jewel , and it's during our lifetime that we're moving off this planet .	我們生活在一個珍貴的珠寶 , 在我們的一生中 , 我們正在離開這個星球 。
please join us in this epic adventure .	請加入我們這個史詩般的冒險 。
medical animator david bolinsky presents 3 minutes of stunning animation that show the bustling life inside a cell .	醫學動畫師大衛•鮑林斯基有三分鐘的驚人動畫 , 顯示細胞內部的破壞性命 。
design , entertainment , film , health , medicine , science , technology , visualizations	設計、娛樂、電影、健康、醫學、科學、技術、視覺化、視覺化 。
david bolinsky animates a cell	davidbolinsky為細胞動畫
i'm a medical illustrator , and i come from a slightly different point of view .	我是醫學插圖師 , 我從一個稍微不同的角度來看 。
i've been watching , since i grew up , the expressions of truth and beauty in the arts and truth and beauty in the sciences .	自從我長大以來 , 我一直在觀察著真相和美的表達 , 在科學中真與美的表達 。
and while these are both wonderful things in their own right they both have very wonderful things going for them truth and beauty as ideals that can be looked at by the sciences and by math are almost like the ideal conjoined twins that a scientist would want to date .	雖然這些都是他們自己的權利中美好的兩者都有非常美妙的事物 , 可以用科學和數學來觀察理想的雙胞胎 , 就像科學家們想約會的那樣 。
these are expressions of truth as awefull things , by meaning they are things you can worship .	這些表達真相是令人敬畏的事物 , 意思是 , 它們是你可以崇拜的事物 。
they are ideals that are powerful . they are irreducible .	它們是強大的理想 , 它們是不可思議的 。
they are unique . they are useful sometimes , often a long time after the fact .	它們是獨一無二的 , 有時是有用的 , 通常是在事實之後很長一段時間 。
and you can actually roll some of the pictures now , because i don't want to look at me on the screen .	你現在可以在螢幕上播放一些照片 , 因為我不想在螢幕上看我 。
truth and beauty are things that are often opaque to people who are not in the sciences .	真相和美 , 常常對那些不在科學領域的人來說是很不可思議的 。
they are things that describe beauty in a way that is often only accessible if you understand the language and the syntax of the person who studies the subject in which truth and beauty is expressed .	它們是用來形容美的事物 , 通常只能用你了解語言和語法的人 , 來研究真相和美的事物 。
if you look at the math , e=mc squared , if you look at the cosmological constant , where there's an anthropic ideal , where you see that life had to evolve from the numbers that describe the universe these are things that are really difficult to understand .	如果你觀察數學 , e=mc平方 , 如果你觀察宇宙的常數 , 人類的理想 , 你可以看到生命必須從描述宇宙的數字中演化出來 , 這些是很難理解的 。
and what i've tried to do since i had my training as a medical illustrator since i was taught animation by my father , who was a sculptor and my visual mentor i wanted to figure out a way to help people understand truth and beauty in the biological sciences by using animation , by using pictures , by telling stories so that the things that are not necessarily evident to people can be brought forth , and can be taught , and can be understood .	自從我受過醫學插圖之後 , 我就嘗試做些什麼 , 我父親被教導 , 他是雕塑家和視覺導師 , 我想要找出一個方法 , 來協助人們了解生物科學的真與美 , 透過動畫 , 用圖片 , 說故事 , 讓人們不見得可以被引進來 , 可以被教導 , 可以被理解 。
students today are often immersed in an environment where what they learn is subjects that have truth and beauty embedded in them , but the way they're taught is compartmentalized and it's drawn down to the point where the truth and beauty are not always evident .	現今的學生通常會沉浸在一個環境中 , 他們學到的是真相和美的主題 , 但他們被教導的方式是相對的 , 被吸引到真實和美的地點 。
it's almost like that old recipe for chicken soup where you boil the chicken until the flavor is just gone .	幾乎就像是雞湯的舊食譜 , 煮雞 , 直到味道消失 。
we don't want to do that to our students .	我們不想對我們的學生這樣做 。
so we have an opportunity to really open up education .	所以我們有機會真正開放教育 。
and i had a telephone call from robert lue at harvard , in the molecular and cellular biology department , a couple of years ago . he asked me if my team and i would be interested and willing to really change how medical and scientific education is done at harvard .	幾年前 , 我接到一通來自哈佛的robertlue , 在分子和細胞生物學部門 , 幾年前 。 他問我 , 我和我的團隊是否有興趣 , 願意真正改變哈佛的醫學和科學教育 。
so we embarked on a project that would explore the cell that would explore the truth and beauty inherent in molecular and cellular biology so that students could understand a larger picture that they could hang all of these facts on .	所以 , 我們開始進行一個探索細胞的計畫 , 來探索分子和細胞生物的真與美 , 讓學生可以了解這些事實的真相 。
they could have a mental image of the cell as a large , bustling , hugely complicated city that's occupied by micromachines .	牠們可能有一塊心智圖像 , 一個巨大、很複雜的城市 , 由微機所佔據 。
and these micromachines really are at the heart of life .	這些微機械是生命的核心 。
these micromachines , which are the envy of nanotechnologists the world over , are selfdirected , powerful , precise , accurate devices that are made out of strings of amino acids .	這些微機械 , 是世界各地的奈米技術人員的嫉妒 , 都是自導、強大、精確、精確的裝置 , 由胺基酸組成 。
and these micromachines power how a cell moves .	這些微機械的力量是如何移動的 。
they power how a cell replicates . they power our hearts .	它們能驅動細胞如何複製 。 它們能驅動我們的心 。
they power our minds .	它們驅使我們的心智 。
and so what we wanted to do was to figure out how we could make this story into an animation that would be the centerpiece of biovisions at harvard , which is a website that harvard has for its molecular and cellular biology students that will in addition to all the textual information , in addition to all the didactic stuff put everything together visually , so that these students would have an internalized view of what a cell really is in all of its truth and beauty , and be able to study with this view in mind , so that their imaginations would be sparked , so that their passions would be sparked and so that they would be able to go on and use these visions in their head to make new discoveries and to be able to find out , really , how life works .	所以 , 我們想要做的是 , 找出如何把這個故事變成一個動畫的中心 , 一個哈佛大學的生物視覺中心 , 一個哈佛大學的網站 , 由它的分子和細胞生物組成的學生 , 除了所有的文字資訊以外 , 外 , 所有教學都把所有的東西都放在一起 , 讓這些學生們可以內心了解細胞的真理和美麗 , 並且能夠在心中學習這個觀點 , 這樣他們的想像力才會被激發出來 , 以至於他們發現它們的生命 。
so we set out by looking at how these molecules are put together .	所以我們開始研究這些分子是如何組合在一起的 。
we worked with a theme , which is , you've got macrophages that are streaming down a capillary , and they're touching the surface of the capillary wall , and they're picking up information from cells that are on the capillary wall , and they are given this information that there's an inflammation somewhere outside , where they can't see and sense .	我們和一個主題合作 , 也就是說 , 你有巨噬細胞在微血管下游 , 它們在觸碰微血管壁的表面 , 它們會從微血管壁上的細胞取得資訊 , 它們會得到這個資訊 , 在外面有發炎的資訊 , 它們無法看見和感覺 。
but they get the information that causes them to stop , causes them to internalize that they need to make all of the various parts that will cause them to change their shape , and try to get out of this capillary and find out what's going on .	但他們會得到造成它們停止的資訊 , 導致它們內化 , 使它們需要製造出各種各樣的部件 , 使它們能夠改變形狀 , 試著從這些微小的微小中找出發生了什麼事 。
so these molecular motors we had to work with the harvard scientists and databank models of the atomically accurate molecules and figure out how they moved , and figure out what they did .	所以這些分子馬達 , 我們必須與哈佛大學的科學家和資料庫研究原子正確的分子模型並找出它們是如何移動的 , 找出它們是怎麼做到的 。
and figure out how to do this in a way that was truthful in that it imparted what was going on , but not so truthful that the compact crowding in a cell would prevent the vista from happening .	弄清楚如何用真相的方式來做這件事 , 讓它在發生了什麼事 , 但不是很誠實的 , 要讓細胞中的擁抱者不會發生這種事 。
and so what i'm going to show you is a threeminute reader's digest version of the first aspect of this film that we produced . it's an ongoing project that's going to go another four or five years .	所以我要給你們看的是一個三分鐘的讀者消化版 , 這是我們製作的這部電影的第一面版本 。 這是一個持續發展的專案計畫 , 將會再花四到五年 。
and i want you to look at this and see the paths that the cell manufactures these little walking machines , they're called kinesins that take these huge loads that would challenge an ant in relative size .	請各位看看這個 , 看看細胞製造這些小行走的小機器的路徑 , 它們被稱為kinesins , 可以在相對大小的螞蟻身上挑戰螞蟻的大小 。
run the movie , please .	請播放這部電影 。
but these machines that power the inside of the cells are really quite amazing , and they really are the basis of all life because all of these machines interact with each other .	但這些驅動細胞內部的機器是非常了不起的 , 它們真的是所有生命的基礎 , 因為這些機器互相作用 。
they pass information to each other .	它們會把資訊傳遞給彼此 。
they cause different things to happen inside the cell .	它們會造成不同的事情發生在細胞內 。
and the cell will actually manufacture the parts that it needs on the fly , from information that's brought from the nucleus by molecules that read the genes .	細胞會製造出果蠅所需要的零件 , 從原子核的資訊中 , 透過讀取基因的分子 , 來製造出它們所需要的零件 。
no life , from the smallest life to everybody here , would be possible without these little micromachines .	沒有生命 , 從最小的生命到這裡的每個人 , 都可能沒有這些微生物 。
in fact , it would really , in the absence of these machines , have made the attendance here , chris , really quite sparse .	事實上 , 在沒有這些機器的情況下 , 克里斯 , 真的很矛盾 。
this is the fedex delivery guy of the cell .	這是細胞的fedex遞送人員 。
this little guy is called the kinesin , and he pulls a sack that's full of brand new manufactured proteins to wherever it's needed in the cell whether it's to a membrane , whether it's to an organelle , whether it's to build something or repair something .	這個小傢伙叫做kinesin , 他把一包包裝滿了全新的製造業蛋白質到細胞所需的位置 , 不論是細胞膜 , 不論是組織 , 不論是用來建造東西或修補東西 。
and each of us has about 100 , 000 of these things running around , right now , inside each one of your 100 trillion cells .	我們每個人身上都有大約十萬個這種東西在你的一百兆個細胞內運行 。
so no matter how lazy you feel , you're not really intrinsically doing nothing .	所以 , 不論你有多懶惰 , 你在本質上什麼都不做 。
so what i want you to do when you go home is think about this , and think about how powerful our cells are .	所以 , 當你回家時 , 我要你怎麼做 , 想想我們的細胞有多強大 。
and think about some of the things that we're learning about cellular mechanics .	想想看 , 我們學到了一些關於細胞機械的知識 。
once we figure out all that's going on and believe me , we know almost a percent of what's going on once we figure out what's going on , we're really going to be able to have a lot of control over what we do with our health , with what we do with future generations , and how long we're going to live .	一旦我們搞懂了一切 , 相信我 , 我們就知道發生了什麼事 , 一旦我們搞清楚到底發生了什麼事 , 我們就能夠控制我們對健康的控制 , 和我們未來的世代的做法 , 以及我們未來的壽命 。
and hopefully we'll be able to use this to discover more truth , and more beauty .	希望我們能用這個方法來發現更多的真相 , 更美麗 。
but it's really quite amazing that these cells , these micromachines , are aware enough of what the cell needs that they do their bidding .	但非常驚人的是這些細胞 , 這些微機械 , 已經足夠地意識到細胞所需要做的事 , 以至於它們在協助 。
they work together . they make the cell do what it needs to do .	它們一起合作 , 讓細胞做該做的事 。
and their working together helps our bodies huge entities that they will never see function properly .	它們一起合作 , 協助我們的身體 , 它們永遠不會看到正常的功能 。
enjoy the rest of the show . thank you .	享受其餘的節目 。 謝謝 。
becky blanton planned to live in her van for a year and see the country , but when depression set in and her freelance job ended , her camping trip turned into homelessness . in this intimate talk , she describes her experience of becoming one of america's working homeless .	貝基•布蘭頓計劃要在她的車上住一年 , 看看這個國家 , 但當憂鬱症和她的自由工作結束時 , 她的營地旅行變成無家可歸 。 在這個親密的演講中 , 她描述她成為美國無家可歸的經驗 。
adventure , happiness , life , personal growth , poverty , social change , society , storytelling	冒險、快樂、生活、個人成長、貧窮、社會改變、說故事、說故事、說故事、個人成長、個人成長、貧窮、社會、社會、社會、社會、說故事、說故事
becky blanton: the year i was homeless	貝琪布蘭頓:那一年我是無家可歸的 。
i'm a writer and a journalist , and i'm also an insanely curious person , so in 22 years as a journalist , i've learned how to do a lot of new things .	我是一位作家和記者 , 我也是個非常好奇的人 , 所以在22年後 , 我身為記者 , 我學會如何做很多新事 。
and three years ago , one of the things i learned how to do was to become invisible .	三年前 , 我學到了如何做一件事 , 就是變成隱形 。
i became one of the working homeless .	我成了無家可歸的無家可歸 。
i quit my job as a newspaper editor after my father died in february of that same year , and decided to travel .	同年二月 , 我辭掉了報紙編輯的工作 , 決定去旅行 。
his death hit me pretty hard .	他的死亡對我來說是非常難的 。
and there were a lot of things that i wanted to feel and deal with while i was doing that .	在我做這件事時 , 我會想和處理很多事情 。
i've camped my whole life . and i decided that living in a van for a year to do this would be like one long camping trip .	我一輩子都在露營 , 我決定住在車上一年要做這件事就像一趟漫長的露營旅行 。
so i packed my cat , my rottweiler and my camping gear into a 1975 chevy van , and drove off into the sunset , having fully failed to realize three critical things .	所以 , 我把我的貓包起來 , 我的推特和我的露營器 , 變成了1975年的一台車 , 開到太陽下 , 完全無法實現三件重要的事 。
one: that society equates living in a permanent structure , even a shack , with having value as a person .	第一:社會等同於生活在一個永久的結構中 , 甚至一個模糊 , 一個人有價值 。
two: i failed to realize how quickly the negative perceptions of other people can impact our reality , if we let it .	第二:我沒意識到 , 其他人的負面感知有多快 , 可以影響我們的現實 , 如果我們放下它 。
three: i failed to realize that homelessness is an attitude , not a lifestyle .	第三:我沒意識到無家可歸是態度 , 而非生活方式 。
at first , living in the van was great .	一開始 , 住在車上是很棒的 。
i showered in campgrounds . i ate out regularly .	我在難民營裡淋浴 , 我經常吃東西 。
and i had time to relax and to grieve .	我有時間放鬆和悲慟 。
but then the anger and the depression about my father's death set in .	但接著 , 憤怒和憂鬱對我父親的死亡設定了 。
my freelance job ended . and i had to get a fulltime job to pay the bills .	我的自由工作結束了 , 我得要有全職工作來支付帳單 。
what had been a really mild spring turned into a miserably hot summer .	真正溫和的春天 , 變成了一個非常熱的夏天 。
and it became impossible to park anywhere without being very obvious that i had a cat and a dog with me , and it was really hot .	在任何地方 , 都不可能停車場 , 很明顯我有一隻貓 , 一隻狗 , 牠和我一起去 , 真的很熱 。
the cat came and went through an open window in the van .	貓來了 , 走過一扇開放的窗口 。
the doggy went into doggy day care .	狗狗去了狗狗的日常照顧 。
whenever i could , i used employee showers in office buildings and truck stops .	每當我可以時 , 我會用辦公大樓的員工和卡車停下來 。
or i washed up in public rest rooms .	或者 , 我在公共休息室被洗了 。
nighttime temperatures in the van rarely dropped below 80 degrees fahrenheit , making it difficult or impossible to sleep .	夜晚的時空溫度在華氏80度以下降 , 使得睡眠難以置信 。
food rotted in the heat .	食物在熱氣中腐爛 。
ice in my ice chest melted within hours , and it was pretty miserable .	冰在我冰上幾小時內就融化了 , 這真的很可悲 。
i couldn't afford to find an apartment , or couldn't afford an apartment that would allow me to have the rottweiler and the cat .	我負擔不起公寓 , 或買不起一間公寓 , 讓我有了腐爛的推特和貓 。
and i refused to give them up , so i stayed in the van .	我拒絕放棄 , 所以我待在車上 。
and when the heat made me too sick to walk the 50 feet to the public restroom outside my van at night , i used a bucket and a trash bag as a toilet .	當熱氣使我太生病了 , 晚上在我車外的公共廁所 , 我用了一個桶子和一個垃圾袋來當廁所 。
when winter weather set in , the temperatures dropped below freezing . and they stayed there .	當冬天氣象出現時 , 溫度下降了 , 牠們留在那裡 。
and i faced a whole new set of challenges .	我面對了全新的挑戰 。
i parked a different place every night so i would avoid being noticed and hassled by the police .	我每天晚上都拆了另一個地方 , 這樣我就能避免被警察察察察覺和被警察察察察覺 。
i didn't always succeed .	我並不總是成功 。
but i felt out of control of my life .	但我覺得自己無法掌控我的人生 。
and i don't know when or how it happened , but the speed at which i went from being a talented writer and journalist to being a homeless woman , living in a van , took my breath away .	我不知道它是怎麼發生的 , 但我從一個有才華的作家和記者變成一個無家可歸的女人 , 住在一輛車內 , 把我的呼吸帶帶走 。
i hadn't changed . my i . q . hadn't dropped .	我還沒改變 , 我的智商 , 還沒下降 。
my talent , my integrity , my values , everything about me remained the same .	我的才華、我的完整性、我的價值觀 , 所有關於我的事 , 都仍然是一樣的 。
but i had changed somehow .	但我已經改變了 。
i spiraled deeper and deeper into a depression .	我把更深、更深入憂鬱 。
and eventually someone referred me to a homeless health clinic .	最終有人把我稱為無家可歸的健康診所 。
and i went . i hadn't bathed in three days .	我去了 。 我三天沒洗澡 。
i was as smelly and as depressed as anyone in line .	我跟排隊的人一樣被羞辱和沮喪 。
i just wasn't drunk or high .	我只是不喝醉或喝醉 。
and when several of the homeless men realized that , including a former university professor , they said , " you aren't homeless . why are you really here ? "	當幾個無家可歸的人意識到 , 包括一位前大學教授 , 他們說: 「 你不是無家可歸 。 為什麼你真的在這裡 ? 」
other homeless people didn't see me as homeless , but i did .	其他無家可歸的人都不認為我是無家可歸的人 , 但我確實如此 。
then the professor listened to my story and he said , " you have a job . you have hope .	接著 , 教授傾聽我的故事 , 他說: 「 你有工作 , 你有希望 。
the real homeless don't have hope . "	真正的無家可歸者沒有希望 。 」
a reaction to the medication the clinic gave me for my depression left me suicidal . and i remember thinking , " if i killed myself , no one would notice . "	診所給我的憂鬱症 , 讓我有自殺傾向 。 我記得我在想: 「 如果我殺了自己 , 沒有人會注意到 。 」
a friend told me , shortly after that , that she had heard that tim russert , a nationally renowned journalist , had been talking about me on national t . v .	沒多久之後 , 一位朋友告訴我 , 她聽到提姆•羅斯特 , 一個全國知名的記者 , 一直在全國電視節目上談論我 。
an essay i'd written about my father , the year before he died , was in tim's new book .	我曾寫過一篇關於我父親的論文 , 在他死前的那一年 , 是在提姆的新書 。
and he was doing the talk show circuit . and he was talking about my writing .	他在演說節目電路 。 他在談我的寫作 。
and when i realized that tim russert , former moderator of " meet the press , " was talking about my writing , while i was living in a van in a walmart parking lot , i started laughing .	當我了解到提姆•羅斯 , 《會見媒體》的前主持人 , 談到我的寫作 , 當我住在華爾瑪的停車場時 , 我開始笑 。
i started laughing because it got to the point where , was i a writer , or was i a homeless woman ?	我開始笑是因為它到達了 , 我是一個作家 , 還是一個無家可歸的女人 ?
so i went in the bookstore . and i found tim's book .	所以我去了書店 , 找到了提姆的書 。
and i stood there . and i reread my essay .	我站在那裡 , 重新寫我的文章 。
because i was a writer .	因為我是一位作家 。
i was a writer .	我是一位作家 。
shortly after that i moved back to tennessee .	在那之後 , 我搬回田納西 。
i alternated between living in a van and couch surfing with friends .	我和朋友住在車內 , 和沙發衝浪之間 。
and i started writing again .	我又開始再寫作了 。
by the summer of the following year i was a working journalist .	接下來的一年夏天 , 我是個工作記者 。
i was winning awards . i was living in my own apartment .	我贏得了獎項 。 我住在我自己的公寓裡 。
i was no longer homeless .	我不再是無家可歸 。
and i was no longer invisible .	我不再是隱形的 。
thousands of people work full and parttime jobs , and live in their cars .	數以千計的人全職兼兼職 , 住在他們的車子裡 。
but society continues to stigmatize and criminalize living in your vehicle or on the streets .	但社會持續汙名並將生活在你的車子或街道上 。
so the homeless , the working homeless , primarily remain invisible .	所以 , 無家可歸、無家可歸、主要仍然是隱形的 。
but if you ever meet one , engage them , encourage them , and offer them hope .	但如果你遇見一個人 , 加入他們 , 鼓勵他們 , 並提供他們希望 。
the human spirit can overcome anything if it has hope .	人類的精神可以克服任何事情 , 如果它有希望的話 。
and i'm not here to be the poster girl for the homeless .	我在這裡並不是要成為一個無家可歸的海報女孩 。
i'm not here to encourage you to give money to the next panhandler you meet .	我不是要鼓勵你把錢捐給下一個乞討者 。
but i am here to tell you that , based on my experience , people are not where they live , where they sleep , or what their life situation is at any given time .	但我在這裡要告訴各位 , 根據我的經驗 , 人們不是他們住的地方 , 他們睡在哪裡 , 或他們的人生狀況 , 在任何時間 。
three years ago i was living in a van in a walmart parking lot , and today i'm speaking at ted .	三年前我住在華爾瑪超市停車場 , 今天我在ted演講 。
hope always , always finds a way . thank you .	希望永遠都能找到方法 。 謝謝 。
at tedxchange , thailand's " mr . condom , " mechai viravaidya , walks us through the country's bold plan to raise its standard of living , starting in the 1970s . first step: population control . and that means a lot of frank , funny and very effective talk about condoms .	在tedxchange , 泰國的《保險套》 , 米塔維拉迪亞 , 帶著我們走遍全國的大膽計劃 , 從70年代開始 。 第一步:人口控制 。 這意味著許多法蘭克 , 很有趣且非常有效的討論保險套 。
culture , global issues , health , population , science	文化、全球議題、健康、人口、科學、科學、科學等問題、
mechai viravaidya: how mr . condom made thailand a better place	米塔維拉迪亞:保險套如何讓泰國成為更好的地方 , 讓泰國先生成為更好的地方 。
now , when i was a young man 40 years ago , the country was very , very poor with lots and lots and lots of people living in poverty .	40年前 , 當我還是個年輕人的時候 , 這個國家非常貧窮 , 有許多人生活在貧窮中 。
we decided to do something about it , but we didn't begin with a welfare program or a poverty reduction program .	我們決定要做點什麼 , 但我們不是從福利計畫開始 , 或減少貧窮計畫 。
but we began with a familyplanning program , following a very successful maternal child health activity , sets of activities .	但我們從一個家庭普及計畫開始 , 追蹤一個非常成功的孕產婦健康活動 , 一組活動 。
so basically , no one would accept family planning if their children didn't survive .	基本上 , 沒有人會接受家庭規劃 , 如果他們的孩子沒有存活下來 。
so the first step: get to the children , get to the mothers , and then follow up with family planning .	第一步:去找孩子 , 去找母親 , 然後跟隨家人規劃 。
not just child mortality alone , you need also family planning .	不僅僅是兒童死亡率 , 你還需要家庭規劃 。
now let me take you back as to why we needed to do it .	現在 , 讓我帶各位回到為什麼我們要這麼做 。
in my country , that was the case in 1974 .	在我的國家 , 那是1974年的案例 。
seven children per family tremendous growth at 3 . 3 percent .	每家人的成長率有7個孩子 , 成長率是3.3% 。
there was just no future .	沒有未來 。
we needed to reduce the population growth rate .	我們需要降低人口成長率 。
so we said , " let's do it . "	我們說: 「 咱們來做吧 。 」
the women said , " we agree . we'll use pills , but we need a doctor to prescribe the pills , " and we had very , very few doctors .	女性說: 「 我們同意 , 我們會用藥 , 但我們需要醫生來開藥 。 」 我們有非常非常少的醫生 。
we didn't take no as an answer ; we took no as a question .	我們不把答案當作一個答案 , 我們把不當做一個問題 。
we went to the nurses and the midwives , who were also women , and did a fantastic job at explaining how to use the pill .	我們去了護士和助產士 , 她們也是女性 , 並且在解釋如何使用藥丸時 , 做了一個很棒的工作 。
that was wonderful , but it covered only 20 percent of the country .	那很棒 , 但它只佔了全國百分之二十 。
what do we do for the other 80 percent leave them alone and say , " well , they're not medical personnel . "	另外80%的人會做些什麼 , 讓他們獨自說: 「 嗯 , 他們不是醫療人士 。 」
no , we decided to do a bit more .	不 , 我們決定再多做一點 。
so we went to the ordinary people that you saw .	所以我們去了普通人 。
actually , below that yellow sign i wish they hadn't wiped that , because there was " cocacola " there .	事實上 , 在那條黃色標誌之下 , 我真希望他們沒那麼想 , 因為那裡有 「 可口可樂 」 。
we were so much bigger than cocacola in those days .	當時我們比可口可樂還要大很多 。
and no difference , the people they chose were the people we chose .	沒有差別 , 他們選的人是我們選的人 。
they were wellknown in the community , they knew that customers were always right , and they were terrific , and they practiced their family planning themselves .	他們在社區中很有名 , 他們知道客戶總是對的 , 且他們是很棒的 , 他們會自行練習自己的計畫 。
so they could supply pills and condoms throughout the country , in every village of the country .	所以他們可以供應全國各地的藥丸和保險套 。
so there we are . we went to the people who were seen as the cause of the problem to be the solution .	我們就來了 。 我們去找那些被視為是解決問題的原因的人 。
wherever there were people and you can see boats with the women , selling things here's the floating market selling bananas and crabs and also contraceptives wherever you find people , you'll find contraceptives in thailand .	不論在哪裡 , 人們 , 你都能看到有女人的船 , 賣的是漂浮的市場 , 賣香蕉、螃蟹 , 還有避孕用品 , 不論你在哪裡找到人 , 你都會在泰國找到避孕品 。
and then we decided , why not get to religion because in the philippines , the catholic church was pretty strong , and thai people were buddhist .	然後我們決定 , 為何不去宗教 , 因為在菲律賓 , 天主教教會很強烈 , 泰國人民是佛教徒 。
we went to them and they said , " look , could you help us ? "	我們去找他們 , 他們說: 「 看 , 你能幫我們嗎 ? 」
i'm there the one in blue , not the yellow holding a bowl of holy water for the monk to sprinkle holy water on pills and condoms for the sanctity of the family .	我在那兒是藍色的 , 不是黃色的 , 帶著一碗神聖的水 , 讓僧侶在藥丸和保險套上灑上神聖的水 。
and this picture was sent throughout the country .	這張照片被送到全國各地 。
so some of the monks in the villages were doing the same thing themselves .	有些村莊的僧侶在做同樣的事 。
and the women were saying , " no wonder we have no sideeffects .	那些女人說: 「 難怪我們沒有副作用 。
it's been blessed . "	它已經被祝福了 。 」
that was their perception .	那是他們的感知 。
and then we went to teachers .	然後我們去找老師 。
you need everybody to be involved in trying to provide whatever it is that make humanity a better place .	你需要每個人參與 , 試著提供任何能讓人類更好的地方 。
so we went to the teachers .	所以我們去了老師們 。
over a quarter of a million were taught about family planning with a new alphabet a , b for birth , c for condom , i for iud , v for vasectomy .	超過25萬人被教導要用一個新的字母a、出生、攝取保險套、iud、v的陰液檢測機 。
and then we had a snakes and ladders game , where you throw dice .	然後我們就有了蛇和梯子遊戲 , 你丟了骰子 。
if you land on anything profamily planning , you move ahead .	如果你降落任何預期的計劃 , 你就會往前走 。
like , " mother takes the pill every night .	比如: 「 媽媽每天晚上吃藥 。
very good , mother . move ahead .	非常好 , 媽媽 , 向前走 。
uncle buys a condom . very good , uncle . move ahead .	叔叔買了一套保險套 , 很好 , 叔叔 , 向前走 。
uncle gets drunk , doesn't use condom . come back , start again . "	叔叔喝醉 , 不用保險套 , 回來 , 再開始吧 。 」
again , education , class entertainment .	同樣的 , 教育 , 娛樂 。
and the kids were doing it in school too .	孩子們也在學校做這件事 。
we had relay races with condoms , we had children's condomblowing championship .	我們和保險套有相對的競賽 , 我們有兒童保險套的冠軍 。
and before long , the condom was know as the girl's best friend .	不久之後 , 保險套就被稱為 「 女孩最好的朋友 」 。
in thailand , for poor people , diamonds don't make it so the condom is the girl's best friend .	在泰國 , 對窮人來說 , 鑽石不會讓它變成保險套 , 是女孩最好的朋友 。
we introduced our first microcredit program in 1975 , and the women who organized it said , " we only want to lend to women who practice family planning .	我們在1975年引進了我們的第一個微型信貸計劃 , 組織了這個計劃的女性說: 「 我們只想借給那些實踐家庭規劃的女性 。
if you're pregnant , take care of your pregnancy .	如果你懷孕了 , 照顧你的懷孕 。
if you're not pregnant , you can take a loan out from us . "	如果你不懷孕 , 你可以從我們身上取出一個貸款 。 」
and that was run by them .	由他們所經營的 。
and after 35/36 years , it's still going on .	在35/36年之後 , 它還在持續著 。
it's a part of the village development bank ; it's not a real bank , but it's a fund microcredit .	它是村落發展銀行的一部分 , 不是真正的銀行 , 而是一個資金小額貸款 。
and we didn't need a big organization to run it it was run by the villagers themselves .	我們不需要一個大型組織來經營這個組織 , 由村民自己經營 。
and you probably hardly see a thai man there , it's always women , women , women , women .	你可能根本看不到一個泰國人 , 總是女人 , 女人 , 女人 。
and then we thought we'd help america , because america's been helping everyone , whether they want help or not .	然後我們認為我們會幫助美國 , 因為美國一直在幫助每個人 , 不論他們是否想要幫忙 。
and this is on the fourth of july .	這是七月第四號 。
we decided to provide vasectomy to all men , but in particular , american men to the front of the queue , right up to the ambassador's residence during his [unclear] .	我們決定為所有男性提供大量昆蟲 , 但尤其是 , 尤其是 , 美國男性在排隊前面 , 就在大使的期間 。
and the hotel gave us the ballroom for it very appropriate room .	這間飯店給了我們一個非常適當的房間 。
and since it was near lunch time , they said , " all right , we'll give you some lunch .	既然快到了午餐時間 , 他們說: 「 好 , 我們會給你吃午餐 。
of course , it must be american cola .	當然 , 它一定是美國的可樂 。
you get two brands , coke and pepsi .	你有兩個品牌 , 可口可樂和百事可樂 。
and then the food is either hamburger or hotdog . "	然後食物是漢堡或熱狗 。 」
and i thought a hotdog will be more symbolic .	我想熱狗會更符號 。
and here is this , then , young man called willy bohm who worked for the usaid .	這裡是這個 , 接著 , 年輕人叫威廉.博爾 , 他為美國國際組織工作 。
obviously , he's had his vasectomy because his hotdog is half eaten , and he was very happy .	很明顯地 , 他的陰道是他的陰道 , 因為他的熱狗被吃了一半 , 他很高興 。
it made a lot of news in america , and it angered some people also .	它在美國做了很多新聞 , 也讓一些人感到憤怒 。
i said , " don't worry . come over and i'll do the whole lot of you . "	我說: 「 別擔心 , 過來 , 我會幫你做很多 。 」
in all this thing , from seven children to 1 . 5 children , population growth rate of 3 . 3 to 0 . 5 .	總而言之 , 從七個孩子到1.5個孩子 , 人口成長率是3.3到0.5 。
you could call it the cocacola approach if you like it was exactly the same thing .	你可以稱它為可口可樂的方法 , 如果你喜歡它是完全一樣的 。
i'm not sure whether cocacola followed us , or we followed cocacola , but we're good friends .	我不確定可口可樂是否跟著我們 , 或者我們跟著可口可樂 , 但我們是好朋友 。
and so that's the case of everyone joining in .	這就是每個人加入的例子 。
we didn't have a strong government . we didn't have lots of doctors .	我們沒有強大的政府 , 我們沒有很多醫生 。
but it's everybody's job who can change attitude and behavior .	但每個人都能改變態度和行為 。
then aids came along and hit thailand , and we had to stop doing a lot of good things to fight aids .	接著 , 愛滋病來了 , 抵達泰國 , 我們得要停止做許多好事來對抗愛滋病 。
but unfortunately , the government was in denial , denial , denial .	但不幸的是 , 政府在否認、否認、否認 。
so our work wasn't affected .	所以 , 我們的工作不會受到影響 。
so i thought , " well , if you can't go to the government , go to the military . "	所以我想: 「 嗯 , 如果你不能去政府 , 去軍隊 。 」
so i went to the military and asked to borrow 300 radio stations .	所以我去了軍隊 , 要求借300個無線電站 。
they have more than the government , and they've got more guns than the government .	他們擁有的比政府還多 , 他們的槍枝比政府還多 。
so i asked them , could they help us in our fight against hiv .	所以我問他們 , 能否幫助我們對抗愛滋病毒 。
and after i gave them statistics , they said , " yes . okay . you can use all the radio stations , television stations . "	在我給他們統計數據後 , 他們說: 「 沒錯 , 你可以用所有的電台 , 電視台 。 」
and that's when we went onto the airwaves .	那時我們就到了空中 。
and then we got a new prime minister soon after that .	不久之後 , 我們得到了一個新的首相 。
and he said , " mechai , could you come and join ? "	他說: 「 米奇 , 你能來加入嗎 ? 」
he asked me in because he liked my wife a lot .	他問我 , 因為他喜歡我太太 。
so i said , " okay . "	我說: 「 好吧 。 」
he became the chairman of the national aids committee and increased the budget fiftyfold .	他成為國家愛滋病委員會的主席 , 增加預算的五倍 。
every ministry , even judges , had to be involved in aids education everyone and we said the public , institutions , religious institutions , schools everyone was involved .	每個部長 , 甚至法官 , 都得參與愛滋病教育每個人 , 我們說公共、機構、宗教機構、學校 , 所有人都參與其中 。
and here , every media person had to be trained for hiv .	這裡 , 每個媒體人員都必須受過愛滋病的訓練 。
and we gave every station half a minute extra for advertising to earn more money .	我們給每一站一半的額外廣告 , 賺更多錢 。
so they were happy with that .	所以他們對此很滿意 。
and then aids education in all schools , starting from university .	接著 , 所有學校的愛滋病教育 , 從大學開始 。
and these are high school kids teaching high school kids .	這些是高中生 , 教導高中生 。
and the best teachers were the girls , not the boys , and they were terrific .	最好的老師是女生 , 不是男孩 , 他們很棒 。
and these girls who go around teaching about safe sex and hiv were known as mother theresa .	而這些在教導安全性愛和愛滋病的女孩 , 被稱為 「 泰蕾莎 」 。
and then we went down one more step .	然後我們再走下一步 。
these are primary school kids third , fourth grade going to every household in the village , every household in the whole of thailand , giving aids information and a condom to every household , given by these young kids .	這些小學三年級、四年級 , 到村落的每個家庭 , 在泰國的每個家庭 , 提供愛滋病信息和保險套給每個家庭 , 給予這些孩子 。
and no parents objected , because we were trying to save lives , and this was a lifesaver .	沒有父母反對 , 因為我們試著拯救生命 , 這是救命的救命 。
and we said , " everyone needs to be involved . "	我們說: 「 每個人都需要參與 。 」
so you have the companies also realizing that sick staff don't work , and dead customers don't buy .	所以你也發現 , 生病人員不管用 , 死亡客戶也不買 。
so they all trained .	所以他們都受過訓練 。
and then we have this captain condom , with his harvard mba , going to schools and night spots .	然後我們有了這個保險套 , 帶著他的哈佛mba , 去學校和夜點 。
and they loved him . you need a symbol of something .	他們很愛他 。 你需要一個東西的象徵 。
in every country , every program , you need a symbol , and this is probably the best thing he's ever done with his mba .	在每個國家 , 每一項計畫 , 你都需要一個符號 , 這可能是他在mba做過最好的一件事 。
and then we gave condoms out everywhere on the streets everywhere , everywhere .	然後我們把保險套送到任何地方 , 到處都有 , 到處都有 。
in taxis , you get condoms .	在計程車上 , 你得到保險套 。
and also , in traffic , the policemen give you condoms our " cops and rubbers " programs .	此外 , 在交通中 , 警察會給你保險套 , 我們的 「 警察 」 計畫 。
so , can you imagine new york policemen giving out condoms ?	所以 , 你能想像紐約警察提供保險套嗎 ?
of course i can . and they'd enjoy it immensely ; i see them standing around right now , everywhere .	當然我可以 。 而且他們會很享受它 , 我現在看到它們站在任何地方 , 到處都是 。

and these were the condoms that we introduced .	這些是我們引入的保險套 。

we found you know somebody here was searching for the weapon of mass destruction , but we have found the weapon of mass protection: the condom .	我們發現這裡有人在尋找大規模毀滅的武器 , 但我們找到了大規模保護的武器:保險套 。
and then it says here , with the american flag , " don't leave home without it . "	接著 , 美國國旗上寫著: 「 不要離開家園 。 」

why just run around ?	為何會跑來跑去 ?
and then finally , in thailand we're buddhist , we don't have a god , so instead , we say , " in rubber we trust . "	最後 , 在泰國 , 我們是佛教徒 , 我們沒有上帝 , 所以我們說: 「 在橡膠上 , 我們信任 。 」
so you can see that we added everything to our endeavor to make life better for the people .	所以你可以看到 , 我們把一切加到我們努力的努力中 , 以讓人民更好的生活 。
we had condoms in all the refrigerators in the hotels and the schools , because alcohol impairs judgment .	我們在旅館和學校裡都有保險套 , 因為酒精損害了判斷 。
and then what happened ?	然後發生了什麼事 ?
after all this time , everybody joined in .	畢竟 , 所有人都加入了 。
according to the u . n . , new cases of hiv declined by 90 percent , and according to the world bank , 7 . 7 million lives were saved .	根據聯合國 , 新愛滋病的案例減少了百分之九十 , 根據世界銀行 , 七百七十萬人的生命被拯救了 。
otherwise there wouldn't be many thais walking around today .	否則 , 今天就不會有很多泰國人走來走去 。
so it just showed you , you could do something about it .	所以這只是給你看 , 你可以做點什麼 。
90 percent of the funding came from thailand .	90%的資金來自泰國 。
there was political commitment , some financial commitment , and everybody joined in the fight .	有政治承諾 , 有些財務承諾 , 每個人都加入了戰鬥 。

and then we decided to help people out of poverty , now that we got aids somewhat out of the way this time , not with government alone , but in cooperation with the business community .	接著 , 我們決定要幫助貧窮的人 , 現在我們得到愛滋病的方式 , 不是單靠政府 , 而是和商業界合作 。
because poor people are business people who lack business skills and access to credit .	因為窮人是商人 , 他們缺乏商業技能和取得信用 。
those are the things to be provided by the business community .	這些是商業界提供的 。
we're trying to turn them into barefoot entrepreneurs , little business people .	我們試著把他們變成赤腳的企業家 , 小小的企業家 。
the only way out of poverty is through business enterprise .	脫離貧窮的唯一方法是透過企業企業 。
so , that was done .	所以 , 已經完成了 。
the money goes from the company into the village via treeplanting .	金錢從公司變成村落 , 透過樹木移植 。
it's not a free gift .	這不是免費的禮物 。
they plant the trees , and the money goes into their microcredit fund , which we call the village development bank .	他們種植樹木 , 錢進入他們的微型信貸基金 , 我們稱之為 「 村落發展銀行 」 。
everybody joins in , and they feel they own the bank , because they have brought the money in .	每個人都加入 , 他們覺得自己擁有銀行 , 因為他們把錢帶進來了 。
and before you can borrow the money , you need to be trained .	在你借錢之前 , 你得要被訓練 。
and we believe if you want to help the poor , those who are living in poverty , access to credit must be a human right .	我們相信如果你想要幫助窮人 , 那些生活在貧窮中的人 , 能取得信用一定是人權 。
access to credit must be a human right .	能取得信用一定是人權 。
otherwise they'll never get out of poverty .	否則他們永遠不會脫離貧窮 。
and then before getting a loan , you must be trained .	在取得貸款之前 , 你必須要受過訓練 。
here's what we call a " barefoot mba , " teaching people how to do business so that , when they borrow money , they'll succeed with the business .	這是我們所謂的 「 赤腳mba 」 , 教導人們如何做生意 , 當他們借錢時 , 他們會成功地做生意 。
these are some of the businesses: mushrooms , crabs , vegetables , trees , fruits , and this is very interesting nike ice cream and nike biscuits ; this is a village sponsored by nike .	這些是一些企業:蘑菇、螃蟹、蔬菜、樹木、水果 , 這是非常有趣的nike冰淇淋和nike餅乾 , 這是由nike贊助的村落 。
they said , " they should stop making shoes and clothes .	他們說: 「 他們應該停止製作鞋子和衣服 。
make these better , because we can afford them . "	把這些做得更好 , 因為我們能負擔得起 。 」
and then we have silk , thai silk .	然後我們有了絲 , 泰國絲 。
now we're making scottish tartans , as you can see on the left , to sell to all people of scottish ancestors .	現在我們在做蘇格蘭的刺青 , 如你所見 , 賣給所有蘇格蘭祖先的人 。
so anyone sitting in and watching tv , get in touch with me .	所以 , 任何坐在一起看電視的人 , 跟我接觸 。
and then this is our answer to starbucks in thailand " coffee and condoms . "	這是我們在泰國的星巴克 「 咖啡和保險套 」 的答案 。
see , starbucks you awake , we keep you awake and alive .	看 , 星巴克你醒著 , 我們讓你清醒且活著 。

you can order your condoms with your with your cappuccino .	你可以將保險套用在你的膠囊裡 。
and then now , finally in education , we want to change the school as being underutilized into a place where it's a lifelong learning center for everyone .	接著 , 最後 , 在教育上 , 我們想要改變學校 , 成為一個被人人人人人終身學習的中心 。
we call this our schoolbased integrated rural development .	我們稱之為 「 學校基礎的農村發展 」 。
and it's a center , a focal point for economic and social development .	它是經濟和社會發展的中心 。
redo the school , make it serve the community needs .	重新設計學校 , 讓它成為社區的需求 。
and here is a bamboo building all of them are bamboo .	這是一棟竹子建築 , 全部都是竹子 。

and we use vegetables around the school ground , so they raise their own vegetables .	我們在學校附近使用蔬菜 , 所以他們會養育自己的蔬菜 。
and then , finally , i firmly believe , if we want the mdgs to work the millennium development goals we need to add family planning to it .	最後 , 我堅信 , 如果我們希望mdgs在千禧年發展目標上 , 我們需要增加家庭規劃 。
of course , child mortality first and then family planning everyone needs family planning service it's underutilized .	當然 , 孩童死亡率先開始 , 家庭規劃每個人都需要家庭規劃的服務 , 卻被充分利用了 。
