your smartphone may feel like a friend but a true friend would give you a smile once in a while . at ted2013 , keller rinaudo demos romo , the smartphonepowered mini robot who can motor along with you on a walk , slide you a cup of coffee across the table , and react to you with programmable expressions .	你的智慧手機可能會感覺像個朋友 , 但真正的朋友會給你一個微笑 , 不久後 , 在ted2013年 , 克萊納多•德摩摩爾 , 智慧型機器人可以在行走上行走 , 幻燈會幫你搭一杯咖啡橫跨桌 , 並對你做出可程式的表達反應 。
keller rinaudo: a mini robot powered by your phone	kellerrinaudo:一個小型的機器人 , 由你的手機發電 , 由你的手機發電 。
so just by a show of hands , how many of you all have a robot at home ?	請舉手 , 你們當中有多少人在家裡都有機器人 ?
not very many of you .	不太多人 。
okay . and actually of those hands , if you don't include roomba how many of you have a robot at home ?	好 , 請舉手 , 如果你不包含在家裡有多少人有機器人呢 ?
that's the problem that we're trying to solve at romotive that i and the other 20 nerds at romotive are obsessed with solving .	這是我們試圖解決在我和其他20位在romotive的romotive的romods , 致力於解決這個問題 。
so we really want to build a robot that anyone can use , whether you're eight or 80 .	所以 , 我們真的想要建造一個任何人都可以使用的機器人 , 不論你是八、八十歲 。
and as it turns out , that's a really hard problem , because you have to build a small , portable robot that's not only really affordable , but it has to be something that people actually want to take home and have around their kids .	結果發現 , 這是一個非常困難的問題 , 因為你必須建造一個小型可攜式的機器人 , 它不只能負擔得起 , 也必須是人們真的想要帶小孩回家 。
this robot can't be creepy or uncanny .	這個機器人不會很可怕或不可思議 。
he should be friendly and cute .	他應該是友善且可愛的 。
romo's a robot that uses a device you already know and love your iphone as his brain .	romo是一個使用你已經知道的裝置 , 愛你的iphone是他的大腦 。
and by leveraging the power of the iphone's processor , we can create a robot that is wifi enabled and computer visioncapable for 150 bucks , which is about one percent of what these kinds of robots have cost in the past .	透過iphone處理器的力量 , 我們就能創造出一個機器人 , 可以用wi-fi和電腦視覺 , 可以達150美元 , 大約是這些機器人在過去所花費的百分之一 。
when romo wakes up , he's in creature mode .	當romo醒來時 , 他正處於生物的模式中 。
so he's actually using the video camera on the device to follow my face .	所以他實際上是在裝置上攝影機來跟著我的臉 。
if i duck down , he'll follow me .	如果我躲下去 , 他會跟著我 。
he's wary , so he'll keep his eyes on me .	他很溫暖 , 所以他會把眼睛留在我身上 。
if i come over here , he'll turn to follow me .	如果我來到這裡 , 他就會跟著我 。
if i come over here he's smart .	如果我來到這裡 , 他很聰明 。
and if i get too close to him , he gets scared just like any other creature .	如果我太靠近他 , 他就會像其他生物一樣害怕 。
so in a lot of ways , romo is like a pet that has a mind of his own .	所以 , 在很多方面 , romo就像是他自己的寵物 。
thanks , little guy .	謝謝 , 小傢伙 。
and if i want to explore the world uhoh , romo's tired if i want to explore the world with romo , i can actually connect him from any other ios device .	如果我想要探究世界 , 嗯 , 羅摩已經累了 , 如果我想要用romo來探索這個世界 , 我可以和任何其他的ios設備連接他 。
so here's the ipad .	這是ipad 。
and romo will actually stream video to this device .	romo實際上會把視頻傳到這個裝置上 。
so i can see everything that romo sees , and i get a robot'seyeview of the world .	所以 , 我可以看見romo所看到的一切 , 我得到了一個機器人的審查世界 。
now this is a free app on the app store , so if any of you guys had this app on your phones , we could literally right now share control of the robot and play games together .	這是appstore的免費應用程式 , 所以如果你們有人在你的手機上有這個應用程式 , 我們現在可以共享機器人的控制權 , 一起玩遊戲 。
so i'll show you really quickly , romo actually he's streaming video , so you can see me and the entire ted audience .	我會很快地展示給你們看 , romo實際上是他在串流影片 , 所以你們可以看見我和整個ted觀眾 。
if i get in front of romo here .	如果我站在romo前面 。
and if i want to control him , i can just drive .	如果我想要控制他 , 我可以開車 。
so i can drive him around , and i can take pictures of you .	所以 , 我可以驅動他 , 我可以為你們拍照 。
i've always wanted a picture of a 1 , 500person ted audience .	我一直都想要一張1500個人的ted觀眾的照片 。
so i'll snap a picture .	我會拍一張照片 。
and in the same way that you scroll through content on an ipad , i can actually adjust the angle of the camera on the device .	就像你在ipad上滑過內容一樣 , 我可以調整裝置上攝影機的角度 。
so there are all of you through romo's eyes .	你們全都穿過romo的眼睛 。
and finally , because romo is an extension of me , i can express myself through his emotions .	最後 , 因為romo是我的延伸 , 我可以透過他的情緒來表達自己 。
so i can go in and i can say let's make romo excited .	所以 , 我可以進去 , 我可以說讓我們做romo很興奮 。
but the most important thing about romo is that we wanted to create something that was literally completely intuitive .	但romo最重要的是 , 我們想要創造一個完全直覺的東西 。
you do not have to teach someone how to drive romo .	你不需要教導別人如何開羅摩 。
in fact , who would like to drive a robot ?	事實上 , 誰想開機械人 ?
thank you , scott .	謝謝你 , 史考特 。
and even cooler , you actually don't have to be in the same geographic location as the robot to control him .	更酷的是 , 你其實不需要和機器人在同一個地理位置來控制他 。
so he actually streams twoway audio and video between any two smart devices .	所以他實際上是在任何兩個智慧裝置之間的雙向音頻和視頻上流 。
so you can log in through the browser , and it's kind of like skype on wheels .	你可以透過瀏覽器登入 , 有點像在輪子上的skype 。
so we were talking before about telepresence , and this is a really cool example .	所以 , 我們先前談到電信 , 這是個很酷的例子 。
you can imagine an eightyearold girl , for example , who has an iphone , and her mom buys her a robot .	舉例來說 , 你可以想像一個八歲的女孩 , 她有iphone , 她的媽媽買了她的機器人 。
that girl can take her iphone , put it on the robot , send an email to grandma , who lives on the other side of the country .	那個女孩可以拿她的iphone , 把它放在機器人上 , 送一封電子郵件給祖母 , 住在這個國家的另一邊 。
grandma can log into that robot and play hideandgoseek with her granddaughter for fifteen minutes every single night , when otherwise she might only be able to get to see her granddaughter once or twice a year .	祖母可以登入這個機器人 , 和她的孫女玩躲起來 , 每晚十五分鐘 , 不然她可能一年或兩次看到她的孫女 。
so those are a couple of the really cool things that romo can do today .	這些是現今romo能做的一些很酷的事 。
but i just want to finish by talking about something that we're working on in the future .	但我想先談談未來我們正在做的事 。
this is actually something that one of our engineers , dom , built in a weekend .	這其實是我們其中一個工程師 , 多姆 , 一個週末建成的 。
it's built on top of a google open framework called blockly .	它是建立在google開放的架構上 , 叫做 「 積木 」 。
this allows you to drag and drop these blocks of semantic code and create any behavior for this robot you want .	這樣你就可以拖著這些微小的語音密碼 , 為你想要的機器人創造任何行為 。
you do not have to know how to code to create a behavior for romo .	你不需要知道如何編寫romo的行為 。
and you can actually simulate that behavior in the browser , which is what you see romo doing on the left .	你可以在瀏覽器中模擬這種行為 , 也就是你在左邊看到romo在做的事 。
and then if you have something you like , you can download it onto your robot and execute it in real life , run the program in real life .	如果你有你喜歡的東西 , 你可以把它下載到你的機器人上 , 並且在現實生活中執行這個程式 。
and then if you have something you're proud of , you can share it with every other person who owns a robot in the world .	如果你有你自豪的東西 , 你可以和世界上所有擁有機器人的人分享它 。
so all of these wifi–enabled robots actually learn from each other .	所有這些無線網路的機器人都能互相學習 。
the reason we're so focused on building robots that everyone can train is that we think the most compelling use cases in personal robotics are personal .	我們之所以如此專注於建造一個人人都能訓練的機器人 , 是因為我們認為 , 在個人機械人中 , 最有說服力的用途是個人的 。
they change from person to person .	它們會從人變成人 。
so we think that if you're going to have a robot in your home , that robot ought to be a manifestation of your own imagination .	所以 , 我們認為如果你要在家裡裝一個機器人 , 機器人應該是你自己的想像力 。
so i wish that i could tell you what the future of personal robotics looks like .	我希望我能告訴各位 , 個人機械人的未來是什麼樣子 。
to be honest , i have no idea .	老實說 , 我不知道 。
but what we do know is that it isn't 10 years or 10 billion dollars or a large humanoid robot away .	但是我們知道的是 , 它不是一百、一百億美金或一台大型人體機器人 。
the future of personal robotics is happening today , and it's going to depend on small , agile robots like romo and the creativity of people like yourselves .	個人機器人的未來正在發生 , 它將取決於小型、敏捷的機器人 , 例如romo , 以及像你這樣的人的創造力 。
so we can't wait to get you all robots , and we can't wait to see what you build .	所以 , 我們等不及要讓你們全部的機器人 , 我們等不及要看你在做什麼 。
author and activist isabel allende discusses women , creativity , the definition of feminism and , of course , passion in this talk .	作者和行動主義者 , 伊莎貝爾會討論女性、創意、女性主義的定義 , 當然 , 這場演說的熱情 。
entertainment , global issues , love , parenting , storytelling , women , world cultures	娛樂、全球議題、愛、養育、說故事、女性、世界文化、文化、女性、女性、說故事、說故事、說故事、說故事、女性、女性、女性、世界文化 。
isabel allende tells tales of passion	伊莎貝爾•艾倫說了充滿熱情的故事 。
thank you so much . it's really scary to be here among the smartest of the smart .	非常謝謝你們 。 這真的很可怕 , 能在這裡是最聰明的人 。
i'm here to tell you a few tales of passion .	我來這裡是要告訴你們一些熱情的故事 。
there's a jewish saying that i love .	有句猶太人說我愛 。
what is truer than truth ? answer: the story .	什麼比真相更真實 ? 答案:故事 。
i'm a storyteller . i want to convey something that is truer than truth about our common humanity .	我是一個說故事的人 , 我想要傳達一個比我們共同的人性更真實的東西 。
all stories interest me , and some haunt me until i end up writing them .	所有故事都感興趣我 , 有些困擾著我 , 直到最後我寫這些故事 。
certain themes keep coming up: justice , loyalty , violence , death , political and social issues , freedom .	某些主題不斷出現:正義、忠誠、暴力、死亡、政治和社會議題 。
i'm aware of the mystery around us , so i write about coincidences , premonitions , emotions , dreams , the power of nature , magic .	我知道我們周圍的謎題 , 所以我寫了關於巧合、先例、情緒、夢想、大自然的力量、魔法 。
in the last 20 years i have published a few books , but i have lived in anonymity until february of 2006 , when i carried the olympic flag in the winter olympics in italy .	在過去的20年中 , 我發表了幾本書 , 但我在匿名生活 , 直到2006年2月 , 當我在義大利的冬季奧林匹克市擔任奧運國旗 。
that made me a celebrity . now people recognize me in macy's , and my grandchildren think that i'm cool .	這讓我成為了名人 。 現在 , 人們認得我是男女 , 我的孫子們認為我很酷 。
allow me to tell you about my four minutes of fame .	讓我來告訴你我的四分鐘的名氣 。
one of the organizers of the olympic ceremony , of the opening ceremony , called me and said that i had been selected to be one of the flagbearers .	一名奧林匹克的組織者 , 開幕式的開幕式 , 打電話給我 , 說我被選為一個旗幟手 。
i replied that surely this was a case of mistaken identity because i'm as far as you can get from being an athlete .	我回答 , 這是個錯誤認同的案例 , 因為我身為運動員的距離 , 遠遠超過你身為運動員的距離 。
actually , i wasn't even sure that i could go around the stadium without a walker .	事實上 , 我甚至不確定我可以在沒有行者的場所四處走動 。
i was told that this was no laughing matter .	我被告知這不是一個笑話 。
this would be the first time that only women would carry the olympic flag .	這是第一次 , 只有女性會帶著奧運國旗 。
five women , representing five continents , and three olympic gold medal winners .	五位女性代表五大洲 , 三位奧林匹克獎得主 。
my first question was , naturally , what was i going to wear ?	我的第一個問題是 , 很自然地 , 我要穿什麼 ?
a uniform , she said , and asked for my measurements .	她說 , 一個制服 , 然後問我的測量結果 。
i had a vision of myself in a fluffy anorak , looking like the michelin man .	我對我自己在流感的奧克 , 看起來就像是米奇林人 。
by the middle of february , i found myself in turin , where enthusiastic crowds cheered when any of the 80 olympic teams was in the street .	到了二月 , 我在土耳其找到了我 , 在那裡熱情的群眾歡呼了80個奧運隊伍都在街上歡呼 。
those athletes had sacrificed everything to compete in the games .	那些運動員犧牲了所有的競爭對手 。
they all deserved to win , but there's the element of luck .	他們都值得贏 , 但有幸運的元素 。
a speck of snow , an inch of ice , the force of the wind , can determine the result of a race or a game .	一片雪 , 一英吋的冰 , 一英吋的風力 , 可以決定一個賽局的結果 。
however , what matters most more than training or luck is the heart .	然而 , 比訓練或運氣還要重要 。
only a fearless and determined heart will get the gold medal .	只有一個無懼且堅定的心會得到金牌 。
it is all about passion .	重點在於熱情 。
the streets of turin were covered with red posters announcing the slogan of the olympics .	土耳其的街道被紅色海報覆著 , 宣佈奧運的口號 。
passion lives here . isn't it always true ?	熱情生活在這裡 , 不是一直都是真的嗎 ?
heart is what drives us and determines our fate .	心是驅使我們並決定我們的命運的原因 。
that is what i need for my characters in my books: a passionate heart .	這是我在書中角色所需要的:熱情的心 。
i need mavericks , dissidents , adventurers , outsiders and rebels , who ask questions , bend the rules and take risks .	我需要mavericks、異議、冒險家、外人和反叛者 , 他們會問問題、扭曲規則、冒險 。
people like all of you in this room .	像在座所有人一樣 。
nice people with common sense do not make interesting characters .	那些有常識的好人 , 並不會做出有趣的角色 。
they only make good former spouses .	它們只能製造出好的前配偶 。
in the green room of the stadium , i met the other flag bearers: three athletes , and the actresses susan sarandon and sophia loren .	在體育場的綠色房間裡 , 我遇見了其他國旗熊:三位運動員 , 還有蘇珊•沙隆和蘇菲亞•洛倫 。
also , two women with passionate hearts: wangari maathai , the nobel prizewinner from kenya who has planted 30 million trees . and by doing so , she has changed the soil , the weather , in some places in africa , and of course the economic conditions in many villages .	此外 , 兩位有熱情心的女士 , wangarimaathai , 來自肯亞的諾貝爾獎得主種了三千萬棵樹 。 透過這麼做 , 她已經改變了土壤 , 在非洲的某些地方 , 當然 , 還有很多村莊的經濟狀況 。
and somaly mam , a cambodian activist who fights passionately against child prostitution .	蘇曼 , 一位柬埔寨的激進分子 , 他們熱愛對抗兒童賣淫 。
when she was 14 years old , her grandfather sold her to a brothel .	當她14歲時 , 她的祖父把她賣到妓院 。
she told us of little girls raped by men who believe that having sex with a very young virgin will cure them from aids .	她告訴我們 , 小女孩被男人強暴 , 她們相信和非常年輕的處女性行為會治好她們的愛滋病 。
and of brothels where children are forced to receive five , 15 clients per day , and if they rebel , they are tortured with electricity .	在那裡 , 孩子們被迫每天收到5、15個客戶 , 如果他們反叛 , 他們就被電擊折磨 。
in the green room i received my uniform .	在綠色的房間裡 , 我收到制服 。
it was not the kind of outfit that i normally wear , but it was far from the michelin man suit that i had anticipated . not bad , really .	我平常穿的那種衣服 , 但它離我所預期的米其林男服還很遠 , 真的很不錯 。
i looked like a refrigerator .	我看起來像個冰箱 。
but so did most of the flagbearers , except sophia loren , the universal symbol of beauty and passion .	除了蘇菲雅羅倫 , 普遍的美和熱情符號
sophia is over 70 and she looks great .	蘇菲雅超過70歲 , 她看起來很棒 。
she's sexy , slim and tall , with a deep tan .	她很性感 , 很輕 , 很高 , 帶著很深的坦白 。
now , how can you have a deep tan and have no wrinkles ?	那麼 , 你要怎麼辦到一個很深的坦克 , 沒有皺紋 ?
when asked in a tv interview , " how could she look so good ? "	當在電視採訪中被問到: 「 她怎麼能看起來這麼好 ? 」
she replied , " posture . my back is always straight , and i don't make old people's noises . "	她說: 「 姿勢 。 我的背一直都很直 , 我不會製造老人的噪音 。 」
so , there you have some free advice from one of the most beautiful women on earth .	所以 , 這裡有一些免費的建議 , 來自地球上最美麗的女性之一 。
no grunting , no coughing , no wheezing , no talking to yourselves , no farting .	沒有抓緊、沒有咳嗽、沒有呼吸、沒有呼吸、沒有自己說話 。
well , she didn't say that exactly .	嗯 , 她沒有這麼說 。
at some point around midnight , we were summoned to the wings of the stadium , and the loudspeakers announced the olympic flag , and the music started by the way , the same music that starts here , the aida march .	在午夜的時候 , 我們被召喚到體育場的翅膀 , 大聲說出奧運國旗 , 音樂始於這裡 , 艾迪達遊行 。
sophia loren was right in front of me she's a foot taller than i am , not counting the poofy hair .	蘇菲亞•羅倫站在我面前 , 她是個比我高高 , 不算頭髮 。
she walked elegantly , like a giraffe on the african savannah , holding the flag on her shoulder . i jogged behind on my tiptoes holding the flag on my extended arm , so that my head was actually under the damn flag .	她優雅地走路 , 像在非洲草原上的長頸鹿 , 把旗子放在肩膀上 。 我在我的腳尖上把旗子放在我的手臂上 , 這樣我的頭就在該死旗下 。
all the cameras were , of course , on sophia .	當然 , 所有的攝影機都是在蘇菲雅 。
that was fortunate for me , because in most press photos i appear too , although often between sophia's legs .	這對我來說很幸運 , 因為在大多數的媒體照片中 , 我也出現在蘇菲雅的雙腳之間 。
a place where most men would love to be .	在那裡 , 大部分男人都喜歡成為一個地方 。
the best four minutes of my entire life were those in the olympic stadium .	我一生中最棒的四分鐘 , 是奧林匹克運動場中的人 。
my husband is offended when i say this although i have explained to him that what we do in private usually takes less than four minutes so he shouldn't take it personally .	當我說這句話時 , 我先生被冒犯了 , 雖然我向他解釋 , 我們在私人生活中所做的 , 通常只花不到四分鐘 , 所以他不應親身服用 。
i have all the press clippings of those four magnificent minutes , because i don't want to forget them when old age destroys my brain cells .	我有這四分鐘的所有媒體點擊 , 因為我不想忘記 , 老年摧毀我的腦細胞 。
i want to carry in my heart forever the key word of the olympics passion .	我心裡想永遠帶著奧運熱情的關鍵字 。
so here's a tale of passion .	這是個熱情的故事 。
the year is 1998 , the place is a prison camp for tutsi refugees in congo .	今年是1998年 , 這個地方是剛果的監獄難民營 。
by the way , 80 percent of all refugees and displaced people in the world are women and girls .	順便一提 , 世界上有百分之八十的難民是女性和女孩 。
we can call this place in congo a death camp , because those who are not killed will die of disease or starvation .	我們可以把這個地方命名為剛果的死營 , 因為那些沒有死於疾病或餓死的人 。
the protagonists of this story are a young woman , rose mapendo , and her children .	這個故事的主角是一位年輕女子 , 羅斯•地圖 , 還有她的孩子 。
she's pregnant and a widow .	她是懷孕和寡婦 。
soldiers have forced her to watch as her husband was tortured and killed .	士兵迫使她看著她的丈夫被折磨並殺害 。
somehow she manages to keep her seven children alive , and a few months later , she gives birth to premature twins .	不知怎麼的 , 她想讓七個孩子活下來 , 幾個月後 , 她生下了早產的雙胞胎 。
two tiny little boys .	兩個小男孩 。
she cuts the umbilical cord with a stick , and ties it with her own hair .	她用棍子剪下麻木頭 , 把它和她自己的頭髮綁起來 。
she names the twins after the camp's commanders to gain their favor , and feeds them with black tea because her milk cannot sustain them .	她以營地指揮官的名字命名為雙胞胎 , 用黑色茶餵食牠們 , 因為她的牛奶無法維持牠們 。
when the soldiers burst in her cell to rape her oldest daughter , she grabs hold of her and refuses to let go , even when they hold a gun to her head .	當士兵衝進她的牢房 , 強暴她最老的女兒 , 她抓住她 , 拒絕放手 , 即使他們抱著槍頭 。
somehow , the family survives for 16 months , and then , by extraordinary luck , and the passionate heart of a young american man , sasha chanoff , who manages to put her in a u . s . rescue plane , rose mapendo and her nine children end up in phoenix , arizona , where they're now living and thriving .	不知怎麼的 , 家庭存活了十六個月 , 接著 , 幸運地 , 一位年輕的美國人 , 薩斯夏•查奈夫 , 他致力於將她放進美國救援飛機 , 羅斯地圖和她的九個孩子最後到了亞利桑納州鳳凰城 , 他們現在住在那裡茁壯 。
mapendo , in swahili , means great love .	在斯瓦希里語的地圖 , 意思是很棒的愛 。
the protagonists of my books are strong and passionate women like rose mapendo .	我書的主角堅強和熱情的女性 , 像羅斯•地圖蘭多 。
i don't make them up . there's no need for that .	我不會讓他們站起來 , 沒有必要的 。
i look around and i see them everywhere .	我環顧四周 , 到處看到他們 。
i have worked with women and for women all my life .	我和我的一生都和女性和女性一起工作 。
i know them well .	我知道他們好 。
i was born in ancient times , at the end of the world , in a patriarchal catholic and conservative family .	我出生於古老的時代 , 在父權的天主教和保守的家庭 。
no wonder that by age five i was a raging feminist although the term had not reached chile yet , so nobody knew what the heck was wrong with me .	難怪 , 五歲時 , 我是個狂熱的女權主義者 , 雖然這個詞還沒到智利 , 所以沒人知道我有什麼問題 。
i would soon find out that there was a high price to pay for my freedom , and for questioning the patriarchy .	我很快就會發現 , 我有很高的代價來支付我的自由 , 並且質疑父權主義 。
but i was happy to pay it , because for every blow that i received , i was able to deliver two .	但我很高興能支付這筆錢 , 因為每次我接到的炸彈 , 我都能遞送兩次 。
once , when my daughter paula was in her twenties , she said to me that feminism was dated , that i should move on .	有一次 , 當我女兒保羅在她二十多歲時 , 她告訴我 , 女權主義是約會的 , 我應該繼續下去 。
we had a memorable fight . feminism is dated ?	我們有一場令人難忘的戰爭 。 女權主義是約會的嗎 ?
yes , for privileged women like my daughter and all of us here today , but not for most of our sisters in the rest of the world who are still forced into premature marriage , prostitution , forced labor they have children that they don't want or they cannot feed .	沒錯 , 對於像我女兒一樣有特權的女性 , 今天在這裡 , 我們所有人 , 但對世界上大部分的姐妹來說 , 她們仍然被迫要結婚、賣淫、強迫她們有孩子 , 她們不想要或無法餵飽 。
they have no control over their bodies or their lives .	他們無法掌控自己的身體或生活 。
they have no education and no freedom .	他們沒有教育 , 也沒有自由 。
they are raped , beaten up and sometimes killed with impunity .	他們被強暴 , 有時被毆打 , 有時被懲罰 。
for most western young women of today , being called a feminist is an insult .	現今大多數西方的年輕女性 , 被稱為女性主義者是種侮辱 。
feminism has never been sexy , but let me assure you that it never stopped me from flirting , and i have seldom suffered from lack of men .	女權主義從來沒有性感過 , 但讓我向你保證 , 從來沒有阻止我調情 , 我也曾被男性缺乏 。
feminism is not dead , by no means .	女性主義沒有死亡 , 沒有意義 。
it has evolved . if you don't like the term , change it , for goddess' sake .	它已經進化了 。 如果你不喜歡這個詞 , 改變它 , 改變它 , 讓神的樣子 。
call it aphrodite , or venus , or bimbo , or whatever you want ; the name doesn't matter , as long as we understand what it is about , and we support it .	稱之為aphrodite , 金星 , 或bimbo , 或任何你想要的 , 這名字不重要 , 只要我們了解它是什麼 , 我們支持它 。
so here's another tale of passion , and this is a sad one .	這是另一個充滿熱情的故事 , 這是個悲傷的故事 。
the place is a small women's clinic in a village in bangladesh .	這個地方是孟加拉的一間小女子診所 。
the year is 2005 .	這一年是2005年 。
jenny is a young american dental hygienist who has gone to the clinic as a volunteer during her threeweek vacation .	珍妮是一位年輕的美國牙醫 , 在她三週假期間 , 她去了診所 。
she's prepared to clean teeth , but when she gets there , she finds out that there are no doctors , no dentists , and the clinic is just a hut full of flies .	她準備好要清潔牙 , 但當她到達那裡時 , 她發現沒有醫生 , 沒有牙醫 , 診所就只是一間蒼蠅的小屋 。
outside , there is a line of women who have waited several hours to be treated .	在外面 , 有一系列的女性 , 等了好幾個小時才被治療 。
the first patient is in excruciating pain because she has several rotten molars .	第一個病患在痛苦之中 , 因為她有好幾個腐爛的老鼠 。
jenny realizes that the only solution is to pull out the bad teeth .	珍妮知道唯一的解決方法就是拉出不好的牙齒 。
she's not licensed for that ; she has never done it .	她不是這樣說的 , 她從來沒有這樣做 。
she risks a lot and she's terrified .	她冒了很多險 , 她嚇壞了 。
she doesn't even have the proper instruments , but fortunately she has brought some novocaine .	她甚至沒有適當的樂器 , 但幸運的是 , 她帶來了一些麻煩 。
jenny has a brave and passionate heart .	珍妮有勇氣和熱情心 。
she murmurs a prayer and she goes ahead with the operation .	她把禱告交給禱告 , 繼續手術前進 。
at the end , the relieved patient kisses her hands .	最後 , 病人鬆了一口氣 , 親吻她的手 。
that day the hygienist pulls out many more teeth .	那天衛生學家抽出更多的牙齒 。
the next morning , when she comes again to the socalled clinic , her first patient is waiting for her with her husband .	隔天早上 , 當她再次到所謂的診所時 , 她的第一個病人正在和她的丈夫等著她 。
the woman's face looks like a watermelon .	這位女士的臉看起來像是一個水母 。
it is so swollen that you can't even see the eyes .	它的腫大到你看不見眼睛 。
the husband , furious , threatens to kill the american .	丈夫、憤怒、威脅要殺害美國人 。
jenny is horrified at what she has done , but then the translator explains that the patient's condition has nothing to do with the operation .	珍妮對她所做的事感到害怕 , 但接著 , 翻譯解釋病人的狀況和操作無關 。
the day before , her husband beat her up because she was not home in time to prepare dinner for him .	前一天 , 她丈夫打她起床 , 因為她不在家準備晚餐 。
millions of women live like this today .	今天有數百萬的女性像這樣生活 。
they are the poorest of the poor .	他們是最貧窮的人 。
although women do twothirds of the world's labor , they own less than one percent of the world's assets .	雖然全世界的勞動力有三分之二女性 , 但她們擁有不到百分之一的資產 。
they are paid less than men for the same work if they're paid at all , and they remain vulnerable because they have no economic independence , and they are constantly threatened by exploitation , violence and abuse .	他們的薪水比男人少 , 如果他們付錢 , 他們仍然脆弱 , 因為他們沒有經濟獨立 , 他們會不斷受到剝削、暴力和虐待的威脅 。
it is a fact that giving women education , work , the ability to control their own income , inherit and own property , benefits the society .	事實上 , 給予婦女教育、工作、控制自己的收入、繼承、擁有自己的財產、受益於社會 。
if a woman is empowered , her children and her family will be better off .	如果一個女人被賦予權力 , 她的孩子和家人就會更好 。
if families prosper , the village prospers , and eventually so does the whole country .	如果家人繁榮 , 村落繁榮 , 最終 , 整個國家也是如此 。
wangari maathai goes to a village in kenya .	wangarimaathai去肯亞的村子 。
she talks with the women and explains that the land is barren because they have cut and sold the trees .	她和婦女談 , 解釋土地是很荒謬的 , 因為他們已經砍了樹 , 賣了樹木 。
she gets the women to plant new trees and water them , drop by drop .	她讓女性種植新樹和水 , 下落 。
in a matter of five or six years , they have a forest , the soil is enriched , and the village is saved .	五、六年之內 , 他們有一片森林 , 土壤充滿豐富 , 村落也存了下來 。
the poorest and most backward societies are always those that put women down .	最貧窮和最後退的社會 , 總是那些讓女性下台的人 。
yet this obvious truth is ignored by governments and also by philanthropy .	然而 , 這個明顯的事實卻被政府忽略 , 也被慈善事業忽略了 。
for every dollar given to a women's program , 20 dollars are given to men's programs .	每給婦女專案的每一塊錢 , 有20塊美金給男性專案 。
women are 51 percent of humankind .	女性是51%的人類 。
empowering them will change everything more than technology and design and entertainment .	賦予他們力量 , 改變一切 , 遠勝於科技、設計和娛樂 。
i can promise you that women working together linked , informed and educated can bring peace and prosperity to this forsaken planet .	我可以向各位保證 , 婦女們合作 , 連結、知情和教育 , 可以帶來和平和和繁榮 , 帶給這個脆弱的地球 。
in any war today , most of the casualties are civilians , mainly women and children . they are collateral damage .	在任何戰爭中 , 大部分的傷亡都是平民 , 主要是婦女和兒童 。 他們是負面的傷害 。
men run the world , and look at the mess we have .	男人經營世界 , 看看我們面臨的混亂 。
what kind of world do we want ?	我們想要什麼樣的世界 ?
this is a fundamental question that most of us are asking .	這是一個我們大部分人都在問的基本問題 。
does it make sense to participate in the existing world order ?	是否合理地參與現有的世界秩序 ?
we want a world where life is preserved and the quality of life is enriched for everybody , not only for the privileged .	我們想要一個保存生命和生活品質的世界 , 能讓每個人更富有 , 不只給予特權 。
in january i saw an exhibit of fernando botero's paintings at the uc berkeley library .	在一月 , 我看到費南多•波特羅在加州大學柏克萊圖書館的畫作 。
no museum or gallery in the united states , except for the new york gallery that carries botero's work , has dared to show the paintings because the theme is the abu ghraib prison .	在美國 , 沒有博物館或畫廊 , 除了紐約畫廊 , 波特羅的作品 , 還敢展示這幅畫 , 因為主題是阿布格萊布監獄 。
they are huge paintings of torture and abuse of power , in the voluminous botero style .	它們是巨大的折磨和濫用權力的畫作 , 在巨大的botero風格中 。
i have not been able to get those images out of my mind or my heart .	我無法從我的心中或心中得到這些影像 。
what i fear most is power with impunity .	我最害怕的是權力 。
i fear abuse of power , and the power to abuse .	我害怕權力濫用 , 以及虐待的力量 。
in our species , the alpha males define reality , and force the rest of the pack to accept that reality and follow the rules .	在我們的物種中 , 雄性領袖定義了現實 , 迫使其他群體接受現實並遵守規則 。
the rules change all the time , but they always benefit them , and in this case , the trickledown effect , which does not work in economics , works perfectly .	規則會隨時改變 , 但它們總是受益 , 在這個例子中 , 棘手的效應 , 在經濟上是行不通的 。
abuse trickles down from the top of the ladder to the bottom .	虐待從梯子的頂端滲透到底部 。
women and children , especially the poor , are at the bottom .	女人和孩子 , 尤其是窮人 , 都在最底層 。
even the most destitute of men have someone they can abuse a woman or a child .	即使是最多男性 , 她們也能虐待女人或小孩 。
i'm fed up with the power that a few exert over the many through gender , income , race , and class .	我充滿了少數的力量 , 透過性別、收入、種族、階級 , 和階級 。
i think that the time is ripe to make fundamental changes in our civilization .	我認為 , 時間是對我們文明的基本改變 。
but for real change , we need feminine energy in the management of the world .	但 , 為了真正的改變 , 我們需要女性化的能量來管理世界 。
we need a critical number of women in positions of power , and we need to nurture the feminine energy in men .	我們需要一群婦女在權力的位置上 , 我們需要培養男性女性化的能量 。
i'm talking about men with young minds , of course .	當然 , 我在說的是有年輕心智的人 。
old guys are hopeless ; we have to wait for them to die off .	老人是無望的 , 我們得要等他們死去 。
yes , i would love to have sophia loren's long legs and legendary breasts .	沒錯 , 我很想有蘇菲雅的長腿和傳奇的胸部 。
but given a choice , i would rather have the warrior hearts of wangari maathai , somaly mam , jenny and rose mapendo .	但 , 為了選擇 , 我寧願有勇氣的心臟 , 天瑪麗•馬塔伊 , 蘇曼 , 珍妮和玫瑰地圖 。
i want to make this world good .	我想讓這個世界變得更好 。
not better , but to make it good .	不是更好 , 而是要讓它更好 。
why not ? it is possible . look around in this room all this knowledge , energy , talent and technology .	為什麼不 ? 它是可能的 。 看看這個房間裡的所有知識、能量、才華和科技 。
let's get off our fannies , roll up our sleeves and get to work , passionately , in creating an almost perfect world .	讓我們脫離我們的粉絲 , 捲起袖子 , 去工作 , 熱情地創造一個幾乎完美的世界 。
every day , in a city the size of london , 30 million meals are served . but where does all the food come from ? architect carolyn steel discusses the daily miracle of feeding a city , and shows how ancient food routes shaped the modern world .	每一天 , 在倫敦的大小 , 有三千萬份餐 , 但 , 所有食物來自哪裡 ? 建築師史黛爾在討論要餵飽一個城市的日常奇蹟 , 展示出古老的食物路線如何影響現代世界 。
cities , culture , food , global issues	城市、文化、食物、全球議題、全球議題 。
carolyn steel: how food shapes our cities	卡羅琳•史黛爾:食物如何塑造我們的城市 , 如何塑造我們的城市 。
how do you feed a city ?	你要如何餵飽一個城市 ?
it's one of the great questions of our time .	這是我們這個時代最偉大的問題之一 。
yet it's one that's rarely asked .	但卻很少被問到 。
we take it for granted that if we go into a shop or restaurant , or indeed into this theater's foyer in about an hour's time , there is going to be food there waiting for us , having magically come from somewhere .	我們把它視為理所當然 , 如果我們去一間商店或餐廳 , 或在一個小時的戲院裡 , 會在那裡等待我們 , 神奇地來自某處 。
but when you think that every day for a city the size of london , enough food has to be produced , transported , bought and sold , cooked , eaten , disposed of , and that something similar has to happen every day for every city on earth , it's remarkable that cities get fed at all .	但當你認為 , 每一天 , 一個像倫敦一樣大的城市 , 足夠的食物必須被生產、運輸、購買、吃飯、廢棄物 , 同樣的事 , 對於世界上的每一座城市 , 都必須有很了不起的意義 。
we live in places like this as if they're the most natural things in the world , forgetting that because we're animals and that we need to eat , we're actually as dependent on the natural world as our ancient ancestors were .	我們生活在像這樣的地方 , 彷彿他們是世界上最自然的事物 , 因為我們是動物 , 也是我們需要吃的 , 我們其實是依賴自然的祖先 。
and as more of us move into cities , more of that natural world is being transformed into extraordinary landscapes like the one behind me it's soybean fields in mato grosso in brazil in order to feed us .	隨著更多人進入城市 , 更多的自然世界被轉化成非凡的地景 , 像我身後的那一塊 , 位在巴西的馬托格羅索的大豆田 , 為了餵飽我們 。
these are extraordinary landscapes , but few of us ever get to see them .	這些是不可思議的地景 , 但我們當中少數人能看到它們 。
and increasingly these landscapes are not just feeding us either .	越來越多的景觀 , 不僅僅是餵飽我們 。
as more of us move into cities , more of us are eating meat , so that a third of the annual grain crop globally now gets fed to animals rather than to us human animals .	隨著我們進入城市 , 越來越多人在吃肉 , 全球每年有三分之一的穀物被餵給動物 , 而非我們人類的動物 。
and given that it takes three times as much grain actually ten times as much grain to feed a human if it's passed through an animal first , that's not a very efficient way of feeding us .	由於它需要三倍的穀物實際上是十倍的穀物來餵飽人類如果它是先通過動物的話那不是非常有效率的餵食方式
and it's an escalating problem too .	這也是一個不斷增加的問題 。
by 2050 , it's estimated that twice the number of us are going to be living in cities .	到2050年 , 據估計 , 我們將會住在城市中的兩倍 。
and it's also estimated that there is going to be twice as much meat and dairy consumed .	估計也會有兩倍的肉和奶類消耗 。
so meat and urbanism are rising hand in hand .	所以 , 肉和城市主義正在崛起 。
and that's going to pose an enormous problem .	這將會是一個巨大的問題 。
six billion hungry carnivores to feed , by 2050 .	到2050年 , 飢餓的食肉動物會餵飽六十億 。
that's a big problem . and actually if we carry on as we are , it's a problem we're very unlikely to be able to solve .	這是個大問題 。 如果我們繼續這樣下去 , 我們就不可能解決這個問題了 。
nineteen million hectares of rainforest are lost every year to create new arable land .	每年有九千萬公頃的雨林消失 , 造成新的可耕地 。
although at the same time we're losing an equivalent amount of existing arables to salinization and erosion .	儘管我們同時失去了相當多的既有的可耕種性 , 來將海水化和侵蝕降低 。
we're very hungry for fossil fuels too .	我們也對化石燃料非常渴望 。
it takes about 10 calories to produce every calorie of food that we consume in the west .	要花十卡路里才能產出我們西方的每一卡路里 。
and even though there is food that we are producing at great cost , we don't actually value it .	儘管我們有很大成本生產的食物 , 我們其實不太重視它 。
half the food produced in the usa is currently thrown away .	美國有一半的食物產量正在被丟棄 。
and to end all of this , at the end of this long process , we're not even managing to feed the planet properly .	為了結束這一切 , 在這個長期的過程結束時 , 我們甚至無法妥當地供應食物給地球 。
a billion of us are obese , while a further billion starve .	十億人是肥胖的 , 而更長的十億人是肥胖的 。
none of it makes very much sense .	這一切都沒有道理 。
and when you think that 80 percent of global trade in food now is controlled by just five multinational corporations , it's a grim picture .	當你認為 , 全球80%的食物交易現在只由五家跨國企業控制 , 這是一張很可怕的照片 。
as we're moving into cities , the world is also embracing a western diet .	當我們進入城市時 , 世界也在擁抱西方的飲食 。
and if we look to the future , it's an unsustainable diet .	如果我們看看未來 , 它是種不穩定的飲食 。
so how did we get here ?	所以 , 我們是怎麼來到這裡的 ?
and more importantly , what are we going to do about it ?	更重要的是 , 我們要怎麼做 ?
well , to answer the slightly easier question first , about 10 , 000 years ago , i would say , is the beginning of this process in the ancient near east , known as the fertile crescent .	首先 , 稍微簡單一點的回答 , 大約一萬年前 , 我會說 , 是這個過程的開端 , 在古老的東方 , 被稱為肥沃土壤 。
because , as you can see , it was crescent shaped .	因為 , 如你所見 , 它是克萊斯的形狀 。
and it was also fertile .	它也很肥沃 。
and it was here , about 10 , 000 years ago , that two extraordinary inventions , agriculture and urbanism , happened roughly in the same place and at the same time .	大約在一萬年前 , 這裡有兩項非凡的發明 , 農業和城市主義 , 發生在同一個地方 , 同時也是如此 。
this is no accident , because agriculture and cities are bound together . they need each other .	這不是意外 , 因為農業和城市是互相連結的 , 他們需要彼此 。
because it was discovery of grain by our ancient ancestors for the first time that produced a food source that was large enough and stable enough to support permanent settlements .	因為這是我們古老的祖先第一次發現穀物 , 產生出足夠大且穩定的食物來源 , 足以支撐永久的居住地 。
and if we look at what those settlements were like , we see they were compact .	如果我們看看這些定居處是什麼樣子 , 我們會看到它們是同伴 。
they were surrounded by productive farm land and dominated by large temple complexes like this one at ur , that were , in fact , effectively , spiritualized , central food distribution centers .	它們被農田包圍 , 被大型寺廟主宰 , 像是烏爾的這一個 , 實際上 , 實際上 , 被心靈化 , 中央食物分佈中心所主宰 。
because it was the temples that organized the harvest , gathered in the grain , offered it to the gods , and then offered the grain that the gods didn't eat back to the people .	因為那是神殿組織了收成的神殿 , 聚集在穀物上 , 將它送給神 , 然後給神們吃不了的穀物 。
so , if you like , the whole spiritual and physical life of these cities was dominated by the grain and the harvest that sustained them .	所以 , 如果你喜歡 , 這些城市的整個靈性和身體生活都是由穀物和收成的 。
and in fact , that's true of every ancient city .	事實上 , 每個古老的城市都是如此 。
but of course not all of them were that small .	但當然不是全部都這麼小 。
famously , rome had about a million citizens by the first century a . d .	著名的是 , 羅馬在第一世紀時就有大約一百萬名公民 。
so how did a city like this feed itself ?	所以 , 像這樣的城市是怎麼養的 ?
the answer is what i call " ancient food miles . "	答案是我稱之為 「 古老的食物里程 」 。
basically , rome had access to the sea , which made it possible for it to import food from a very long way away .	基本上 , 羅馬可以取得海洋 , 讓它能在很遠的距離取得進口糧食 。
this is the only way it was possible to do this in the ancient world , because it was very difficult to transport food over roads , which were rough .	這是唯一能在古代世界做這件事的方式 , 因為在道路上 , 要運送食物是非常困難的 。
and the food obviously went off very quickly .	食物顯然很快就開始了 。
so rome effectively waged war on places like carthage and egypt just to get its paws on their grain reserves .	所以羅馬有效地為像卡特和埃及這樣的地方爭取戰爭 , 只為了讓它停在他們的穀物上 。
and , in fact , you could say that the expansion of the empire was really sort of one long , drawn out militarized shopping spree , really .	事實上 , 你可以說 , 帝國的擴張是非常漫長的 , 用軍事化的購物速度 , 真的是如此 。
in fact i love the fact , i just have to mention this: rome in fact used to import oysters from london , at one stage . i think that's extraordinary .	事實上 , 我很喜歡這個事實 , 我只需要提一下:羅馬曾經是從倫敦到倫敦的牡蠣 。 我認為這很了不起 。
so rome shaped its hinterland through its appetite .	所以羅馬形塑了它的暗落 , 通過它的食慾 。
but the interesting thing is that the other thing also happened in the preindustrial world .	但有趣的是 , 另一件事也發生在工業前的世界 。
if we look at a map of london in the 17th century , we can see that its grain , which is coming in from the thames , along the bottom of this map .	如果我們看一下十七世紀倫敦的地圖 , 我們可以看到它的穀物 , 它的穀物是從這張地圖的底部來的 。
so the grain markets were to the south of the city .	所以 , 穀物市場就在城市南方 。
and the roads leading up from them to cheapside , which was the main market , were also grain markets .	道路從它們變成廉價 , 主要的市場也是穀物市場 。
and if you look at the name of one of those streets , bread street , you can tell what was going on there 300 years ago .	如果你看看其中一條街道的名字 , 布雷德街 , 你可以在300年前知道那裡發生了什麼事 。
and the same of course was true for fish .	當然 , 對魚來說也是如此 。
fish was , of course , coming in by river as well . same thing .	當然 , 魚也是靠河流進來的 。
and of course billingsgate , famously , was london's fish market , operating onsite here until the mid1980s .	當然 , billgate , 著名的 , 是倫敦的魚市場 , 直到1980年代中期 。
which is extraordinary , really , when you think about it .	這真是不可思議 , 真的 , 仔細想想 。
everybody else was wandering around with mobile phones that looked like bricks and sort of smelly fish happening down on the port .	所有人都在用手機散步 , 看起來像是磚塊 , 有點像是在港口發生的煙囪魚 。
this is another thing about food in cities: once its roots into the city are established , they very rarely move .	這是城市中食物的另一件事:一旦根植入城市就會被建立起來 , 他們就很少移動 。
meat is a very different story because , of course , animals could walk into the city .	肉類是非常不同的 , 因為 , 當然 , 動物可以走進城市 。
so much of london's meat was coming from the northwest , from scotland and wales .	倫敦大部分的肉來自西北部蘇格蘭和威爾斯 。
so it was coming in , and arriving at the city at the northwest , which is why smithfield , london's very famous meat market , was located up there .	所以它進入了 , 到達了西北的城市 , 這就是為什麼史密斯菲爾德 , 倫敦著名的肉市場 , 位在那裏 。
poultry was coming in from east anglia and so on , to the northeast .	家禽從東加利亞來到東北部 。
i feel a bit like a weather woman doing this . anyway , and so the birds were coming in with their feet protected with little canvas shoes .	不管怎樣 , 我感覺有點像一位天氣女子 , 鳥兒們就來到他們的腳上 , 用小的帆布來保護 。
and then when they hit the eastern end of cheapside , that's where they were sold , which is why it's called poultry .	當他們到達廉價的東邊時 , 他們就被賣掉了 , 這就是為什麼它會被稱為 「 模仿 」 。
and , in fact , if you look at the map of any city built before the industrial age , you can trace food coming in to it .	事實上 , 如果你看任何一個城市在工業時代之前建立的地圖 , 你可以追蹤食物進來 。
you can actually see how it was physically shaped by food , both by reading the names of the streets , which give you a lot of clues .	你可以看到它的身體形狀 , 無論是閱讀街道的名字 , 都可以給你很多線索 。
friday street , in a previous life , is where you went to buy your fish on a friday .	星期五街 , 以前你在星期五去買魚 。
but also you have to imagine it full of food .	但同時你也要想像它充滿食物 。
because the streets and the public spaces were the only places where food was bought and sold .	因為街道和公共空間是唯一食物被賣掉的地方 。
and if we look at an image of smithfield in 1830 you can see that it would have been very difficult to live in a city like this and be unaware of where your food came from .	如果我們看一下1830年史密斯菲爾德的圖像 , 你可以看到 , 在像這樣的城市生活是非常困難的 , 不知你的食物從何而來 。
in fact , if you were having sunday lunch , the chances were it was mooing or bleating outside your window about three days earlier .	事實上 , 如果你有星期天午餐 , 可能在三天前你窗外流浪或在你窗外流浪 。
so this was obviously an organic city , part of an organic cycle .	這顯然是一個有機城市 , 一個有機循環的一部分 。
and then 10 years later everything changed .	十年後 , 一切都改變了 。
this is an image of the great western in 1840 .	這是1840年的大西部大西部的照片 。
and as you can see , some of the earliest train passengers were pigs and sheep .	如你所見 , 最早的火車乘客是豬和羊 。
so all of a sudden , these animals are no longer walking into market .	突然間 , 這些動物不再走進市場 。
they're being slaughtered out of sight and mind , somewhere in the countryside .	他們被從視覺和心智中屠殺 , 在鄉下的某處 。
and they're coming into the city by rail .	他們是以鐵路來到城市的 。
and this changes everything .	這改變了一切 。
to start off with , it makes it possible for the first time to grow cities , really any size and shape , in any place .	首先 , 首次要種植城市 , 大小和形狀 , 在任何地方 。
cities used to be constrained by geography ; they used to have to get their food through very difficult physical means .	過去 , 城市被地理限制 ; 過去他們必須透過非常困難的實體來取得食物 。
all of a sudden they are effectively emancipated from geography .	突然間 , 他們從地理上有效地解放 。
and as you can see from these maps of london , in the 90 years after the trains came , it goes from being a little blob that was quite easy to feed by animals coming in on foot , and so on , to a large splurge , that would be very , very difficult to feed with anybody on foot , either animals or people .	如你所見 , 從倫敦的地圖來看 , 在火車經過的90年後 , 它從一個小小的小小點 , 由動物在腳上餵食 , 至於一個巨大的噴泉 , 非常非常難以滿足任何人 , 動物或人類 。
and of course that was just the beginning . after the trains came cars , and really this marks the end of this process .	當然 , 這只是開端 。 火車來了 , 真的是這整個過程的終點 。
it's the final emancipation of the city from any apparent relationship with nature at all .	這是城市的最後一個解放 , 完全從大自然的任何明顯關係中解放 。
and this is the kind of city that's devoid of smell , devoid of mess , certainly devoid of people , because nobody would have dreamed of walking in such a landscape .	這是一種沒有嗅覺、缺乏混亂的城市 , 肯定沒有人 , 因為沒有人會夢想走在這樣的地景中 。
in fact , what they did to get food was they got in their cars , drove to a box somewhere on the outskirts , came back with a week's worth of shopping , and wondered what on earth to do with it .	事實上 , 他們為了得到食物的成果是他們在車子上開車到外面的一個盒子上 , 帶著一週的購物回來 , 想知道地球上要怎麼做 。
and this really is the moment when our relationship , both with food and cities , changes completely .	此時此刻 , 我們與食物和城市的關係 , 完全改變了 。
here we have food that used to be the center , the social core of the city at the periphery .	以前我們有食物是市中心 , 市區的社會核心 。
it used to be a social event , buying and selling food .	它以前是社交活動 , 購買和賣食物 。
we used to cook ; now we just add water , or a little bit of an egg if you're making a cake or something .	我們以前會煮飯 , 只要加水 , 或加一點點蛋 , 只要你做蛋糕或其他東西 。
we don't smell food to see if it's okay to eat .	我們不會聞到食物 , 看看它是否可以吃 。
we just read the back of a label on a packet .	我們只是讀一個包裝後面的標籤 。
and we don't value food . we don't trust it .	我們不重視食物 。 我們不信任它 。
so instead of trusting it , we fear it .	所以 , 我們不再相信它 , 而是害怕它 。
and instead of valuing it , we throw it away .	而不是在評估它 , 而是丟掉它 。
one of the great ironies of modern food systems is that they've made the very thing they promised to make easier much harder .	現代食品系統的諷刺之處在於他們已經做出了他們承諾要讓它變得更容易 。
by making it possible to build cities anywhere and any place , they've actually distanced us from our most important relationship , which is that of us and nature .	藉由讓城市在任何地方或任何地方 , 它們都能讓我們遠離我們最重要的關係 , 也就是我們和大自然 。
and also they've made us dependent on systems that only they can deliver , that , as we've seen , are unsustainable .	此外 , 它們也讓我們依賴只有它們能傳遞的系統 , 如我們所見 , 它們是不可持續的 。
so what are we going to do about that ?	所以 , 我們該怎麼做 ?
it's not a new question .	這不是一個新問題 。
500 years ago it's what thomas more was asking himself .	五百年前 , 湯瑪斯更多問自己 。
this is the frontispiece of his book " utopia . "	這是他的《烏托邦》這本書的首映 。
and it was a series of semiindependent citystates , if that sounds remotely familiar , a day's walk from one another where everyone was basically farmingmad , and grew vegetables in their back gardens , and ate communal meals together , and so on .	這是一系列半自主的城市如果這聽起來很熟悉 , 某個日子的人會從一個地方走出來 , 在那裡基本上每個人都是農場養殖民者 , 在他們的後花園中種植蔬菜 , 吃下午餐等等 。
and i think you could argue that food is a fundamental ordering principle of utopia , even though more never framed it that way .	我認為你可以說食物是烏托邦的基本規則即使更別把食物分成那樣
and here is another very famous " utopian " vision , that of ebenezer howard , " the garden city . "	還有另外一個著名的 「 烏托邦 」 視覺 , 埃比沙尼茲霍華 , 「 花園城市 」 。
same idea: series of semiindependent citystates , little blobs of metropolitan stuff with arable land around , joined to one another by railway .	同樣的想法是:半自主城市 , 小型的大都市 , 附近有可耕地 , 加入了鐵路 。
and again , food could be said to be the ordering principle of his vision .	同樣的 , 食物可以被說是他視覺的順序原則 。
it even got built , but nothing to do with this vision that howard had .	它甚至被建造出來了 , 但和霍華德的視野一點關係都沒有 。
and that is the problem with these utopian ideas , that they are utopian .	這就是這些烏托邦的想法 , 他們是烏托邦 。
utopia was actually a word that thomas moore used deliberately .	烏托邦其實是湯瑪斯•摩爾刻意使用的詞 。
it was a kind of joke , because it's got a double derivation from the greek .	這是個笑話 , 因為它是從希臘來的兩倍衍生的 。
it can either mean a good place , or no place .	它可能意味著一個好地方 , 或沒有地方 。
because it's an ideal . it's an imaginary thing . we can't have it .	因為它是理想的 , 它是想像的 。 我們不能擁有它 。
and i think , as a conceptual tool for thinking about the very deep problem of human dwelling , that makes it not much use .	我認為 , 作為一個概念工具 , 來思考人類的極深問題 , 讓它不太有用 。
so i've come up with an alternative , which is sitopia , from the ancient greek , " sitos " for food , and " topos " for place .	所以我想出了一個替代方案 , 來自西托邦 , 古希臘 , 「 西托 」 供食物和 「 波斯 」 。
i believe we already live in sitopia .	我相信我們已經生活在西托邦 。
we live in a world shaped by food , and if we realize that , we can use food as a really powerful tool a conceptual tool , design tool , to shape the world differently .	我們生活在一個由食物塑造的世界 , 如果我們意識到 , 我們能用食物作為一個強大的工具 , 一個有力的概念工具 , 設計工具 , 來形塑世界 。
so if we were to do that , what might sitopia look like ?	所以如果我們這樣做 , 西托邦看起來會是什麼樣子 ?
well i think it looks a bit like this .	我想這看起來有點像這樣 。
i have to use this slide . it's just the look on the face of the dog .	我得用這張投影片 , 只不過是狗的臉 。
but anyway , this is it's food at the center of life , at the center of family life , being celebrated , being enjoyed , people taking time for it .	但無論如何 , 這是食物在生活中心 , 在家庭生活的中心 , 被讚頌、享受、享受、花點時間 。
this is where food should be in our society .	這就是食物應該在我們的社會裡 。
but you can't have scenes like this unless you have people like this .	但除非你有像這樣的人 , 你就不可能有這樣的場景 。
by the way , these can be men as well .	順道一提 , 這些也可以是男人 。
it's people who think about food , who think ahead , who plan , who can stare at a pile of raw vegetables and actually recognize them .	它是那些思考食物的人 , 想著 , 誰計劃 , 誰可以盯著一堆原始蔬菜 , 並且認可他們 。
we need these people . we're part of a network .	我們需要這些人 , 我們是網路的一部分 。
because without these kinds of people we can't have places like this .	因為如果沒有這些人 , 我們就不可能有這樣的場所 。
here , i deliberately chose this because it is a man buying a vegetable .	在這裡 , 我故意選這個 , 因為它是一個男人買蔬菜 。
but networks , markets where food is being grown locally .	但網絡 , 食物本地生長的市場 。
it's common . it's fresh .	它很常見 , 很新鮮 。
it's part of the social life of the city .	它是城市社會生活的一部分 。
because without that , you can't have this kind of place , food that is grown locally and also is part of the landscape , and is not just a zerosum commodity off in some unseen hellhole .	因為 , 若沒有這樣 , 你就不能有這種地方 , 當地生長的食物 , 也是地景的一部分 , 而不只是零和商品 , 在一些未知的地獄中 。
cows with a view .	牛的觀點是 。
steaming piles of humus .	一堆混合物 。
this is basically bringing the whole thing together .	這基本上是把整個東西整合在一起 。
and this is a community project i visited recently in toronto .	這是我最近在多倫多拜訪的一個社區計畫 。
it's a greenhouse , where kids get told all about food and growing their own food .	這是一間溫室 , 孩子們會告訴所有關於食物和種植食物的東西 。
here is a plant called kevin , or maybe it's a plant belonging to a kid called kevin . i don't know .	這裡有一株叫做凱文的植物 , 或許是植物屬於一個叫凱文的孩子 。 我不知道 。
but anyway , these kinds of projects that are trying to reconnect us with nature is extremely important .	但無論如何 , 這些計畫試圖和大自然重新連結 , 非常重要 。
so sitopia , for me , is really a way of seeing .	所以 , 對我來說 , 希托邦是種看法 。
it's basically recognizing that sitopia already exists in little pockets everywhere .	基本上 , 西托邦已經在各處存在了小口袋裡 。
the trick is to join them up , to use food as a way of seeing .	訣竅是要加入它們 , 把食物當作一種看法 。
and if we do that , we're going to stop seeing cities as big , metropolitan , unproductive blobs , like this .	如果我們這樣做 , 我們將會停止把城市視為大型、大都會、不生產力的大型城市 , 像這樣 。
we're going to see them more like this , as part of the productive , organic framework of which they are inevitably a part , symbiotically connected .	我們將看到它們更像這樣 , 作為有生產力、有機架構的一部分 , 它們是無可避免的一部分 , 相同的連結 。
but of course , that's not a great image either , because we need not to be producing food like this anymore .	但當然 , 這也不是一個偉大的圖像 , 因為我們不需要再像這樣生產食物 。
we need to be thinking more about permaculture , which is why i think this image just sums up for me the kind of thinking we need to be doing .	我們需要更深入思考永續文化 , 這就是為什麼我認為這張圖只是總結一下我們需要做的事 。
it's a reconceptualization of the way food shapes our lives .	它是重新思考食物如何塑造我們的生活的方式 。
the best image i know of this is from 650 years ago .	我所知道最棒的圖像是650年前 。
it's ambrogio lorenzetti's " allegory of good government . "	阿布羅吉歐•洛倫澤蒂的《好政府的寓言》 。
it's about the relationship between the city and the countryside .	重點是城市和鄉村之間的關係 。
and i think the message of this is very clear .	我認為這個訊息非常明確 。
if the city looks after the country , the country will look after the city .	如果城市照顧這個國家 , 這個國家會照顧這個城市 。
and i want us to ask now , what would ambrogio lorenzetti paint if he painted this image today ?	我現在要問我們 , 阿布羅吉歐•洛倫澤蒂是否能畫出這張照片 ?
what would an allegory of good government look like today ?	今天美好政府的寓言會是什麼樣子 ?
because i think it's an urgent question .	因為我認為這是一個急迫的問題 。
it's one we have to ask , and we have to start answering .	這是我們必須問的 , 我們必須開始回答 。
we know we are what we eat .	我們知道我們在吃什麼 。
we need to realize that the world is also what we eat .	我們需要了解到 , 世界也是我們所吃的 。
but if we take that idea , we can use food as a really powerful tool to shape the world better .	但如果我們採用這個想法 , 我們就可以把食物當作一個非常強大的工具來形塑世界更好 。
weeks from the charter for compassion launch , karen armstrong looks at religion's role in the 21st century: will its dogmas divide us ? or will it unite us for common good ? she reviews the catalysts that can drive the world's faiths to rediscover the golden rule .	數週後 , 同情心發射 , 卡倫•阿姆斯壯觀察宗教在21世紀扮演的角色:它的教義會分裂我們嗎 ? 或者它會使我們團結在一起 ? 她會審視世界上的催化劑 , 來重新發現黃金法則 。
god , ted prize , global issues , politics , religion , tedglobal2009 , violence	上帝 , ted的獎、全球議題、政治、宗教、tedglobal-2009、暴力 。
karen armstrong: let's revive the golden rule	卡倫•阿姆斯壯:讓我們重現黃金法則 。
for years i've been feeling frustrated , because as a religious historian , i've become acutely aware of the centrality of compassion in all the major world faiths .	多年來 , 我感到挫敗 , 因為身為宗教歷史學家 , 我漸漸意識到 , 同情心的中心性 , 在世界的主要信仰中 。
every single one of them has evolved their own version of what's been called the golden rule .	每一位都演化出他們自己的 「 黃金法則 」 的版本 。
sometimes it comes in a positive version " always treat all others as you'd like to be treated yourself . "	有時它會出現一個正面的版本: 「 總是把他人當成你想治療自己的方式 。 」
and equally important is the negative version " don't do to others what you would not like them to do to you . "	同樣重要的是負面的版本: 「 不要對別人做你不希望他們做的事 。 」
look into your own heart , discover what it is that gives you pain and then refuse , under any circumstance whatsoever , to inflict that pain on anybody else .	看看你自己的心 , 發現你的痛苦是什麼 , 然後拒絕 , 在任何情況下 , 在任何情況下 , 將痛苦給任何其他人 。
and people have emphasized the importance of compassion , not just because it sounds good , but because it works .	人們強調的是同情心的重要性 , 不只是因為它聽起來很好 , 也因為它有效 。
people have found that when they have implemented the golden rule as confucius said , " all day and every day , " not just a question of doing your good deed for the day and then returning to a life of greed and egotism , but to do it all day and every day , you dethrone yourself from the center of your world , put another there , and you transcend yourself .	人們發現 , 當他們把黃金法則當成混亂 , 說: 「 整天和每一天 」 , 不只是做好事 , 然後回到貪婪和自我主義的一生 , 每天都要做 , 把自己從世界的中心擺脫出來 , 然後超越你自己 。
and it brings you into the presence of what's been called god , nirvana , rama , tao .	它將你帶入了被稱為神的存在 , 尼爾瓦拉、拉馬、tao 。
something that goes beyond what we know in our egobound existence .	超越我們所知的存在 。
but you know you'd never know it a lot of the time , that this was so central to the religious life .	但你知道你從來不知道 , 這對宗教生活是如此的核心 。
because with a few wonderful exceptions , very often when religious people come together , religious leaders come together , they're arguing about abstruse doctrines or uttering a council of hatred or inveighing against homosexuality or something of that sort .	因為有了一些很棒的例外 , 宗教團體聚在一起 , 宗教領袖聚集在一起 , 他們爭論的是荒誕的教條 , 或說出仇恨的議會 , 或對抗同性戀或其他類型的人 。
often people don't really want to be compassionate .	通常 , 人們並不想要有同情心 。
i sometimes see when i'm speaking to a congregation of religious people a sort of mutinous expression crossing their faces because people often want to be right instead .	有時 , 我會看到我在和宗教聚會談話時 , 有點像是跨越他們的臉 , 因為人們通常會想要是對的 。
and that of course defeats the object of the exercise .	當然 , 這也打敗了運動的物體 。
now why was i so grateful to ted ?	我為什麼很感激ted ?
because they took me very gently from my booklined study and brought me into the 21st century , enabling me to speak to a much , much wider audience than i could have ever conceived .	因為他們很溫柔地從我的書籍研究帶我進入21世紀 , 讓我能和一個更廣泛的觀眾說話 。
because i feel an urgency about this .	因為我對此感到急迫 。
if we don't manage to implement the golden rule globally , so that we treat all peoples , wherever and whoever they may be , as though they were as important as ourselves , i doubt that we'll have a viable world to hand on to the next generation .	如果我們無法在全球執行黃金法則 , 這樣我們就能對待所有人 , 不論他們在哪裡 , 不論他們在哪裡 , 都一樣重要 , 我懷疑我們會有一個可實現的世界 , 來接近下一代 。
the task of our time , one of the great tasks of our time , is to build a global society , as i said , where people can live together in peace .	我們這個時代的任務之一 , 就是要建立一個全球社會 , 如我所說 , 在那裡 , 人們可以在和平生活 。
and the religions that should be making a major contribution are instead seen as part of the problem .	而應該要做出重大貢獻的宗教 , 卻被視為是問題的一部分 。
and of course it's not just religious people who believe in the golden rule .	當然 , 不只是宗教信仰黃金法則的人 。
this is the source of all morality , this imaginative act of empathy , putting yourself in the place of another .	這是所有道德的來源 , 這種想像力的行為 , 把你自己放在另一個地方 。
and so we have a choice , it seems to me .	所以 , 我們有一個選擇 , 似乎對我來說 。
we can either go on bringing out or emphasizing the dogmatic and intolerant aspects of our faith , or we can go back to the rabbis . rabbi hillel , the older contemporary of jesus , who , when asked by a pagan to sum up the whole of jewish teaching while he stood on one leg , said , " that which is hateful to you , do not do to your neighbor .	我們要不就是要把我們信仰的教義和包容的觀點提醒 , 要不我們回到拉比 。 拉比希爾 , 古老的耶穌 , 當他在一條腿上總結猶太教時 , 說: 「 這對你是很討厭的 , 不要對你的鄰居做事 。
that is the torah and everything else is only commentary . "	那就是 「 塔拉 」 和 「 一切都只是評論 」 。
and the rabbis and the early fathers of the church who said that any interpretation of scripture that bred hatred and disdain was illegitimate .	教堂早期的rabbis和早期的父親說 , 任何與討厭的劇本的詮釋都是違法的 。
and we need to revive that spirit .	我們需要重生那種精神 。

we have to make this happen , and we can do it with the modern communications that ted has introduced .	我們必須讓這一切發生 , 並且我們可以用現代的溝通來實現ted介紹 。
already i've been tremendously heartened at the response of all our partners .	我已經對我們所有夥伴的反應感到極大的鼓舞 。
in singapore , we have a group going to use the charter to heal divisions recently that have sprung up in singaporean society , and some members of the parliament want to implement it politically .	在新加坡 , 我們有一個團體最近要用章節來治療新加坡社會的癒合分裂 , 議會中的一些成員想在政治上實施它 。
in malaysia , there is going to be an art exhibition in which leading artists are going to be taking people , young people , and showing them that compassion also lies at the root of all art .	在馬來西亞 , 將會有一個藝術展覽 , 領導的藝術家將會帶領人們、年輕人 , 並展現出同情心在所有藝術的根源上 。
throughout europe , the muslim communities are holding events and discussions , are discussing the centrality of compassion in islam and in all faiths .	在整個歐洲 , 穆斯林群體正在舉辦活動和討論 , 都是在討論伊斯蘭和所有信仰中的同情心中心 。
but it can't stop there . it can't stop with the launch .	但它不能停止 。 它不能停止發射 。
religious teaching , this is where we've gone so wrong , concentrating solely on believing abstruse doctrines .	宗教教義 , 這是我們錯了的地方 , 只靠信仰absstruse的教義 。

people often think it simply means feeling sorry for somebody .	人們常常認為這意味著對某人感到遺憾 。
but of course you don't understand compassion if you're just going to think about it .	但 , 當然 , 如果你只是想一想的話 , 你不會了解同情心 。

the same applies to educators .	教育者也適用於教學
i'd like youth to get a sense of the dynamism , the dynamic and challenge of a compassionate lifestyle .	我希望年輕人能了解動態、動態和挑戰同情的生活方式 。

i'd like to call upon scholars to explore the compassionate theme in their own and in other people's traditions .	我想打電話給學者 , 來探索他們自己的同情心主題 , 以及其他人的傳統 。
and perhaps above all , to encourage a sensitivity about uncompassionate speaking , so that because people have this charter , whatever their beliefs or lack of them , they feel empowered to challenge uncompassionate speech , disdainful remarks from their religious leaders , their political leaders , from the captains of industry .	最重要的是 , 鼓勵不熱情說話的敏感度 , 如此一來 , 人們有這個特徵 , 不論他們的信念或缺乏信仰 , 他們會覺得有能力去挑戰不熱情的言論、不穩定的言論 , 來自他們的宗教領袖、政治領袖、他們的政治領袖 。

he said that he distinguished between erotic love , when two people gaze , spellbound , into each other's eyes .	他說他分辨了愛情 , 當兩個人凝視著咒語時 , 彼此之間的眼睛 。
and then he compared that to friendship , when two people stand side by side , as it were , shoulder to shoulder , with their eyes fixed on a common goal .	接著 , 他把這和友誼比較 , 當兩個人站在旁邊 , 肩膀肩膀時 , 眼睛被固定在一個共同的目標上 。
we don't have to fall in love with each other , but we can become friends .	我們不必要愛上彼此 , 但我們可以成為朋友 。

this thing would be flying over or past or be parked in front of , but it would be like having a ruler sort of travel through the pages without being a ruler .	這東西會飛越或過去 , 或在前面停車 , 但它就像是有統治者穿越了頁面 , 而不是統治者 。

this is beatrix . she has a dog named ajax , she has purchased a dirigible a small dirigible she's assembling the structure , ajax is sniffing for holes in the balloon before they set off .	這是beatrix 。 她有隻叫ajax的狗 , 她買了一台很小的飛行器 , 她組裝了這個結構 , ajax在氣球上聞到漏洞的味道 。
she launches this thing above the spanish steps and sets off for an aerial tour of the city .	她在西班牙階梯上推出這個東西 , 為城市的空中巡迴演出 。

a nice way to show that river , that stream sort of pouring down the hill .	展現這條河 , 河流有點像倒下山丘 。

a spectacular framework , inside of which you see , usually , extraordinary blue sky .	一個壯觀的架構 , 在裡面 , 通常是非常不凡的藍天 。

the text here is right side and upside down so that you are forced to turn the book around , and you can see it from ground point of view and from her point of view looking in the hole , getting a different kind of perspective , moving you around the space . particularly appropriate in a building that can contain perfectly a sphere dimensions of the diameter being the same as the distance from the center of the floor to the center of the oculus .	這裡的文字是對的側邊 , 所以你被迫把書轉過來 , 你可以看到它從地面的視角 , 從洞的角度來看 , 得到不同的觀點 , 特別適合在一棟大樓裡 , 直徑的角度和距離相同 。
unfortunately for her , the anchor line gets tangled around the feet of some boy scouts who are visiting the pantheon , and they are immediately yanked out and given an extraordinary but terrifying tour of some of the domes of rome , which would , from their point of view , naturally be hanging upside down .	很不幸的是 , 連接線被綁在一些小孩子的腳上 , 探訪了萬神廟 , 他們馬上就被擠出來 , 出去了不凡又嚇人的旅程 , 那些羅馬的主題 , 從他們的角度來看 , 很自然地 , 被吊死了 。

they keep on motoring towards the campo de' fiori , which they soon reach . ajax the dog is put in a basket and lowered with a list of food into the marketplace , which flourishes there until about one in the afternoon , and then is completely removed and doesn't appear again until six or seven the following morning .	他們繼續前進柬埔寨的fiori , 很快就會到達 。 ajax把狗放進籃子裡 , 下載一份食物到市場上 , 直到下午一個 , 然後完全消失 , 直到下午六到七點 。

at the end of lunch , they untie the anchor , they set off through the baths of caracalla and over the walls of the city and then an abandoned gatehouse and decide to take one more look at the pyramid of cestius , which has this lightning rod on top .	在午餐結束時 , 他們打開了主管 , 他們打開了卡拉卡拉的浴室 , 穿越城市的牆壁 , 然後一個廢棄的大門 , 決定再看一下cestius的金字塔 , 上面有一條閃電路 。
unfortunately , that's a problem: they get a little too close , and when you're in a dirigible you have to be very careful about spikes .	不幸的是 , 這是個問題:它們太靠近了 , 當你在潛水中時 , 你必須非常小心地想起尖峰 。
so that sort of brings her little story to a conclusion .	所以這有點像是把她小故事帶到一個結論中 。
marcello , on the other hand , is sort of a lazy guy , but he's not due at work until about noon .	另一方面 , 馬賽洛是個懶惰的人 , 但他一直都在工作 , 直到下午 。

he gets up , leaps onto his scooter , races through the city past the church of santa maria della pace , down the alleys , through the streets that tourists may be wandering through , disturbing the quiet backstreet life of rome at every turn .	他站起來 , 躍上他的摩托車 , 越過城市 , 越過聖塔瑪利亞的教堂 , 走下巷子 , 穿過街頭遊走 , 每次都在羅馬的安靜生活 。
that speed with which he is moving , i hope i have suggested in this little image , which , again , can be turned around and read from both sides because there's text on the bottom and text on the top , one of which is upside down in this image .	他正在移動的速度 , 我希望我在這張小圖片中提到 , 再一次 , 可以從兩邊轉過來閱讀 , 因為上面有文字 , 上面有文字 , 其中一張圖片上下顛倒了 。

right through the piazza della rotonda , in front of the pantheon again wreaking havoc and finally getting to work .	就在潘薩•德拉達面前 , 在萬神殿前 , 又再次破壞了 , 終於成功了 。
marcello , as it turns out , is the driver of the number 64 bus , and if you've been on the number 64 bus , you know that it's driven with the same kind of exuberance as marcello demonstrated on his scooter .	結果發現 , 馬賽洛的驅動力是64輛巴士的駕駛 , 如果你上過了64輛巴士 , 你知道它的驅動力和馬爾賽羅的摩托車一樣 。

enters the courtyard and talks to the custodian , who tells him that there's been a disaster in the palazzo ; nobody's tvs are working and there's a big soccer game coming up , and the crowd is getting a little restless and a little nervous .	進入法庭院 , 和顧客交談 , 他告訴他 , 在巴拉西有一場災難 ; 沒有人在電視上有一場大型的足球比賽 , 群眾變得有點無休止 , 有點緊張 。
he goes down to the basement and starts to check the wiring , and then gradually works his way up to the top of the building , apartment by apartment , checking every television , checking every connection , hoping to find out what this problem is .	他下到地下室 , 開始檢查電線 , 然後逐漸地工作 , 到建築的頂端 , 透過公寓檢查 , 檢查每個電視 , 檢查所有連線 , 希望能找出這個問題的結果 。
he works his way up , finally , the grand staircase and then a smaller staircase until he reaches the attic .	終於 , 他爬上了大樓梯 , 爬上了小樓梯 , 直到他抵達了閣樓 。
he opens the window of the attic , of course , and there's a tablecloth wrapped around the building's television antenna .	他打開閣樓的窗戶 , 當然 , 有一張桌布包圍在大樓的電視天線上 。

all he has to do now , with a perfect table , is wait for her to arrive .	他現在只需要做一個完美的桌子 , 等著她來到這裡 。
that was the first attempt , but it didn't seem substantial enough to convey whatever it was i wanted to convey about rome .	那是第一個嘗試 , 但似乎還不夠實質 , 來傳達我想要傳達的關於羅馬的意見 。

and then i thought , that's too complicated . no , i'll just take my favorite bits and pieces and i'll put them inside the pantheon but keep the scale , so you can see the top of sant'ivo and the pyramid of cestius and the tempietto of bramante all side by side in this amazing space .	然後我想 , 這太複雜了 。 不 , 我會把我最喜歡的部分和碎片放進去 , 把它們放進萬神殿裡 , 這樣你就可以看見聖誕節的頂端和c-stius的金字塔 , 在這神奇的空間中 。
now that's one drawing , so i thought maybe it's time for piranesi to meet escher .	這是一幅畫 , 所以我想也許是該見escher的時候了 。
you see that i'm beginning to really lose control here and also hope .	你可以看到 , 我開始真的失去控制權 , 也開始失去希望 。
there's a very thin blue line of exhaust that sort of runs through this thing that would be kind of the trail that holds it all together .	這裡有一條非常薄的藍色線 , 一路穿過這個東西 , 有點像是把它們整合在一起的軌跡 。
then i thought , " wait a minute , what am i doing ? "	然後我想: 「 等等 , 我在做什麼 ? 」
a book is not only a neat way of collecting and storing information , it's a series of layers .	一本書不僅是收集和儲存資訊的方式 , 而是一系列的層次 。
i mean , you always peel one layer off another ; we think of them as pages , doing it a certain way .	我的意思是 , 你總是把一層剝離另一層 , 我們認為它們是頁面 , 以某種方式做 。
but think of them as layers . i mean , rome is a place of layers horizontal layers , vertical layers and i thought , well just peeling off a page would allow me to if i got you thinking about it the right way would allow me to sort of show you the depth of layers .	但把他們想成一層層 。 我的意思是 , 羅馬是一個層層層的水平層 , 垂直層 , 我心想 , 只要把一頁剝離一頁 , 就會讓我想 , 若我用正確的方式 , 讓我可以向你展示一層的深度 。
the stucco on the walls of most of the buildings in rome covers the scars ; the scars of centuries of change as these structures have been adapted rather than being torn down .	羅馬大廈的牆壁上 , 大部分的建築都覆蓋著疤痕 , 數世紀以來 , 改變的疤痕已經被改造 , 而不是被摧毀 。
if i do a foldout page on the lefthand side and let you just unfold it , you see behind it what i mean by scar tissue .	如果我在左手邊做摺紙 , 讓你展開它 , 你可以看到我所謂的 「 疤組織 」 的背後 。
you can see that in 1635 , it became essential to make smaller windows because the bad guys were coming or whatever .	你可以看到 , 在1635年 , 製造小窗戶是必要的 , 因為壞傢伙來了 , 不管怎麼樣 。
adaptations all get buried under the stucco .	適應系統都被埋在黏土下 。
i could peel out a page of this palazzo to show you what's going on inside of it .	我可以把這一頁的巴拉zo給你看看裡面發生了什麼事 。
but more importantly , i could also show you what it looks like at the corner of one of those magnificent buildings with all the massive stone blocks , or the fake stone blocks done with brick and stucco , which is more often the case .	但更重要的是 , 我還可以向你們展示 , 那些偉大的建築的角落 , 上面有著巨大的石塊 , 或用磚塊做假石塊 , 通常是這樣 。
so it becomes slightly threedimensional .	所以它變得有點三維 。
i could take you down one of those narrow little streets into one of those surprising piazzas by using a double gate fold double foldout page which , if you were like me reading a popup book as a child , you hopefully stick your head into .	我可以把你們其中一條狹窄的小街帶到其中一個令人驚訝的比賽中 , 用一雙雙折疊的頁面 , 如果你像我小時候一樣 , 你希望能把你的頭伸進去 。
you wrap the pages around your head and are in that piazza for that brief period of time .	你把你的頭包裹起來 , 在那短暫的時期 。
and i've really not done anything much more complicated than make foldout pages .	我真的沒有做任何更複雜的事情 , 比摺疊頁面更複雜 。
but then i thought , maybe i could be simpler here .	但我想 , 也許我可以更簡單一點 。
let's look at the pantheon and the piazza della rotonda in front of it .	咱們來看看萬神殿和帕亞薩•德拉 , 就在它面前 。
here's a book completely wide open .	這是一本完全開放的書 。
ok , if i don't open the book the whole way , if i just open it 90 degrees , we're looking down the front of the pantheon , and we're looking sort of at the top , more or less down on the square .	好 , 如果我不打開這本書 , 如果我打開它90度 , 我們就在下面的萬神廟 , 我們就在向上看 , 在廣場上下看 。
and if i turn the book the other way , we're looking across the square at the front of the pantheon .	如果我轉換這本書 , 我們在萬神廟前面看到的正方形 。
no foldouts , no tricks just a book that isn't open the whole way .	沒有摺疊 , 沒有把戲 , 只是一本不打開的書 。
that seemed promising . i thought , maybe i'll do it inside and i can even combine the foldouts with the only partially opened book .	這聽起來很有希望 。 我想 , 也許我可以在裡面做 , 我甚至可以把摺疊技術和唯一的開放書結合起來 。
so we get inside the pantheon and it grows and so on and so forth .	所以 , 我們進到萬神廟裡 , 它會不斷成長 , 等等 。
and i thought , maybe i'm on the right track , but it sort of lost its human quality .	我想 , 也許我在正確的軌道上 , 但它有點失去了人類的特質 。
so i went back to the notion of story , which is always a good thing to have if you're trying to get people to pay attention to a book and pick up information along the way .	所以我回到故事的概念 , 如果你想讓大家注意一本書 , 一路上收集資訊 , 總是一件好事 。
" pigeon's progress " struck me as a catchy title .	「 鴿子的進步 」 把我當作 「 抓住 」 標題 。
if it was a homing pigeon , it would be called " homer's odyssey . "	如果這隻鴿子叫作荷馬的奧德西 "
but it was the journey of the . . .	但那是那段旅程......
i mean , if a title works , use it . but it would be a journey that went through rome and showed all the things that i like about rome .	我的意思是 , 如果一個標題能用 , 但這將會是一段旅程 , 經過羅馬 , 展現我喜歡的羅馬 。
it's a pigeon sitting on top of a church .	這是一隻鴿子坐在教堂的上方 。
goes off during the day and does normal pigeon stuff . comes back , the whole place is covered with scaffolding and green netting and there's no way this pigeon can get home .	白天時 , 做正常的鴿子 , 回來 , 整個地方充滿了支架和綠色的網絡 , 這隻鴿子不可能回家了 。
so it's a homeless pigeon now and it's going to have to find another place to live , and that allows me to go through my catalog of favorite things , and we start with the tall ones and so on .	它現在是無家可歸的鴿子 , 它必須找到另一個居住的地方 , 這樣我才能穿越我最喜歡的目錄 , 我們就從高處開始 。
maybe it has to go back and live with family members ; that's not always a good thing , but it does sort of bring pigeons together again .	也許它必須回到家裡和家人住在一起 , 那不一定是件好事 , 但它會再次把鴿子帶回來 。
and i thought , that's sort of interesting , but maybe there's a person who should be involved in this in some way .	我心想 , 這有點有趣 , 但也許有個人應該以某種方式參與其中 。
so i kind of came up with this old guy who spends his life looking after sick pigeons .	所以我想出了一個老人 , 他一生都在照顧生病的鴿子 。
he'll go anywhere to get them dangerous places and whatnot and they become really friends with this guy , and learn to do tricks for him and entertain him at lunchtime and stuff like that .	他會到哪裡去找他們危險的地方 , 他們會變成和這傢伙真正的朋友 , 學著為他做技倆 , 在午餐時間和其他地方娛樂他 。
there's a real bond that develops between this old man and these pigeons .	在這個老人和鴿子之間 , 有一個真正的聯繫 。
but unfortunately he gets sick . he gets really sick at the end of the story .	但不幸的是 , 他生病了 。 他在故事結束時真的生病了 。
he's taught them to spell his name , which is aldo .	他被教導要拼他的名字 , 艾爾多 。

so anyway , i went through . . . and again , if packaging doesn't work and if the stories aren't going anywhere , i just come up with titles and hope that a title will sort of kick me off in the right direction .	總之 , 我經歷了一次 , 如果包裝不成功 , 如果故事不在任何地方 , 我只是想出一個標題 , 希望一個標題能讓我走向正確的方向 。
and sometimes it does focus me enough and i'll even do a title page .	有時它會讓我專注 , 我甚至會做一個標題 。
so , these are all title pages that eventually led me to the solution i settled on , which is the story of a young woman who sends a message on a homing pigeon she lives outside the walls of the city of rome to someone in the city .	所以 , 這些都是標題 , 最終引領我到我定居的解決方案 , 就是一個年輕女子的故事 , 她在羅馬城外面的一面牆上傳訊息給城市中的某個人 。

past the pyramid of cestius these will seem very familiar to you , even if you haven't been to rome recently past the gatehouse .	經過cestius的金字塔 , 這些金字塔對你來說是很熟悉的 , 即使你最近還沒去過羅馬 。

so , we circle around the coliseum , past the church of santa maria in cosmedin and the temple of hercules towards the river .	所以 , 我們繞過哥倫比山 , 穿越了聖母堂 , 穿越了哥薩米德州的聖殿 , 以及海克斯的神殿朝著河流前進 。

the only rule of perspective that i think matters is if it looks believable , you've succeeded .	我認為唯一重要的規則是它看起來是可信的 , 你成功了 。

and if you do want to see santa maria della pace , these books are really flexible , incredibly interactive just turn it around and look at it the other way .	如果你真的想看聖誕老人瑪麗亞•德拉的步調 , 這些書很有彈性 , 非常互動 , 只要把它轉過來 , 再看看另一種方式 。
through the alley , we can see the impact is captured in the red line .	透過巷子 , 我們可以看到紅線的影響 。
and then bird manages to pull itself together past this medieval tower one of the few remaining medieval towers towards the church of sant'agnese and around the dome looking down into piazza navona which we've already mentioned and seen and flown over a couple of times ; there's the bernini statue of the four rivers and then past the wonderful borromini sant'ivo , stopping just long enough on the 26foot diameter oculus of the pantheon to catch our breath .	接著 , 鳥類會自行拉過去這個中世紀塔 , 只有少數幾個中世紀的中世紀塔 , 朝聖城教堂前進 , 四個圓頂向下看 , 我們已經看過和流過幾次 ; 伯尼•史托爾特是四條河的聖母大樓 , 經過了這四條河的美妙無邊緣 , 停止了26英呎直徑的萬物直徑來抓住我們的呼吸 。
and then we can swoop inside and around ; and because we're flying , we don't really have to worry about gravity at this particular moment in time , so this drawing can be oriented in any way on the page .	然後我們可以在裡面四處轉動 , 因為我們在飛行 , 我們不用擔心重力在這個時刻 , 不用擔心重力 , 所以這幅圖可以在頁面上隨時隨地移動 。
we get a little exuberant as we pass gesu ; it's not surprising to sort of mimic the architecture in this way .	在我們通過gesu時 , 我們變得有點自豪 ; 不是很讓人驚訝的 , 以這種方式模仿建築 。
past the wonderful wall filled with the juxtaposition that i was talking about ; beautiful carvings set into the walls above the neon " ristorante " sign , and so on .	過去 , 充滿了我所說的美麗的牆壁 , 美麗的雕刻在新生 「 崛起 」 的牆上 , 諸如此類 。

as we look at the drawing board , we see what he's working on is , in fact , a map of the journey that the pigeon has just taken , and the red line extends through all the sights .	看看這幅畫板 , 我們看到他正在做的事 , 事實上 , 這趟鴿子剛拍的旅程地圖 , 紅線穿越了所有的視線 。
and if you want the information , so that we complete this cycle of understanding , all you have to do is read these paragraphs .	如果你想要資訊 , 這樣我們才能完成理解的循環 , 你只需要閱讀這些段落 。

mit researcher skylar tibbits works on selfassembly the idea that instead of building something , we can create materials that build themselves , much the way a strand of dna zips itself together . it's a big concept at early stages ; tibbits shows us three inthelab projects that hint at what a selfassembling future might look like .	麻省理工學院的研究者skylartibbit是自我組裝的概念 , 我們能創造出自身建構的材料 , 大多是dna短片本身的大概念 。 這是個早期的階段 ; tibbit向我們展示了三項以往自我組裝的計畫 。
skylar tibbits: can we make things that make themselves ?	skylartibbit:我們能製造製造自己的東西嗎 ?
today i'd like to show you the future of the way we make things .	今天 , 我想向大家展示我們製造東西的未來 。
i believe that soon our buildings and machines will be selfassembling , replicating and repairing themselves .	我相信很快我們的建築和機器會自我組裝、複製、修復自己 。
so i'm going to show you what i believe is the current state of manufacturing , and then compare that to some natural systems .	所以我要向你們展示我相信目前的製造業狀態 , 然後將它和一些自然系統做比較 。
so in the current state of manufacturing , we have skyscrapers two and a half years [of assembly time] , 500 , 000 to a million parts , fairly complex , new , exciting technologies in steel , concrete , glass .	在目前的製造業狀態 , 我們有摩天大樓 , 兩年半的時間 , 五十萬到一百萬個零件 , 相當複雜、令人興奮的新技術 , 在鋼鐵、混凝土、玻璃 。
we have exciting machines that can take us into space five years [of assembly time] , 2 . 5 million parts .	我們有令人興奮的機器可以帶我們進入太空五年 , 組裝時間有250萬個部分 。
but on the other side , if you look at the natural systems , we have proteins that have two million types , can fold in 10 , 000 nanoseconds , or dna with three billion base pairs we can replicate in roughly an hour .	但另一方面 , 如果你看一下自然系統 , 我們有兩百萬種類型的蛋白質 , 可以在一萬奈秒摺疊 , 或是dna有三十億個鹼基對 , 我們可以在大約一小時內複製 。
so there's all of this complexity in our natural systems , but they're extremely efficient , far more efficient than anything we can build , far more complex than anything we can build .	所以 , 我們自然系統的複雜性 , 但它們是非常有效率的 , 比任何我們能建造的東西還要有效率 , 遠遠比任何我們能建造的東西都還要複雜 。
they're far more efficient in terms of energy .	在能源方面 , 它們的效率更高 。
they hardly ever make mistakes .	他們幾乎無法犯錯 。
and they can repair themselves for longevity .	牠們可以長壽地修復自己 。
so there's something super interesting about natural systems .	所以 , 關於自然系統的超級有趣 。
and if we can translate that into our built environment , then there's some exciting potential for the way that we build things .	如果我們可以將它翻譯成我們的建設環境 , 那麼 , 對於我們建造東西的方式有一些令人興奮的潛力 。
and i think the key to that is selfassembly .	我認為關鍵在於自我組裝 。
so if we want to utilize selfassembly in our physical environment , i think there's four key factors .	所以 , 如果我們想在我們的物理環境中自組裝 , 我想有四個關鍵因子 。
the first is that we need to decode all of the complexity of what we want to build so our buildings and machines .	第一 , 我們需要解碼所有我們想建造的東西的複雜性 , 以便我們的建築和機器 。
and we need to decode that into simple sequences basically the dna of how our buildings work .	我們需要將它解碼成簡單的序列 , 基本上就是我們的建築物如何運作的dna 。
then we need programmable parts that can take that sequence and use that to fold up , or reconfigure .	接著 , 我們需要可編程的零件 , 可以用它來摺疊 , 或重組 。
we need some energy that's going to allow that to activate , allow our parts to be able to fold up from the program .	我們需要一些能量來啟動 , 使我們的零件能夠從程式中摺出來 。
and we need some type of error correction redundancy to guarantee that we have successfully built what we want .	我們需要某種類型的錯誤修正 , 來確保我們成功的建立我們想要的 。
so i'm going to show you a number of projects that my colleagues and i at mit are working on to achieve this selfassembling future .	所以我要給你們看幾個項目 , 我和麻省理工學院的同事正在努力實現這個自我組裝的未來 。
the first two are the macrobot and decibot .	第一個是麥克羅機器人和decibot 。
so these projects are largescale reconfigurable robots 8 ft . , 12 ft . long proteins .	這些計畫是大規模的可重組的機器人 , 8英尺 , 12英尺長的蛋白質 。
they're embedded with mechanical electrical devices , sensors .	它們嵌入了機械電子設備、感應器 。
you decode what you want to fold up into , into a sequence of angles so negative 120 , negative 120 , 0 , 0 , 120 , negative 120 something like that ; so a sequence of angles , or turns , and you send that sequence through the string .	解碼你想要摺疊成一連串的角度 , 負120 , 負120 , 0 , 120 , 120 , 負120 , 負120 , 類似這樣的東西 。 所以一連串的角度 , 就會透過弦 , 將這個序列發送出 。
each unit takes its message so negative 120 it rotates to that , checks if it got there and then passes it to its neighbor .	每單位單位都用它的信息為120它旋轉 , 檢查是否到那裡 , 然後傳給鄰居 。
so these are the brilliant scientists , engineers , designers that worked on this project .	這些是傑出的科學家、工程師、設計師在這個專案上工作 。
and i think it really brings to light: is this really scalable ?	我認為它真的能帶來光明嗎 ?
i mean , thousands of dollars , lots of man hours made to make this eightfoot robot .	我的意思是 , 數千美金 , 許多人小時製造了這個八英尺的機器人 。
can we really scale this up ? can we really embed robotics into every part ?	我們真的能把這個規模擴大嗎 ? 我們真的能把機械人的每一個部分嵌入其中嗎 ?
the next one questions that and looks at passive nature , or passively trying to have reconfiguration programmability .	下一個問題是 「 被動 」 , 或 「 被動地試圖有重組程式性 」 。
but it goes a step further , and it tries to have actual computation .	但它進一步進一步 , 試圖進行實際的計算 。
it basically embeds the most fundamental building block of computing , the digital logic gate , directly into your parts .	它基本上嵌入了計算最基本的基礎 , 數位邏輯門 , 直接進入你的零件中 。
so this is a nand gate .	這是一個nand大門 。
you have one tetrahedron which is the gate that's going to do your computing , and you have two input tetrahedrons .	有一個四面體 , 就是這個門 , 它會做你的電腦運算 , 你有兩個輸入的四面體 。
one of them is the input from the user , as you're building your bricks .	其中一個是來自使用者的輸入 , 因為你正在建造你的磚塊 。
the other one is from the previous brick that was placed .	另外一個是從先前被放置的磚塊 。
and then it gives you an output in 3d space .	然後它會給你一個3d空間的輸出 。
so what this means is that the user can start plugging in what they want the bricks to do .	這意味著 , 使用者可以開始加入他們想要的磚塊 。
it computes on what it was doing before and what you said you wanted it to do .	它計算它之前的做法 , 和你說你想要它做什麼 。
and now it starts moving in threedimensional space so up or down .	現在它開始在三維空間中移動 , 或向下移動 。
so on the lefthand side , [1 , 1] input equals 0 output , which goes down .	在左手邊 , [1、1]輸入等於0輸出 , 結果會下降 。
on the righthand side , [0 , 0] input is a 1 output , which goes up .	在右手邊 , 0 , 輸入是1輸出 , 上升 。
and so what that really means is that our structures now contain the blueprints of what we want to build .	這意味著我們的結構現在包含了我們想建造的東西的藍圖 。
so they have all of the information embedded in them of what was constructed .	所以他們有所有的信息嵌入其中 , 內容是建構出來的 。
so that means that we can have some form of selfreplication .	這意味著我們可以有某種形式的自我複製 。
in this case i call it selfguided replication , because your structure contains the exact blueprints .	在這個案例中 , 我稱它為自動複製 , 因為你的結構包含了精確的藍圖 。
if you have errors , you can replace a part .	如果你有錯誤 , 你可以取代一個部分 。
all the local information is embedded to tell you how to fix it .	所有當地的資訊都被嵌入 , 告訴你如何修復它 。
so you could have something that climbs along and reads it and can output at one to one .	所以你可以有一些可以爬上去讀的東西 , 可以輸出一個到一個 。
it's directly embedded ; there's no external instructions .	它是直接嵌入的 ; 沒有外部的指示 。
so the last project i'll show is called biased chains , and it's probably the most exciting example that we have right now of passive selfassembly systems .	最後一個專案叫做 「 偏見鏈 」 , 它可能是目前最令人興奮的例子 , 我們現在有被動的自組裝系統 。
so it takes the reconfigurability and programmability and makes it a completely passive system .	所以它需要可重組和可程式性 , 讓它成為一個完全被動的系統 。
so basically you have a chain of elements .	基本上你有一連串的元素 。
each element is completely identical , and they're biased .	每個元素都是完全相同的 , 且它們有偏見 。
so each chain , or each element , wants to turn right or left .	每一個鏈 , 或每一個元素 , 都想要轉向右或左轉 。
so as you assemble the chain , you're basically programming it .	所以 , 當你組裝鏈時 , 你基本上是在編寫它 。
you're telling each unit if it should turn right or left .	你要告訴每個單位是否應該左轉或左轉 。
so when you shake the chain , it then folds up into any configuration that you've programmed in so in this case , a spiral , or in this case , two cubes next to each other .	所以 , 當你搖動鏈 , 就會摺疊成任何你編寫的裝置 , 在這個案例中 , 螺旋 , 或在這個案例中 , 兩個立方體 。
so you can basically program any threedimensional shape or onedimensional , twodimensional up into this chain completely passively .	基本上 , 你可以設計任何三維形狀或單元 , 二維 , 完全被動地進入這個鏈中 。
so what does this tell us about the future ?	所以 , 這告訴我們未來是什麼 ?
i think that it's telling us that there's new possibilities for selfassembly , replication , repair in our physical structures , our buildings , machines .	我認為它告訴我們 , 自我組裝、複製、修復我們的實體結構、建築物、機器 。
there's new programmability in these parts .	這些部分有新的可程式性 。
and from that you have new possibilities for computing .	由此你有新的可能性可以用來計算 。
we'll have spatial computing .	我們將會有空間的運算 。
imagine if our buildings , our bridges , machines , all of our bricks could actually compute .	想像一下 , 如果我們的建築物、橋樑、機器 , 我們所有的磚塊都能計算出來 。
that's amazing parallel and distributed computing power , new design possibilities .	那是很了不起的平行和分散式的運算能力 , 新的設計可能性 。
so it's exciting potential for this .	所以這很讓人興奮 。
so i think these projects i've showed here are just a tiny step towards this future , if we implement these new technologies for a new selfassembling world .	所以我認為我在這裡展示的這些專案只是對於未來的一個小步驟 , 如果我們將這些新技術實現一個新的自我組裝的世界 。
