we've been to the moon , we've mapped the continents , we've even been to the deepest point in the ocean twice . what's left for the next generation to explore ? biologist and explorer nathan wolfe suggests this answer: almost everything . and we can start , he says , with the world of the unseeably small .	我們去過月球 , 我們繪製了大陸 , 我們也去過海洋中最深的一點 。 下一代要探究的是什麼 ? 生物學家和探險家納森•沃爾夫夫夫夫夫夫斯提出這個答案:幾乎每樣東西 。 然後我們開始 , 他可以說 , 帶著一個極小的世界 。
biodiversity , exploration , microbiology , science	生物多樣性、探索、微生物學、科學、科學、科學、科學 。
nathan wolfe: what's left to explore ?	nathanwolfe:還有什麼可以探索的 ?
recently i visited beloit , wisconsin .	最近我拜訪了威斯康辛州的貝洛特 。
and i was there to honor a great 20th century explorer , roy chapman andrews .	我在那裡榮耀一位偉大的20世紀探險家羅伊•查普曼•安德魯斯 。
during his time at the american museum of natural history , andrews led a range of expeditions to uncharted regions , like here in the gobi desert .	在他美國自然歷史博物館的時期 , 安德魯斯帶領一系列的探險領域 , 來揭開未知的區域 , 例如戈壁沙漠 。
he was quite a figure .	他算是個數字 。
he was later , it's said , the basis of the indiana jones character .	他後來被說是印第安納瓊斯角色的基礎 。
and when i was in beloit , wisconsin , i gave a public lecture to a group of middle school students .	當我在威斯康辛州 , 我向一群中學學生公開演講 。
and i'm here to tell you , if there's anything more intimidating than talking here at ted , it'll be trying to hold the attention of a group of a thousand 12yearolds for a 45minute lecture .	我來這裡是要告訴各位 , 如果在ted演講中比在ted這裡更嚇人 , 它會試著把一千二百二百二十五分鐘的小朋友的注意力集中在45分鐘的講座上 。
at the end of the lecture they asked a number of questions , but there was one that's really stuck with me since then .	演講結束後 , 他們問了幾個問題 , 但從那時起 , 有一個真的困擾著我 。
there was a young girl who stood up , and she asked the question: " where should we explore ? "	有一個年輕女孩站起來 , 她問了一個問題: 「 我們該在哪裡探索 ? 」
i think there's a sense that many of us have that the great age of exploration on earth is over , that for the next generation they're going to have to go to outer space or the deepest oceans in order to find something significant to explore .	我想大家都有一種感覺 , 地球上偉大的探索時代已經結束了 , 對下一代而言 , 他們必須要去外太空或深海 , 才能找到重要的探索 。
but is that really the case ?	但這是真的嗎 ?
is there really nowhere significant for us to explore left here on earth ?	地球上究竟沒有什麼值得我們探索的嗎 ?
it sort of made me think back to one of my favorite explorers in the history of biology .	這讓我回想起生物史上最喜歡的探險家之一 。
this is an explorer of the unseen world , martinus beijerinck .	這是一位探險家 , 馬丁•貝西尼克 。
so beijerinck set out to discover the cause of tobacco mosaic disease .	所以 , beijerinck開始發現菸草病的原因 。
what he did is he took the infected juice from tobacco plants and he would filter it through smaller and smaller filters .	他所做的是從菸草植物中感染到的汁液 , 他會用較小、較小的過濾器過濾它 。
and he reached the point where he felt that there must be something out there that was smaller than the smallest forms of life that were ever known bacteria , at the time .	他到了那個時點 , 他覺得一定有某種比當時所知最小的細菌更小的東西 。
he came up with a name for his mystery agent .	他想出了他的神秘經紀人的名字 。
he called it the virus latin for " poison . "	他稱之為 「 毒藥 」 病毒 。
and in uncovering viruses , beijerinck really opened this entirely new world for us .	在揭露病毒的過程中 , beijerinck為我們打開了整個新世界 。
we now know that viruses make up the majority of the genetic information on our planet , more than the genetic information of all other forms of life combined .	我們現在知道病毒是由地球上大部分的基因信息組成的 , 遠超過所有其他形式的生命組合 。
and obviously there's been tremendous practical applications associated with this world things like the eradication of smallpox , the advent of a vaccine against cervical cancer , which we now know is mostly caused by human papillomavirus .	很明顯地 , 和這個世界有著巨大的實際應用 , 像是天花的消滅 , 這種疫苗在對抗子宮頸癌 , 我們現在知道 , 主要是由人類乳癌所造成的 。
and beijerinck's discovery , this was not something that occurred 500 years ago .	而beijerinck的發現 , 這不是500年前發生的事 。
it was a little over 100 years ago that beijerinck discovered viruses .	大約一百多年前 , beijerinck發現了病毒 。
so basically we had automobiles , but we were unaware of the forms of life that make up most of the genetic information on our planet .	基本上 , 我們有了汽車 , 但我們不知道地球上大部分的基因資訊的形式 。
we now have these amazing tools to allow us to explore the unseen world things like deep sequencing , which allow us to do much more than just skim the surface and look at individual genomes from a particular species , but to look at entire metagenomes , the communities of teeming microorganisms in , on and around us and to document all of the genetic information in these species .	我們現在有了這些驚人的工具 , 讓我們可以探索未知的世界 , 像是深度定序 , 讓我們能做的不只是滑雪表面 , 還可以從特定物種身上看個別的基因組 , 而是去看整個金屬群體 , 群體在我們周圍的微生物群落 , 以及記錄所有這些物種的基因信息 。
we can apply these techniques to things from soil to skin and everything in between .	我們可以將這些技術應用到從土壤到皮膚的所有東西上 。
in my organization we now do this on a regular basis to identify the causes of outbreaks that are unclear exactly what causes them .	在我的組織中 , 我們定期做這件事 , 來找出疾病爆發的成因 , 不清楚會造成什麼原因 。
and just to give you a sense of how this works , imagine that we took a nasal swab from every single one of you .	為了讓各位了解這如何運作 , 想像一下 , 我們從你們每一個人身上取得了nasal的腫脹 。
and this is something we commonly do to look for respiratory viruses like influenza .	這是我們常做的事 , 用來尋找呼吸道的病毒 , 如流感病毒 。
the first thing we would see is a tremendous amount of genetic information .	首先 , 我們會看到的是大量的基因信息 。
and if we started looking into that genetic information , we'd see a number of usual suspects out there of course , a lot of human genetic information , but also bacterial and viral information , mostly from things that are completely harmless within your nose .	如果我們開始研究這些基因信息 , 當然 , 我們會發現許多人的基因信息 , 還有細菌和病毒資訊 , 大多來自鼻子中完全無害的事物 。
but we'd also see something very , very surprising .	但我們也看到了非常非常令人驚訝的現象 。
as we started to look at this information , we would see that about 20 percent of the genetic information in your nose doesn't match anything that we've ever seen before no plant , animal , fungus , virus or bacteria .	當我們開始研究這些資訊時 , 我們會發現 , 在你的鼻子裡大約有20%的基因信息並不符合我們以前從未見過的植物、動物、真菌、病毒或細菌 。
basically we have no clue what this is .	基本上 , 我們根本不知道這是什麼 。
and for the small group of us who actually study this kind of data , a few of us have actually begun to call this information biological dark matter .	對於研究這種數據的小組 , 我們當中有一些人開始稱之為 「 生物暗物質 」 。
we know it's not anything that we've seen before ; it's sort of the equivalent of an uncharted continent right within our own genetic information .	我們知道這不是我們以前看過的東西 , 而是類似我們基因信息中未知的大陸 。
and there's a lot of it .	還有很多 。
if you think 20 percent of genetic information in your nose is a lot of biological dark matter , if we looked at your gut , up to 40 or 50 percent of that information is biological dark matter .	如果你認為你鼻子裡百分之二十的基因信息是許多生物暗物質 , 如果我們觀察你的腸子 , 大約百分之四十或五十的信息是生物暗物質 。
and even in the relatively sterile blood , around one to two percent of this information is dark matter can't be classified , can't be typed or matched with anything we've seen before .	即使在相對的無菌血液中 , 大約有1%到2%是暗物質無法被分類 , 無法和我們以前見過的任何東西做配對 。
at first we thought that perhaps this was artifact .	一開始 , 我們認為這可能是人工藝品 。
these deep sequencing tools are relatively new .	這些深度定序的工具相對比較新 。
but as they become more and more accurate , we've determined that this information is a form of life , or at least some of it is a form of life .	但隨著他們變得越來越準確 , 我們已經決定這資訊是生命的一種形式 , 或至少其中一些是生命的形式 。
and while the hypotheses for explaining the existence of biological dark matter are really only in their infancy , there's a very , very exciting possibility that exists: that buried in this life , in this genetic information , are signatures of as of yet unidentified life .	雖然解釋生物暗物質存在的假設只是在嬰兒期間 , 有一個非常非常令人興奮的可能性存在於這個生命中 , 被埋在這個基因信息中 , 代表著尚未明確的生命特徵 。
that as we explore these strings of a's , t's , c's and g's , we may uncover a completely new class of life that , like beijerinck , will fundamentally change the way that we think about the nature of biology .	當我們探索a、t、c、g的弦時 , 我們可能會發現一個全新的生物類型 , 例如beijerinck , 會徹底改變我們對生物的本質的看法 。
that perhaps will allow us to identify the cause of a cancer that afflicts us or identify the source of an outbreak that we aren't familiar with or perhaps create a new tool in molecular biology .	也許這會讓我們辨識出一種癌症的原因 , 或辨識出我們不熟悉的疫情來源 , 或創造分子生物學的新工具 。
i'm pleased to announce that , along with colleagues at stanford and caltech and ucsf , we're currently starting an initiative to explore biological dark matter for the existence of new forms of life .	我很高興地宣佈 , 和史丹佛、加州理工學院、加州理工學院的同事 , 我們目前正開始著手探索生物暗物質 , 來探索新的生命形式的存在 。
a little over a hundred years ago , people were unaware of viruses , the forms of life that make up most of the genetic information on our planet .	大約一百多年前 , 人們對病毒一無所知 , 生命形式創造了地球上大部分的遺傳信息 。
a hundred years from now , people may marvel that we were perhaps completely unaware of a new class of life that literally was right under our noses .	一百年後 , 人們可能會驚嘆我們可能完全沒有意識到一種新的生命類型 , 真的就在我們的鼻子底下 。
it's true , we may have charted all the continents on the planet and we may have discovered all the mammals that are out there , but that doesn't mean that there's nothing left to explore on earth .	這是真的 , 我們可能已經查過地球上所有的大陸 , 我們可能已經發現外面所有哺乳類的哺乳類 , 但這並不表示地球上沒有任何東西可以探索 。
beijerinck and his kind provide an important lesson for the next generation of explorers people like that young girl from beloit , wisconsin .	beijerinck和他的同事為下一代的探險家提供了一堂重要的教訓 , 像是那位來自威斯康辛的年輕女孩 。
and i think if we phrase that lesson , it's something like this: don't assume that what we currently think is out there is the full story .	我想如果我們說出了這一課 , 就有點像這樣:不要假設我們現在所認為的完全是全面的故事 。
go after the dark matter in whatever field you choose to explore .	在你選擇探索的領域中 , 去追尋暗物質 。
there are unknowns all around us and they're just waiting to be discovered .	我們身邊無所知 , 他們只是等待被發現 。
legendary scientist david deutsch puts theoretical physics on the back burner to discuss a more urgent matter: the survival of our species . the first step toward solving global warming , he says , is to admit that we have a problem .	傳奇科學家daviddeutsch把理論物理放在後面的漢堡 , 討論一個更迫切的問題:我們物種的存活率 。 他說 , 要承認我們有問題 。
climate change , cosmos , culture , environment , global issues , physics , science , technology , universe	氣候變遷、宇宙、文化、環境、全球議題、物理、科學、科技、宇宙、宇宙、科學、科學、科技、科技、宇宙等等 。
david deutsch on our place in the cosmos	大衛•德歇斯基於宇宙中的位置 。
we've been told to go out on a limb and say something surprising .	我們被告知要走上肢體 , 說出令人驚訝的事情 。
so i'll try and do that , but i want to start with two things that everyone already knows .	我來試試看 , 但我想要從大家已經知道的兩件事開始 。
and the first one , in fact , is something that has been known for most of recorded history .	事實上 , 首先 , 已經是歷史上大部分的歷史所知的 。
and that is that the planet earth , or the solar system , or our environment or whatever , is uniquely suited to sustain our evolution or creation , as it used to be thought and our present existence , and most important , our future survival .	那就是地球 , 或太陽系 , 或我們的環境 , 或其它 , 都適用於維持我們的演化或創意 , 以前 , 思想和現存 , 最重要的是 , 我們未來的生存 。
nowadays this idea has a dramatic name: spaceship earth .	今日這個想法有個很戲劇性的名字:太空船地球 。
and the idea there is that outside the spaceship , the universe is implacably hostile , and inside is all we have , all we depend on .	這個想法是 , 在太空船之外 , 宇宙是不可置信的 , 而內部是我們所擁有的 , 我們只需要仰賴的 。
and we only get the one chance: if we mess up our spaceship , we've got nowhere else to go .	我們只有一個機會:如果我們搞砸了我們的太空船 , 我們就沒有其他地方可以去 。
now , the second thing that everyone already knows is that contrary to what was believed for most of human history , human beings are not , in fact , the hub of existence .	第二件事 , 大家已經知道的是 , 對大部分人類歷史所相信的相反 , 人類其實不是存在的中心 。
as stephen hawking famously said , we're just a chemical scum on the surface of a typical planet that's in orbit around a typical star , which is on the outskirts of a typical galaxy , and so on .	正如史蒂芬•霍金所說 , 我們只是一個典型的星球表面 , 在一個典型的恆星周圍繞繞著一個典型的星球 , 在一個典型的銀河系的外部 , 諸如此類 。
now the first of those two things that everyone knows is kind of saying that we're at a very untypical place , uniquely suited and so on , and the second one is saying that we're at a typical place .	大家都知道的兩件事的第一件事 , 是我們處在一個非常不尋常的地方 , 獨特的服裝等等 , 第二個是說我們在一個典型的地方 。
and especially if you regard these two as deep truths to live by and to inform your life decisions , then they seem a little bit to conflict with each other .	尤其是如果你把這兩種真相視為深刻的真相 , 告訴你的人生決策 , 那麼它們似乎有點衝突 。
but that doesn't prevent them from both being completely false .	但這並不會阻止他們完全錯誤 。
and they are . so let me start with the second one: typical . well is this a typical place ? well , let's look around , you know , and look in a random direction , and we see a wall , and chemical scum and that's not typical of the universe at all .	它們是的 。 所以 , 讓我從第二個例子開始吧 。 嗯 , 這是典型的地方嗎 ? 讓我們看看四周看看四周 , 看看一個隨機的方向 , 我們看到一面牆 , 化學的雕塑 , 完全不是宇宙的典型 。
all you've got to do is go a few hundred miles in that same direction and look back , and you won't see any walls or chemical scum at all all you see is a blue planet . and if you go further than that , you'll see the sun , the solar system , and the stars and so on .	你所要做的就是走幾百英里 , 回頭看 , 你看不到任何牆或化學雕像 , 你所看到的都是藍色的星球 。 如果你走得更遠 , 你會看到太陽 , 太陽系 , 恆星等等 。
but that's still not typical of the universe , because stars come in galaxies .	但這仍然不是典型的宇宙 , 因為恆星在星系中出現 。
and most places in the universe , a typical place in the universe , is nowhere near any galaxies .	宇宙中的大部分地方 , 宇宙中典型的地方 , 幾乎沒有任何銀河系 。
so let's go out further , till we're outside the galaxy , and look back , and yeah , there's the huge galaxy with spiral arms laid out in front of us .	所以 , 讓我們再向外走 , 直到我們走出星系 , 回頭看 , 是的 , 有一個巨大的星系 , 在我們面前有螺旋臂 。
and at this point we've come 100 , 000 light years from here .	在這個時點 , 我們已經有十萬光年了 。
but we're still nowhere near a typical place in the universe .	但是我們至今仍處於宇宙中典型的地方 。
to get to a typical place , you've got to go 1 , 000 times as far as that into intergalactic space .	為了達到典型的地點 , 你必須將一千倍的速度傳到星系間 。
and so what does that look like ? typical .	這看起來是什麼樣子 ? 典型 。
what does a typical place in the universe look like ?	宇宙中一個典型的位置是什麼樣子 ?
well , at enormous expense , ted has arranged a highresolution immersion virtual reality rendering of intergalactic space the view from intergalactic space .	嗯 , 在巨大的昂貴中 , ted已經安排了高解析度的虛擬實境 , 虛擬實境 , 來自星際空間的景象 。
so can we have the lights off , please , so we can see it ?	所以 , 請把燈關掉 , 請看 , 我們能看到嗎 ?
well , not quite , not quite perfect you see , in intergalactic space intergalactic space is completely dark , pitch dark .	嗯 , 不太完美 , 你可以看到 , 在星系間空間中間的空間是完全黑暗的 , 漆黑的 。
it's so dark that if you were to be looking at the nearest star to you , and that star were to explode as a supernova , and you were to be staring directly at it at the moment when its light reached you , you still wouldn't be able to see even a glimmer .	很黑暗 , 如果你在看最近的星星 , 那星星是以超新星爆炸的 , 而你在閃爍的那一刻 , 直到你眼睛時 , 你依然看不見星星 。
that's how big and how dark the universe is .	這就是宇宙有多大 , 有多黑暗 。
and that's despite the fact that a supernova is so bright , so brilliant an event , that it would kill you stone dead at a range of several light years .	儘管有一顆超新星如此明亮 , 所以很棒的一場活動 , 會讓你在幾光年內死去 。
and yet from intergalactic space , it's so far away you wouldn't even see it .	然而 , 從星系間的空間來看 , 它是如此遙遠 , 你甚至看不到它 。
it's also very cold out there less than three degrees above absolute zero .	在絕對零度之上 , 它也非常寒冷 。
and it's very empty . the vacuum there is one million times less dense than the highest vacuum that our best technology on earth can currently create . so that's how different a typical place is from this place .	而它是非常空的 。 真空的密度比地球上最高的真空還要低一百萬倍 , 目前我們最好的科技可以創造 。 所以 , 在這個地方 , 不同的地方是如此 。
and that is how untypical this place is .	這就是這個地方的典型 。
so can we have the lights back on please ? thank you .	所以 , 我們能把燈打回來嗎 ? 謝謝 。
now how do we know about an environment that's so far away , and so different , and so alien , from anything we're used to ?	現在我們如何知道一個距離如此遙遠的環境 , 又如此不同 , 外星人 , 從任何我們習以為常的環境中 ?
well , the earth our environment , in the form of us is creating knowledge .	嗯 , 地球我們的環境 , 以我們所創造的知識 。
well , what does that mean ? well , look out even further than we've just been i mean from here , with a telescope and you'll see things that look like stars .	嗯 , 這意味著什麼呢 ? 嗯 , 看看比我們剛剛看到的更遠--我是說 , 用望遠鏡 , 然後你會看到像恆星的東西 。
they're called " quasars . " quasars originally meant quasistellar object .	它們被稱為 「 夸拉 」 。 原本是 「 量子力物體 」 。
which means things that look a bit like stars . but they're not stars .	這意味著 , 看起來有點像恆星 , 但它們不是恆星 。
and we know what they are . billions of years ago , and billions of light years away , the material at the center of a galaxy collapsed towards a supermassive black hole .	我們知道它們是什麼 。 數十億年前 , 數十億光年之外 , 銀河系中間的物質落在一個超大質量的黑洞中 。
and then intense magnetic fields directed some of the energy of that gravitational collapse . and some of the matter , back out in the form of tremendous jets which illuminated lobes with the brilliance of i think it's a trillion suns .	接著 , 強烈的磁場引力倒塌了一些能量 。 其中的一些物質 , 回到了巨大的噴射流的形式 , 會照亮葉子的亮點 , 我認為它是一兆個太陽 。
now , the physics of the human brain could hardly be more unlike the physics of such a jet .	現在 , 人類大腦的物理學幾乎不像這種噴射流的物理 。
we couldn't survive for an instant in it . language breaks down when trying to describe what it would be like in one of those jets .	我們不能馬上存活下來 , 語言會在試圖描述在其中一個噴射機中會是什麼樣子的情況時 , 語言會瓦解 。
it would be a bit like experiencing a supernova explosion , but at pointblank range and for millions of years at a time .	這有點像經歷過超新星的爆炸 , 但在時空的範圍內 , 每次有數百萬年的時間 。
and yet , that jet happened in precisely such a way that billions of years later , on the other side of the universe , some bit of chemical scum could accurately describe , and model , and predict , and explain , above all there's your reference what was happening there , in reality .	然而 , 這種噴射機在數十億年後 , 在宇宙的另一端 , 一些化學污垢可以準確地描述 , 模型 , 預測和解釋 , 最重要的是你的參考事實 , 在現實中發生了什麼事 。
the one physical system , the brain , contains an accurate working model of the other the quasar .	一個實體系統 , 大腦 , 包含一個精確的工作模型 , 其它的 「 夸拉 」 。
not just a superficial image of it , though it contains that as well , but an explanatory model , embodying the same mathematical relationships and the same causal structure .	不僅僅是它的超級形象 , 還包含了它 , 而是一個解釋性的模型 , 體現了相同的數學關係以及因果關係結構 。
now that is knowledge . and if that weren't amazing enough , the faithfulness with which the one structure resembles the other is increasing with time . that is the growth of knowledge .	這是知識 。 如果這還不夠驚人 , 信心和哪個結構相似 , 其它的結構會隨著時間增長 。 這就是知識的增長 。
so , the laws of physics have this special property .	所以 , 物理定律有這種特殊的特性 。
that physical objects , as unlike each other as they could possibly be , can nevertheless embody the same mathematical and causal structure and to do it more and more so over time .	這種實體物體 , 和它們之間的可能性不同 , 不論是用相同的數學和因果結構 , 以及隨時間來做更多 。
so we are a chemical scum that is different . this chemical scum has universality .	所以我們是一個不一樣的化學螺絲 。 這個化學螺絲具有普遍性 。
its structure contains , with everincreasing precision , the structure of everything . this place , and not other places in the universe , is a hub which contains within itself the structural and causal essence of the whole of the rest of physical reality . and so , far from being insignificant , the fact that the laws of physics allow this , or even mandate that this can happen , is one of the most important things about the physical world .	它的結構含有著不斷的精確度 , 一切的結構 。 這個地方 , 而不是宇宙的其他地方 , 它是一個包含在整個物理現實的結構和因果的本質 。 所以 , 遠離被忽視的物理定律 , 事實上 , 物理的定律允許這個定律 , 甚至是強迫它發生 , 它是物理世界中最重要的事之一 。
now how does the solar system and our environment , in the form of us acquire this special relationship with the rest of the universe ?	那麼 , 太陽系和我們的環境是如何形成一個與宇宙其餘的特殊關係 ?
well , one thing that's true about stephen hawking's remark i mean , it is true , but it's the wrong emphasis . one thing that's true about it is that it doesn't do it with any special physics . there's no special dispensation , no miracles involved . it does it simply with three things that we have here in abundance .	嗯 , 史蒂芬•霍金的筆記 , 我是說 , 這是真的 , 但它是錯的強調 。 真正的重點是它並沒有用任何特殊的物理來做 。 沒有特殊的解剖 , 沒有奇蹟涉入 。 它只用三樣東西來做我們在這兒所擁有的豐富 。
one of them is matter , because the growth of knowledge is a form of information processing . information processing is computation , computation requires a computer there's no known way of making a computer without matter .	其中一個是很重要的 , 因為知識的增長是資訊處理的形式 。 資訊處理是計算 , 計算需要電腦 , 沒有任何東西可以製造電腦 。
we also need energy to make the computer , and most important , to make the media in effect onto which we record the knowledge that we discover .	我們也需要能量來製造電腦 , 最重要的是 , 讓媒體對我們所發現的知識有所影響 。
and then thirdly , less tangible , but just as essential for the openended creation of knowledge , of explanations , is evidence .	第三 , 不太具體 , 但對開放式的知識、解釋的創造而言 , 重要的是證據 。
now , our environment is inundated with evidence .	現在 , 我們的環境充滿了證據 。
we happen to get round to testing , let's say , newton's law of gravity about 300 years ago .	例如 , 牛頓的重力定律大約在300年前發生 。
but the evidence that we used to do that was falling down on every square meter of the earth for billions of years before that , and will continue to fall on for billions of years afterwards . and the same is true for all the other sciences .	但是我們過去數十億年前所做的證據顯示地球每一平方米落下 , 數十億年之後繼續下去 。 其它科學也是如此 。
as far as we know , evidence to discover the most fundamental truths of all the sciences is here just for the taking on our planet .	據我們所知 , 發現所有科學中最基本的真理 , 只是為了取代地球 。
our location is saturated with evidence , and also with matter and energy .	我們的位置充滿了證據 , 也充滿了物質和能量 。
out in intergalactic space , those three prerequisites for the openended creation of knowledge are at their lowest possible supply .	在星系間空間中 , 這三個創造開放式知識的前提是最低的供應 。
as i said , it's empty ; it's cold ; and it's dark out there . or is it ?	如我所說 , 它是空的 , 它很冷 , 外面是黑暗的 , 還是它 ?
now actually , that's just another parochial misconception .	實際上 , 這只是另一個關於偏見的誤解 。
because imagine a cube out there in intergalactic space , the same size as our home , the solar system . now that cube is very empty by human standards , but that still means that it contains over a million tons of matter .	因為想像一個在星系間的立方體 , 和我們的家一樣大 , 太陽系 。 現在這個立方體是非常空的 , 由人類標準所組成 , 但這仍然意味著它含有超過一百萬噸的物質 。
and a million tons is enough to make , say , a selfcontained space station , on which there's a colony of scientists that are devoted to creating an openended stream of knowledge , and so on .	一百萬噸足以製造出自足的太空站 , 其中有一群科學家致力於創造一個開放式的知識流 , 諸如此類 。
now , it's way beyond present technology to even gather the hydrogen from intergalactic space and form it into other elements and so on .	現在 , 它已經超越了現有的技術 , 把來自星系空間的氫收集起來 , 將氫變成其他元素等等 。
but the thing is , in a comprehensible universe , if something isn't forbidden by the laws of physics , then what could possibly prevent us from doing it , other than knowing how ?	但 , 重點是 , 在一個可理解的宇宙中 , 如果某個東西不被物理定律禁止 , 那麼 , 什麼能阻止我們去做 , 除了知道怎麼做 ?
in other words , it's a matter of knowledge , not resources .	換句話說 , 它是知識的問題 , 而非資源 。
and the same well , if we could do that we'd automatically have an energy supply , because the transmutation would be a fusion reactor and evidence ?	同樣的 , 如果我們能自動提供能源供應 , 因為交通運輸會是核融合反應器和證據嗎 ?
well , again , it's dark out there to human senses . but all you've got to do is take a telescope , even one of presentday design , look out and you'll see the same galaxies as we do from here .	嗯 , 再說一次 , 它對人類的感官很暗 。 但你要做的就是拿一個望遠鏡 , 甚至今天的設計 , 看看外面 , 你會看到相同的銀河系 。
and with a more powerful telescope , you'll be able to see stars , and planets .	有了更強大的望遠鏡 , 你就能看見恆星 , 行星 。
in those galaxies , you'll be able to do astrophysics , and learn the laws of physics .	在那些星系中 , 你可以做天體物理學 , 並學習物理定律 。
and locally there you could build particle accelerators , and learn elementary particle physics , and chemistry , and so on .	你可以在當地建立粒子加速器 , 學習基本粒子物理 , 化學等等 。
probably the hardest science to do would be biology field trips because it would take several hundred million years to get to the nearest lifebearing planet and back .	最難的科學可能是生物的實地旅行 , 因為它要花上幾億年才能到最近的地球回去 。
but i have to tell you and sorry , richard but i never did like biology field trips much , and i think we can just about make do with one every few hundred million years .	但是我必須告訴你們 , 理查 , 理查 , 但是我從來不太喜歡生物學領域 , 我想我們可以每幾億年就做一次 。
so in fact , intergalactic space does contain all the prerequisites for the openended creation of knowledge . any such cube , anywhere in the universe , could become the same kind of hub that we are , if the knowledge of how to do so were present there .	事實上 , 星系間空間確實包含了開放式的知識 。 任何這些立方體 , 在宇宙的任何地方 , 都可以成為我們一樣的樞紐 , 假如我們是如何在現場實現的知識 。
so we're not in a uniquely hospitable place .	所以 , 我們不是獨一無二的居住地 。
if intergalactic space is capable of creating an openended stream of explanations , then so is almost every other environment . so is the earth . so is a polluted earth .	如果星系間空間能夠創造出一個開放式的解釋 , 那麼幾乎所有其他的環境 。 這就是地球 。 這是個污染的地球 。
and the limiting factor , there and here , is not resources , because they're plentiful , but knowledge , which is scarce .	而限制因素 , 在這裡 , 沒有資源 , 因為它們很豐富 , 但知識 , 很稀少 。
now this cosmic knowledgebased view may and i think ought to make us feel very special . but it should also make us feel vulnerable , because it means that without the specific knowledge that's needed to survive the ongoing challenges of the universe , we won't survive them .	現在這個宇宙知識的觀點 , 或許我認為應該讓我們覺得很特別 , 但這也應該讓我們覺得脆弱 , 因為這意味著 , 若要讓宇宙持續的挑戰存活下來 , 我們就不會存活下來 。
all it takes is for a supernova to go off a few light years away , and we'll all be dead !	只需要一個超級新星才能在幾光年內離開 , 我們都死了 !
martin rees has recently written a book about our vulnerability to all sorts of things , from astrophysics , to scientific experiments gone wrong , and most importantly to terrorism with weapons of mass destruction .	馬丁•雷斯最近寫了一本關於我們對各種事物的脆弱的書 , 從天體物理學 , 到科學實驗都錯了 , 最重要的是用大規模毀滅性武器來恐怖主義 。
and he thinks that civilization has only a 50 percent chance of surviving this century .	他認為文明只有50%的機會在這個世紀存活下來 。
i think he's going to talk about that later in the conference .	我想他會在會議後談到這一點 。
now i don't think that probability is the right category to discuss this issue in .	我不認為機率是正確的分類來討論這個議題 。
but i do agree with him about this . we can survive , and we can fail to survive .	但我同意他這件事 , 我們可以生存下來 , 我們無法生存下來 。
but it depends not on chance , but on whether we create the relevant knowledge in time .	但它取決於機會 , 但不論我們是否在時間內建立相關的知識 。
the danger is not at all unprecedented . species go extinct all the time .	危險並不是史無前例的物種會隨時滅絕
civilizations end . the overwhelming majority of all species and all civilizations that have ever existed are now history .	文明終究會結束 , 絕大多數的物種和所有現存的文明都是歷史 。
and if we want to be the exception to that , then logically our only hope is to make use of the one feature that distinguishes our species , and our civilization , from all the others namely , our special relationship with the laws of physics , our ability to create new explanations , new knowledge to be a hub of existence .	如果我們想成為一個例外 , 那麼 , 我們唯一的希望就是利用一個特徵來區別我們的物種 , 而我們的文明 , 也就是說 , 我們與物理定律的特殊關係 , 我們創造新的解釋能力 , 新的知識成為存在的中心 。
so let me now apply this to a current controversy , not because i want to advocate any particular solution , but just to illustrate the kind of thing i mean .	所以 , 讓我把這個應用到目前的爭議中 , 不是因為我想要倡導任何特定的解決方案 , 只為了說明我的意思 。
and the controversy is global warming .	爭議是全球暖化 。
now , i'm a physicist , but i'm not the right kind of physicist . in regard to global warming , i'm just a layman . and the rational thing for a layman to do is to take seriously the prevailing scientific theory . and according to that theory , it's already too late to avoid a disaster .	現在 , 我是物理學家 , 但我不是那種對的物理學家 。 關於全球暖化 , 我只是一個懶人 。 理性的事情是要認真看待科學理論 。 根據這個理論 , 已經太晚了 , 避免一個災難 。
because if it's true that our best option at the moment is to prevent co2 emissions with something like the kyoto protocol , with its constraints on economic activity and its enormous cost of hundreds of billions of dollars or whatever it is , then that is already a disaster by any reasonable measure .	因為 , 如果我們現在最好的選項是要預防二氧化碳排放 , 例如京都議定書 , 對於經濟活動的限制 , 以及它數百億元或其它的成本 , 那就已經是個災難 。
and the actions that are advocated are not even purported to solve the problem , merely to postpone it by a little . so it's already too late to avoid it , and it probably has been too late to avoid it ever since before anyone realized the danger .	倡導的行動甚至沒有被驅逐去解決問題 , 只能稍微延後它 。 所以它已經太晚了 , 已經無法避免它了 , 自從任何人意識到危險之前就已經太晚了 。
it was probably already too late in the 1970s , when the best available scientific theory was telling us that industrial emissions were about to precipitate a new ice age in which billions would die .	在1970年代早就已經太晚了 , 當最好的科學理論告訴我們 , 工業排放將要在數十億人死亡時 。
now the lesson of that seems clear to me , and i don't know why it isn't informing public debate .	這教訓對我來說是很明顯的 , 我不知道為何它沒有公眾辯論 。
it is that we can't always know . when we know of an impending disaster , and how to solve it at a cost less than the cost of the disaster itself , then there's not going to be much argument , really .	是我們無法永遠知道的 。 當我們知道一個即將面臨的災難 , 以及如何用少於災難本身的成本 , 那麼就不會有太多的爭論 。
but no precautions , and no precautionary principle , can avoid problems that we do not yet foresee .	但沒有預防措施 , 也沒有預防的原則 , 可以避免我們還沒預料到的問題 。
hence , we need a stance of problemfixing , not just problemavoidance .	因此 , 我們需要解決問題的穩定 , 不只是重視問題 。
and it's true that an ounce of prevention equals a pound of cure , but that's only if we know what to prevent .	這是真的 , 一盎司的預防措施等同於一磅的治療方法 , 但這只是我們知道如何預防 。
if you've been punched on the nose , then the science of medicine does not consist of teaching you how to avoid punches .	如果你在鼻子上被打 , 那麼醫學的科學就不會教你如何避免打孔 。
if medical science stopped seeking cures and concentrated on prevention only , then it would achieve very little of either .	如果醫學停止尋求治療 , 並專注在預防上 , 那它也無法達成 。
the world is buzzing at the moment with plans to force reductions in gas emissions at all costs .	此時此刻 , 世界正在發動計畫 , 要讓氣體排放量降低所有成本 。
it ought to be buzzing with plans to reduce the temperature , and with plans to live at the higher temperature and not at all costs , but efficiently and cheaply . and some such plans exist , things like swarms of mirrors in space to deflect the sunlight away , and encouraging aquatic organisms to eat more carbon dioxide .	該計劃應該要讓溫度降低 , 計畫要在更高的溫度下生存 , 不需花費 , 而是有效率地、便宜 。 有些計畫存在 , 例如大量的鏡子 , 來將陽光轉移 , 並鼓勵水產量的有機體吃更多的二氧化碳 。
at the moment , these things are fringe research .	此時此刻 , 這些是邊緣研究 。
they're not central to the human effort to face this problem , or problems in general .	它們不是人類努力去解決這個問題的核心 , 也不是一般來說的問題 。
and with problems that we are not aware of yet , the ability to put right not the sheer good luck of avoiding indefinitely is our only hope , not just of solving problems , but of survival .	我們還沒察覺到的問題 , 要把正確的能力 , 不是無限中避免無限運氣的能力 , 是我們唯一的希望 , 不只是解決問題 , 而是生存 。
so take two stone tablets , and carve on them .	拿兩個石板板 , 刻在上面 。
on one of them , carve: " problems are soluble . "	其中一個是 " 問題是 "
and on the other one carve: " problems are inevitable . "	另一部曲子是: 「 問題是不可避免的 。 」
how can a struggling country break out of poverty if it's trapped in a system of bad rules ? economist paul romer unveils a bold idea: " charter cities , " cityscale administrative zones governed by a coalition of nations .	如果它被困在一個不好的規則制度中 , 一個掙扎的國家如何破壞貧窮 ? 經濟學家保羅默揭露了一個大膽想法: 「 特殊城市 」 、 「 城市管理區 , 由國家聯盟統治 。
business , culture , economics , global issues , politics	商業、文化、全球議題、政治議題、商業、經濟問題、經濟問題、
paul romer's radical idea: charter cities	保羅•羅姆的激進想法:特區城市 。
take a look at this picture .	看看這張照片 。
it poses a very fascinating puzzle for us .	它為我們帶來了一個令人著迷的謎題 。
these african students are doing their homework under streetlights at the airport in the capital city because they don't have any electricity at home .	這些非洲學生在首都機場的街燈下做功課 , 因為他們家裡沒有電力 。
now , i haven't met these particular students , but i've met students like them .	我還沒見過這些特別的學生 , 但我遇到了像他們一樣的學生 。
let's just pick one for example , the one in the green shirt .	咱們來挑一個例子 , 綠色襯衫裡的那個 。
let's give him a name , too: nelson .	我們也給他一個名字:nelson 。
i'll bet nelson has a cellphone .	我打賭nelson有手機 。
so here is the puzzle .	這是個謎題 。
why is it that nelson has access to a cuttingedge technology , like the cellphone , but doesn't have access to a 100yearold technology for generating electric light in the home ?	為什麼nelson能接觸到尖端科技 , 例如手機 , 卻無法取得一百歲的技術 , 供電給家裡的電燈 ?
now , in a word , the answer is " rules . "	換句話說 , 答案是 「 規則 」 。
bad rules can prevent the kind of winwin solution that's available when people can bring new technologies in and make them available to someone like nelson .	不好的規則可以預防這種雙贏的解決方案 , 當人們可以把新科技帶進去 , 讓它成為像nelson這樣的人 。
what kinds of rules ?	什麼樣的規則 ?
the electric company in this nation operates under a rule , which says that it has to sell electricity at a very low , subsidized price in fact , a price that is so low it loses money on every unit that it sells .	這個國家的電力公司在一個規則下運作 , 說它必須以非常低的補貼價格銷售出電力 , 事實上 , 價格低到每一單位都被賣掉 。
so it has neither the resources , nor the incentives , to hook up many other users .	所以它既不是資源 , 也不是激勵機制 , 也不是鼓勵許多其他使用者 。
the president wanted to change this rule .	總統想要改變這個規則 。
he's seen that it's possible to have a different set of rules , rules where businesses earn a small profit , so they have an incentive to sign up more customers .	他看過 , 有一套不同的規則 , 企業賺得很小的利潤 , 所以他們有動機去簽更多客戶 。
that's the kind of rules that the cellphone company that nelson purchases his telephony from operates under .	這種規則就是尼爾遜公司在運作下方購買了他的電話 。
the president has seen how those rules worked well .	總統看過這些規則如何順利運作 。
so he tried to change the rules for pricing on electricity , but ran into a firestorm of protest from businesses and consumers who wanted to preserve the existing subsidized rates .	所以他試著改變電價的規則 , 但他遇到了企業和消費者 , 他們想要保有現有的補助率 。
so he was stuck with rules that prevented him from letting the winwin solution help his country .	所以他陷入了規則 , 阻止他放下雙贏的解決方案來協助他的國家 。
and nelson is stuck studying under the streetlights .	nelson在街燈下研究的 。
the real challenge then , is to try to figure out how we can change rules .	真正的挑戰是試著找出我們能如何改變規則 。
are there some rules we can develop for changing rules ?	是否有一些規則可以改變規則 ?
i want to argue that there is a general abstract insight that we can make practical , which is that , if we can give more choices to people , and more choices to leaders who , in many countries , are also people .	我想爭辯的是 , 有一個普遍的抽象洞見 , 我們可以實用 , 那就是 , 如果我們能給人民更多選擇 , 在許多國家 , 對於領導者 , 也是人 。
but , it's useful to present the opposition between these two .	但 , 要展現這兩者之間的反對是有用的 。
because the kind of choice you might want to give to a leader , a choice like giving the president the choice to raise prices on electricity , takes away a choice that people in the economy want .	因為你可能想給領導者一個選擇 , 例如給總統一個選擇 , 提高電力的價格 , 消除人民在經濟中想要的選擇 。
they want the choice to be able to continue consuming subsidized electric power .	他們希望能選擇繼續消耗電力 。
so if you give just to one side or the other , you'll have tension or friction .	所以如果你給予一方或另一方 , 你會有張力或摩擦力 。
but if we can find ways to give more choices to both , that will give us a set of rules for changing rules that get us out of traps .	但如果我們能找到更多選擇的方式 , 就能給予我們一套改變規則的規則 , 來讓我們脫離陷阱 。
now , nelson also has access to the internet .	現在 , nelson也能上網 。
and he says that if you want to see the damaging effects of rules , the ways that rules can keep people in the dark , look at the pictures from nasa of the earth at night .	他說如果你想看到規則的損害 , 規則的威脅會讓人們在黑暗中留在黑暗中 , 看看美國太空總署的照片 。
in particular check out asia .	特別是在亞洲 。
if you zoom in here , you can see north korea , in outline here , which is like a black hole compared to its neighbors .	如果你放大這裡 , 你可以看到北韓 , 這裡的線上 , 和其鄰居相比 , 黑洞就像是黑洞 。
now , you won't be surprised to learn that the rules in north korea keep people there in the dark .	現在 , 你不會驚訝地知道北韓的規則會讓人們處在黑暗中 。
but it is important to recognize that north korea and south korea started out with identical sets of rules in both the sense of laws and regulations , but also in the deeper senses of understandings , norms , culture , values and beliefs .	但 , 重要的是要認出北韓和南韓的規則始於一模一樣的規則 , 無論是法律和規範 , 還是在更深層層的理解、規範、文化、價值、信念 。
when they separated , they made choices that led to very divergent paths for their sets of rules .	當他們分開時 , 他們做出選擇 , 導致他們一系列的規則非常明顯的路徑 。
so we can change we as humans can change the rules that we use to interact with each other , for better , or for worse .	所以 , 我們可以改變我們人類可以改變我們使用的規則 , 來和彼此互動 , 做得更好 , 或更糟 。
now let's look at another region , the caribbean .	現在我們來看看加勒比海另一個區域 。
zoom in on haiti , in outline here .	放大海地 , 這裡的線上 。
haiti is also dark , compared to its neighbor here , the dominican republic , which has about the same number of residents .	海地也是黑暗的 , 相較於其鄰居 , 多明尼加共和國 , 居民的數量是相同的 。
both of these countries are dark compared to puerto rico , which has half as many residents as either haiti or the dominican republic .	這兩個國家都和波多黎各相較 , 居民的數量有一半是海地或多明尼亞共和國 。
what haiti warns us is that rules can be bad because governments are weak .	海地提醒我們 , 規則可能會很糟 , 因為政府很弱 。
it's not just that the rules are bad because the government is too strong and oppressive , as in north korea .	不只是規則不好 , 因為政府太強壯、壓迫 , 和北韓一樣 。
so that if we want to create environments with good rules , we can't just tear down .	所以 , 如果我們想要用好的規則來創造環境 , 我們就不能把環境撕碎 。
we've got to find ways to build up , as well .	我們也必須找到方法來建構 。
now , china dramatically demonstrates both the potential and the challenges of working with rules .	中國戲劇性地展示了與規則的潛力和挑戰 。
back in the beginning of the data presented in this chart , china was the world's hightechnology leader .	回到這張圖表的一開始 , 中國是世界上高科技領袖 。
chinese had pioneered technologies like steel , printing , gunpowder .	中國的先驅技術如鋼鐵、列印、槍枝等 。
but the chinese never adopted , at least in that period , effective rules for encouraging the spread of those ideas a profit motive that could have encouraged the spread .	但中國從來沒有採用過 , 至少在那段期間 , 有效的規則是鼓勵這些點子的散播 , 能夠鼓勵傳播 。
and they soon adopted rules which slowed down innovation and cut china off from the rest of the world .	他們很快就採用了規則 , 讓創新慢下來 , 讓中國脫離世界其他地方 。
so as other countries in the world innovated , in the sense both of developing newer technologies , but also developing newer rules , the chinese were cut off from those advances .	所以 , 如同世界上其他國家所創新的 , 在發展新科技的同時也發展出新的規則 , 中國人從那些進步中脫離了 。
income there stayed stagnant , as it zoomed ahead in the rest of the world .	收入保持停滯不前 , 世界其他地方的收入也一直被放大 。
this next chart looks at more recent data .	接下來這張圖表看到更近期的數據 。
it plots income , average income in china as a percentage of average income in the united states .	它描繪了中國的平均收入比美國平均收入的百分比 。
in the '50s and '60s you can see that it was hovering at about three percent .	在1950和60年代 , 你可以看到它大約佔據了3% 。
but then in the late '70s something changed .	但在70年代末期 , 改變了 。
growth took off in china . the chinese started catching up very quickly with the united states .	成長在中國 , 中國開始迅速地和美國接觸 。
if you go back to the map at night , you can get a clue to the process that lead to the dramatic change in rules in china .	如果你晚上回頭看地圖 , 你就能得到一條線索 , 線索會導致中國的戲劇性改變 。
the brightest spot in china , which you can see on the edge of the outline here , is hong kong .	中國最明亮的地點 , 你可以看到 , 在這個區域的邊緣 , 是香港 。
hong kong was a small bit of china that , for most of the 20th century , operated under a very different set of rules than the rest of mainland china rules that were copied from working market economies of the time , and administered by the british .	香港是中國的一小部分 , 在二十世紀大部分的時候 , 都在非常不同的規則下運作 , 和當時在職場經濟體中被制定的中國規則相比 , 並且由英國政府負責 。
in the 1950s , hong kong was a place where millions of people could go , from the mainland , to start in jobs like sewing shirts , making toys .	在1950年代 , 香港是個地方 , 在那裡 , 數百萬人可以從大陸開始 , 像是縫紉、製造玩具 。
but , to get on a process of increasing income , increasing skills led to very rapid growth there .	但 , 為了要達到增加收入的過程 , 增加的技能 , 會導致非常快速的成長 。
hong kong was also the model which leaders like deng xiaoping could copy , when they decided to move all of the mainland towards the market model .	香港也是典型的典型 , 像是狄米科普這樣的領導人 , 當他們決定將所有大陸移到市場模式上 。
but deng xiaoping instinctively understood the importance of offering choices to his people .	但匈牙利直覺地了解到提供他人民選擇的重要性 。
so instead of forcing everyone in china to shift immediately to the market model , they proceeded by creating some special zones that could do , in a sense , what britain did: make the opportunity to go work with the market rules available to the people who wanted to opt in there .	所以 , 與其強迫在中國的所有人馬上移到市場模式上 , 他們以創造一些特殊區塊來進行 , 在某種意義上 , 英國做的是:讓機會與市場規則一起合作 , 讓那些想要在市場上選擇的人一起工作 。
so they created four special economic zones around hong kong: zones where chinese could come and work , and cities grew up very rapidly there ; also zones where foreign firms could come in and make things .	所以他們在香港周圍創立了四個經濟區:中國可以到那裡工作 , 城市很快就在那裡成長 ; 外國公司也能進來製造東西 。
one of the zones next to hong kong has a city called shenzhen .	香港旁邊的一個區域有一個叫做深圳的城市 。
in that city there is a taiwanese firm that made the iphone that many of you have , and they made it with labor from chinese who moved there to shenzhen .	在那個城市 , 有一個台灣公司 , 讓你們許多人有的iphone , 他們用中國人的勞工 , 搬到深圳 。
so after the four special zones , there were 14 coastal cites that were open in the same sense , and eventually demonstrated successes in these places that people could opt in to , that they flocked to because of the advantages they offered .	所以 , 在四個特區之後 , 有14個海岸的白蟻也在同一個意義上開放 , 最終 , 在這些地方展示了人們可以選擇的成功 , 他們會因為他們提供的優勢而被鎖住 。
demonstrated successes there led to a consensus for a move toward the market model for the entire economy .	證明成功導致了共識轉向整個經濟體的市場模式 。
now the chinese example shows us several points .	現在 , 中國的例子顯示了幾個分數 。
one is: preserve choices for people .	第一:保存人們的選擇 。
two: operate on the right scale .	第二:在正確的規模上運轉 。
if you try to change the rules in a village , you could do that , but a village would be too small to get the kinds of benefits you can get if you have millions of people all working under good rules .	如果你試著改變村落裡的規則 , 你可以做到 , 但村落會太小 , 以得到你能得到的好處 , 如果你有數百萬人在好的規則下工作 。
on the other hand , the nation is too big .	另一方面 , 國家太大了 。
if you try to change the rules in the nation , you can't give some people a chance to hold back , see how things turn out , and let others zoom ahead and try the new rules .	如果你試著改變這個國家的規則 , 你不能給某些人一個機會 , 看看事情的結果如何 , 讓其他人放大 , 嘗試新的規則 。
but cities give you this opportunity to create new places , with new rules that people can opt in to .	但城市給你機會創造新地方 , 讓人們可以選擇的新規則 。
and they're large enough to get all of the benefits that we can have when millions of us work together under good rules .	它們夠大 , 才能得到我們能擁有的所有利益 , 讓數百萬人在好的規則下工作 。
so the proposal is that we conceive of something called a charter city .	提案是我們想出了一個叫做特區的城市 。
we start with a charter that specifies all the rules required to attract the people who we'll need to build the city .	我們從一個特定規則開始 , 把所有規則都吸引到需要建造城市的人 。
we'll need to attract the investors who will build out the infrastructure the power system , the roads , the port , the airport , the buildings .	我們需要吸引投資者 , 來建立基礎建設電力系統、道路、港口、機場、大樓 。
you'll need to attract firms , who will come hire the people who move there first .	你會需要吸引公司 , 誰會先僱用先前移民的人 。
and you'll need to attract families , the residents who will come and live there permanently , raise their children , get an education for their children , and get their first job .	你會需要吸引家庭 , 那些會永久來到那裡的居民 , 培育他們的孩子 , 為他們的孩子接受教育 , 取得他們的第一份工作 。
with that charter , people will move there .	有了這個特點 , 人們就會搬到那裡去 。
the city can be built .	城市可以被建造出來 。
and we can scale this model .	我們可以擴大這個模型 。
we can go do it over and over again .	我們可以一遍又一遍做 。
to make it work , we need good rules . we've already discussed that .	要成功 , 我們需要好的規則 。 我們已經討論過了 。
those are captured in the charter .	這些都是章節拍的 。
we also need the choices for people .	我們也需要人民的選擇 。
that's really built into the model if we allow for the possibility of building cities on uninhabited land .	這真的是建立在模型中如果我們能讓建立在無居住的土地上
you start from uninhabited territory .	從未居住的領域開始 。
people can come live under the new charter , but no one is forced to live under it .	人們可以生活在新的章節之下 , 但沒有人會被迫生活在其中 。
the final thing we need are choices for leaders .	最後 , 我們需要的是領導者的選擇 。
and , to achieve the kind of choices we want for leaders we need to allow for the potential for partnerships between nations: cases where nations work together , in effect , de facto , the way china and britain worked together to build , first a little enclave of the market model , and then scale it throughout china .	為了達成我們想為領導者的選擇 , 我們要讓國家之間的合作夥伴有潛力:國家合作 , 實際上 , 中國和英國同心協力 , 首先建立市場模式 , 然後將它擴大到整個中國 。
in a sense , britain , inadvertently , through its actions in hong kong , did more to reduce world poverty than all the aid programs that we've undertaken in the last century .	在某種意義上 , 英國 , 不經意地 , 透過香港的行動 , 減少了世界貧窮的程度 , 比上個世紀的援助計畫還多 。
so if we allow for these kind of partnerships to replicate this again , we can get those kinds of benefits scaled throughout the world .	所以如果我們允許這種合作關係再複製 , 我們就能得到全世界的這些好處 。
in some cases this will involve a delegation of responsibility , a delegation of control from one country to another to take over certain kinds of administrative responsibilities .	在某些情況下 , 這會涉及到責任的程度 , 從一個國家的控制權 , 到另一個國家的控制權 , 來克服某些行政責任 。
now , when i say that , some of you are starting to think , " well , is this just bringing back colonialism ? "	現在 , 當我這麼說的時候 , 有些人開始想: 「 嗯 , 這只是帶回殖民主義嗎 ? 」
it's not . but it's important to recognize that the kind of emotions that come up when we start to think about these things , can get in the way , can make us pull back , can shut down our ability , and our interest in trying to explore new ideas .	不是 。 但很重要的是 , 當我們開始思考這些東西時 , 會出現的情緒 , 會讓我們退一步 , 可以阻止我們的能力 , 以及我們想要探索新點子的興趣 。
why is this not like colonialism ?	為什麼這不像殖民主義 ?
the thing that was bad about colonialism , and the thing which is residually bad in some of our aid programs , is that it involved elements of coercion and condescension .	殖民主義是不好的 , 在我們的一些援助計畫中是不好的 , 就是它涉及了合作和承認的元素 。
this model is all about choices , both for leaders and for the people who will live in these new places .	這個模式是關於選擇 , 無論是對領導者或對住在這些新地方的人來說 。
and , choice is the antidote to coercion and condescension .	而 , 選擇就是要強迫和接受的解藥 。
so let's talk about how this could play out in practice .	咱們來談談如何在練習上演出 。
let's take a particular leader , raul castro , who is the leader of cuba .	咱們來看看一位特定的領袖 , 拉爾•卡斯楚 , 他是古巴領導者 。
it must have occurred to castro that he has the chance to do for cuba what deng xiaoping did for china , but he doesn't have a hong kong there on the island in cuba .	它一定發生在卡斯楚 , 他有機會為古巴所做的事 , 為中國做了什麼 , 但他在古巴島沒有香港 。
he does , though , have a little bit of light down in the south that has a very special status .	不過 , 他的確有一點光在南方有非常特別的地位 。
there is a zone there , around guantanamo bay , where a treaty gives the united states administrative responsibility for a piece of land that's about twice the size of manhattan .	那裡有一個區塊 , 附近是關塔納摩灣 , 在那裡 , 一個條約給美國行政部門負責一塊土地的大小大約是曼哈頓的兩倍 。
castro goes to the prime minister of canada and says , " look , the yankees have a terrible pr problem .	卡斯楚去到加拿大的總理 , 說: 「 看 , 雅肯斯有一個很糟糕的問題 。
they want to get out .	他們想出去 。
why don't you , canada , take over ?	為何你不 , 加拿大 , 接管你 ?
build run a special administrative zone .	建造一個特殊的行政區 。
allow a new city to be built up there .	讓一個新城市在上面建造 。
allow many people to come in .	讓許多人進來 。
let us have a hong kong nearby .	讓我們附近有香港 。
some of my citizens will move into that city as well .	我的一些市民也會搬進那個城市 。
others will hold back . but this will be the gateway that will connect the modern economy and the modern world to my country . "	其他人則會退回 。 但這將會是將現代經濟和現代社會連結起來的大門 。 」
now , where else might this model be tried ?	現在 , 這個模型還在哪裡呢 ?
well , africa . i've talked with leaders in africa .	嗯 , 非洲 。 我和非洲的領導人談過 。
many of them totally get the notion of a special zone that people can opt into as a rule .	許多人完全理解一個特殊區塊的概念 , 讓人們可以以一個規則作選擇 。
it's a rule for changing rules .	它是改變規則的規則 。
it's a way to create new rules , and let people optin without coercion , and the opposition that coercion can force .	它是一種創造新規則的方法 , 讓人們不需要受到威脅 , 反對法則 。
they also totally get the idea that in some instances they can make more credible promises to longterm investors the kind of investors who will come build the port , build the roads , in a new city they can make more credible promises if they do it along with a partner nation .	他們也完全了解到 , 在某些情況下 , 他們可以讓長期投資人更有信心 , 投資者將來建立港口、建立道路 , 在一個新的城市中 , 他們能做出更有信用的承諾 , 如果他們能和一個夥伴國家合作 。
perhaps even in some arrangement that's a little bit like an escrow account , where you put land in the escrow account and the partner nation takes responsibility for it .	也許甚至在某些安排中 , 有點像人工帳戶 , 你把土地放進帳戶裡 , 伴侶的國家需要負起責任 。
there is also lots of land in africa where new cities could be built .	非洲還有很多土地 , 在那裡 , 新城市可以建造 。
this is a picture i took when i was flying along the coast .	這張照片是我在沿著海岸飛行時拍的 。
there are immense stretches of land like this land where hundreds of millions of people could live .	這裡有大量的土地 , 像這樣的土地 , 數億人可以居住 。
now , if we generalize this and think about not just one or two charter cites , but dozens cities that will help create places for the many hundreds of millions , perhaps billions of people who will move to cities in the coming century is there enough land for them ?	現在 , 若我們把這件事歸納起來 , 想想看 , 不只一或二個特定的居民 , 還能協助數十億的城市創造地方 , 也許數十億人會搬到未來的城市 , 對他們來說有足夠的土地 ?
well , throughout the world , if we look at the lights at night , the one thing that's misleading is that , visually , it looks like most of the world is already built out .	嗯 , 在世界各地 , 如果我們晚上看燈 , 誤導的一件事是 , 視覺上看來 , 大部分的世界已經被建造出來了 。
so let me show you why that's wrong .	所以 , 讓我告訴你們為什麼會這樣 。
take this representation of all of the land .	以所有土地為例 。
turn it into a square that stands for all the arable land on earth .	把它變成一個正方形 , 代表地球上所有可耕地 。
and let these dots represent the land that's already taken up by the cities that three billion people now live in .	讓這些點代表已經被城市佔據的土地 , 現在有三十億人口居住的城市 。
if you move the dots down to the bottom of the rectangle you can see that the cities for the existing three billion urban residents take up only three percent of the arable land on earth .	如果你把這些點移到長方形的底部 , 你可以看到現有的城市有30億的城市居民佔了地球上耕地的3% 。
so if we wanted to build cities for another billion people , they would be dots like this .	所以如果我們想為其他十億人建造城市 , 他們會像這樣做 。
we'd go from three percent of the arable land , to four percent .	我們將從百分之三的耕地變成百分之四 。
we'd dramatically reduce the human footprint on earth by building more cities that people can move to .	我們會大幅降低地球上人類的足跡 , 以建造更多人可以搬到的城市 。
and if these are cities governed by good rules , they can be cities where people are safe from crime , safe from disease and bad sanitation , where people have a chance to get a job .	如果這些都市被好的規則治理 , 他們可以成為城市 , 在那裡 , 人們安全於犯罪、疾病和衛生設施 , 在那裡 , 人們有機會得到工作 。
they can get basic utilities like electricity .	它們能得到基本的功用 , 例如電力 。
their kids can get an education .	他們的孩子可以接受教育 。
so what will it take to get started building the first charter cities , scaling this so we build many more ?	所以 , 要開始建造第一座特區的城市 , 擴大規模 , 才能建造更多 ?
it would help to have a manual .	它會幫助有手冊 。
what university professors could do is write some details that might go into this manual .	大學教授可以做的是寫一些細節 , 可以進入這個手冊 。
you wouldn't want to let us run the cities , go out and design them .	你不會想讓我們經營城市 , 去設計它們 。
you wouldn't let academics out in the wild .	你不會在野外放學者 。
but , you could set us to work thinking about questions like , suppose it isn't just canada that does the deal with raul castro .	但 , 你可以讓我們開始思考像這樣的問題 , 假設這不僅僅是加拿大 , 還能處理拉爾•卡斯楚 。
perhaps brazil comes in as a participant , and spain as well . and perhaps cuba wants to be one of the partners in a fourway joint venture .	也許巴西是參與者 , 也是西班牙 。 也許古巴想要成為四通的合作夥伴之一 。
how would we write the treaty to do that ?	我們要怎麼寫條約才能做到這一點 ?
there is less precedent for that , but that could easily be worked out .	這樣做沒什麼先例 , 但那很容易就成功了 。
how would we finance this ?	我們要如何資助這點呢 ?
turns out singapore and hong kong are cities that made huge gains on the value of the land that they owned when they got started .	結果發現 , 新加坡和香港是城市 , 在他們開始時 , 取得了巨大的利益 。
you could use the gains on the value of the land to pay for things like the police , the courts , but the school system and the health care system too , which make this a more attractive place to live , makes this a place where people have higher incomes which , incidentally , makes the land more valuable .	你可以用土地的價值來支付像警察、法庭、學校體制 , 及健康照護體制 , 讓這個更吸引人的地方居住 , 讓居民有更高的收入 , 順帶一提 , 讓土地更有價值 。
so the incentives for the people helping to construct this zone and build it , and set up the basic rules , go very much in the right direction .	所以 , 人們的動機來協助建構這個區域 , 並建立基礎規則 , 走向正確的方向 。
so there are many other details like this .	所以還有很多類似的細節 。
how could we have buildings that are low cost and affordable for people who work in a first job , assembling something like an iphone , but make those buildings energy efficient , and make sure that they are safe , so they don't fall down in an earthquake or a hurricane .	我們如何能有低成本的建築物 , 讓第一份工作的人能負擔得起 , 組裝像iphone一樣的建築物 , 同時確保他們是安全的 , 所以他們不會落在地震或颶風中 。
many technical details to be worked out , but those of us who are already starting to pursue these things can already tell that there is no roadblock , there's no impediment , other than a failure of imagination , that will keep us from delivering on a truly global winwin solution .	許多技術上的細節 , 都已經開始追尋這些東西的人 , 已經知道沒有道路 , 沒有任何障礙 , 除了缺乏想像力的失敗 , 會讓我們無法實現真正的全球風力解決方案 。
let me conclude with this picture .	讓我總結一下這張照片 。
the reason we can be so well off , even though there is so many people on earth , is because of the power of ideas .	我們之所以能如此順利 , 即使地球上有這麼多人 , 是因為想法的力量 。
we can share ideas with other people , and when they discover them , they share with us .	我們可以和其他人分享想法 , 當他們發現它們時 , 他們會和我們分享 。
it's not like scarce objects , where sharing means we each get less .	它不像稀少物體 , 共享的意思是我們每人的收入較少 。
when we share ideas we all get more .	當我們分享想法時 , 我們都會得到更多 。
when we think about ideas in that way , we usually think about technologies .	當我們以這種方式思考想法時 , 我們通常會想到科技 。
but there is another class of ideas: the rules that govern how we interact with each other ; rules like , let's have a tax system that supports a research university that gives away certain kinds of knowledge for free .	但還有另一種想法:管理我們如何和彼此互動的規則 ; 例如 , 讓我們有一個計程車系統 , 支援一個研究大學 , 讓一些知識自由 。
let's have a system where we have ownership of land that is registered in a government office , that people can pledge as collateral .	讓我們有一個體制 , 我們有政府辦公室註冊的土地 , 人們可以把權力當作商店 。
if we can keep innovating on our space of rules , and particularly innovate in the sense of coming up with rules for changing rules , so we don't get stuck with bad rules , then we can keep moving progress forward and truly make the world a better place , so that people like nelson and his friends don't have to study any longer under the streetlights . thank you .	如果我們能繼續創新我們的規則 , 特別是創新 , 要有改變規則的規則 , 我們就不會陷入不好的規則 , 那麼我們就能繼續進步 , 讓世界變得更美好 , 像nelson和他的朋友不用再在街燈下學習 。 謝謝 。
genomics pioneer craig venter takes a break from his epic roundtheworld expedition to talk about the millions of genes his team has discovered so far in its quest to map the ocean’s biodiversity .	基因組學先驅克萊格•凡特在他的史詩遺棄的探險中休息一下他的團隊發現了數百萬個基因 , 到目前為止 , 以繪製海洋生物多樣性 。
dna , biosphere , biotech , entrepreneur , genetics , invention , oceans , science , technology	dna、生態圈、生物科技、企業家、遺傳學、發明、海洋、科學、科技、科技、科技、科技、科技、科技、科技、科技、科技、科技、科技、科技、科技、科技、科技、科技、科技、
craig venter on dna and the sea	dna上的克萊格•凡特和海面上的克萊格•凡特 。
at the break , i was asked by several people about my comments about the aging debate .	休息時間 , 我被幾個人問到我對衰老辯論的評論 。
and this will be my only comment on it .	這將會是我唯一的評論 。
and that is , i understand that optimists greatly outlive pessimists .	那就是 , 我了解樂觀主義者大多超越悲觀主義者 。
what i'm going to tell you about in my 18 minutes is how we're about to switch from reading the genetic code to the first stages of beginning to write the code ourselves .	在我18分鐘內 , 我要告訴各位 , 我們將如何從閱讀基因密碼轉換到開始寫程式碼的第一步 。
it's only 10 years ago this month when we published the first sequence of a freeliving organism , that of haemophilus influenzae .	僅僅在十年前 , 我們發表了一系列免費的有機體 , 大氣流感的第一序列 。
that took a genome project from 13 years down to four months .	這個計畫花了13年到4個月 。
we can now do that same genome project in the order of two to eight hours .	我們現在可以在兩到八個小時內完成同樣的基因組計畫 。
so in the last decade , a large number of genomes have been added: most human pathogens , a couple of plants , several insects and several mammals , including the human genome .	過去十年來 , 大部份的基因組都被加入了:大部份的人類病原體、幾種植物、幾種昆蟲和哺乳類 , 包括人類基因組 。
genomics at this stage of the thinking from a little over 10 years ago was , by the end of this year , we might have between three and five genomes sequenced ; it's on the order of several hundred .	十多年前 , 在這個想法的階段 , 基因組學在今年年底 , 我們可能有三到五個基因組序列 ; 它是數百個 。
we just got a grant from the gordon and betty moore foundation to sequence 130 genomes this year , as a side project from environmental organisms .	我們剛從戈登和貝蒂•摩爾基金會得到獎助 , 到今年的130個基因組序列 , 作為環保有機體的副程式 。
so the rate of reading the genetic code has changed .	所以 , 閱讀基因編碼的速度已經改變了 。
but as we look , what's out there , we've barely scratched the surface on what is available on this planet .	但當我們看 , 外面是什麼 , 我們幾乎沒有抓住地球上可得的表面 。
most people don't realize it , because they're invisible , but microbes make up about a half of the earth's biomass , whereas all animals only make up about one onethousandth of all the biomass .	大部分的人都不知道 , 因為他們是看不見的 , 但微生物組成了地球生物量的一半 , 而所有的動物卻只有三分之一的生物組成 。
and maybe it's something that people in oxford don't do very often , but if you ever make it to the sea , and you swallow a mouthful of seawater , keep in mind that each milliliter has about a million bacteria and on the order of 10 million viruses .	可能是牛津人通常不會做的事 , 但如果你有機會把它做成海水 , 吞下一口海水 , 記住每毫升都有大約一百萬個細菌和一千萬個病毒 。
less than 5 , 000 microbial species have been characterized as of two years ago , and so we decided to do something about it .	不到五千種微生物物種在兩年前就被特徵化了 , 所以我們決定要做點什麼 。
and we started the sorcerer ii expedition , where we were , as with great oceanographic expeditions , trying to sample the ocean every 200 miles .	然後我們開始了 「 冷漠二 」 的探險 , 在那裡 , 我們和大海的探險一樣 , 嘗試在每200英里採集海洋樣本 。
we started in bermuda for our test project , then moved up to halifax , working down the u . s . east coast , the caribbean sea , the panama canal , through to the galapagos , then across the pacific , and we're in the process now of working our way across the indian ocean .	我們從bermuda開始做測試 , 然後搬到哈利法克斯 , 沿著美國東岸工作 , 加勒比海 , 巴拿馬 , 穿越加拉帕戈斯 , 橫越太平洋 , 我們現在正處於橫跨印度洋的過程中 。
it's very tough duty ; we're doing this on a sailing vessel , in part to help excite young people about going into science .	這是非常艱難的任務 ; 我們在航海船上做這件事 , 部分是為了幫助年輕人進入科學領域 。
the experiments are incredibly simple .	實驗非常簡單 。
we just take seawater and we filter it , and we collect different size organisms on different filters , and then take their dna back to our lab in rockville , where we can sequence a hundred million letters of the genetic code every 24 hours .	我們只用海水過濾 , 用不同的過濾器收集不同的大小生物 , 然後把它們的dna帶回我們在岩石維爾的實驗室 , 我們可以每24小時就將一億個字母的基因編碼定下來 。
and with doing this , we've made some amazing discoveries .	藉由這樣做 , 我們有了一些驚人的發現 。
for example , it was thought that the visual pigments that are in our eyes there was only one or two organisms in the environment that had these same pigments .	例如 , 認為在我們的眼睛中只有一兩種有機體存在於環境中 , 有著相同的色素 。
it turns out , almost every species in the upper parts of the ocean in warm parts of the world have these same photoreceptors , and use sunlight as the source of their energy and communication .	結果發現 , 幾乎所有海洋上半部的生物都有相同的光受器 , 用太陽光來作為它們的能量和溝通來源 。
from one site , from one barrel of seawater , we discovered 1 . 3 million new genes and as many as 50 , 000 new species .	從一個地方 , 從一桶海水中 , 我們發現了一百三十萬個新的基因 , 以及五萬個新物種 。
we've extended this to the air now with a grant from the sloan foundation .	我們現在已經把這張圖延伸到空氣中 , 由sloan基金會的補助 。
we're measuring how many viruses and bacteria all of us are breathing in and out every day , particularly on airplanes or closed auditoriums .	我們在測量我們所有人每天都在呼吸的病毒和細菌 , 特別是在飛機上或封閉的聽眾 。
we filter through some simple apparatuses ; we collect on the order of a billion microbes from just a day filtering on top of a building in new york city .	我們過濾了一些簡單的裝置 ; 我們只需要一天從紐約市的一座建築上一天就收集到十億微生物的數量 。
and we're in the process of sequencing all that at the present time .	而我們正處於當下所有這些資料的過程 。
just on the data collection side , just where we are through the galapagos , we're finding that almost every 200 miles , we see tremendous diversity in the samples in the ocean .	就在數據收集的一面 , 我們穿過加拉巴哥群島 , 我們發現幾乎每200英里 , 我們在海洋的樣本中會看到巨大的多樣性 。
some of these make logical sense , in terms of different temperature gradients .	有些是合理的 , 以不同的溫度來看 , 有些是合理的 。
so this is a satellite photograph based on temperatures red being warm , blue being cold and we found there's a tremendous difference between the warm water samples and the cold water samples , in terms of abundant species .	這是一張衛星照片 , 以紅色的溫度為基礎 , 藍色是溫暖 , 藍色是冷的 , 我們發現溫暖的水樣和冷水的樣本有著巨大的差別 。
the other thing that surprised us quite a bit is these photoreceptors detect different wavelengths of light , and we can predict that based on their amino acid sequence .	另一件令我們驚訝的事情是這些光受體偵測到不同的光波長 , 我們可以根據它們的氨基酸序列來預測 。
and these vary tremendously from region to region .	這些差異來自地區到地區 。
maybe not surprisingly , in the deep ocean , where it's mostly blue , the photoreceptors tend to see blue light .	也許不意外的是 , 在深海中 , 它大部分是藍色的 , 光受體通常會看到藍光 。
when there's a lot of chlorophyll around , they see a lot of green light .	當有很多葉綠素附近時 , 它們會看到很多綠光 。
but they vary even more , possibly moving towards infrared and ultraviolet in the extremes .	但它們可能更加不同 , 可能是朝向紅外線和紫外線的極端移動 。
just to try and get an assessment of what our gene repertoire was , we assembled all the data including all of ours thus far from the expedition , which represents more than half of all the gene data on the planet and it totaled around 29 million genes .	只為了試著評估我們的基因的功用 , 我們把所有的資料組合起來 , 包括我們所有的資料 , 遠遠遠超過地球上超過一半的基因資料 , 總共大約有兩千九百萬個基因 。
and we tried to put these into gene families to see what these discoveries are: are we just discovering new members of known families , or are we discovering new families ?	我們試著把這些資料放進基因家庭中 , 看看這些發現是什麼:我們只是發現已知家庭的新成員 , 還是我們發現了新的家庭 ?
and it turns out we have about 50 , 000 major gene families , but every new sample we take in the environment adds in a linear fashion to these new families .	結果發現 , 我們有大約五萬個主要基因家庭 , 但每一種新樣本 , 我們在環境中的每一種樣本 , 都會在這些新家庭中加上線性 。
so we're at the earliest stages of discovery about basic genes , components and life on this planet .	我們在地球上最早期發現基本的基因、元件和生命的階段 。
when we look at the socalled evolutionary tree , we're up on the upper righthand corner with the animals .	當我們觀察所謂的演化樹 , 我們就在右上角和動物一起 。
of those roughly 29 million genes , we only have around 24 , 000 in our genome .	在兩千九百萬個基因中 , 我們的基因只有大約兩萬四千個 。
and if you take all animals together , we probably share less than 30 , 000 and probably maybe a dozen or more thousand different gene families .	如果你把所有動物聚集在一起 , 我們可能就有不到三萬個 , 也許有十萬個不同的基因家庭 。
i view that these genes are now not only the design components of evolution .	我覺得這些基因不僅僅是演化的設計成分 。
and we think in a genecentric view maybe going back to richard dawkins' ideas than in a genomecentric view , which are different constructs of these gene components .	我們認為在一個基因方面也許會回到理查德•達金斯的想法 , 而不是從基因的角度來看 , 這些基因組成的結構是不同的 。
synthetic dna , the ability to synthesize dna , has changed at sort of the same pace that dna sequencing has over the last decade or two , and is getting very rapid and very cheap .	合成dna的能力 , 合成dna的能力 , 隨著dna定序的步驟改變 , 在過去十年或二十年間 , dna的速度越來越快 , 非常便宜 。
our first thought about synthetic genomics came when we sequenced the second genome back in 1995 , and that from mycoplasma genitalium .	我們首先想到合成基因組在1995年我們將第二個基因組定序 , 再從mycollsma的生殖器取得 。
and we have really nice tshirts that say , you know , " i heart my genitalium . "	我們有很棒的t恤 , 上面寫著: 「 我愛我的生殖器 。 」
this is actually just a microorganism .	這其實只是微生物 。
but it has roughly 500 genes .	但它大約有500個基因 。
haemophilus had 1 , 800 genes .	哈伊菲爾斯有1800個基因 。
and we simply asked the question , if one species needs 800 , another 500 , is there a smaller set of genes that might comprise a minimal operating system ?	我們只需要問一個問題 , 如果一個物種需要800 , 另外還有500種 , 是否有較小的基因 , 會組成最小的作業系統 ?
so we started doing transposon mutagenesis .	所以我們開始做跨性別突變 。
transposons are just small pieces of dna that randomly insert in the genetic code .	轉基因只是小小的dna , 隨機插入遺傳密碼 。
and if they insert in the middle of the gene , they disrupt its function .	如果他們在基因的中間插入 , 他們會打斷它的功能 。
so we made a map of all the genes that could take transposon insertions and we called those " nonessential genes . "	所以 , 我們做了一張地圖 , 所有可以將轉性器插入的基因 , 我們稱之為 「 不必要的基因 」 。
but it turns out the environment is very critical for this , and you can only define an essential or nonessential gene based on exactly what's in the environment .	但事實證明 , 環境是非常關鍵的 , 你只能根據環境中什麼東西來定義一個必要或不必要的基因 。
we also tried to take a more directly intellectual approach with the genomes of 13 related organisms , and we tried to compare all of those , to see what they had in common .	我們也嘗試用更直接的智能方法來處理13個相關生物的基因組 , 我們試圖將這些基因做比較 , 看看它們有什麼共通點 。
and we got these overlapping circles . and we found only 173 genes common to all 13 organisms .	我們得到了這些重疊的圓圈 。 我們發現 , 只有173個基因共有13個有機體 。
the pool expanded a little bit if we ignored one intracellular parasite ; it expanded even more when we looked at core sets of genes of around 310 or so .	如果我們忽略一個細胞寄生蟲 , 糞便會擴大一點 ; 當我們觀察核心的核心基因組時 , 糞便會擴大一點 。
so we think that we can expand or contract genomes , depending on your point of view here , to maybe 300 to 400 genes from the minimal of 500 .	所以我們認為我們可以擴大或收縮基因組 , 取決於你的觀點 , 到500年最低的300個基因 。
the only way to prove these ideas was to construct an artificial chromosome with those genes in them , and we had to do this in a cassettebased fashion .	要證明這些點子的唯一方法是建構一個人造染色體 , 與這些基因組組合 , 我們必須在以口袋為基礎的時尚中做這件事 。
we found that synthesizing accurate dna in large pieces was extremely difficult .	我們發現 , 在大片中合成精確的dna是非常困難的 。
ham smith and clyde hutchison , my colleagues on this , developed an exciting new method that allowed us to synthesize a 5 , 000base pair virus in only a twoweek period that was 100 percent accurate , in terms of its sequence and its biology .	哈姆斯•史密斯和克萊德•哈奇森 , 我的同事開發了一種令人興奮的新方法 , 讓我們能在兩週的序列中合成一個5000個鹼基對病毒 , 它的序列和它的生物學 。
it was a quite exciting experiment when we just took the synthetic piece of dna , injected it in the bacteria and all of a sudden , that dna started driving the production of the virus particles that turned around and then killed the bacteria .	這是個相當令人興奮的實驗 , 當我們把合成dna注入細菌中 , 突然間 , dna就開始驅動病毒粒子的生產 , 然後殺死細菌 。
this was not the first synthetic virus a polio virus had been made a year before but it was only one tenthousandth as active and it took three years to do .	這不是第一個合成病毒--小兒麻痺病毒在一年前被製造出來的 , 但它只有一個堅定的活性 , 花了三年才完成 。
this is a cartoon of the structure of phi x 174 .	這是phix-174的結構圖
this is a case where the software now builds its own hardware , and that's the notions that we have with biology .	這是一個軟體現在建立自己的硬體 , 這就是我們對生物的概念 。
people immediately jump to concerns about biological warfare , and i had recent testimony before a senate committee , and a special committee the u . s . government has set up to review this area .	人們馬上就開始關心生物戰事 , 最近我在參議院委員會前證詞 , 美國政府設立了特殊委員會來審查這個區域 。
and i think it's important to keep reality in mind , versus what happens with people's imaginations .	我認為 , 要把現實留在心中是很重要的 , 和人們的想像力是怎樣的 。
basically , any virus that's been sequenced today that genome can be made .	基本上 , 任何今天被基因組定序的病毒 , 都可以被製造出來 。
and people immediately freak out about things about ebola or smallpox , but the dna from this organism is not infective .	人們馬上就對伊波拉或天花感到驚奇 , 但這些生物的dna並不感染 。
so even if somebody made the smallpox genome , that dna itself would not cause infections .	所以即使有人做了天花基因 , dna本身就不會造成感染 。
the real concern that security departments have is designer viruses .	安全部門真正關心的是設計師病毒 。
and there's only two countries , the u . s . and the former soviet union , that had major efforts on trying to create biological warfare agents .	只有兩個國家 , 美國和前蘇聯 , 致力於創造生物戰事代理 。
if that research is truly discontinued , there should be very little activity on the knowhow to make designer viruses in the future .	如果這項研究真的無法持續下去 , 未來應該有非常少的活動來製造設計師病毒 。
i think singlecell organisms are possible within two years .	我認為 , 在兩年內 , 單細胞有機體是有可能的 。
and possibly eukaryotic cells , those that we have , are possible within a decade .	可能是真菌細胞 , 那些我們擁有的細胞 , 可能在十年內就有可能 。
so we're now making several dozen different constructs , because we can vary the cassettes and the genes that go into this artificial chromosome .	所以 , 我們現在正在製造數十種不同的結構 , 因為我們可以將種姓和基因轉換成這種人造染色體 。
the key is , how do you put all of the others ?	關鍵是 , 你要如何把他人放進去 ?
we start with these fragments , and then we have a homologous recombination system that reassembles those into a chromosome .	我們從這些片段開始 , 然後我們有一個同性組合系統 , 將這些片段重新組合成一個染色體 。
this is derived from an organism , deinococcus radiodurans , that can take three million rads of radiation and not be killed .	由一種有機體衍生 , 失智症患者 , 可以接受三百萬張無線輻射 , 不會被殺 。
it reassembles its genome after this radiation burst in about 12 to 24 hours , after its chromosomes are literally blown apart .	它在這個輻射爆發後的基因組 , 大約在12到24小時後 , 它的染色體會被完全拆解 。
this organism is ubiquitous on the planet , and exists perhaps now in outer space due to all our travel there .	這種生物在地球上無所不在 , 或許存在於外太空 , 因為我們的旅行 。
this is a glass beaker after about half a million rads of radiation .	這是一台玻璃啤酒 , 經過五十萬張放射線 。
the glass started to burn and crack , while the microbes sitting in the bottom just got happier and happier .	玻璃開始燃燒和裂縫 , 坐在底部的微生物就變得更快樂、更快樂 。
here's an actual picture of what happens: the top of this shows the genome after 1 . 7 million rads of radiation .	這是一張實際發生的圖片 , 上面顯示了一百七十萬張放射線後的基因組 。
the chromosome is literally blown apart .	染色體是分開的 。
and here's that same dna automatically reassembled 24 hours later .	同樣的dna在24小時後自動重組 。
it's truly stunning that these organisms can do that , and we probably have thousands , if not tens of thousands , of different species on this planet that are capable of doing that .	真的令人驚訝的是 , 這些生物可以做到這一點 , 我們可能有上千種 , 如果不是上萬種 , 在地球上 , 可以做到這一點 。
after these genomes are synthesized , the first step is just transplanting them into a cell without a genome .	在這些基因組被合成之後 , 第一步就是把它們移植到一個沒有基因組的細胞中 。
so we think synthetic cells are going to have tremendous potential , not only for understanding the basis of biology but for hopefully environmental and society issues .	所以我們認為合成細胞將會有巨大的潛力 , 不僅為了了解生物學的基礎 , 還能為環境和社會議題提供希望 。
for example , from the third organism we sequenced , methanococcus jannaschii it lives in boiling water temperatures ; its energy source is hydrogen and all its carbon comes from co2 it captures back from the environment .	例如 , 從第三個我們序列的生物中 , 甲腎上腺素jannaschii它生活在沸騰的水溫中 , 它的能量來源是氫 , 所有的碳來自二氧化碳 , 它從環境中獲取回來 。
so we know lots of different pathways , thousands of different organisms now that live off of co2 , and can capture that back .	所以 , 我們知道許多不同的途徑 , 數千種不同的生物 , 活在二氧化碳之外 , 還能捕捉到它 。
so instead of using carbon from oil for synthetic processes , we have the chance of using carbon and capturing it back from the atmosphere , converting that into biopolymers or other products .	所以 , 與其使用石油作為合成過程 , 我們有使用碳的機會 , 將它從大氣中捕捉回來 , 將它轉換成生物聚合物或其他產品 。
we have one organism that lives off of carbon monoxide , and we use as a reducing power to split water to produce hydrogen and oxygen .	我們有一種生物存在於一氧化碳之外 , 我們用它來降低水分解的能量來產生氫和氧氣 。
also , there's numerous pathways that can be engineered metabolizing methane .	此外 , 有許多途徑可以被改造甲烷 。
and dupont has a major program with statoil in norway to capture and convert the methane from the gas fields there into useful products .	杜邦在挪威有一項重大的計畫 , 來捕集並將甲烷從加油場轉換成有用的產品 。
within a short while , i think there's going to be a new field called " combinatorial genomics , " because with these new synthesis capabilities , these vast gene array repertoires and the homologous recombination , we think we can design a robot to make maybe a million different chromosomes a day .	短暫之內 , 我想有一個新的領域 , 叫做 「 組合基因 」 , 因為這些新的合成能力 , 這些廣大的基因陣列 , 和同性重新組合 , 我們認為我們可以設計一個機器人 , 一天製造一百萬個不同的染色體 。
and therefore , as with all biology , you get selection through screening , whether you're screening for hydrogen production , or chemical production , or just viability .	因此 , 就像所有生物學一樣 , 你透過篩檢來選擇 , 不論你是在為氫生產篩選 , 或是化學生產 , 或單純的可行性 。
to understand the role of these genes is going to be well within reach .	若要了解這些基因的作用 , 就會很明顯 。
we're trying to modify photosynthesis to produce hydrogen directly from sunlight .	我們試著修改光合作用 , 直接從太陽光產生氫 。
photosynthesis is modulated by oxygen , and we have an oxygeninsensitive hydrogenase that we think will totally change this process .	光合作用會調節氧氣 , 我們有一種氧氣敏感的氧氣 , 我們認為會完全改變這個過程 。
we're also combining cellulases , the enzymes that break down complex sugars into simple sugars and fermentation in the same cell for producing ethanol .	我們也在結合細胞 , 酵素會將複雜的糖分解成簡單的糖和發酵 , 以產生乙醇的細胞 。
pharmaceutical production is already under way in major laboratories using microbes .	藥物生產已經在使用微生物的大型實驗室中進行了 。
the chemistry from compounds in the environment is orders of magnitude more complex than our best chemists can produce .	環境中的化合物的化學性質比我們最好的化合物所產生的更複雜 。
i think future engineered species could be the source of food , hopefully a source of energy , environmental remediation and perhaps replacing the petrochemical industry .	我想未來的工程物種可能是食物的來源 , 希望是能量的來源 , 環境的復甦 , 也許可以替代石化產業 。
let me just close with ethical and policy studies .	讓我用倫理和政策研究來做結尾 。
we delayed the start of our experiments in 1999 until we completed a yearandahalf bioethical review as to whether we should try and make an artificial species .	我們在1999年開始了實驗 , 直到我們完成了一年半的生物倫理評論 , 來評估我們是否該嘗試製造人造物種 。
every major religion participated in this .	每一大宗教都參與其中 。
it was actually a very strange study , because the various religious leaders were using their scriptures as law books , and they couldn't find anything in them prohibiting making life , so it must be ok . the only ultimate concerns were biological warfare aspects of this , but gave us the go ahead to start these experiments for the reasons we were doing them .	這其實是個很奇怪的研究 , 因為各式各樣的宗教領袖使用他們的文字作為法律 , 他們無法在他們禁止製造生命的過程中找到任何東西 , 所以 , 沒關係 。 唯一的擔憂是生物戰爭方面的面向 , 但給了我們開始這些實驗 , 原因是我們做這些實驗的理由 。
right now the sloan foundation has just funded a multiinstitutional study on this , to work out what the risk and benefits to society are , and the rules that scientific teams such as my own should be using in this area , and we're trying to set good examples as we go forward .	現在 , sloan基金會剛剛資助了一項跨機構的研究 , 研究對社會的風險和利益 , 以及科學團隊的規則 , 如同我自己應該在這個領域中使用的規則 , 我們正試著在我們繼續前進時設定好的例子 。
these are complex issues .	這些都是複雜的問題 。
except for the threat of bioterrorism , they're very simple issues in terms of , can we design things to produce clean energy , perhaps revolutionizing what developing countries can do and provide through various simple processes .	除了生物恐怖主義的威脅 , 它們是非常簡單的問題 , 我們能否設計出能產生乾淨能源的東西 , 或許能改變開發中國家能做些什麼 , 透過各種簡單的過程提供 。
psychologist philip zimbardo says happiness and success are rooted in a trait most of us disregard: the way we orient toward the past , present and future . he suggests we calibrate our outlook on time as a first step to improving our lives .	心理學家philipzimardo說快樂和成功是根根植在我們大多數人不關心的特質上:我們往過去、現在、未來方向邁進的方式 。 他建議我們在時間軸上 , 來改善我們的生命 。
brain , business , happiness , mind , psychology , science	大腦、商業、快樂、心智、心理、科學、科學、科學、科學、科學、科學、
philip zimbardo prescribes a healthy take on time	philipzimardo開了一段很健康的時間 。
i want to share with you some ideas about the secret power of time , in a very short time .	我想和大家分享一些關於時間的秘密力量的概念 , 很短的時間內 。
video: all right , start the clock please . 30 seconds studio .	影片:好 , 開始時鐘 。 三十秒的工作室 。
keep it quiet please . settle down .	請安靜下來 , 安靜下來 。
it's about time . end sequence . take one .	大概是時間 。 終結一次 。
10 , nine , eight , seven , six , five , four , three , two . . .	10、9、8、7、6、5、4、3、2......
philip zimbardo: let's tune into the conversation of the principals in adam's temptation .	philipzimbardo:咱們來談談亞當的校長在亞當的誘惑中 。
" come on adam , don't be so wishywashy . take a bite . " " i did . "	「 拜託亞當 , 不要那麼願望 , 吃點東西 。 」 我就這麼做了 。 」
" one bite , adam . don't abandon eve . "	「 一口 , adam , 不要放棄eve 。 」
" i don't know , guys .	「 我不知道 , 各位 。
i don't want to get in trouble . "	我不想惹上麻煩 。 」
" okay . one bite . what the hell ? "	「 好 , 一口 , 到底是怎麼回事 ? 」
life is temptation . it's all about yielding , resisting , yes , no , now , later , impulsive , reflective , present focus and future focus .	生命是誘人的 。 它是關於產量、抗拒、是的 , 是的 , 不 , 之後 , 衝動、當下、焦點、未來焦點 。
promised virtues fall prey to the passions of the moment .	受益的美德落在那一刻的熱情中 。
of teenage girls who pledged sexual abstinence and virginity until marriage thank you george bush the majority , 60 percent , yielded to sexual temptations within one year .	十幾歲的女孩 , 她們主宰性腹部和處女 , 直到結婚 , 感謝你 , 喬治布希大部份 , 百分之六十 , 她們在一年內就有性誘惑 。
and most of them did so without using birth control .	大多數人沒有使用生育控制 。
so much for promises .	這麼多的承諾 。
now lets tempt fouryearolds , giving them a treat .	現在讓我們試試四歲的孩子 , 給他們一個治療方法 。
they can have one marshmallow now . but if they wait until the experimenter comes back , they can have two .	他們現在可以有一顆棉花糖 , 但如果他們等到實驗員回來 , 他們就可以有兩顆 。
of course it pays , if you like marshmallows , to wait .	當然 , 如果你喜歡marshmallows , 可以等待它 。
what happens is twothirds of the kids give in to temptation .	發生的事是三分之二的孩子給予誘惑 。
they cannot wait . the others , of course , wait .	他們不能等待 , 當然 , 其他的 , 等等 。
they resist the temptation . they delay the now for later .	他們抗拒誘惑 , 延遲現在 。
walter mischel , my colleague at stanford , went back 14 years later , to try to discover what was different about those kids .	沃爾特•米歇爾 , 我在史丹佛的同事 , 14年後 , 試圖找出那些孩子的不同 。
there were enormous differences between kids who resisted and kids who yielded , in many ways .	在許多方面 , 孩子抗拒和孩子之間有著巨大的差異 。
the kids who resisted scored 250 points higher on the sat .	那些在坐上抗拒評分的孩子 , 高出250分 。
that's enormous . that's like a whole set of different iq points .	這很巨大 。 這就像是一整套不同的智商點 。
they didn't get in as much trouble . they were better students .	他們不會惹上麻煩 , 他們是比較好的學生 。
they were selfconfident and determined . and the key for me today , the key for you , is , they were futurefocused rather than presentfocused .	它們是自信和決心 。 今天對我來說 , 關鍵是 , 它們是未來的發展 , 而非具備現代化 。
so what is time perspective ? that's what i'm going to talk about today .	所以 , 時間的觀點是什麼 ? 這是我今天要談的 。
time perspective is the study of how individuals , all of us , divide the flow of your human experience into time zones or time categories .	時間的觀點是關於個人的研究 , 我們所有人 , 把你人類經驗的流程分成時間區或時間分類 。
and you do it automatically and nonconsciously .	然後你就自動做 , 無意識地做 。
they vary between cultures , between nations , between individuals , between social classes , between education levels .	它們不同於文化、國家、個人、社會階級、教育程度之間的差異 。
and the problem is that they can become biased , because you learn to overuse some of them and underuse the others .	問題是 , 它們可以變得偏見 , 因為你學會過度使用其中的一些 , 用到其他的 。
what determines any decision you make ?	你做了什麼決定 ?
you make a decision on which you're going to base an action .	你要做出決定 , 決定你要採取行動 。
for some people it's only about what is in the immediate situation , what other people are doing and what you're feeling .	對某些人來說 , 只是關於立即的狀況 , 其他人在做什麼 , 以及你在想什麼 。
and those people , when they make their decisions in that format we're going to call them " presentoriented , " because their focus is what is now .	而那些人 , 當他們做出決策時 , 我們會稱他們為 「 簡報 」 , 因為他們的焦點是現在 。
for others , the present is irrelevant .	對其他人來說 , 現在是不相關的 。
it's always about " what is this situation like that i've experienced in the past ? "	總是關於 「 我過去所經歷過的這種情況是什麼 ? 」
so that their decisions are based on past memories .	所以他們的決定基於過去的記憶 。
and we're going to call those people " pastoriented , " because they focus on what was .	我們要稱這些人為 「 過去式 」 , 因為他們把焦點放在什麼 。
for others it's not the past , it's not the present , it's only about the future .	對其他人來說 , 不是過去 , 不是現在 , 而是關於未來 。
their focus is always about anticipated consequences .	他們的焦點總是預期後果 。
we're going to call them " futureoriented . " their focus is on what will be .	我們稱之為 「 未來式 」 。 他們的焦點在於將來會發生的事 。
so , time paradox , i want to argue , the paradox of time perspective , is something that influences every decision you make , you're totally unaware of .	所以 , 時間悖論 , 我想說的是 , 時間的悖論 , 是影響你所做的每一決定的影響力 , 你完全不知道的 。
namely , the extent to which you have one of these biased time perspectives .	換句話說 , 你有這種偏見的時間觀點 。
well there is actually six of them . there are two ways to be presentoriented .	其實有六個 。 有兩種方式可以用在現場 。
there is two ways to be pastoriented , two ways to be future .	過去有兩種方式 , 有兩種方式可以成為未來 。
