you can focus on pastpositive , or pastnegative .	你可以把焦點放在正面或負面 。
you can be presenthedonistic , namely you focus on the joys of life , or presentfatalist it doesn't matter , your life is controlled .	你可以做個簡報 , 也就是你把焦點放在生活的喜悅上 , 或說簡報主義者不重要 , 你的生活是受控制的 。
you can be futureoriented , setting goals .	你可以是未來的目標 , 設定目標 。
or you can be transcendental future: namely , life begins after death .	或你可能是超然的未來:即 , 生命從死亡開始 。
developing the mental flexibility to shift time perspectives fluidly depending on the demands of the situation , that's what you've got to learn to do .	發展出能夠改變時間的靈活度的靈活度 , 取決於情況的需求 , 那就是你必須學會做的事 。
so , very quickly , what is the optimal time profile ?	所以 , 很快地 , 最佳的時間檔案是什麼 ?
high on pastpositive . moderately high on future .	正面的高度 。 未來的高度 。
and moderate on presenthedonism .	現代主義的現代主義 。
and always low on pastnegative and presentfatalism .	總是低估了過去的負面和當今的論點 。
so the optimal temporal mix is what you get from the past pastpositive gives you roots . you connect your family , identity and your self .	所以最佳的顳葉混合是你從過去的積極中得到的 , 會給你根 , 連接你的家人、身份和你的自我 。
what you get from the future is wings to soar to new destinations , new challenges .	你從未來得到的是翅膀 , 到新目的地 , 新的挑戰 。
what you get from the present hedonism is the energy , the energy to explore yourself , places , people , sensuality .	你從現在的愛德華主義中得到的能量 , 去探索你自己 , 地點 , 人們 , 人們 , 感覺 。
any time perspective in excess has more negatives than positives .	任何時間的觀點都比正面更負面 。
what do futures sacrifice for success ?	未來對成功的犧牲是什麼 ?
they sacrifice family time . they sacrifice friend time .	他們犧牲家人的時間 , 他們犧牲了朋友的時間 。
they sacrifice fun time . they sacrifice personal indulgence .	他們犧牲了有趣的時光 , 他們犧牲了個人的干擾 。
they sacrifice hobbies . and they sacrifice sleep . so it affects their health .	他們犧牲了嗜好 , 他們犧牲了睡眠 。 這影響了他們的健康 。
and they live for work , achievement and control .	他們為工作、成就和控制權而活 。
i'm sure that resonates with some of the tedsters .	我相信 , 和一些ted者共鳴 。
and it resonated for me . i grew up as a poor kid in the south bronx ghetto , a sicilian family everyone lived in the past and present .	對我來說 , 我是南布朗克斯ghetto的一個可憐的孩子 , 一個西西里的家庭 , 住在過去和現在 。
i'm here as a futureoriented person who went over the top , who did all these sacrifices because teachers intervened , and made me future oriented .	我來這裡是一位有著未來的人 , 走過頂端 , 因為老師們採取了這些犧牲 , 讓我成為未來的方向 。
told me don't eat that marshmallow , because if you wait you're going to get two of them , until i learned to balance out .	告訴我不要吃棉花糖 , 因為如果你在等著你會拿到兩個 , 直到我學會了平衡 。
i've added presenthedonism , i've added a focus on the pastpositive , so , at 76 years old , i am more energetic than ever , more productive , and i'm happier than i have ever been .	我加上了 「 簡報主義 」 , 我把焦點放在過去的積極 , 76歲時 , 我比以往更有活力 , 更有生產力 , 我比以前更快樂 。
i just want to say that we are applying this to many world problems: changing the dropout rates of school kids , combating addictions , enhancing teen health , curing vets' ptsd with time metaphors getting miracle cures promoting sustainability and conservation , reducing physical rehabilitation where there is a 50percent drop out rate , altering appeals to suicidal terrorists , and modifying family conflicts as timezone clashes .	我想說的是 , 我們把這個應用到許多世界問題上:改變學校的輟學率、結合成癮、提升青少年健康、治癒vthsd的方式 , 提升了永續發展和保育 , 讓物理復健率降低了50%的輟學率 , 改變了自殺的恐怖份子 , 以及修改了家庭衝突 。
so i want to end by saying: many of life's puzzles can be solved by understanding your time perspective and that of others .	最後 , 我想說的是:許多生命的謎題可以透過了解你的時間的觀點和其他時間來解決 。
and the idea is so simple , so obvious , but i think the consequences are really profound .	這個想法很簡單 , 很明顯 , 但我認為結果非常深遠 。
how many of today's headlines will matter in 100 years ? 1000 ? kirk citron's " long news " project collects stories that not only matter today , but will resonate for decades even centuries to come . at ted2010 , he highlights recent headlines with the potential to shape our future .	一百年後 , 有多少頭條新聞會造成影響 ? 一百百篇 ? kirkcron的 「 長期新聞計畫 」 收集了許多故事 , 收集了數十年來 , 在ted2010年 , 他發表了近期的頭條 , 以形塑我們未來的潛力 。
future , global issues , media , news , science	未來、全球議題、媒體、科學、科學、科學問題、
kirk citron: and now , the real news	kirkcitron:現在 , 真正的消息是:
we are drowning in news .	新聞淹沒了我們 。
reuters alone puts out three and a half million news stories a year .	光是通勤者每年就發表了三百五十萬個新聞報導 。
that's just one source .	這只是其中一個來源 。
my question is: how many of those stories are actually going to matter in the long run ?	我的問題是:在長期間 , 到底有多少故事會很重要 ?
that's the idea behind the long news .	這是長期新聞背後的想法 。
it's a project by the long now foundation , which was founded by tedsters including kevin kelly and stewart brand .	這個計畫是長期的基金會 , 由tedster所創立的 , 包括凱文凱利和史都華特品牌 。
and what we're looking for is news stories that might still matter 50 or 100 or 10 , 000 years from now .	而我們正在尋找的新聞報導 , 新聞報導來自50或1000或1000年後 。
and when you look at the news through that filter , a lot falls by the wayside .	當你透過那個過濾器看新聞時 , 很多事都跌倒了 。
to take the top stories from the a . p . this last year , is this going to matter in a decade ?	以從a.p.的最佳故事為例 , 去年 , 這會對十年有影響嗎 ?
is this going to matter in 50 or 100 years ?	這在50或100年內是很重要的嗎 ?
okay , that was kind of cool .	好吧 , 真的很酷 。
but the top story of this past year was the economy , and i'm just betting that , sooner or later , this particular recession is going to be old news .	但過去一年最棒的故事是經濟 , 我打賭 , 很快 , 或之後 , 這種衰退將會是老消息 。
so , what kind of stories might make a difference for the future ?	所以 , 什麼樣的故事可能對未來造成影響 ?
well , let's take science .	嗯 , 咱們來看科學 。
someday , little robots will go through our bloodstreams fixing things .	有一天 , 小機器人會透過我們的血液來解決問題 。
that someday is already here if you're a mouse .	某一天 , 如果你是一隻老鼠 , 就已經存在了 。
some recent stories: nanobees zap tumors with real bee venom ; they're sending genes into the brain ; a robot they built that can crawl through the human body .	一些最近的故事:奈米蜜蜂帶有真正的蜜蜂毒液 ; 它們將基因送到大腦中 ; 它們建造的機器人可以爬過人體 。
what about resources ? how are we going to feed nine billion people ?	資源呢 ? 我們要如何餵飽九十億人 ?
we're having trouble feeding six billion today .	我們今天正面臨六十億人的糧食問題 。
as we heard yesterday , there's over a billion people hungry .	正如我們昨天聽到的 , 有超過十億人挨餓 。
britain will starve without genetically modified crops .	英國人不會因為基因改造作物而餓死 。
bill gates , fortunately , has bet a billion on [agricultural] research .	幸運的是 , 比爾•蓋茨在研究中有十億人是賭 。
what about global politics ?	全球政治呢 ?
the world's going to be very different when and if china sets the agenda , and they may .	當中國設定議程時 , 世界會變得非常不同 , 他們可能會 。
they've overtaken the u . s . as the world's biggest car market , they've overtaken germany as the largest exporter , and they've started doing dna tests on kids to choose their careers .	他們已經超過了美國 , 作為世界上最大的汽車市場 , 他們已經把德國當作最大的出口國 , 他們開始在孩子們身上做dna檢測 。
we're finding all kinds of ways to push back the limits of what we know .	我們找到各式各樣的方法 , 來推回我們所知的極限 。
some recent discoveries: there's an ant colony from argentina that has now spread to every continent but antarctica ; there's a selfdirected robot scientist that's made a discovery soon , science may no longer need us , and life may no longer need us either ; a microbe wakes up after 120 , 000 years .	最近的一些發現:阿根廷的蟻群現在已經擴散到每一塊大陸 , 但南極洲 , 有一個自主導的機器人 , 很快就發現了 , 科學不再需要我們 , 生命也不再需要我們 ; 一個微生物在十二萬年後出現了 。
it seems that with or without us , life will go on .	看似有沒有我們 , 生命會持續下去 。
but my pick for the top long news story of this past year was this one: water found on the moon .	但是我在過去一年的長篇報導中挑選了這篇文章:水在月球上找到了 。
makes it a lot easier to put a colony up there .	讓蟻群更容易放到那裡 。
and if nasa doesn't do it , china might , or somebody in this room might write a big check .	如果太空總署不做 , 中國可能 , 或在座的某個人可能會寫很大的支票 。
my point is this: in the long run , some news stories are more important than others .	我的重點是:在長期來看 , 有些新聞故事比其他新聞更重要 。
planetary scientist carolyn porco shows images from the cassini voyage to saturn , focusing on its largest moon , titan , and on frozen enceladus , which seems to shoot jets of ice .	地球科學家carolynporco展示了來自卡西尼航行到土星的影像 , 把焦點放在最大的月球、土衛二 , 和冰凍的土衛二上 , 這似乎是冰射擊 。
nasa , design , exploration , science , space , technology , universe , visualizations	nasa、設計、探索、科學、太空、科技、宇宙 , 視覺化視覺化 。
carolyn porco flies us to saturn	卡羅琳•普拉科斯讓我們飛來土星飛來飛去 。
in the next 18 minutes , i'm going to take you on a journey .	在接下來的18分鐘裡 , 我要帶你們踏上一段旅程 。
and it's a journey that you and i have been on for many years now , and it began some 50 years ago , when humans first stepped off our planet .	這段旅程是你和我已經經歷了好幾年 , 五十年前 , 人類第一次踏出地球 。
and in those 50 years , not only did we literally , physically set foot on the moon , but we have dispatched robotic spacecraft to all the planets all eight of them and we have landed on asteroids , we have rendezvoused with comets , and , at this point in time , we have a spacecraft on its way to pluto , the body formerly known as a planet .	在那50年裡 , 我們不僅僅是真的在月球上定下來 , 我們還將機械太空船分散到所有行星中的八個行星上 , 我們已經登上了小行星 , 在此時此刻 , 我們有了一艘太空船 , 航行到冥王星的路上 , 前面被稱為 「 行星 」 。
and all of these robotic missions are part of a bigger human journey: a voyage to understand something , to get a sense of our cosmic place , to understand something of our origins , and how earth , our planet , and we , living on it , came to be .	所有這些機械任務都是人類旅程的一部分:一趟旅程 , 去理解某樣東西 , 去了解我們的宇宙起源 , 了解我們的地球 , 以及我們居住的地球 。
and of all the places in the solar system that we might go to and search for answers to questions like this , there's saturn . and we have been to saturn before we visited saturn in the early 1980s but our investigations of saturn have become far more indepth in detail since the cassini spacecraft , traveling across interplanetary space for seven years , glided into orbit around saturn in the summer of 2004 , and became at that point the farthest robotic outpost that humanity had ever established around the sun .	而太陽系中所有我們可能去尋找像這樣的問題的答案 , 土星在1980年代早期我們去過土星探訪過土星 , 但我們對土星的調查已經變得更加深刻 , 自卡西尼號太空船七年來 , 橫跨星際空間 , 橫跨土星 , 在2004年夏天就在土星周圍繞行 , 當時人類在太陽周圍的最遙遠的飛行軌道上 。
now , the saturn system is a rich planetary system .	土星系統是個豐富的行星系統 。
it offers mystery , scientific insight and obviously splendor beyond compare , and the investigation of this system has enormous cosmic reach .	它提供了神秘、科學的洞察 , 顯然 , 除了比賽之外 , 對於這個系統的調查有巨大的宇宙接觸 。
in fact , just studying the rings alone , we stand to learn a lot about the discs of stars and gas that we call the spiral galaxies .	事實上 , 光靠研究圓圈 , 我們就有很多關於恆星的圓盤和氣體的知識 , 我們稱之為 「 螺旋星系 」 。
and here's a beautiful picture of the andromeda nebula , which is our closest , largest spiral galaxy to the milky way .	這裡有一個美麗的圖片 , 由andromedanebula , 這是我們最接近的最大螺旋星系 , 到銀河系 。
and then , here's a beautiful composite of the whirlpool galaxy , taken by the hubble space telescope .	然後 , 這是個美麗的旋風星系 , 由哈伯太空望遠鏡所拍攝的 。
so the journey back to saturn is really part of and is also a metaphor for a much larger human voyage to understand the interconnectedness of everything around us , and also how humans fit into that picture .	所以 , 回到土星的旅程其實是人類旅行的一部分 , 也是人類旅行的象徵 , 來了解我們周圍的所有事物之間的關聯性 , 以及人類如何融入這張照片 。
and it pains me that i can't tell you all that we have learned with cassini .	這讓我感到痛苦 , 我無法告訴你們我們在卡西尼學到的一切 。
i can't show you all the beautiful pictures that we've taken in the last two and a half years , because i simply don't have the time .	我無法向你們展示我們過去兩年半所拍攝的美麗照片 , 因為我沒有時間 。
so i'm going to concentrate on two of the most exciting stories that have emerged out of this major exploratory expedition that we are conducting around saturn , and have been for the past two and a half years .	所以我要專注於這次重大的探索探險旅程中 , 兩個最令人興奮的故事 , 我們正在進行土星的探險 , 過去兩年半以來都是如此 。
saturn is accompanied by a very large and diverse collection of moons .	土星是由一大群多樣的衛星所組成的 。
they range in size from a few kilometers across to as big across as the u . s .	它們的大小範圍是從幾公里長到像美國一樣大 。
most of the beautiful pictures we've taken of saturn , in fact , show saturn in accompaniment with some of its moons . here's saturn with dione , and then , here's saturn showing the rings edgeon , showing you just how vertically thin they are , with the moon enceladus .	我們拍攝的土星大部分的美麗照片 , 事實上 , 和一些月球共存 , 這裡是土星的土星 , 這裡是土星 , 這裡是土星 , 這裡是土星的邊緣 , 向你展示它們是多麼薄 , 它們是月球土衛二 。
now , two of the 47 moons that saturn has are standouts .	土星的47個衛星中有兩個是站著的 。
and those are titan and enceladus . titan is saturn's largest moon , and , until cassini had arrived there , was the largest single expanse of unexplored terrain that we had remaining in our solar system .	這些是土衛二和土衛二 。 土衛六是土星最大的衛星 , 直到卡西尼抵達那裡 , 是我們太陽系中最大的一個未被探索的地形 。
and it is a body that has long intrigued people who've watched the planets .	這個身體有著很長的好奇心 , 看過這個星球的人 。
it has a very large , thick atmosphere , and in fact , its surface environment was believed to be more like the environment we have here on the earth , or at least had in the past , than any other body in the solar system .	它的大氣層非常厚 , 事實上 , 它的表面環境被認為比較像我們在地球上所擁有的環境 , 或至少在過去 , 比太陽系中任何其他的身體都更像 。
its atmosphere is largely molecular nitrogen , like you are breathing here in this room , except that its atmosphere is suffused with simple organic materials like methane and propane and ethane .	它的大氣是大氣中的分子氮 , 就像你在這個房間裡呼吸一樣 , 除了它的大氣中有機物質 , 像是甲烷、丙烷和乙烷 。
and these molecules high up in the atmosphere of titan get broken down , and their products join together to make haze particles .	這些分子在泰坦的大氣層中高度被破壞 , 它們的產品結合在一起 , 製造了 「 駭 」 粒子 。
this haze is ubiquitous . it's completely global and enveloping titan .	這種帽子無所不在 , 完全是全球性的 , 包含了土衛六 。
and that's why you cannot see down to the surface with our eyes in the visible region of the spectrum .	這也是為什麼你看不見我們眼睛的表面 , 在可見的光譜範圍內 。
but these haze particles , it was surmised , before we got there with cassini , over billions and billions of years , gently drifted down to the surface and coated the surface in a thick organic sludge .	但在我們和卡西尼來到那裡之前 , 已經有數十億年了 , 溫和地面覆蓋了表面 , 以厚厚的有機水泥覆蓋了表面 。
so like the equivalent , the titan equivalent , of tar , or oil , or what we didn't know what .	如同土衛六、油、石油等同於我們不知道的
but this is what we suspected . and these molecules , especially methane and ethane , can be liquids at the surface temperatures of titan .	但這是我們懷疑的 。 這些分子 , 尤其是甲烷和乙烷 , 在泰坦的表面溫度下 , 可能是液體 。
and so it turns out that methane is to titan what water is to the earth .	結果發現 , 甲烷就是土衛六 , 水對地球來說是什麼 。
it's a condensable in the atmosphere , and so recognizing this circumstance brought to the fore a whole world of bizarre possibilities . you can have methane clouds , ok , and above those clouds , you have this hundreds of kilometers of haze , which prevent any sunlight from getting to the surface .	它在大氣中是可容忍的 , 所以意識到這種狀況 , 導致整個怪異的可能性世界 。 你可以有甲烷雲 , 在那些雲層之上 , 你有數百公里的洞 , 防止陽光到達地表 。
the temperature at the surface is some 350 degrees below zero fahrenheit .	表面的溫度低於華氏零度的350度 。
but despite that cold , you could have rain falling down on the surface of titan .	儘管如此寒冷 , 你還是可以在泰坦的表面下降雨 。
and doing on titan what rain does on the earth: it carves gullies ; it forms rivers and cataracts ; it can create canyons ; it can pool in large basins and craters .	在土衛二上所做的:它雕刻了水道 , 形成了河流和洞穴 ; 它可以創造峽谷 ; 它可以在大盆地和坑洞中池塘 。
it can wash the sludge off high mountain peaks and hills , down into the lowlands . so stop and think for a minute .	它可以洗掉高山峰和山丘 , 進入低地 。 停下來 , 思考一下 。
try to imagine what the surface of titan might look like .	試著想像土衛六的表面看起來是什麼樣子 。
it's dark . high noon on titan is as dark as deep earth twilight on the earth .	它是黑暗的 , 鐵達尼號的高度和地球深海一樣黑暗 。
it's cold , it's eerie , it's misty , it might be raining , and you might be standing on the shores of lake michigan brimming with paint thinner .	它很冷 , 很爛 , 很糟糕 , 可能是下雨 , 你可能會站在密西根湖邊的密西根湖邊 , 用油漆刷刷 。
that is the view that we had of the surface of titan before we got there with cassini , and i can tell you that what we have found on titan , though it is not the same in detail , is every bit as fascinating as that story is .	這是我們在和卡西尼去到那裡之前的土衛六表面 , 我可以告訴你 , 我們在土衛六所發現的 , 雖然它的細節不一樣 , 和那個故事一樣迷人 。
and for us , it has been like the cassini people it has been like a jules verne adventure come true .	對我們來說 , 這就像是卡西尼人一樣 , 曾經是青少年的冒險 。
as i said , it has a thick , extensive atmosphere .	如我所說 , 它有很厚的大氣層 。
this is a picture of titan , backlit by the sun , with the rings as a beautiful backdrop .	這是一張泰坦的背景 , 背面是太陽 , 光環是美麗的背景 。
and yet another moon there i don't even know which one it is . it's a very extensive atmosphere .	另外一個月球 , 我甚至不知道它是哪一個 。 它是非常廣泛的大氣層 。
we have instruments on cassini which can see down to the surface through this atmosphere , and my camera system is one of them .	我們有卡西尼號的儀器可以透過大氣層看到表面 , 我的攝影機系統是其中之一 。
and we have taken pictures like this .	我們拍了像這樣的照片 。
and what you see is bright and dark regions , and that's about as far as it got for us .	而你所看到的是明亮又暗的區域 , 就跟我們所看到的一樣 。
it was so mystifying: we couldn't make out what we were seeing on titan .	這太神秘了:我們無法在泰坦看到什麼 。
when you look closer at this region , you start to see things like sinuous channels we didn't know . you see a few round things .	當你仔細看這個區域 , 你就會開始看到像我們所不知道的一連串頻道 。 你可以看到一些圓形的東西 。
this , we later found out , is , in fact , a crater , but there are very few craters on the surface of titan , meaning it's a very young surface .	後來我們發現 , 事實上 , 一個坑洞 , 但土衛六表面有很少的坑坑 , 意思是它是很年輕的表面 。
and there are features that look tectonic .	有些特徵看起來很像地形 。
they look like they've been pulled apart .	看起來他們被拉開了 。
whenever you see anything linear on a planet , it means there's been a fracture , like a fault .	每當你在星球上看到任何線性時 , 它就意味著有一種裂痕 , 像個錯 。
and so it's been tectonically altered .	所以它已經在線性上改變了 。
but we couldn't make sense of our images , until , six months after we got into orbit , an event occurred that many have regarded as the highlight of cassini's investigation of titan .	但我們無法理解我們的影像 , 直到我們進入軌道六個月後 , 一個事件發生了 , 許多人已經被視為是卡西尼對泰坦的調查 。
and that was the deployment of the huygens probe , the europeanbuilt huygens probe that cassini had carried for seven years across the solar system . we deployed it to the atmosphere of titan , it took two and a half hours to descend , and it landed on the surface .	那個就是蜂巢探測器的部署 , 歐洲建造的蜂箱 , 卡西尼號在太陽系的七年間運送了它 。 我們將它部署到泰坦的大氣層 , 花了兩個半小時的時間在下降 , 然後它落在地表上 。
and i just want to emphasize how significant an event this is .	我想強調一下這個事件有多重要 。
this is a device of human making , and it landed in the outer solar system for the first time in human history .	這是人類製造的裝置 , 它是人類史上第一次登陸的太陽系 。
it is so significant that , in my mind , this was an event that should have been celebrated with ticker tape parades in every city across the u . s . and europe , and sadly , that wasn't the case .	在我腦海中 , 這件事實在太重要了 , 在美國和歐洲和歐洲的每個城市 , 都應該要慶祝 , 不幸的是 , 這並非如此 。
it was significant for another reason . this is an international mission , and this event was celebrated in europe , in germany , and the celebratory presentations were given in english accents , and american accents , and german accents , and french and italian and dutch accents .	這是另一個原因 。 這是國際使命 , 這個事件在歐洲、德國、慶祝的 , 和慶祝的簡報在英國、美國口音、德國口音、法語、義大利語、義大利語、荷蘭語和荷蘭口音 。
it was a moving demonstration of what the words " united nations " are supposed to mean: a true union of nations joined together in a colossal effort for good .	它是一個動人的演示 , 說明了 「 聯合國 」 這個詞的真正意義:一個真正的聚會 , 團結在一個好的努力中 。
and , in this case , it was a massive undertaking to explore a planet , and to come to understand a planetary system that , for all of human history , had been unreachable , and now humans had actually touched it .	在這個案例中 , 要探索一個星球 , 要了解一個行星的行星系統 , 對於所有人類歷史來說 , 都難以置信 , 現在人類已經碰到它了 。
so it was i mean , i'm getting goose bumps just talking about it .	所以 , 我的意思是 , 我只是在談它 。
it was a tremendously emotional event , and it's something that i will personally never forget , and you shouldn't either .	那是個極大的情緒事件 , 我個人永遠不會忘記 , 而你也不該忘記 。
but anyway , the probe took measurements of the atmosphere on the way down , and it also took panoramic pictures .	但總之 , 探測器在降低大氣層的測量結果也拍了全景照片 。
and i can't tell you what it was like to see the first pictures of titan's surface from the probe . and this is what we saw .	我不能告訴你們 , 第一次從探測器看到泰坦的表面是什麼樣子 。 這是我們所看到的 。
and it was a shocker , because it was everything we wanted those other pictures taken from orbit to be .	這是個令人震驚的事件 , 因為我們希望這些照片從軌道上拍下的 。
it was an unambiguous pattern , a geological pattern .	它是個不可思議的模式 , 一個地質的模式 。
it's a dendritic drainage pattern that can be formed only by the flow of liquids .	這種傾斜的排水模式只能透過液體流來形成 。
and you can follow these channels and you can see how they all converge .	你可以跟著這些管道 , 你可以看到它們是如何融合的 。
and they converge into this channel here , which drains into this region .	他們把這個管道轉換成這個區域 。
you are looking at a shoreline .	你正在看海岸線 。
was this a shoreline of fluids ? we didn't know .	這是流體的海岸線嗎 ? 我們不知道 。
but this is somewhat of a shoreline .	但這是一條海岸線 。
this picture is taken at 16 kilometers .	這張照片是在16公里拍的 。
this is the picture taken at eight kilometers , ok ? again , the shoreline .	這張照片拍攝於8公里 , 好嗎 ? 同樣的 , 海岸線 。
okay , now , 16 kilometers , eight kilometers this is roughly an airline altitude .	好 , 現在 , 16公里 , 8公里--這大概是一架飛機的高度 。
if you were going to take an airplane trip across the u . s . , you would be flying at these altitudes .	如果你要穿越美國的飛機 , 你會在這些高度飛行 。
so , this is the picture you would have at the window of titanian airlines as you fly across the surface of titan .	這張照片是你在鐵達尼亞航空的窗邊飛過泰坦海面時會看到的 。
and then finally , the probe came to rest on the surface , and i'm going to show you , ladies and gentlemen , the first picture ever taken from the surface of a moon in the outer solar system .	最後 , 探測器到了地表上 , 我要給你們看的是 , 女士們先生們 , 這是從外太陽系表面拍的第一張照片 。
and here is the horizon , ok ?	這是地平線 , 好嗎 ?
these are probably water ice pebbles , yes ?	這些可能是冰石 , 對嗎 ?
and obviously , it landed in one of these flat , dark regions and it didn't sink out of sight . so it wasn't fluid that we landed in .	很顯然 , 它落在一個平坦、黑暗的區域中 , 它並沒有從視線下沉 。 所以它不是我們降落的液體 。
what the probe came down in was basically the titan equivalent of a mud flat .	探測器的來源基本上等同於泥土的平面 。
this is an unconsolidated ground that is suffused with liquid methane .	這是一個沒有隔離的土地 , 被液態甲烷給淹沒了 。
and it's probably the case that this material has washed off the highlands of titan through these channels that we saw , and has drained over billions of years to fill in lowlying basins .	可能是這樣 , 這種材料已經從土衛六的高地上清洗掉了土衛六 , 經過我們看到的這些管道 , 已經耗盡了數十億年的時間 , 來填補低盆地 。
and that is what the huygens probe landed in .	而那就是赤裸的探測器所在的地方 。
but still , there was no sign in our images , or even in the huygens' images , of any large , open bodies of fluids .	但是 , 我們的影像中沒有任何跡象 , 甚至在huygens的影像中 , 任何大型、開放的液體 。
where were they ? it got even more puzzling when we found dunes .	牠們在哪裡 ? 當我們發現沙丘時 , 牠們會變得更困惑 。
ok , so this is our movie of the equatorial region of titan , showing these dunes . these are dunes that are 100 meters tall , separated by a few kilometers , and they go on for miles and miles and miles .	好 , 這是我們在titan的赤道區域的電影 , 顯示這些沙丘 。 這些是100公尺高的沙丘 , 分離了幾公里 , 數英里長 。
there's hundreds , up to a 1 , 000 or 1 , 200 miles of dunes .	有數百、一千或一百英里的沙丘 。
this is the saharan desert of titan .	這是泰坦的撒哈拉沙漠
it's obviously a place which is very dry , or you wouldn't get dunes .	很明顯地 , 這個地方很乾燥 , 或你沒辦法得到沙丘 。
so again , it got puzzling that there were no bodies of fluid , until finally , we saw lakes in the polar regions .	再一次 , 這讓人感到困惑 , 那時沒有液體 , 直到終於 , 我們在北極地區看到湖泊 。
and there is a lake scene in the south polar region of titan .	在titan南極有一個湖景 。
it's about the size of lake ontario .	大約是安大略湖的大小 。
and then , only a week and a half ago , we flew over the north pole of titan and found , again , we found a feature here the size of the caspian sea .	接著 , 半年前 , 我們飛越了泰坦北極 , 再次發現 , 我們發現一個特徵 , 大小和卡斯比亞海一樣大 。
so it seems that the liquids , for some reason we don't understand , or during at least this season , are apparently at the poles of titan .	所以 , 似乎液體 , 基於某些原因 , 至少在這個季節 , 很明顯地位在泰坦的北極 。
and i think you would agree that we have found titan is a remarkable , mystical place . it's exotic , it's alien , but yet strangely earthlike , and having earthlike geological formations and a tremendous geographical diversity , and is a fascinating world whose only rival in the solar system for complexity and richness is the earth itself .	我想你會認同我們已經發現土衛六是一個非常奇特、神秘的地方 。 它是外星人 , 但卻是很奇怪的地球形式 , 像地球一樣 , 地球有著巨大的地理多樣性 , 也是一個令人著迷的世界 , 一個在太陽系中只有複雜和豐富才是地球本身 。
and so now we go onto enceladus . enceladus is a small moon , it's about a tenth the size of titan . and you can see it here next to england , just to show you the size . this is not meant to be a threat .	現在我們來到土衛二 。 土衛二是一個小月 , 它的大小大約是土衛六的十分之一 。 你可以看到它旁邊的英格蘭 , 只是要給你看大小 。 這不是威脅 。
and enceladus is very white , it's very bright , and its surface is obviously wrecked with fractures .	土衛二是非常白的 , 它是非常明亮的 , 它的表面很明顯地破碎了 。
it is a very geologically active body .	它是非常地活躍的身體 。
but the mother lode of discoveries on enceladus was found at the south pole and we're looking at the south pole here where we found this system of fractures .	但在土衛二上的發現之母就在南極找到了 , 我們現在看到的是南極 , 我們發現了這個碎形系統 。
and they're a different color because they're a different composition .	它們是不同的顏色 , 因為它們是不同的組成 。
they are coated . these fractures are coated with organic materials .	它們是被覆蓋的 。 這些碎片是被有機材料覆蓋的 。
moreover , this whole , entire region , the south polar region , has elevated temperatures . it's the hottest place on the planet , on the body .	此外 , 整個南極地區 , 已經升高溫度 。 這是地球上最熱的地方 。
that's as bizarre as finding that the antarctic on the earth is hotter than the tropics .	這有點奇怪 , 發現地球上南極洲的溫度比熱帶地區熱帶的溫度更高 。
and then , when we took additional pictures , we discovered that from these fractures are issuing jets of fine , icy particles extending hundreds of miles into space .	接著 , 當我們拍了額外的照片 , 我們發現 , 從這些碎片中 , 正引發好的噴射機 , 冰粒將數百英里延伸到太空中 。
and when we colorcode this image , to bring out the faint light levels , we see that these jets feed a plume that , in fact , we see , in other images , goes thousands of miles into the space above enceladus .	當我們把這張影像編碼出來 , 把這些微弱的光線引出來 , 我們可以看到這些噴射機在其他圖片中 , 事實上 , 我們看到 , 在土衛二上千英里的太空中 。
my team and i have examined images like this , and like this one , and have thought about the other results from cassini .	我和我的團隊已經檢查過像這樣的影像 , 像這張 , 考慮了卡西尼的其他結果 。
and we have arrived at the conclusion that these jets may be erupting from pockets of liquid water under the surface of enceladus .	我們得出的結論是這些噴射機可能是從土衛二表面下的液態水中噴出來的 。
so we have , possibly , liquid water , organic materials and excess heat .	所以 , 我們有 , 可能是液態水、有機物質和過度熱能 。
in other words , we have possibly stumbled upon the holy grail of modern day planetary exploration , or in other words , an environment that is potentially suitable for living organisms .	換句話說 , 我們可能偶然發現了現代行星探索的聖杯 , 或者 , 換句話說 , 一個適合生物的環境 。
and i don't think i need to tell you that the discovery of life elsewhere in our solar system , whether it be on enceladus or elsewhere , would have enormous cultural and scientific implications .	我不認為我需要告訴你們 , 在太陽系中其他地方發現了生命 , 不論是在土衛二或其他地方 , 都會有巨大的文化和科學上的影響 。
because if we could demonstrate that genesis had occurred not once , but twice , independently , in our solar system , then that means , by inference , it has occurred a staggering number of times throughout the universe and its 13 . 7 billion year history .	因為如果我們能夠證明 , 不只一次 , 而是在我們的太陽系獨立的兩倍 , 那就意味著 , 基礎上 , 它在宇宙中發生了驚人的數量 , 且它的歷史有十三十七億年 。
right now , earth is the only planet still that we know is teeming with life .	現在 , 地球是唯一一個我們所知是充滿生命的行星 。
it is precious , it is unique , it is still , so far , the only home we've ever known .	它是珍貴的 , 它是獨一無二的 , 到目前為止 , 只有我們所知唯一的家 。
and if any of you were alert and coherent during the 1960s and we'd forgive you , if you weren't , ok you would remember this very famous picture taken by the apollo 8 astronauts in 1968 .	如果你們當中有人在1960年代和1960年代的警告和協調 , 我們會原諒你們 , 如果你不是 , 那你會記得1968年阿波羅8號太空人拍的這張著名的照片 。
it was the first time that earth was imaged from space , and it had an enormous impact on our sense of place in the universe , and our sense of responsibility for the protection of our own planet .	這是第一次 , 地球是來自太空的影像 , 它對我們在宇宙中的位置有著巨大的影響 , 我們對於保護地球的責任感有著巨大的影響 。
well , we on cassini have taken an equivalent first , a picture that no human eye has ever seen before .	嗯 , 我們在卡西尼拍了一張相同的第一張照片 , 一張前所未見的人類眼睛 。
it is a total eclipse of the sun , seen from the other side of saturn .	它是太陽的完整日蝕 , 從土星的另一側看到 。
and in this impossibly beautiful picture , you see the main rings backlit by the sun , you see the refracted image of the sun and you see this ring created , in fact , by the exhalations of enceladus .	在這張不可思議的美麗照片中 , 你可以看到太陽的主要環狀物 , 你可以看到太陽的折射影像 , 你可以看到這個環 , 事實上 , 由土衛二的排除 。
but as if that weren't brilliant enough , we can spot , in this beautiful image , sight of our own planet , cradled in the arms of saturn's rings .	但如果這還不夠聰明 , 我們可以在這個美麗的圖像中看到我們星球的景象 , 在土星的環中爬行 。
now , there is something deeply moving about seeing ourselves from afar , and capturing the sight of our little , blueocean planet in the skies of other worlds .	現在 , 深深地看待我們自己從遠處移動 , 捕捉我們在其他世界的藍綠色星球的視野 。
and that , and the perspective of ourselves that we gain from that , may be , in the end , the finest reward that we earn from this journey of discovery that started half a century ago .	這樣 , 和我們從中得到的觀點 , 可能是 , 最終 , 我們從這個發現的旅程中得到最好的獎賞 , 從半個世紀開始 。
as of 2005 , only 15 percent of the world was mapped . this slows the delivery of aid after a disaster and hides the economic potential of unused lands and unknown roads . in this short talk , google's lalitesh katragadda demos map maker , a group mapmaking tool that people around the globe are using to map their world .	在2005年 , 只有15%的世界被繪製了 。 這個緩慢的援助 , 在災難之後 , 隱藏了無用的土地和未知的道路 。 在這個短短的演講中 , google的拉利特•卡特拉特•德達德莫斯地圖 , 一個團體的地圖工具 , 全世界的人都在用繪製他們的世界地圖 。
collaboration , design , map , technology	合作、設計、地圖、科技、科技、科技、
lalitesh katragadda: making maps to fight disaster , build economies	拉利特•卡拉特達:創造出對抗災難的地圖 , 建立經濟體 。
in 2008 , cyclone nargis devastated myanmar .	2008年 , 颶風納吉斯摧毀了緬甸 。
millions of people were in severe need of help .	數百萬人急需幫忙 。
the u . n . wanted to rush people and supplies to the area .	聯合國想要趕人並供應給這個區域 。
but there were no maps , no maps of roads , no maps showing hospitals , no way for help to reach the cyclone victims .	但沒有地圖 , 沒有道路的地圖 , 沒有顯示醫院的地圖 , 無法幫助到周邊的受害者 。
when we look at a map of los angeles or london , it is hard to believe that as of 2005 , only 15 percent of the world was mapped to a geocodable level of detail .	當我們看洛杉磯或倫敦的地圖時 , 很難相信 , 在2005年 , 世界上只有15%的人口被繪製成地理的細節 。
the u . n . ran headfirst into a problem that the majority of the world's populous faces: not having detailed maps .	聯合國執行一個問題 , 讓世界上大部分的民眾面孔都能解決:沒有詳細的地圖 。
but help was coming .	但幫助即將來臨 。
at google , 40 volunteers used a new software to map 120 , 000 kilometers of roads , 3 , 000 hospitals , logistics and relief points .	在google , 40個志工用了新軟體來繪製十二萬公里的道路 , 三千間醫院、物流和鬆散點 。
and it took them four days .	他們花了四天的時間 。
the new software they used ? google mapmaker .	他們使用的新軟體 ? google地圖製造商 。
google mapmaker is a technology that empowers each of us to map what we know locally .	谷歌地圖製造者是一項技術 , 讓我們每個人都能夠繪製我們所知的地圖 。
people have used this software to map everything from roads to rivers , from schools to local businesses , and video stores to the corner store .	人們用這個軟體來繪製所有東西 , 從道路到河流 , 從學校到當地企業 , 影片店到角落商店 。
nobel prize nominee hernando de soto recognized that the key to economic liftoff for most developing countries is to tap the vast amounts of uncapitalized land .	諾貝爾獎提名henandodes意識到 , 對大部分發展中國家經濟利益的關鍵是要處理大量未受影響的土地 。
for example , a trillion dollars of real estate remains uncapitalized in india alone .	例如 , 僅僅在印度 , 一兆美金的房地產仍未被監禁 。
in the last year alone , thousands of users in 170 countries have mapped millions of pieces of information , and created a map of a level of detail never thought viable .	光在去年 , 就有數以千計的使用者在170個國家已經繪製了數百萬個資訊的地圖 , 創造出了一層不可思議的細節 。
and this was made possible by the power of passionate users everywhere .	這使得世界各地充滿熱情使用者的力量 。
let's look at some of the maps being created by users right now .	咱們來看看目前使用者所創造的一些地圖 。
so , as we speak , people are mapping the world in these 170 countries .	所以 , 如同我們所說 , 在170個國家 , 人們正在繪製這個世界 。
you can see bridget in africa who just mapped a road in senegal .	你可以看到在非洲的橋樑 , 在塞內加爾剛繪製了一條道路 。
and , closer to home , chalua , an n . g . road in bangalore .	靠近家鄉 , 夏盧亞 , 班加羅爾的公路 。
this is the result of computational geometry , gesture recognition , and machine learning .	這是計算幾何、手勢識別、機器學習的結果 。
this is a victory of thousands of users , in hundreds of cities , one user , one edit at a time .	這是數以千計的使用者的勝利 , 在數百個城市中 , 一個使用者 , 一個編輯 。
this is an invitation to the 70 percent of our unmapped planet .	這是一個邀請給我們未開發的地球70%的全球70% 。
welcome to the new world .	歡迎來到新世界 。
in 2003 , the palestinian village of budrus mounted a 10monthlong nonviolent protest to stop a barrier being built across their olive groves . did you hear about it ? didn't think so . brazilian filmmaker julia bacha asks why we only pay attention to violence in the israelpalestine conflict and not to the nonviolent leaders who may one day bring peace .	在2003年 , 巴勒斯坦村落的布德魯斯登上了十個月的非暴力抗爭 , 來阻止他們橫跨他們的橄欖球 。 你們有聽過嗎 ? 布拉西尼亞的製片人茱莉亞.巴希問:為什麼我們只關注在以色列巴勒斯坦衝突中 , 而非暴力領袖有一天可能會帶來和平 。
arts , communication , compassion , entertainment , film , peace , violence , war	藝術、溝通、同情、娛樂、電影、和平、暴力、戰爭、戰爭、戰爭、戰爭、戰爭、戰爭、戰爭、戰爭、戰爭、
julia bacha: pay attention to nonviolence	juliabacha:請注意非暴力事件 。
for the last 8 years , i have dedicated my life to documenting the work of israelis and palestinians who are trying to end the conflict using peaceful means .	過去八年 , 我致力於記錄以色列和巴勒斯坦人的作品 , 他們試圖用和平的手段來結束衝突 。
when i travel with my work across europe and the united states , one question always comes up: where is the palestinian gandhi ?	當我在歐洲和美國旅行時 , 有一個問題總是出現:巴勒斯坦甘地在哪裡 ?
why aren't palestinians using nonviolent resistance ?	為什麼巴勒斯坦人不用非暴力抗爭 ?
the challenge i face when i hear this question is that often i have just returned from the middle east where i spent my time filming dozens of palestinians who are using nonviolence to defend their lands and water resources from israeli soldiers and settlers .	當我聽到這個問題時 , 我面臨的挑戰是 , 我常常從中東回來 , 在那裡 , 我花了很多時間拍攝數十位巴勒斯坦人 , 他們用非暴力的方式來保護他們的土地和水資源 , 來自以色列士兵和移民者 。
these leaders are trying to forge a massive national nonviolent movement to end the occupation and build peace in the region .	這些領導人試圖去維護一個巨大的國家非暴力運動 , 來終止這個地區的職業 , 並建立和平 。
yet , most of you have probably never heard about them .	然而 , 你們大多數人可能從來沒有聽過他們 。
this divide between what's happening on the ground and perceptions abroad is one of the key reasons why we don't have yet a palestinian peaceful resistance movement that has been successful .	這種分歧在國外發生和感知之間的差異 , 是我們尚未有的巴勒斯坦和平抗爭運動的關鍵原因之一 。
so i'm here today to talk about the power of attention , the power of your attention , and the emergence and development of nonviolent movements in the west bank , gaza and elsewhere but today , my case study is going to be palestine .	所以我今天要來談談注意力的力量 , 關注的力量 , 以及在西岸、加薩和其他地方的非暴力運動的出現和發展 , 但今天 , 我的案例研究將成為巴勒斯坦 。
i believe that what's mostly missing for nonviolence to grow is not for palestinians to start adopting nonviolence , but for us to start paying attention to those who already are .	我相信 , 最缺乏非暴力的行為 , 不是要讓巴勒斯坦人開始採用非暴力行為 , 而是要我們開始注意那些已經有的人 。
allow me to illustrate this point by taking you to this village called budrus .	讓我來說明一下這個點 , 帶你到一個叫做布德鲁斯村的村子 。
about seven years ago , they faced extinction , because israel announced it would build a separation barrier , and part of this barrier would be built on top of the village .	大約七年前 , 他們面臨絕種 , 因為以色列宣布要建立一個獨立的障礙 , 而這個障礙的一部分會在村落上建成 。
they would lose 40 percent of their land and be surrounded , so they would lose free access to the rest of the west bank .	他們會失去40%的土地 , 被包圍住 , 所以他們會失去西岸其他地方的取得權 。
through inspired local leadership , they launched a peaceful resistance campaign to stop that from happening .	透過當地的領導力 , 他們發起了和平的抗爭活動 , 阻止這一切發生 。
let me show you some brief clips , so you have a sense for what that actually looked like on the ground .	讓我給你們看一段短片 , 你對地面上看起來是什麼樣子 。
palestinian woman: we were told the wall would separate palestine from israel .	巴勒斯坦女人:我們被告知牆會和以色列隔離巴勒斯坦 。
here in budrus , we realized the wall would steal our land .	在布德魯斯 , 我們發現牆會偷我們的土地 。
israeli man: the fence has , in fact , created a solution to terror .	以色列男人:圍籬事實上 , 造成了恐怖的解決方案 。
man: today you're invited to a peaceful march .	男子:今天你被邀請到一個和平的遊行 。
you are joined by dozens of your israeli brothers and sisters .	你被幾十位以色列兄弟和姊妹團結 。
israeli activist: nothing scares the army more than nonviolent opposition .	以色列的行動主義者:軍隊比非暴力反對更害怕 。
woman: we saw the men trying to push the soldiers , but none of them could do that .	女子:我們看到男人試圖推進士兵 , 但沒有人能做到 。
but i think the girls could do it .	但我認為女孩們可以做到 。
fatah party member: we must empty our minds of traditional thinking .	法塔赫派對成員:我們必須忽視傳統思維的思想 。
hamas party member: we were in complete harmony , and we wanted to spread it to all of palestine .	哈馬斯派對成員:我們完全和諧 , 我們想要把它傳播給所有巴勒斯坦 。
chanting: one united nation .	查理:一個聯合國 。
fatah , hamas and the popular front !	法塔 , 哈馬斯和大眾的前線 !
news anchor: the clashes over the fence continue .	新聞主持人:圍籬的關節持續下去 。
reporter: israeli border police were sent to disperse the crowd .	記者:以色列邊界警察被派去分散群眾 。
they were allowed to use any force necessary .	他們被允許使用任何必要的力量 。
man: these are live bullets .	男子:這些是現場的子彈 。
it's like fallujah . shooting everywhere .	這就好像摔角了 。 射擊到處都是 。
israeli activist: i was sure we were all going to die .	以色列的行動主義者:我相信我們都會死 。
but there were others around me who weren't even cowering .	但在我身邊有一些人 , 甚至還沒做牛仔 。
israeli soldier: a nonviolent protest is not going to stop the [unclear] .	以色列的士兵:非暴力抗爭不會阻止他們 。
protester: this is a peaceful march .	普斯特:這是一個和平的遊行 。
there is no need to use violence .	不需要使用暴力 。
chanting: we can do it ! we can do it !	查爾斯:我們能做到 ! 我們能做到 !
julia bacha: when i first heard about the story of budrus , i was surprised that the international media had failed to cover the extraordinary set of events that happened seven years ago , in 2003 .	朱莉亞.巴哈:當我第一次聽到布德魯斯的故事時 , 我感到驚訝 , 國際媒體沒有報導發生在七年前的非凡事件 。
what was even more surprising was the fact that budrus was successful .	更令人驚訝的是布德魯斯成功的事實 。
the residents , after 10 months of peaceful resistance , convinced the israeli government to move the route of the barrier off their lands and to the green line , which is the internationally recognized boundary between israel and the palestinian territories .	居民 , 十個月的和平抗爭之後 , 說服了以色列政府將他們的土地的路線移到綠線 , 也就是國際認可了以色列和巴勒斯坦領土之間的界線 。
the resistance in budrus has since spread to villages across the west bank and to palestinian neighborhoods in jerusalem .	布德魯斯的抗爭從此傳播到西岸的村落以及耶路撒冷的巴勒斯坦社區 。
yet the media remains mostly silent on these stories .	但媒體仍然沉默在這些故事上 。
this silence carries profound consequences for the likelihood that nonviolence can grow , or even survive , in palestine .	這種沉默帶著深刻的後果 , 導致非暴力的可能性成長 , 甚至在巴勒斯坦生存 。
violent resistance and nonviolent resistance share one very important thing in common ; they are both a form of theater seeking an audience to their cause .	暴力抗爭和非暴力抗爭有一項非常重要的共通點 ; 它們都是一種形式的劇場 , 尋求觀眾的成因 。
if violent actors are the only ones constantly getting frontpage covers and attracting international attention to the palestinian issue , it becomes very hard for nonviolent leaders to make the case to their communities that civil disobedience is a viable option in addressing their plight .	如果暴力演員是唯一的封面 , 並且吸引國際的關注在巴勒斯坦議題上 , 對非暴力的領導者來說 , 要讓公民不服從是可行的選項 。
the power of attention is probably going to come as no surprise to the parents in the room .	注意力的力量可能對在座的父母而言是毫無意外的 。
the surest way to make your child throw increasingly louder tantrums is by giving him attention the first time he throws a fit .	要讓你的孩子更加明顯地發出聲響的確是讓他注意到他第一次投入一個音符 。
the tantrum will become what childhood psychologists call a functional behavior , since the child has learned that he can get parental attention out of it .	蟻群會變成童年心理學家所謂的功能性行為 , 因為孩子們已經學會了他能從中獲得父母的注意力 。
parents can incentivize or disincentivize behavior simply by giving or withdrawing attention to their children .	父母可以透過給予孩童的注意力來鼓勵或忽視行為 。
but that's true for adults too .	但對成年人也是如此 。
in fact , the behavior of entire communities and countries can be influenced , depending on where the international community chooses to focus its attention .	事實上 , 整個社區和國家的行為會受到影響 , 根據國際社會選擇集中注意力的位置 。
i believe that at the core of ending the conflict in the middle east and bringing peace is for us to transform nonviolence into a functional behavior by giving a lot more attention to the nonviolent leaders on the ground today .	我相信 , 終結中東衝突的核心 , 帶來和平 , 是我們要把非暴力的非暴力行為轉變成功能性行為 , 讓更多關注在現今的非暴力領袖 。
in the course of taking my film to villages in the west bank , in gaza and in east jerusalem , i have seen the impact that even one documentary film can have in influencing the transformation .	在加薩和東耶路撒冷的村子裡 , 我已經看過一部紀錄片能影響到轉變的影響 。
in a village called wallajeh , which sits very close to jerusalem , the community was facing a very similar plight to budrus .	在一個叫華拉傑的村落 , 離耶路撒冷很近 , 社區正面臨著一個與布德魯斯非常相似的困境 。
they were going to be surrounded , lose a lot of their lands and not have freedom of access , either to the west bank or jerusalem .	他們會被包圍 , 失去很多土地 , 沒有取得自由 , 不論是西岸或耶路撒冷 。
they had been using nonviolence for about two years but had grown disenchanted since nobody was paying attention .	兩年來 , 他們一直在使用非暴力 , 但自從沒有人在注意力時 , 一直都很不滿意 。
so we organized a screening .	所以我們組織了一場屏幕 。
a week later , they held the most wellattended and disciplined demonstration to date .	一個禮拜後 , 他們舉辦了最好且最專業的示範 。
the organizers say that the villagers , upon seeing the story of budrus documented in a film , felt that there were indeed people following what they were doing , that people cared .	組織者說 , 村民們 , 看到布德魯斯的故事在電影中被記錄下來 , 覺得有一些人在追蹤他們在做什麼 , 人們在關心 。
so they kept on going .	所以他們繼續前進 。
on the israeli side , there is a new peace movement called solidariot , which means solidarity in hebrew .	在以色列 , 有一個新的和平運動 , 叫做索麗達里特 , 意思是希伯來語的團結 。
the leaders of this movement have been using budrus as one of their primary recruiting tools .	這項運動的領導人 , 已經把布德魯斯當作他們主要的招募工具之一 。
they report that israelis who had never been active before , upon seeing the film , understand the power of nonviolence and start joining their activities .	他們報告以色列從來沒有活躍過 , 看過電影 , 了解非暴力的力量 , 並開始加入他們的活動 。
the examples of wallajeh and the solidariot movement show that even a smallbudget independent film can play a role in transforming nonviolence into a functional behavior .	瓦拉賈和索利德運動的例子顯示 , 即使是一部小型的獨立電影也能扮演一個角色 , 將非暴力變成功能性行為 。
now imagine the power that big media players could have if they started covering the weekly nonviolent demonstrations happening in villages like bil'in , ni'lin , wallajeh , in jerusalem neighborhoods like sheikh jarrah and silwan the nonviolent leaders would become more visible , valued and effective in their work .	想像一下 , 大型媒體播放者的力量 , 如果他們開始報導每週的非暴力行為 , 發生在村落裡 , 像是bil'in、nin、rajeh、jeh、耶路撒冷的社區 , 像sikhjarrah和silwan這樣的非暴力領導人 , 會變得更明顯、更有價值、更有效率 。
i believe that the most important thing is to understand that if we don't pay attention to these efforts , they are invisible , and it's as if they never happened .	我相信最重要的是要了解如果我們不注意這些努力 , 它們是隱形的 , 就好像它們從來沒有發生過一樣 。
but i have seen first hand that if we do , they will multiply .	但是如果我們這樣做 , 他們就會倍增 。
if they multiply , their influence will grow in the overall israelipalestinian conflict .	如果他們倍增 , 他們的影響會在以色列巴勒斯坦的衝突中成長 。
and theirs is the kind of influence that can finally unblock the situation .	他們的影響力終於可以解開這個情況 。
these leaders have proven that nonviolence works in places like budrus .	這些領導人證明 , 非暴力在像布德魯斯這樣的地方有用 。
let's give them attention so they can prove it works everywhere .	讓我們給他們注意 , 這樣他們就能證明它無所不在 。
simon sinek has a simple but powerful model for inspirational leadership all starting with a golden circle and the question " why ? " his examples include apple , martin luther king , and the wright brothers . . .	西蒙•海克有一個簡單但有力的模型 , 能鼓舞人心的領導力 , 始於黃金圓圈 , 問題是 「 為什麼 ? 」 他的例子包括蘋果、馬丁路德金 , 以及萊特兄弟......
bullseye , business , entrepreneur , leadership , sales , selling , success	bullsee、商業、企業家、領導力、銷售、販售、成功、成功、成功、企業家、領導力、銷售、銷售、販售、成功、成功、成功、企業家、企業家、領導力、
simon sinek: how great leaders inspire action	西蒙.海克:偉大的領袖鼓舞了行動 。
how do you explain when things don't go as we assume ?	你要如何解釋當事情不如我們所想時 ?
or better , how do you explain when others are able to achieve things that seem to defy all of the assumptions ?	或者 , 更好 , 如何解釋 , 當他人能夠做到似乎違背所有假設時 , 你要如何解釋 ?
for example: why is apple so innovative ?	例如:為什麼蘋果如此創新 ?
year after year , after year , after year , they're more innovative than all their competition .	年復一年 , 年復一年 , 他們比他們所有的競爭都更有創意 。
and yet , they're just a computer company .	然而 , 他們只是一家電腦公司 。
they're just like everyone else .	他們和其他人一樣 。
they have the same access to the same talent , the same agencies , the same consultants , the same media .	他們擁有相同的人才 , 相同的機構 , 相同的顧問 , 相同的媒體 。
then why is it that they seem to have something different ?	為何他們看起來有所不同 ?
why is it that martin luther king led the civil rights movement ?	為什麼馬丁•路德•金恩帶領民權運動 ?
he wasn't the only man who suffered in a precivil rights america , and he certainly wasn't the only great orator of the day .	他不是唯一一個在美國受苦的人 , 他肯定不是當代最偉大的演說家 。
and why is it that the wright brothers were able to figure out controlled , powered man flight when there were certainly other teams who were better qualified , better funded . . .	為何萊特兄弟能夠找出控制權力的人飛行 , 尤其是其他更有資格、更好的資金的團隊 。
and they didn't achieve powered man flight , and the wright brothers beat them to it .	他們沒有達到人類飛行的動力 , 萊特兄弟打敗他們 。
there's something else at play here .	這裡還有別的東西 。
about three and a half years ago i made a discovery .	大約三年半前 , 我發現了一項發現 。
and this discovery profoundly changed my view on how i thought the world worked , and it even profoundly changed the way in which i operate in it .	這個發現深深地改變了我的觀點我認為這個世界是如何運作的 , 甚至深深地改變了我在其中運作的方式 。
as it turns out , there's a pattern .	結果發現 , 有一個模式 。
as it turns out , all the great and inspiring leaders and organizations in the world whether it's apple or martin luther king or the wright brothers they all think , act and communicate the exact same way .	結果發現 , 世界上所有偉大、鼓舞人心的領導人和組織 , 無論是蘋果、馬丁路德金恩 , 或萊特兄弟 , 他們都認為 , 行為和溝通方式都一樣 。
and it's the complete opposite to everyone else .	和其他人完全相反 。
all i did was codify it , and it's probably the world's simplest idea .	我所做的只是編寫它 , 可能是世界上最簡單的點子 。
i call it the golden circle .	我稱之為黃金圓圈 。
why ? how ? what ?	為什麼 ? 什麼 ?
this little idea explains why some organizations and some leaders are able to inspire where others aren't .	這個小小的點子解釋了為什麼有些組織和一些領導人能夠鼓舞其他人不在哪裡 。
let me define the terms really quickly .	讓我很快地定義這個詞 。
every single person , every single organization on the planet knows what they do , 100 percent .	每個人 , 地球上的每一個組織都知道他們在做什麼 , 百分之百 。
some know how they do it , whether you call it your differentiated value proposition or your proprietary process or your usp .	有些人知道他們是如何做到的 , 不論你稱它為你不同的價值觀 , 或你的財產流程 , 或你的usp 。
but very , very few people or organizations know why they do what they do .	但很少人或組織知道他們怎麼做 。
and by " why " i don't mean " to make a profit . "	意思是 「 為什麼 」 不是 「 創造利潤 」 。
that's a result . it's always a result .	這是結果 。 結果總是結果 。
by " why , " i mean: what's your purpose ?	「 為什麼 」 我的意思是:你的目的是什麼 ?
what's your cause ? what's your belief ?	你的成因是什麼 ? 你的信念是什麼 ?
why does your organization exist ?	你的組織為什麼存在 ?
why do you get out of bed in the morning ?	為什麼你早上出床 ?
and why should anyone care ?	為何有人要在乎 ?
well , as a result , the way we think , the way we act , the way we communicate is from the outside in .	結果就是 , 我們思考的方式 , 我們溝通的方式是來自外界的 。
it's obvious . we go from the clearest thing to the fuzziest thing .	很明顯的 , 我們從最明顯的事物轉變成最模糊的事物 。
but the inspired leaders and the inspired organizations regardless of their size , regardless of their industry all think , act and communicate from the inside out .	但鼓舞人心的領導人和激勵人心的組織 , 不管他們的大小 , 不管他們的產業都認為 , 行為和溝通都來自內部 。
let me give you an example .	讓我舉個例子 。
i use apple because they're easy to understand and everybody gets it .	我用蘋果是因為他們很容易理解 , 每個人都懂 。
if apple were like everyone else , a marketing message from them might sound like this: " we make great computers .	如果蘋果和其他人一樣 , 他們的行銷訊息可能聽起來像這樣: 「 我們會製造出很棒的電腦 。
they're beautifully designed , simple to use and user friendly .	它們設計得很漂亮 , 很簡單 , 很容易使用 , 且很友善 。
want to buy one ? " " meh . "	想要買一台嗎 ? 」
and that's how most of us communicate .	那就是我們大多數人溝通的方式 。
that's how most marketing is done , that's how most sales is done and that's how most of us communicate interpersonally .	這就是大部分的行銷方式 , 大部分的銷售都是如此 , 那就是我們大多數人之間交流的方式 。
we say what we do , we say how we're different or how we're better and we expect some sort of a behavior , a purchase , a vote , something like that .	我們會說我們所做的事 , 我們會說我們有多不同 , 或如何做得更好 , 我們期待某種行為、購買、投票、類似的行為 。
here's our new law firm: we have the best lawyers with the biggest clients , we always perform for our clients who do business with us .	這是我們的新法律公司:我們有最好的律師和最大客戶 , 我們總是為和我們做生意的客戶表演 。
here's our new car: it gets great gas mileage , it has leather seats , buy our car .	這是我們的新車:它有很大的氣體 , 它有皮革座位 , 買我們的車 。
here's how apple actually communicates .	蘋果是如何溝通的 。
" everything we do , we believe in challenging the status quo .	「 我們所做的每件事 , 我們相信挑戰現狀 。
we believe in thinking differently .	我們相信不同的思考方式 。
the way we challenge the status quo is by making our products beautifully designed , simple to use and user friendly .	我們挑戰現狀的方式 , 是讓我們的產品精美地設計 , 簡單地使用和使用者 。
we just happen to make great computers .	我們剛好製造了很棒的電腦 。
want to buy one ? "	想要買一台嗎 ? 」
totally different right ? you're ready to buy a computer from me .	完全不一樣嗎 ? 你準備好要跟我買一台電腦 。
all i did was reverse the order of the information .	我所做的只是反轉資訊的順序 。
what it proves to us is that people don't buy what you do ; people buy why you do it .	它向我們證明了人們不買你做什麼 ; 人們買你為什麼去做 。
people don't buy what you do ; they buy why you do it .	人們不買你做什麼 ; 他們買你為什麼要做 。
this explains why every single person in this room is perfectly comfortable buying a computer from apple .	這解釋了為什麼在座的每一個人都很自在買蘋果電腦 。
but we're also perfectly comfortable buying an mp3 player from apple , or a phone from apple , or a dvr from apple .	但我們也非常自在地買蘋果電腦的mp3播放器 , 或蘋果電腦的手機 , 或蘋果電腦的dvr 。
but , as i said before , apple's just a computer company .	但 , 就像我之前說的 , 蘋果只是一家電腦公司 。
there's nothing that distinguishes them structurally from any of their competitors .	沒有任何東西可以從結構中分辨它們 , 不用任何競爭者 。
their competitors are all equally qualified to make all of these products .	他們的競爭者都同樣資格做出這些產品 。
in fact , they tried .	事實上 , 他們試了 。
a few years ago , gateway came out with flat screen tvs .	幾年前 , 高速公路出櫃了平面的電視機 。
they're eminently qualified to make flat screen tvs .	他們很有資格製作平面的電視 。
they've been making flat screen monitors for years .	數年來 , 他們一直在製作平面的螢幕螢幕 。
dell came out with mp3 players and pdas , and they make great quality products , and they can make perfectly welldesigned products and nobody bought one .	德魯爾走出了mp3播放器和pda , 他們製作了很棒的品質產品 , 他們可以做出完美的設計產品 , 沒有人買了 。
in fact , talking about it now , we can't even imagine buying an mp3 player from dell .	事實上 , 談到現在 , 我們甚至無法想像從德國購買mp3播放器 。
why would you buy an mp3 player from a computer company ?	你為什麼要從一家電腦公司買一台mp3播放器 ?
but we do it every day .	但我們每天都會這樣做 。
people don't buy what you do ; they buy why you do it .	人們不買你做什麼 ; 他們買你為什麼要做 。
the goal is not to do business with everybody who needs what you have .	目標不是要和需要你所需要的人做生意 。
the goal is to do business with people who believe what you believe .	目標是和那些相信你所相信的人做生意 。
here's the best part: none of what i'm telling you is my opinion .	最棒的部分是:我所說的 , 沒有一個是我的意見 。
it's all grounded in the tenets of biology .	一切都在生物的10%之內 。
not psychology , biology .	不是心理學 , 生物學 。
if you look at a crosssection of the human brain , looking from the top down , what you see is the human brain is actually broken into three major components that correlate perfectly with the golden circle .	如果你看一下人類大腦的交叉位置 , 從上方看 , 你看到的是人類的大腦實際上被分解成三個主要元件 , 與黃金圈完全相關 。
our newest brain , our homo sapien brain , our neocortex , corresponds with the " what " level .	我們最新的大腦 , 人類的大腦 , 我們的新皮層 , 與 「 等級 」 相對應 。
the neocortex is responsible for all of our rational and analytical thought and language .	新皮質負責我們所有的理性、分析性思維和語言 。
the middle two sections make up our limbic brains , and our limbic brains are responsible for all of our feelings , like trust and loyalty .	中間兩個部分組成了我們的腦 , 我們的邊緣大腦負責我們所有的感覺 , 像是信任和忠誠 。
it's also responsible for all human behavior , all decisionmaking , and it has no capacity for language .	它也負責所有人類的行為 , 所有的決策 , 沒有語言的能力 。
in other words , when we communicate from the outside in , yes , people can understand vast amounts of complicated information like features and benefits and facts and figures .	換句話說 , 當我們從外面溝通時 , 是的 , 人們可以了解很多複雜的資訊 , 比如特徵、利益、事實和數字 。
it just doesn't drive behavior .	它不會驅動行為 。
when we can communicate from the inside out , we're talking directly to the part of the brain that controls behavior , and then we allow people to rationalize it with the tangible things we say and do .	當我們能從內部向外溝通時 , 我們直接和控制行為的部分溝通 , 接著 , 我們就允許人們將之合理化為我們所說和做的事 。
this is where gut decisions come from .	這是腸道決策的來源 。
you know , sometimes you can give somebody all the facts and figures , and they say , " i know what all the facts and details say , but it just doesn't feel right . "	有時候你會給某人所有的事實和數字 , 他們會說: 「 我知道所有事實和細節會說什麼 , 但感覺不對 。 」
why would we use that verb , it doesn't " feel " right ?	為什麼我們要用那動詞 , 它不會 「 感覺 」 呢 ?
because the part of the brain that controls decisionmaking doesn't control language .	因為大腦控制決策的部分無法控制語言 。
and the best we can muster up is , " i don't know . it just doesn't feel right . "	我們最好的辦法是: 「 我不知道 , 感覺不對 。 」
or sometimes you say you're leading with your heart , or you're leading with your soul .	或者有時候你會說你在帶著你的心 , 或者你帶著你的靈魂 。
well , i hate to break it to you , those aren't other body parts controlling your behavior .	嗯 , 我討厭打破它 , 這些不是其他身體部位控制你的行為 。
it's all happening here in your limbic brain , the part of the brain that controls decisionmaking and not language .	一切都發生在你的邊緣大腦中 , 控制決策的部分 , 而非語言 。
but if you don't know why you do what you do , and people respond to why you do what you do , then how will you ever get people to vote for you , or buy something from you , or , more importantly , be loyal and want to be a part of what it is that you do .	但如果你不知道你為什麼做你所做的事 , 人們會回應你為什麼做你所做的事 , 那麼你要如何讓人們投票給你 , 或買東西 , 更重要的是 , 做忠誠 , 想要成為你所做的一部分 。
again , the goal is not just to sell to people who need what you have ; the goal is to sell to people who believe what you believe .	同樣的 , 目標不只是要賣給需要你的人 ; 目標是要賣給那些相信你所相信的人 。
the goal is not just to hire people who need a job ; it's to hire people who believe what you believe .	目標不只是要僱用需要工作的人 ; 而是要僱用相信你所相信的人 。
i always say that , you know , if you hire people just because they can do a job , they'll work for your money , but if you hire people who believe what you believe , they'll work for you with blood and sweat and tears .	我總是這樣說 , 如果你雇用人 , 只因為他們可以做事 , 他們會為你的錢工作 , 但如果你雇用相信你所相信的人 , 他們會為你帶來血汗和淚水 。
and nowhere else is there a better example of this than with the wright brothers .	其他地方都沒有比萊特兄弟更好的例子 。
most people don't know about samuel pierpont langley .	大部分的人不知道samuelpierpontlangley 。
and back in the early 20th century , the pursuit of powered man flight was like the dot com of the day .	回到二十世紀初 , 追求電力飛行的追求 , 就像是白天的點com 。
everybody was trying it .	每個人都在試 。
and samuel pierpont langley had , what we assume , to be the recipe for success .	而samuelpierpontlangley有 , 我們假設是成功的秘訣 。
i mean , even now , you ask people , " why did your product or why did your company fail ? "	我的意思是 , 即使現在 , 你問別人: 「 為什麼你的產品或為什麼你的公司會失敗 ? 」
and people always give you the same permutation of the same three things: undercapitalized , the wrong people , bad market conditions .	人們總是會給你相同的三樣東西:不適合的人、壞人、壞市場條件 。
it's always the same three things , so let's explore that .	總是相同的三件事 , 讓我們來探討一下 。
samuel pierpont langley was given 50 , 000 dollars by the war department to figure out this flying machine .	samuelpierpontlangley被戰爭部門給五萬美金 , 想出這台飛行機器 。
money was no problem .	金錢沒有問題 。
he held a seat at harvard and worked at the smithsonian and was extremely wellconnected ; he knew all the big minds of the day .	他在哈佛舉辦了一座位子 , 在史密森尼人工作 , 當時是非常好的連結 ; 他知道當時的所有大型思維 。
he hired the best minds money could find and the market conditions were fantastic .	他僱用最好的思想錢 , 能找到市場條件是很棒的 。
the new york times followed him around everywhere , and everyone was rooting for langley .	《紐約時報》追蹤他到處跑 , 每個人都在為langley開車 。
then how come we've never heard of samuel pierpont langley ?	那麼我們怎麼可能從來沒有聽過samuelpierpontlangley ?
a few hundred miles away in dayton ohio , orville and wilbur wright , they had none of what we consider to be the recipe for success .	離俄亥俄州的幾百英哩遠 , 奧維爾和威爾布萊特 , 他們沒有我們認為的成功的秘訣 。
they had no money ; they paid for their dream with the proceeds from their bicycle shop ; not a single person on the wright brothers' team had a college education , not even orville or wilbur ; and the new york times followed them around nowhere .	他們沒有錢 , 他們付了他們的夢想 , 用自行車購物的代價 ; 沒有一個人在萊特兄弟的團隊中受過大學教育 , 甚至不是鄉村或威爾布爾 ; 紐約時報追蹤他們到處都是 。
the difference was , orville and wilbur were driven by a cause , by a purpose , by a belief .	差別在於 , 奧維爾和威爾布爾被一個目標所驅使 , 一個信念驅使 。
they believed that if they could figure out this flying machine , it'll change the course of the world .	他們相信如果他們能想出這台飛行機器 , 會改變世界的軌道 。
samuel pierpont langley was different .	samuelpierpontlangley是不同的 。
he wanted to be rich , and he wanted to be famous .	他想成為富人 , 他想成為有名人物 。
he was in pursuit of the result .	他在追求結果 。
he was in pursuit of the riches .	他在追求富人 。
and lo and behold , look what happened .	看 , 看看發生了什麼事 。
the people who believed in the wright brothers' dream worked with them with blood and sweat and tears .	相信萊特兄弟的夢想 , 和他們一起工作 , 用血汗和淚水 。
the others just worked for the paycheck .	其他人則是為了支付錢而工作 。
and they tell stories of how every time the wright brothers went out , they would have to take five sets of parts , because that's how many times they would crash before they came in for supper .	他們會說故事 , 每當萊特兄弟出門時 , 他們就得要採取五組零件 , 因為那是他們在供應商前撞了多少次 。
and , eventually , on december 17th , 1903 , the wright brothers took flight , and no one was there to even experience it .	最後 , 在1903年12月17日 , 萊特兄弟飛行 , 甚至沒有人在那兒體驗它 。
we found out about it a few days later .	幾天後 , 我們發現了它 。
and further proof that langley was motivated by the wrong thing: the day the wright brothers took flight , he quit .	更進一步的證據證明 , 蕾莉的動機是錯誤的:萊特兄弟飛行的那天 , 他辭掉了 。
he could have said , " that's an amazing discovery , guys , and i will improve upon your technology , " but he didn't .	他可能會說: 「 這是很棒的發現 , 各位 , 我會改善你們的科技 。 」 但他並沒有 。
he wasn't first , he didn't get rich , he didn't get famous so he quit .	他不是第一個 , 他沒有得到富人 , 他沒有得到有名的 , 所以他放棄了 。
people don't buy what you do ; they buy why you do it .	人們不買你做什麼 ; 他們買你為什麼要做 。
and if you talk about what you believe , you will attract those who believe what you believe .	如果你談到你所相信的 , 你會吸引那些相信你所相信的人 。
but why is it important to attract those who believe what you believe ?	但為什麼吸引那些相信你所相信的人是很重要的 ?
something called the law of diffusion of innovation , and if you don't know the law , you definitely know the terminology .	一個叫做創新的擴散法則 , 如果你不知道法律 , 你絕對知道它的術語 。
the first two and a half percent of our population are our innovators .	前2%的人口是我們的創新者 。
the next 13 and a half percent of our population are our early adopters .	接下來的13.5%的人口是我們早期的採用者 。
the next 34 percent are your early majority , your late majority and your laggards .	接下來的34%是你早期的大多數人 , 你的下半數和你的懶惰 。
the only reason these people buy touch tone phones is because you can't buy rotary phones anymore .	這些人只能買到接觸電話的唯一理由 , 是因為你不能再買零售手機了 。
we all sit at various places at various times on this scale , but what the law of diffusion of innovation tells us is that if you want massmarket success or massmarket acceptance of an idea , you cannot have it until you achieve this tipping point between 15 and 18 percent market penetration , and then the system tips .	我們都坐在這個規模不同的地方 , 但創新的散播法則告訴我們 , 如果你想要大眾市場成功或大眾市場接受一個想法 , 你就不能直到你達成這個臨界點 , 直到你達到15%到18%的市場滲透率 , 然後系統就開始了 。
and i love asking businesses , " what's your conversion on new business ? "	我喜歡問企業: 「 你對新生意的轉變是什麼 ? 」
and they love to tell you , " oh , it's about 10 percent , " proudly .	他們喜歡跟你說: 「 喔 , 這大概是百分之十 , 」 很驕傲 。
well , you can trip over 10 percent of the customers .	嗯 , 你可以嘗試超過百分之十的客戶 。
we all have about 10 percent who just " get it . "	我們都有大約10%的人 「 懂 」 。
that's how we describe them , right ?	這就是我們如何描述它們 , 對吧 ?
that's like that gut feeling , " oh , they just get it . "	那就像是直覺 , 感覺: 「 喔 , 他們就懂了 。 」
the problem is: how do you find the ones that get it before you're doing business with them versus the ones who don't get it ?	問題是:如何在你和他們做生意之前 , 找到他們 , 而不是那些不懂的人 ?
so it's this here , this little gap that you have to close , as jeffrey moore calls it , " crossing the chasm " because , you see , the early majority will not try something until someone else has tried it first .	這裡是這個 , 你必須關閉的小缺口 , 就像傑佛里摩爾所說的 , 「 跨越教室 」 , 因為 , 你看 , 早期大多數人不會嘗試 , 直到其他人先試過它 。
and these guys , the innovators and the early adopters , they're comfortable making those gut decisions .	這些人 , 創新者和早期的採用者 , 他們很舒適地做出這些直覺決策 。
they're more comfortable making those intuitive decisions that are driven by what they believe about the world and not just what product is available .	他們更自在地做出那些直覺的決定 , 由他們對世界的信念所驅使 , 而不僅僅是產品可以取得的 。
these are the people who stood in line for six hours to buy an iphone when they first came out , when you could have just walked into the store the next week and bought one off the shelf .	這些人排隊排隊六小時 , 當他們第一次出門時 , 買iphone , 下週你只要走進商店 , 買下架 。
these are the people who spent 40 , 000 dollars on flat screen tvs when they first came out , even though the technology was substandard .	這些人花了四萬美金在平面的螢幕上 , 第一次出櫃 , 即便這項技術是替代品 。
and , by the way , they didn't do it because the technology was so great ; they did it for themselves .	順帶一提 , 他們並沒有這麼做 , 因為這項技術太棒了 , 他們為自己做這件事 。
it's because they wanted to be first .	因為他們想要成為第一 。
people don't buy what you do ; they buy why you do it and what you do simply proves what you believe .	人們不買你所做的事 ; 他們買你為什麼做的事 , 以及你所做的 , 證明了你所相信的事 。
in fact , people will do the things that prove what they believe .	事實上 , 人們會做他們所相信的事 。
the reason that person bought the iphone in the first six hours , stood in line for six hours , was because of what they believed about the world , and how they wanted everybody to see them: they were first .	一個人在前六個小時買iphone的理由 , 排長六個小時 , 是因為他們對這個世界的信念 , 以及他們想要每個人看他們的方式:他們是第一個 。
people don't buy what you do ; they buy why you do it .	人們不買你做什麼 ; 他們買你為什麼要做 。
so let me give you a famous example , a famous failure and a famous success of the law of diffusion of innovation .	讓我舉個有名的例子 , 一個有名的失敗和一個有名的成功 , 來說明創新的散播法則 。
first , the famous failure .	首先 , 著名的失敗 。
it's a commercial example .	這是個商業的例子 。
as we said before , a second ago , the recipe for success is money and the right people and the right market conditions , right ? you should have success then .	正如我們先前所說的 , 成功的秘訣是金錢、對的人、對的市場條件 , 對嗎 ? 你應該成功了 。
from the time tivo came out about eight or nine years ago to this current day , they are the single highestquality product on the market , hands down , there is no dispute .	從八、九年前到今日 , 到目前為止 , 它們是市場上最高品質的產品 , 手上也沒有爭議 。
they were extremely wellfunded .	他們非常受歡迎 。
market conditions were fantastic .	市場狀況很棒 。
i mean , we use tivo as verb .	我的意思是 , 我們把tivo當作動詞 。
i tivo stuff on my piece of junk time warner dvr all the time .	我隨時都在我的垃圾時間華納dvr上 。
but tivo's a commercial failure .	但tivo是一個商業上的失敗 。
they've never made money .	他們從來沒有賺到錢 。
and when they went ipo , their stock was at about 30 or 40 dollars and then plummeted , and it's never traded above 10 .	當他們去ipo時 , 他們的股票大約是三、四十元 , 然後爆炸了 , 從來沒有在10歲以上交易 。
in fact , i don't think it's even traded above six , except for a couple of little spikes .	事實上 , 我不認為它在六號以上的交易 , 除了幾個小尖峰之外 。
because you see , when tivo launched their product they told us all what they had .	因為你看 , 當tivo推出他們的產品時 , 他們告訴我們他們所擁有的一切 。
they said , " we have a product that pauses live tv , skips commercials , rewinds live tv and memorizes your viewing habits without you even asking . "	他們說: 「 我們有一個會暫停現場電視的產品 , 滑雪廣告 , 重塑現場電視 , 記住你的觀看習慣 , 甚至你會問 。 」
and the cynical majority said , " we don't believe you .	憤世嫉俗的多數人說: 「 我們不相信你 。
we don't need it . we don't like it .	我們不需要它 , 我們不喜歡它 。
you're scaring us . "	你害怕我們 。 」
what if they had said , " if you're the kind of person who likes to have total control over every aspect of your life , boy , do we have a product for you .	如果他們說: 「 若你是那種想要完全掌控你人生的各個面向的人 , 男孩 , 我們有產品給你 。
it pauses live tv , skips commercials , memorizes your viewing habits , etc . , etc . "	它會暫停電視 , 跳過廣告 , 記住你的觀看習慣 , 等等 。 」
people don't buy what you do ; they buy why you do it , and what you do simply serves as the proof of what you believe .	人們不買你做什麼 ; 他們買你為什麼這麼做 , 而你所做的就是證明你所相信的事 。
now let me give you a successful example of the law of diffusion of innovation .	讓我給你們一個成功的例子 , 說明創新的擴散法則 。
in the summer of 1963 , 250 , 000 people showed up on the mall in washington to hear dr . king speak .	在1963年夏天 , 有二十五萬人出現在華盛頓的購物中心 , 聽到金恩博士演說 。
they sent out no invitations , and there was no website to check the date .	他們沒有發送任何邀請 , 也沒有網站來檢查約會 。
how do you do that ?	要怎麼做呢 ?
well , dr . king wasn't the only man in america who was a great orator .	金恩博士不是美國唯一一個偉大的演說家 。
he wasn't the only man in america who suffered in a precivil rights america .	他不是美國唯一一個被處於普通的美國人 。
in fact , some of his ideas were bad .	事實上 , 他的一些想法很糟 。
but he had a gift .	但他有一個禮物 。
he didn't go around telling people what needed to change in america .	他沒有到處告訴人們在美國需要什麼改變 。
he went around and told people what he believed .	他四處走 , 告訴大家他所相信的 。
" i believe , i believe , i believe , " he told people .	「 我相信 , 我相信 , 我相信 , 「 他告訴人們 。
and people who believed what he believed took his cause , and they made it their own , and they told people .	相信他所造成的成因 , 並且他們自己做出來 , 告訴人們 。
and some of those people created structures to get the word out to even more people .	其中一些人創造了結構 , 讓這個詞傳遞給更多人 。
and lo and behold , 250 , 000 people showed up on the right day at the right time to hear him speak .	你看 , 25 , 000人在適當的日子 , 聽到他說話 。
how many of them showed up for him ?	有多少人為他出席 ?
they showed up for themselves .	他們為了自己而出 。
it's what they believed about america that got them to travel in a bus for eight hours to stand in the sun in washington in the middle of august .	他們相信美國能讓他們在公車上旅行八小時 , 讓他們站在華盛頓 , 站在八月中央 。
it's what they believed , and it wasn't about black versus white: 25 percent of the audience was white .	這是他們所相信的 , 重點不是黑人和白人:25%的觀眾是白人 。
dr . king believed that there are two types of laws in this world: those that are made by a higher authority and those that are made by man .	金恩博士相信世界上有兩種法律:那些由高權威制定的法律 , 而這些法律是由男性組成的 。
and not until all the laws that are made by man are consistent with the laws that are made by the higher authority will we live in a just world .	直到人類所制定的所有法則都與較高權威制定的法律一致 , 我們就能生活在一個公平的世界 。
it just so happened that the civil rights movement was the perfect thing to help him bring his cause to life .	剛好是公民權運動是幫助他終身的完美 。
we followed , not for him , but for ourselves .	我們追隨了 , 不是為了他 , 而是為了我們自己 。
and , by the way , he gave the " i have a dream " speech , not the " i have a plan " speech .	順帶一提 , 他給了 「 我有一個夢想 」 演講 , 而不是 「 我有一個計劃 」 演講 。
listen to politicians now , with their comprehensive 12point plans .	現在 , 聽政治人物 , 用他們全面的12點的植物聽著 。
they're not inspiring anybody .	他們沒有鼓舞任何人 。
because there are leaders and there are those who lead .	因為有領導者 , 也有領導者 。
leaders hold a position of power or authority , but those who lead inspire us .	領導者擁有權力或權威的位置 , 但領導人卻鼓舞了我們 。
whether they're individuals or organizations , we follow those who lead , not because we have to , but because we want to .	不論是個人或組織 , 我們追隨領導的人 , 不是因為我們必須 , 而是我們想要 。
we follow those who lead , not for them , but for ourselves .	我們遵循那些領導者 , 不是為了他們 , 而是為了我們自己 。
and it's those who start with " why " that have the ability to inspire those around them or find others who inspire them .	正是那些從 「 為什麼 」 開始的人 , 能夠鼓舞他們身邊的人 , 或找到那些激勵他們的人 。
how do you remember where you parked your car ? how do you know if you're moving in the right direction ? neuroscientist neil burgess studies the neural mechanisms that map the space around us , and how they link to memory and imagination .	你如何記得你在哪兒停車 ? 你如何知道你是否在正確的方向移動 ? 神經科學家neilburges研究我們周圍的神經機制 , 以及它們如何連結記憶和想像力 。
brain , cognitive science , exploration , neuroscience , science	大腦、認知科學、探索、神經科學、科學、科學、科學 。
neil burgess: how your brain tells you where you are	neilburgeges:你的大腦如何告訴你你的位置在哪裡 。
when we park in a big parking lot , how do we remember where we parked our car ?	當我們在一個大停車場停車場時 , 我們如何記得停車位在哪裡 ?
here's the problem facing homer .	這是面對荷馬的問題 。
and we're going to try to understand what's happening in his brain .	我們會試著去了解他的大腦裡發生了什麼事 。
so we'll start with the hippocampus , shown in yellow , which is the organ of memory .	所以 , 我們先從海馬體開始 , 黃色的就是記憶的器官 。
if you have damage there , like in alzheimer's , you can't remember things including where you parked your car .	如果你在那兒受傷 , 像阿茲海默那樣 , 你就無法記起事情 , 包括你在哪裡停車 。
it's named after latin for " seahorse , " which it resembles .	它是以拉丁文為名的 , 它是以拉丁文為名 , 它是相似的 。
and like the rest of the brain , it's made of neurons .	就像大腦的其餘部分 , 它是由神經元組成的 。
so the human brain has about a hundred billion neurons in it .	人類的大腦有大約一千億個神經元 。
and the neurons communicate with each other by sending little pulses or spikes of electricity via connections to each other .	神經元彼此互相溝通 , 通過發送小脈衝或電流 , 通過互相連結 。
the hippocampus is formed of two sheets of cells , which are very densely interconnected .	海馬體是兩種細胞的組成 , 非常緊密的相互連結 。
and scientists have begun to understand how spatial memory works by recording from individual neurons in rats or mice while they forage or explore an environment looking for food .	科學家開始了解空間記憶是如何運作的 , 藉由記錄老鼠或老鼠在覓食或探索環境尋找食物時記錄個人的神經元 。
so we're going to imagine we're recording from a single neuron in the hippocampus of this rat here .	想像一下 , 我們要從這隻老鼠的海馬體中記錄下來 。
and when it fires a little spike of electricity , there's going to be a red dot and a click .	當它開啟一點電力衝動時 , 會有一個紅點 , 點擊一下 。
so what we see is that this neuron knows whenever the rat has gone into one particular place in its environment .	所以 , 我們看到這個神經元每當老鼠進入某個特定的位置時 , 就會知道這個位置的位置 。
and it signals to the rest of the brain by sending a little electrical spike .	它會傳送到大腦的其他部位 , 藉由發送一個小小的電流 。
so we could show the firing rate of that neuron as a function of the animal's location .	所以 , 我們可以將神經元的激發率呈現為動物所在位置的功能 。
and if we record from lots of different neurons , we'll see that different neurons fire when the animal goes in different parts of its environment , like in this square box shown here .	如果我們從許多不同的神經元中記錄下來 , 我們會發現 , 當動物進入環境的不同部位時 , 會產生不同的神經元發射 , 就像這邊的正方形盒子 。
so together they form a map for the rest of the brain , telling the brain continually , " where am i now within my environment ? "	所以 , 它們一起組成了一張大腦的地圖 , 不斷地告訴大腦: 「 我現在在我的環境中在哪裡 ? 」
place cells are also being recorded in humans .	位置細胞也被記錄在人類身上 。
so epilepsy patients sometimes need the electrical activity in their brain monitoring .	所以癲癇患者有時需要腦部監控的電活動 。
and some of these patients played a video game where they drive around a small town .	有些病人玩了一個電玩遊戲 , 他們在一個小鎮附近開車 。
and place cells in their hippocampi would fire , become active , start sending electrical impulses whenever they drove through a particular location in that town .	海馬體內的細胞會啟動 , 活躍 , 開始發送電脈衝 , 在他們開車穿過這個城鎮的特定位置 。
so how does a place cell know where the rat or person is within its environment ?	所以 , 一個地方細胞如何知道老鼠或人在其環境中的位置 ?
well these two cells here show us that the boundaries of the environment are particularly important .	這兩個細胞告訴我們 , 環境的界線特別重要 。
so the one on the top likes to fire sort of midway between the walls of the box that their rat's in .	最上方的這個 , 像是在老鼠的牆壁中發火一樣 。
and when you expand the box , the firing location expands .	當你拓展盒子時 , 發射地點會擴張 。
the one below likes to fire whenever there's a wall close by to the south .	下面的這一面 , 每當有一面牆靠近南方時 , 就會有一面牆 。
and if you put another wall inside the box , then the cell fires in both place wherever there's a wall to the south as the animal explores around in its box .	如果你把另一面牆放在盒子裡 , 細胞會在兩邊都有牆壁的位置 , 以動物的盒子來探索 。
so this predicts that sensing the distances and directions of boundaries around you extended buildings and so on is particularly important for the hippocampus .	這種預測 , 感應到你周圍的距離和距離 , 延伸出建築物 , 對於海馬體來說 , 尤其重要 。
and indeed , on the inputs to the hippocampus , cells are found which project into the hippocampus , which do respond exactly to detecting boundaries or edges at particular distances and directions from the rat or mouse as it's exploring around .	的確 , 在海馬體的輸入中 , 細胞會發現海馬體的專案 , 它會根據特定距離來偵測海馬體的界線或邊緣 , 尤其是來自老鼠或老鼠的方向 。
so the cell on the left , you can see , it fires whenever the animal gets near to a wall or a boundary to the east , whether it's the edge or the wall of a square box or the circular wall of the circular box or even the drop at the edge of a table , which the animals are running around .	左邊的細胞 , 你可以看到 , 當動物靠近牆時 , 它會發出火焰 , 或是向東邊邊界線 , 不論是方形的邊緣 , 或圓形的圍牆 , 或甚至是桌子的邊緣 , 動物會跑來跑去 。
and the cell on the right there fires whenever there's a boundary to the south , whether it's the drop at the edge of the table or a wall or even the gap between two tables that are pulled apart .	而在右邊的細胞 , 每當有南邊界時 , 都會被激發 , 不論是桌子的邊緣或是牆壁的邊緣 , 或甚至兩張桌子之間的鴻溝 。
so that's one way in which we think place cells determine where the animal is as it's exploring around .	這是我們認為位置細胞的一種方式 , 決定動物在周圍探索的位置 。
we can also test where we think objects are , like this goal flag , in simple environments or indeed , where your car would be .	我們還可以測試我們認為物體的位置 , 比如這個目標 , 在簡單的環境中 , 或你的車子會在哪裡 。
so we can have people explore an environment and see the location they have to remember .	所以我們可以讓人們去探索一個環境 , 看看他們需要記得的地點 。
and then , if we put them back in the environment , generally they're quite good at putting a marker down where they thought that flag or their car was .	接著 , 如果我們把它們放回環境中 , 通常它們都很擅長把標記放在他們認為旗幟或車的位置上 。
but on some trials , we could change the shape and size of the environment like we did with the place cell .	但在某些試驗中 , 我們能改變環境的形狀和大小 , 就像我們用位置細胞所做的一樣 。
in that case , we can see how where they think the flag had been changes as a function of how you change the shape and size of the environment .	在這個案例中 , 我們可以看到他們認為旗幟的改變是如何改變環境的形狀和大小 。
and what you see , for example , if the flag was where that cross was in a small square environment , and then if you ask people where it was , but you've made the environment bigger , where they think the flag had been stretches out in exactly the same way that the place cell firing stretched out .	舉例來說 , 你所看到的旗幟在一個小平方的環境中 , 然後如果你問人們在哪裡 , 但你讓環境更大 , 他們認為旗幟在哪裡被延伸出來 , 完全相同地點細胞爆炸的方式 。
it's as if you remember where the flag was by storing the pattern of firing across all of your place cells at that location , and then you can get back to that location by moving around so that you best match the current pattern of firing of your place cells with that stored pattern .	彷彿你還記得旗幟的位置 , 藉由儲存你在那個位置的所有位置細胞的圖案 , 然後你就可以回到那個位置 , 這樣你就可以把你位置細胞的激發模式和那個儲存的圖案進行配對 。
that guides you back to the location that you want to remember .	那會引導你回到你想要記住的位置 。
but we also know where we are through movement .	但我們也知道我們透過運動來做什麼 。
so if we take some outbound path perhaps we park and we wander off we know because our own movements , which we can integrate over this path roughly what the heading direction is to go back .	所以如果我們把一些外觀的路徑停下來 , 我們就知道 , 因為我們自己的運動 , 我們可以整合這條路徑 , 來回回走 。
and place cells also get this kind of path integration input from a kind of cell called a grid cell .	位置細胞也會得到這種路徑整合 , 來自一種叫做格狀細胞的細胞 。
now grid cells are found , again , on the inputs to the hippocampus , and they're a bit like place cells .	同樣的 , 網格細胞在海馬體的輸入 , 它們有點像個地方細胞 。
but now as the rat explores around , each individual cell fires in a whole array of different locations which are laid out across the environment in an amazingly regular triangular grid .	但現在 , 當老鼠四處探索時 , 每一塊細胞會在不同的地點上發射 , 這些地點是以驚人的三角形狀在周圍形成的 。
and if you record from several grid cells shown here in different colors each one has a gridlike firing pattern across the environment , and each cell's gridlike firing pattern is shifted slightly relative to the other cells .	若你從數個網格中記錄到這裡的不同顏色 , 每個細胞都有像網格一樣的旋轉圖案 , 每個細胞的網狀圖案會稍微轉移到其他細胞上 。
so the red one fires on this grid and the green one on this one and the blue on on this one .	紅色的這條格子上是綠色的 , 藍色是這條格子上的藍色 。
so together , it's as if the rat can put a virtual grid of firing locations across its environment a bit like the latitude and longitude lines that you'd find on a map , but using triangles .	所以 , 一起來 , 老鼠就好像可以在其周遭的虛擬網狀網格 , 有點像你在地圖上找到的緯度和長度線 , 但用三角形 。
and as it moves around , the electrical activity can pass from one of these cells to the next cell to keep track of where it is , so that it can use its own movements to know where it is in its environment .	當它移動時 , 電子活動會從其中一個細胞傳遞到下一個細胞 , 持續追蹤它的位置 , 這樣它就可以利用它自己的移動 , 來知道它在周圍的位置 。
do people have grid cells ?	人們有網格細胞嗎 ?
well because all of the gridlike firing patterns have the same axes of symmetry , the same orientations of grid , shown in orange here , it means that the net activity of all of the grid cells in a particular part of the brain should change according to whether we're running along these six directions or running along one of the six directions in between .	因為所有像網格般的通路圖案都有相同的對稱軸 , 圖中的格狀 , 圖中顯示橘色代表的是 , 所有網格細胞在某個區域的net活動 , 應該根據我們在這些六個方向進行的改變 , 或在六個方向的運作 。
so we can put people in an mri scanner and have them do a little video game like the one i showed you and look for this signal .	所以 , 我們可以把人放進核磁共振造影機 , 讓他們做個小遊戲 , 就像我剛才展示的一樣 , 去尋找這個信號 。
and indeed , you do see it in the human entorhinal cortex , which is the same part of the brain that you see grid cells in rats .	的確 , 你的確在人類的腦皮質中看到的 , 和你在老鼠身上看到的網格細胞一樣 。
so back to homer .	回到荷馬 。
he's probably remembering where his car was in terms of the distances and directions to extended buildings and boundaries around the location where he parked .	他可能還記得車子的距離和方向 , 來延伸建築物和界線 , 在停車位的位置上 。
and that would be represented by the firing of boundarydetecting cells .	由邊界檢測細胞的發射所代表 。
he's also remembering the path he took out of the car park , which would be represented in the firing of grid cells .	他還記得他走出車子公園的路徑 , 它會被代表在網格細胞的發射中 。
now both of these kinds of cells can make the place cells fire .	兩種類型的細胞都可以使地方細胞發光 。
and he can return to the location where he parked by moving so as to find where it is that best matches the firing pattern of the place cells in his brain currently with the stored pattern where he parked his car .	他可以回到他移動的位置 , 找到最好的位置 , 配對大腦中細胞的激發模式 , 目前他用儲存的模式 , 把他的車子停在位置上 。
and that guides him back to that location irrespective of visual cues like whether his car's actually there .	那引導他回到那個地點 , 不像他的車子是否真的在那兒 。
maybe it's been towed .	也許它是被推翻的 。
but he knows where it was , so he knows to go and get it .	但他知道它在哪裡 , 所以他知道要去找它 。
so beyond spatial memory , if we look for this gridlike firing pattern throughout the whole brain , we see it in a whole series of locations which are always active when we do all kinds of autobiographical memory tasks , like remembering the last time you went to a wedding , for example .	所以 , 除了空間記憶之外 , 如果我們在整個大腦中尋找像網格般的激動模式 , 我們會在一系列的位置上看到 , 當我們做各種自傳記憶的任務時 , 總是活躍起來 , 比如記住你上次去婚禮時的最後一次 。
so it may be that the neural mechanisms for representing the space around us are also used for generating visual imagery so that we can recreate the spatial scene , at least , of the events that have happened to us when we want to imagine them .	所以 , 可能是因為我們周遭的神經機制也用來產生視覺影像 , 使我們能夠重現空間的場景 , 至少 , 當我們想想像它們時發生的事件 。
so if this was happening , your memories could start by place cells activating each other via these dense interconnections and then reactivating boundary cells to create the spatial structure of the scene around your viewpoint .	所以 , 如果這發生了 , 你的記憶可以從這些密度的相互連結開始 , 再次啟動邊界細胞 , 來創造你觀點周圍的空間結構 。
and grid cells could move this viewpoint through that space .	網格細胞可以在這個空間中移動這個觀點 。
another kind of cell , head direction cells , which i didn't mention yet , they fire like a compass according to which way you're facing .	另外一種細胞 , 頭部的方向細胞 , 我還沒提到 , 它們會像一個指針一樣 , 根據你正在面對的方向 。
they could define the viewing direction from which you want to generate an image for your visual imagery , so you can imagine what happened when you were at this wedding , for example .	他們可以根據你的視覺圖像來定義視覺的方向 , 例如 , 當你在婚禮上時 , 會發生什麼事 。
